It is December 1989 in Bethel Township, Clark County, Ohio.  The opening scene takes place on the property owned by the parents of **JEREMY** **GILLEY**.  

**JEREMY GILLEY** is 18 years old and is a high school senior.  Because his best friend has the same name, everyone calls him **GILLEY**, to avoid confusion.  **GILLEY** is very tall, lanky, awkward, and wears Coke-bottle style glasses that emphasize his nearsightedness.  **GILLEY**’s role in the band is front man, male vocals, and rhythm guitar.  At best, his guitar playing is diffident.  **GILLEY** has animal magnetism and incredible smoothness and charm with the ladies.

**GILLEY**’s best friend is **JEREMY Evans**, 17 years old.  **JEREMY** is a high school senior.  Physically, he’s 6’1” and is a good two inches shorter than his best friend.  **JEREMY** has an awkward looking mustache, and a severe buzz cut.  Even now, it’s clear that he’s losing his head of hair.  **JEREMY** is whip-smart, well-mannered, well-liked and wickedly competitive.  He’s a self-taught guitar player who needs significant practice to develop into a guitar hero. 

**[[4.3 JEFF EVANS character bible|Jeff Evans]]** is **JEREMY’s** older brother.  **JEFF** has just turned 19 years old and attends university.  **JEFF** is the same height as **JEREMY** but where **JEREMY** is thin and wiry, **JEFF** is broad-shouldered and solidly built.  **JEFF** wears silver wire framed glasses, has wild, slicked back hair, and is even smarter than his brother **JEREMY**.  **JEFF** is an extreme introvert, and an undiagnosed yet high functioning autistic young man.  He plays bass with slightly more skill than his younger brother but not by much.  Jeff is a bored college student at Wright State University.

**James Brown** is also 19 years old.  Brown always uses “**JIM**” informally.  **JIM** is a tad bit shorter than both **JEFF** and **JEREMY**.  **JIM** has a rich baritone voice.  **JIM** is also very smart and a bit of an intellectual and has had a life-long fascination with percussion.  **JIM** has cobbled together his first real drum kit from thrift shows, garage sales, and pawn shops, and is proud about the accomplishment.  **JIM** has a cherubic round face with ruddy red cheeks and animated blue eyes.  **JIM** has started attending Wright State University.  

**BILL Davenport** is 18 years old and is a good friend of **GILLEY**’s.  Over the last two years, he’s started friendships with the Evans Brothers.  **BILL** is the shortest, yet most athletic of all the five men.  He’s built like a weightlifter.  Oddly, **BILL** refused to play sports during high school and is a band kid.  He already has mastered playing multiple instruments, but his favorite is the synthesizer.  **BILL** is a better musician right now than anyone else in the band because of years of practice.  **BILL** has luscious wavy hair that would fit well with any 1980’s hair band.  

**KATHY Espich** is a 19-year-old woman and has known **GILLEY**, **JEFF**, and **JIM** since elementary school.  **KATHY** is about 5’6”, far shorter than everyone else in the band.  She has medium length dirty blonde hair.  She met **GILLEY**, **JEFF** and **JIM** in the school district’s gifted classes.  **KATHY** is a very late bloomer and is extremely introverted at first.  She is painfully aware that she is the lone female in the band.  Worse, she knows that her bandmates treat her like she’s one of the guys, and she’s not very comfortable about that, but lacks the confidence to speak up.  **KATHY** hides her curves and breasts with layers of clothing.  She dresses like what will be called grunge in a couple of years’ time.  In a band composed of guys with hair trigger bad attitudes, **KATHY** is clearly the member of the band with the worst anger management issues.  **KATHY** is scraping up the time for classes at Clark Technical College.

---

**INT. GILLEY'S PARENTS' GARAGE – LATE AFTERNOON – DECEMBER 1989**

The garage is a monument to suburban neglect. Tools hang haphazardly, a rusted lawnmower lurks in the corner, and oily rags are strewn across a workbench. The air is thick with the smell of motor oil and stale beer (courtesy of **GILLEY**’s older brother, presumably). A single bare bulb hangs precariously from the ceiling, casting harsh shadows.

**GILLEY**, all six-foot-four of him, hunched over like a praying mantis in oversized glasses, gestures with a half-empty can of Mr. Pibb. 

**GILLEY** 
Gentlemen, and **KATHY**… Behold! Our temple of rock. Or, you know, whatever the hell this is.

He kicks a stack of old newspapers, sending them scattering.

**DAVENPORT** (Dryly) 
Looks more like a shrine to your dad’s handyman career.

Davenport, compact and muscular, surveys the mess with disdain. He’s already meticulously wiping down his synthesizer, a gleaming, futuristic beacon in the grime.

**JEFF** (Pushing up his glasses) 
Function over form, **BILL**. Besides, the acoustics in here are… suboptimal.

**JEFF**, hunched over like his friend **GILLEY**, but with a more intense, almost twitchy energy, adjusts his bass.

**BROWN** (Grinning, patting his Frankenstein drum kit) 
Suboptimal? Man, this place is perfect! It’s got that raw, primal vibe. Like… like a goddamn cave.

**JIM**, beaming, adjusts a cymbal that looks like it was salvaged from a junkyard.

**KATHY**, dressed in an oversized flannel shirt and ripped jeans, stands awkwardly near the back, clutching a battered guitar case. She avoids eye contact.

**KATHY** (Muttering) 
It’s… cozy.

**GILLEY** 
Cozy? Honey, this ain’t no goddamn tea party. This is where we forge legends. This is where we…

He trails off, searching for the right words.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
…where we make some goddamn noise!

Just then, the garage door burst open, revealing **JEREMY** EVANS, breathless. He’s clutching a textbook.

**JEREMY** 
Sorry, sorry! Calculus. Fucking calculus.

**JEFF** (Snapping) 
Calculus? We’ve been waiting for half an hour! This ain’t no goddamn study group!

**JEREMY** (Wiping sweat from his brow) 
I know, I know. But Mrs. Crabtree… she’s got eyes like a goddamn hawk. And breath that could strip paint.

**(IMAGINE A QUICK CUT, CLOSE UP ON JEREMY'S FACE)**

**JEREMY (V.O.)** Crabtree. That bitch could smell fear from a mile away. And teenage desperation? That was her goddamn perfume.

**(CUT BACK TO THE GARAGE)**

**DAVENPORT** (Scoffs) 
Excuses, excuses. Next time, skip the quadratic equations and prioritize the power chords.

**GILLEY** (Winking at **KATHY**) 
Speaking of power… **KATHY**, you ready to unleash your inner rock goddess?

**KATHY** recoils, pulling her flannel tighter around her.

**KATHY** (Mumbling) 
Just… let’s play.

**(CAMERA PUSHES IN ON KATHY’S HANDS, TIGHTLY GRIPPING HER GUITAR. A BEAD OF SWEAT TRICKLES DOWN HER FOREHEAD. THE LIGHT CATCHES THE FAINT OUTLINE OF HER BRA STRAP BENEATH HER SHIRT.)**

**SOUND:** The distorted opening riff of a heavy metal song blasts from Davenport's synthesizer, cutting through the tension.

**BROWN** (Counting off wildly) 
One! Two! Three! Four! Let’s fucking do this!

The band erupts into a cacophony. **GILLEY**’s guitar playing is sloppy, **JEFF**’s bass is a rumble, **JIM**’s drums are a chaotic explosion, but Davenport’s synth cuts through it all, a laser beam of pure sound.

**SOUND:** A dog barks furiously from next door, followed by a woman's shrill yell.

**GILLEY** (Grinning) 
Sounds like the neighbors are enjoying the show!

**JEFF** (Eyes narrowed, lost in the music) 
They’ll be begging for an encore.

**TOUCHSTONE** **MOMENT:**

**(SLOW MOTION SHOT OF KATHY’S FOOT TAPPING TO THE BEAT. THE CAMERA ZOOMS IN ON HER BOOT, THEN CUTS TO A CLOSE UP OF HER FACE. A SMALL, ALMOST IMPERCEPTIBLE SMILE PLAYS ON HER LIPS.)**

**VOICEOVER (KATHY):** That’s when it started. Not the band, not really. But something inside me. Something… dangerous.

**(CLOSE UP ON GILLEY, HIS FACE RED WITH EFFORT, HIS GLASSES SLIGHTLY CROOKED. HE LOOKS DIRECTLY AT THE CAMERA, A WILD, ALMOST MANIC LOOK IN HIS EYES.)**

**GILLEY (V.O.)** 
We were young. We were loud. And we were gonna fuckin’ conquer the world. Or at least Bethel Township.

**SOUND:** The music crashes to a halt. The band members stand panting, the air thick with sweat and raw energy.

**ENDING SHOT:**

**(THE CAMERA PANS ACROSS THE GARAGE, LINGERING ON EACH BAND MEMBER’S FACE. EACH FACE IS ILLUMINATED BY THE SINGLE BARE BULB, CREATING A SERIES OF HARSH, UNFLATTERING PORTRAITS. THE CAMERA STOPS ON KATHY, WHO IS LOOKING DIRECTLY AT THE LENS, HER EXPRESSION UNREADABLE.)**

**FADE TO BLACK.**

---

**MONTAGE: THE RISE OF COMMUTED (DECEMBER 1989 – MEMORIAL DAY WEEKEND 1990)**

**(SOUND:** A distorted, feedback-laden guitar chord explodes, then cuts abruptly to silence. Then a single, insistent drumbeat begins, building in intensity.)

**(VISUAL:** Quick cuts: a close-up of a frozen puddle in the driveway outside the garage followed by a shot of the band's breath misting in the cold air inside. Then a close up of **GILLEY**’s fingers fumbling on the guitar strings. He looks frustrated.)

**SCENE 1: WINTER'S GRIP (DECEMBER 1989– FEBRUARY 1990)**

**(SOUND:** The muffled thump of the bass drum, the scrape of a guitar pick against frozen strings.)

**(VISUAL:** The band, bundled in coats and hats, struggles to move a massive engine block – not machinery, but a deliberate act of macho posturing by **GILLEY**. **JEREMY** Evans, arriving late, slips on a patch of ice, sending his books flying. He scrambles to pick them up, his face flushed with embarrassment. **Mr. GILLEY** watches from the kitchen window, a mug of coffee in his hand, a flicker of amusement in his eyes. He never moves, never speaks.)

**(CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT:** **GILLEY** starts wearing leather jackets indoors, affecting a rock star swagger. **JEREMY** Evans begins to compensate for his lateness and clumsiness by becoming obsessively focused on his guitar playing, practicing relentlessly. **JEFF** begins to wear fingerless gloves all the time, even when it is not cold. **JIM** starts to wear bandanas on his head to keep his hair out of his face while drumming.)

**(TOUCHSTONE** **MOMENT):** Extreme close-up on **KATHY**'s hands, raw and red from the cold, as she struggles to tune her guitar. The camera lingers on a small cut on her finger.

---

**SCENE 2: THE THAW (MARCH 1990 – APRIL 1990)**

**(SOUND:** The drip of melting snow, the tentative chirping of birds, the increasingly confident strumming of guitars.)

**(VISUAL:** The garage door is now partially open, letting in a sliver of sunlight. The band practices with more energy. **GILLEY**, now sporting a bad perm, struts around the garage, microphone in hand. He is now wearing sunglasses indoors. He starts to make suggestive faces towards **KATHY**. **KATHY** ignores him and looks at the ground. **JEFF** is now wearing a trench coat everywhere, even in the garage. He is now wearing sunglasses indoors as well. **JIM** now has a full beard and is wearing a wool cap all the time. **JEREMY** is now playing with a pick, rather than his fingers.)

**(CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT:** **GILLEY**’s ego inflates. He starts hitting on girls at school, bragging about the band. **JEREMY** Evans’s guitar playing improves dramatically, but he becomes increasingly withdrawn, focused only on his music. **JEFF** develops an intense, almost competitive rivalry with **JEREMY** as they both play guitar. **JIM** is constantly adjusting his drum set, becoming obsessed with getting the perfect sound.)

**(TOUCHSTONE** **MOMENT):** **Mr. GILLEY** is outside, ostensibly working on his car, but his gaze is fixed on the garage, on his son. He takes a long drag from his cigarette, his eyes narrowed.

---

**SCENE 3: SUMMER'S HEAT (MAY 1990 – MEMORIAL DAY WEEKEND)**

**(SOUND:** The buzzing of bees, the roar of amplifiers, the pounding of drums, the full sound of a band finally clicking.)

**(VISUAL):** The garage door is wide open, bathed in sunlight. The band is now playing with a raw, powerful energy. **GILLEY**, shirtless, is now wearing a bandanna around his head, and now has a full sleeve of temporary tattoos. He now has a permanent sneer on his face. **JEREMY** **EVANS** is now playing complex guitar solos with his eyes closed. He has grown his hair out some to cover his balding head. **JEFF** is now wearing a leather vest over his bare chest. He has grown his hair out and now slicks it back. **JIM** has removed the sleeves from all his shirts. He is now wearing wristbands. **KATHY** is now wearing all black clothing all the time. She now has a permanent scowl on her face. She has started smoking cigarettes. She has started wearing dark lipstick.)

**(CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT):** The band's music is now tight and powerful. Their egos have exploded. They act like they are rock stars, even though they have only played in a garage. **KATHY** starts to assert herself musically, her guitar playing becoming more aggressive and powerful. She has started to become more confident and has started to talk back to **GILLEY**. **GILLEY** has started to ignore her.)

**(TOUCHSTONE** **MOMENT):** Slow-motion shot of **JIM** hitting a cymbal, the light glinting off the metal. The camera zooms in on his face, a look of pure ecstasy. Then cut to **MR**. **GILLEY**, standing in the shadows of the garage, a barely perceptible smile on his lips.

**(SOUND):** The music reaches a crescendo, then cuts abruptly to silence.)

**(VISUAL):** The band stands panting, sweat dripping from their faces. They look at each other, a sense of shared accomplishment in their eyes.)

**(FINAL SHOT:** The camera focuses on **MR**. **GILLEY**, who is now standing in the driveway, watching the band. He slowly shakes his head, a look of quiet disapproval on his face. He then turns and walks into the house, leaving the garage door wide open.)

---

**EXT. TECUMSEH HIGH SCHOOL PARKING LOT – DAY – MEMORIAL DAY WEEKEND 1990**

The parking lot is a chaotic symphony of car horns, cheering parents, and the clatter of tossed mortarboards. The air is thick with the smell of sunscreen and cheap perfume. Sunlight glints off the chrome of classic American cars, a perfect backdrop for this quintessential small-town graduation scene.

**JEREMY GILLEY**, looking slightly overwhelmed but beaming nonetheless, stands amidst the swirling chaos. His mop of hair is now styled (badly) to give him a more mature look. He’s weighed down with academic regalia – multiple sashes, cords, and medals.

**COMMUTED** surrounds him like a protective, yet boisterous, entourage. **BILL** Davenport, looking impossibly buff in his graduation gown, playfully punches **JEREMY** on the arm.

**BILL** 
Well, I’ll be a son of a bitch. Little Einstein actually did it.

**JEFF** (A rare smile playing on his lips) 
Against all odds, he hath managed to escape the clutches of Tecumseh High. More or less intact.

**JEFF** adjusts his glasses, then quickly looks away, a flicker of something unreadable in his eyes.

**GILLEY** (Grinning) 
Hey, I had good teachers. And even better… distractions.

He glances at **KATHY**, who is approaching the group. She’s ditched the grunge look for a summery floral dress, though she still wears her signature dark lipstick and oversized sunglasses. She looks… different. more confident.

**KATHY** (Offering a genuine smile) 
Congrats, **GILLEY**. You made it.

**GILLEY** (Blushing slightly) 
Thanks, **KATHY**. Couldn’t have done it without… you guys.

**(AWKWARD ATTRACTION – JEFF AND KATHY):**

**JEFF** clears his throat, fidgeting with the collar of his shirt. He opens his mouth to speak, then closes it again.

**JEFF** (Stammering) 
That… uh… that dress… it’s… nice.

**KATHY** blushes, pushing her sunglasses up her nose.

**KATHY** (Looking down) 
Thanks. It’s… new.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **JEFF**’s hand as he nervously adjusts his glasses. The camera then cuts to **KATHY**’s hand as she fidgets with the strap of her purse. Their hands almost touch, but then they both pull away quickly.

**GILLEY** (Slapping **JEREMY** on the back) 
Alright, enough with the mushy shit! Let’s celebrate! Tonight, we rock!

**JIM**, now sporting a full-on ZZ Top beard and a wide-brimmed Union Army cavalry slouch hat, lets out a whoop.

**JIM** 
Yeah! Graduation party at my place! My dad is out of town!

**JEREMY (V.O.)** 
**JIM**’s parents being out of town? That was like striking gold. It was a goddamn invitation to party like it was 1999… even though it was only 1990.

The group erupts in cheers. They start taking pictures, striking ridiculous poses. **GILLEY** tries to drape his arm around **KATHY**, but she subtly shrugs him off.

**GILLEY (V.O.)** 
**KATHY**… she was always a tough nut to crack. But I knew, deep down, she dug me. Every woman did. It was just a matter of time.

**(VISUAL):** Quick cut to **KATHY** rolling her eyes, a slight smile on her face.

**(MONTAGE OF CELEBRATION):**

- The band piles into **JIM**’s beat-up van, blasting loud music.
- They drive through town, honking the horn and waving to friends.
- They stop at a gas station, where **GILLEY** buys everyone pop and snacks.
- They arrive at **JIM**’s house, which is already decorated with balloons and streamers.

**(SOUND:** Upbeat rock music plays throughout the montage. Intercut with snippets of dialogue and laughter.)

---

**(AWKWARD ATTRACTION – JEFF AND KATHY CONTINUES):**

At **JIM**’s house, **JEFF** and **KATHY** find themselves alone for a Moment in the kitchen. **JEFF** is attempting to make small talk, but he keeps getting flustered.

**JEFF** 
So… uh… you… you’re going to… college, right?

**KATHY** (Nodding) 
Yeah. Clark Technical. Just… for now.

**JEFF** (Nodding vigorously) 
Right, right. Community college. Good… good choice. Practical.

He trails off, then blurts out:

**JEFF (CONT’D)** 
I like… your… hair.

**KATHY** touches her hair self-consciously.

**KATHY** 
Thanks.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **JEFF**’s hand as he reaches out to touch a strand of **KATHY**’s hair, then quickly pulls back.

**(SOUND:** The music from the party swells, drowning out their awkward conversation.)

**(FINAL SHOT):** The band is gathered on **JIM**’s back deck, watching the sunset. They are all smiling, laughing, and full of hope for the future.

**(GILLEY (V.O.):**
We were on top of the world. We were young, we were talented, and we were unstoppable. We were Commuted, and we were just getting started.

**(FREEZE FRAME ON THE BAND, SILHOUETTED AGAINST THE SETTING SUN.)**

---

**MONTAGE: SUMMER OF '90 (JUNE – AUGUST 1990)**

**(SOUND:** A driving, hard rock riff kicks in, interspersed with snippets of conversation, laughter, and the occasional frustrated yell.)

**(VISUAL:** Quick cuts: Close-up of a calendar flipping through June, July, and August. Then a shot of sweat dripping onto a guitar fretboard. Then a shot of a dog howling at the moon.)

**SCENE 1: THE WORKBENCH (JUNE 1990)**

**(SOUND:** Heavy breathing, grunts of exertion, the scrape of metal against concrete.)

**(VISUAL:** The band members, now slightly more muscular and sporting summer tans, struggle to maneuver a heavy workbench into the garage. It’s clearly too big for the space. **JEFF** and **KATHY** are on one end, their hands brushing awkwardly. They both pull away quickly, blushing. **Mr. GILLEY** watches from the driveway, leaning against his car, a barely perceptible smile on his face. He takes a long drag from his cigarette. The workbench is finally inside, but it takes up most of the room.)

**(CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT/AWKWARD ROMANCE):** **JEFF** keeps trying to initiate conversations with **KATHY** about mundane topics like power tools and lumber. **KATHY** responds with polite, one-word answers. It is clear they are both attracted to each other, but both are too shy to do anything about it.

**(TOUCHSTONE** **MOMENT –):** Extreme close-up on **JEFF**’s hand, covered in grease, as he accidentally touches **KATHY**'s arm. She flinches slightly.

---

**SCENE 2: LATE-NIGHT REHEARSALS (JULY 1, 1990)**

**(SOUND:** The pounding of drums, the thumping of bass, the screech of electric guitars, the howl of the neighbor’s dog.)

**(VISUAL:** The garage is lit by a single bare bulb, casting long shadows. The band is playing with more confidence and precision. **JEREMY**, now sporting a new effects pedal, is experimenting with different sounds, creating a surprisingly professional tone. **GILLEY**, however, is still stuck on the same three power chords. **JIM** is now playing a much larger drum kit. It barely fits in the garage. He too is now wearing fingerless gloves while he plays. **KATHY** is playing with more aggression than ever before. She is now wearing a leather jacket all the time, even though it is very hot.

**(CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT/MUSICAL GROWTH):** **JEREMY’s** guitar playing has improved dramatically, growing more meticulous and witty. **JIM** has become a very good drummer. **KATHY** has become a decent guitar player. **GILLEY** has not improved. **GILLEY** is becoming more and more jealous of **JEREMY’s** improvement on the guitar.

**GILLEY** (Frustrated) 
What the hell is that noise, **JEREMY**? Sounds like a goddamn dying cat.

**JEREMY** (Adjusting his pedal) 
It’s called a delay pedal, **GILLEY**. It’s supposed to sound like that.

**JIM** (Grinning) 
Sounds pretty badass to me.

**TOUCHSTONE** **MOMENT:** **Mr. GILLEY** is sitting in his living room, reading the newspaper. The music from the garage is clearly audible. He lowers his newspaper slightly, a look of contemplation on his face.

**(MR. GILLEY’S V. O.)**
They’re getting better. But are they good enough to go anywhere?

---

**SCENE 3: CLEANUP (AUGUST 1990)**

**(SOUND:** The clatter of tools, the swish of a broom, the sound of ice clinking in glasses of lemonade.)

**(VISUAL:** The band, sweaty and exhausted, is cleaning up the garage after a particularly intense rehearsal. **JEFF** and **KATHY** are sweeping the floor together, their hands brushing again. This time, they don't pull away as quickly. They share a brief, awkward smile. **GILLEY** is sitting on the workbench, watching them with a scowl.

**(CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT/AWKWARD ROMANCE):** **JEFF** and **KATHY** are now making more of an effort to talk to each other, but their conversations are still filled with awkward silences and nervous laughter. **GILLEY** is becoming increasingly jealous of their growing connection.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **KATHY**’s hand as she wipes a bead of sweat from her forehead. The camera then cuts to **JEFF**, who is staring at her, a look of admiration in his eyes. He quickly looks away when she notices him.


---

**SCENE 4: THE NOD (AUGUST 1990)**

**(SOUND:** The heavy breathing of the band members as they struggle to move the workbench back to its original position.)

**(VISUAL:** The band is struggling to move the workbench back out of the garage. It’s even harder than it was to get it in. Mr. **GILLEY** is watching from the driveway, his arms crossed. He simply nods his head, his expression unreadable. The band members exchange glances, then redouble their efforts. They finally manage to get the workbench back outside.)

**(CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT):** The band has learned to work together as a team. They have also learned that Mr. **GILLEY**’s approval is not easily earned.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The band is standing in the driveway, exhausted but satisfied. They look at Mr. **GILLEY**, who gives them a small, almost imperceptible nod of approval. He then turns and walks into the house.

---

**EXT. SUBURBAN NEIGHBORHOOD – MORNING – LABOR DAY WEEKEND 1990**

The sun beats down mercilessly. The air shimmers with heat. Lawnmowers drone, kids shriek in backyard pools, the smell of barbecue hangs heavy in the air. A picture of idyllic suburban life, a stark contrast to the simmering tension within **GILLEY**’s garage.

**INT. GILLEY'S GARAGE – MORNING**

The garage is an inferno. Tools and equipment are scattered haphazardly. The air is thick with sweat, stale beer, and the metallic tang of overheated amplifiers. The band members are drenched, their clothes clinging to their bodies. They’re all on edge, pushed to their limits by the heat, the pressure, and their own simmering frustrations.

**SOUND:** The distorted, out-of-tune opening chords of a song they’ve been trying to perfect for weeks. It stops abruptly.

**GILLEY** (Screaming) 
Goddamn it, Davenport! You’re rushing again! Can’t you keep a goddamn beat?!

**GILLEY** throws his guitar pick down in disgust. His face is flushed, his eyes bloodshot.

**DAVENPORT** (Wiping sweat from his brow) 
Maybe if you weren’t trying to turn us into goddamn virtuosos, we could actually have some fun! You think we’re gonna be fuckin’ Bon Jovi overnight?

**GILLEY** (Spitting)
Fun? This isn’t about fun, you little prick! This is about making something great! Something that matters! Unlike your goddamn Casio keyboard symphonies!

**JEFF** (Muttering, pushing up his glasses) 
Can we just… take five? I feel like I’m gonna pass out.

**JIM** (Rolling his eyes, hitting his drums with increasing force)  
Yeah, let’s just pack it in. Go home and watch some goddamn TV. We’re never gonna be anything anyway.

**KATHY** (Voice strained, barely containing her anger) 
Can you all just shut the fuck up for five goddamn seconds?! We’re so close!

**GILLEY (V.O.)** 
Close? We were close to killing each other. That’s what we were close to.

The band tries to start the song again, but the tension is too thick. They stumble through the first few bars before **GILLEY** explodes again.

**GILLEY** (Roaring) 
You’re dragging, Evans! You’re always fucking dragging! You play like a goddamn snail!

**JEREMY** (His voice trembling with rage) 
At least I can actually play, **GILLEY**! You can barely string two chords together without sounding like a goddamn train wreck!

**JEFF** (Turning on **KATHY**, his voice dripping with venom) 
And you… you’re just… there. You’re like a goddamn ghost. You don't even play the right notes, and you look like you’d rather be anywhere else.

**JIM** (Joining in, his voice surprisingly harsh) 
Yeah, **KATHY**. You’re just dead weight. You’re the reason we sound like a goddamn garage band.

**KATHY**’s face crumples. She’s fighting back tears, but her voice is shaking with fury.

**KATHY** (Her voice cracking) 
At least I’m not a talentless, egotistical, insecure…

She can’t finish the sentence. The words catch in her throat.

**JEFF** (Spitting the words out like poison) 
A what, **KATHY**? A cunt? Is that what you were gonna say? Because that’s what you are.

**(VISUAL):** Extreme close-up on **KATHY**’s face, a single tear rolling down her cheek. The camera then quickly cuts to **JEFF**’s face, his expression a mixture of anger and regret.

**KATHY** (Screaming) 
You know what? Fine! I fucking quit!

She grabs her guitar case, slams it against the workbench, and storms out of the garage, leaving the door wide open.  The remaining band members stand in stunned silence, the air thick with tension and regret.

**GILLEY** (Shaking his head, his voice flat) 
You guys are worse than a bunch of goddamn animals.

**MR**. **GILLEY**, who has been standing in the shadows of the garage, his face etched with disappointment, slowly shakes his head. He then turns and walks into the house, but this time, he doesn't disappear. He stops at the doorway, looks back at the band, and then disappears into the house.
