**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – EARLY AFTERNOON**

The garage is bathed in golden summer light filtering through dusty windows. Gear is set up. Amps hum. No one's playing yet. The energy is oddly still, like the room is waiting for something.

**JEFF** stands near his bass, holding it but not playing. He keeps adjusting the strap even though it’s fine. His fingers twitch like they want to tune something but don’t know what.

**KATHY** walks in. She’s got on black jeans, a faded band shirt tied to the waist, and a cigarette behind her ear. No guitar yet — just watching. She pauses, clocking **JEFF**’s energy instantly.

**KATHY** (softly, almost amused)

You look like you just disarmed a bomb with the wrong wire.

**JEFF** (startled)

What? No—I mean. Yeah. Maybe.

(beat)

I was… just thinking. You know, getting into the headspace for practice.

**KATHY** (slow nod)

Sure. Headspace.

She walks past him casually, giving him a wide berth. Not cold — just careful. **JEFF** stares at the floor like it owes him a refund.

**JEFF** (stammering)

**KATHY**, can I—uh, can I talk to you? Just for a minute?

She turns, surprised. She gives a tiny nod, sets her jacket on an amp.

**KATHY**

Alright. I’m listening.

**JEFF** (exhaling)

Okay. Okay. So. Look. I know I’ve been acting like… weird. Around you. Or not around you. Or just—generally weird.

**KATHY**

You’re a guy in a garage band who alphabetizes his vinyl collection. I expected something weird.

(beat)

But yeah. I noticed.

**JEFF**

I’ve tried to, like… ignore it. Get past it. Just play music and pretend that I don’t, um… notice you. Not that I notice-notice you like—

**KATHY** (interrupting gently)

**JEFF**?

He freezes.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**

Just say what you actually mean. You don’t need a decoder ring.

**JEFF** (quietly)

I like you.

(beat)

I’ve liked you for months. And I’ve done everything but say it. Because every time I try, I get… scared. Like if I say it out loud, it’ll ruin whatever this is. Or that you’ll laugh. Or worse… say yes, and then I won’t know what the hell to do next.

**KATHY** takes this in. No sarcasm. No smile. She steps closer, arms crossed, her expression soft but unreadable.

**KATHY**

**JEFF**… I like you too. You know that, right?

**JEFF**

(surprised)

No. No, I didn’t. I—I thought maybe you just… tolerated me.

**KATHY**

I don’t undress in front of people I simply tolerate.

(beat)

I’ve wanted this too. I just didn’t wanna chase you like a deer across a freeway. I figured if you wanted me, you’d eventually stop running.

**JEFF** laughs nervously. Rubs the back of his neck.

**JEFF**

I jerked off this morning.

**KATHY** (chokes a laugh)

Jesus, **JEFF**.

**JEFF**

No, I mean—I did it to try and not feel this way. To take the edge off so I could talk to you like a person and not some lovesick raccoon who forgot how to use words. And it didn’t work. At all. I still feel like my brain’s on fire every time you walk into the room.

**KATHY** (smiling softly)

You could’ve just said hi.

(beat)

Or kissed me six weeks ago when we were in your car, and you stared at my mouth for five straight minutes like it had the answers to the SATs.

**JEFF**

I wanted to.

**KATHY**

So did I.

They stare at each other for a long, charged Moment. It's not romantic — it’s honest. Messy.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**

Look, I’m not here to drag you. I’m not here to fix you. But I’m not waiting forever, either.

**JEFF** (softly)

What do you want?

She steps in close — not touching, but close enough to feel her warmth. She smells like soap and ashtray and something faintly floral.

**KATHY**

I want to be in your day. I want you to talk to me like this again. I want you to stop being afraid of me.

(beat)

And yeah, eventually? I wanna fuck. Not because you owe me or because I’m bored or to cross something off your to-do list. I want it because I want you. All of you. Even the awkward, overthinking parts.

She lets that land. Then gives him a soft tap on the chest.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**

But only if you want it too.

She grabs her guitar from the wall and slings it over her shoulder.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**

Now. Let’s play. We’ve got noise to make.

She walks past him, plugging in without waiting for his response.

**JEFF (V.O.)**

She didn’t just walk into the room. She carved a door in me and strolled through it like she owned the goddamn place.

He turns toward his bass. His hands shake, just a little.

He smiles.

**EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY –** MOMENT**S LATER**

The distinct sputter-choke-growl of **JIM**’s battered yellow Toyota Celica rolls up like a dying lawn mower with ambition. The suspension squeaks in protest as he pulls to a stop, half on the driveway, half in the yard.

**SOUND:** A faint thud from the trunk.

**INT. TOYOTA CELICA – CONTINUOUS**

**JIM** leans forward over the steering wheel, squinting through the cracked windshield like it’s trying to lie to him.

**JIM** (to himself)

You hold together five more minutes, you rusted-out bastard. Then I’ll give you a drink of actual oil.

He shuts off the engine. It shudders once. Twice. Then dies with a final wheeze.

**EXT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

Inside, **KATHY** is tuning her guitar. **JEFF**’s still standing near his amp, eyes following her, trying not to look like he’s doing it.

The garage quiet is broken by:

**JIM (O.S.)**

HEY! Somebody with unbroken vertebrae help me out here!

**JEFF** blinks like he’s just returned from another dimension.

**KATHY** (grinning)

Guess you’re needed, Romeo.

**JEFF** exhales and heads outside.

**EXT. DRIVEWAY –** MOMENT**S LATER**

**JIM**’s standing at the open trunk of the Celica. Inside: a massive, gleaming new kick drum, still half-wrapped in cardboard, surrounded by piles of cracked cymbal stands, fast food bags, and a full quart of Quaker State.

**JIM**

Ta-da. Fresh from the pawn shop. Traded in three snare rims and a soul fragment. Worth it.

**JEFF**

That thing's huge.

**JIM**

It’s a 24-inch bass cannon. It doesn’t thump, it declares war.

**KATHY (O.S.)**

Need one more helper?

She strolls up, cigarette now lit, resting it on the side of her mouth like a jazz assassin.

**JIM**

Bless you. Both of you. **GILLEY** won’t lift a finger unless I promise him free beer or sexual favors. Sometimes both.

They lift the kick drum out together. It’s awkward, bulky, and heavy — **JEFF** ends up carrying more than he expected, and **JIM** is definitely not carrying his share.

**JEFF**

You know this is going to shake the whole garage, right?

**JIM**

That’s the point. I want Mr. **GILLEY** to feel it in his fillings.

**KATHY**

He’ll say nothing. But he’ll glare. He’s good at that.

They shuffle toward the garage, backs hunched under the awkward weight. The kick drum bumps **JEFF** in the crotch. He winces.

**JIM**

Careful. That’s where the magic happens.

**JEFF**

Not lately.

**KATHY** catches that. Her eyes flick toward him — brief, unreadable.

They reach the garage and set the drum down with a THUD.

**JIM** (stretching)

Alright! Let’s make noise. Let’s make God cry.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE –** MOMENT**S LATER**

The new kick drum is now front and center. **JEFF** tightens the last clamp, **JIM** adjusts a cymbal, and **KATHY** flicks her cigarette out the open garage door, then picks up a broom and starts sweeping.

They move in sync, casual but efficient — clearly familiar with the routine of setting up and cleaning this shared sacred ground.

**JIM**

(grunting, wiping sweat)

I gotta say it again: **GILLEY**’s old man’s a goddamn saint, **JEFF**.

**KATHY**

No kidding. Anybody else would’ve kicked us out after the first broken lightbulb and second noise complaint.

**JEFF**

Mr. **GILLEY** says he doesn't hear it.

(beat)

I don’t believe him, but he says it.

**JIM**

Nah, he hears it. He just doesn't give a shit. That’s the difference. Man’s got a Zen monk’s tolerance.

**KATHY**

This garage? This is a fucking golden ticket. Most people have to beg for rehearsal space. Pay by the hour. Haul gear into basements that smell like mildew and cat piss.

She sweeps around the kick drum like she’s protecting it.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**

We get to leave our stuff set up. Play whenever. Volume at eleven. All for the price of… what, sweeping out beer cans and old motor oil every night?

**JEFF**

And making sure **BILL** doesn’t lean his synth on the paint cans again.

**JIM**

Hell of a deal.

They pause for a Moment. The garage hums with quiet — not awkward, just settled. A band-sized inhale.

**KATHY** (softly)

We’re lucky.

**JIM**

Yeah. We really are.

**JEFF**

It’s easy to forget. But yeah.

They exchange a rare three-way look of agreement — not dramatic, not cheesy, just true. These are kids who don’t have much, but they have this.

**SOUND:** Outside, a lawnmower drones. Inside, a tuning fork rings as **KATHY** strikes it.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**

Let’s not screw it up.

**JIM**

Too late for that. But we’ll make it sound cool.

They laugh, and the sound bounces off the garage walls like music waiting to be born.

**EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – MINUTES LATER**

The faint rumble of **BILL** Davenport’s Honda Prelude cuts through the fall air — the kind of rumble that says, I taped a Whitesnake cassette over my dad’s Frank Sinatra tape and I regret nothing.

He parks crooked, as always. Steps out in tight jeans, boots, and a leather jacket that screams synthwave samurai. Slung over his shoulder: his flight case full of custom synth patches and ego.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** is mid-scale run. **JEFF** is checking the tuning. **JIM** is tightening his new kick drum’s pedal. The garage has found its rhythm again.

Davenport walks in like a man with a mission. He sets his synth down with care — the kind a priest gives communion wafers.

**DAVENPORT**

Alright. Before we start? I need five minutes. Band meeting. Just us.

Everyone exchanges a glance. **JEFF** raises an eyebrow.

**JEFF**

Okay…

**KATHY**

Uh-oh. Someone’s got opinions.

**JIM**

Bet he wrote a manifesto in the car again.

**DAVENPORT** (grinning, but dead serious)

Shut up, all of you. I’m serious.

(beat)

Look—Seattle’s cool. I get it. The flannel, the fuzz, the angst. It’s loud, it’s raw, it’s sexy in that I-haven’t-showered-since-February way. But if I hear one more band say they’re the next Nirvana, I’m gonna dropkick someone into a stack of milk crates.

**JEFF**

So… you’re not into grunge?

**DAVENPORT**

I’m not into cloning. That’s the point.

(beat)

Everyone’s gonna chase that sound. Labels are gonna eat it up. It’s gonna be a race to the bottom of a muddy distortion pedal.

**KATHY**

You want us to be different.

**DAVENPORT**

I want us to be us.

(steps closer, lowering his voice)

I’ve been listening to our demos. There’s something there when we lean into the synths. Something sharp. Cold. Cinematic. Like… if Depeche Mode had a chainsaw.

**JIM**

That’s… oddly vivid.

**DAVENPORT**

We don’t have to abandon the grit. I’m not saying stop dressing like we’re from Miami Vice. But the sound—the textures? This shit can cut deeper than another blown-out Marshall stack ever will.

(beat)

And yeah, I’ll say it. I’m the best musician in the fuckin’ band. I’ve been playing since I was eleven. I can layer arpeggios, patch MIDI by ear, and I know what the hell LFO means without having to look it up.

Silence. Not hostile. Just honest.

**KATHY**

(smiling, slow clap)

Well, damn. The kid showed up with balls and a synthesizer.

**JEFF**

You’re not wrong. You’re just… loud.

**DAVENPORT**

We’ve got a shot to do something that’s not just derivative. We don’t need to be Seattle’s little brother. We can be Bethel Township’s weird-ass, synth-driven, guitar-snarling, pissed-off answer to the whole scene.

**JIM**

With a better kick drum.

**DAVENPORT** (with a grin)

Exactly.

**JEFF (V.O.)**

He was arrogant. But he wasn’t wrong. There was something about the way his synth lines crawled under the guitars like wires under skin. It made the songs feel… electric. Alien. Ours.

They all pause, looking at one another. Something’s shifted.

**KATHY**

Alright, Davenport. You’ve got your five minutes.

(beat)

Now plug in. Let’s make some noise that doesn’t sound like anything else.

**EXT. GILLEY’S BACK DOOR – SECONDS LATER**

The screen door creaks open with the haunted rasp of a thousand late-night exits.

**JEREMY GILLEY** steps out like he’s just walked off the set of Miami Vice—if Don Johnson lived in Ohio, smoked menthols, and forgot shoes were a thing.

He’s wearing a white linen blazer over a hot pink tank top, with acid-washed jeans cuffed at the ankles. He’s completely barefoot. A cigarette hangs from his lip at an impossible angle, like gravity knows not to mess with him.

**SOUND:** A dog barks two houses down. **GILLEY** doesn’t blink.

**GILLEY** (squinting toward the garage)

What’s all this? Band meeting or political rally?

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

Everyone looks toward the open garage door like an incoming storm just said something sarcastic.

**DAVENPORT**

Speak of the devil. And he’s wearing linen!

**KATHY**

Goddamn, **GILLEY**. You look like you just lost a cocaine shipment off the coast of Key West.

**GILLEY** (strolling in, unbothered)

It’s called style, children. Try to keep up.

He flicks his cigarette into an empty beer can with disturbing precision, then kicks the doorstop into place with his heel.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)** (to **JEFF**)

My old man’s got the water heater goin’. Feels like a goddamn steam room in there.

(beat)

Perfect weather for art.

**JIM**

You mean “perfect weather for trench foot.”

**JEFF**

Or heat stroke.

**GILLEY** walks through the room like a rock star surveying the wreckage of a hotel room he technically rented. He taps the new kick drum with his toe.

**GILLEY**

Damn. That thing thumps. **JIM**, you finally buy a drum that doesn’t look like it escaped a dumpster?

**JIM**

Don’t get used to it. It’s not paid off yet.

**GILLEY** (smiling)

Credit is punk rock, baby.

He finally stops at the center of the room, striking a pose like he’s waiting for someone to cue his entrance music.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**

So? Are we grunge now? Synthwave? Ska? Don’t tell me we’re going folk.

**DAVENPORT**

We’re working on not sounding like everyone else.

**GILLEY** (spreads arms)

Then let’s start by sounding like us. Less talking, more distortion.

He grabs a mic stand and spins it once, casually.

**KATHY (V.O.)**

He was barefoot. Smoking. Dressed like a nightclub bouncer from a rejected Magnum P.I. reboot.

(beat)

And he was still the goddamn front man. God, why’d I get wet?

**EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – LATE AFTERNOON**

The air is thick. The sun is still blinding even though it's low, like it’s refusing to go down easy.

A dusty tan Dodge Aries pulls up slowly and sighs to a stop. The door opens. **JEREMY** Evans climbs out like every muscle has a separate vendetta against him.

He’s in a sweat-darkened T-shirt that probably started gray and cargo shorts that used to have structure. His buzzcut is plastered to his scalp, and there's a smear of dried something across his arm — probably beer, probably not his.

He carries a guitar case in one hand and the thousand-yard stare of a man who’s seen the ass end of a beer truck at 4 a.m.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY**’s adjusting pedals. **JEFF** is fidgeting with his tuning. Davenport is eyeing his synth like it offended him. **JIM**’s tapping his kick drum like it’s a lie detector.

Then the door creaks open.

**JEREMY EVANS** enters, slow, dragging, like gravity's pulling extra on just him today.

**JIM**

Evans. You look like a man who regrets every life choice that led to this Moment.

**JEREMY** (gravel dry)

Started loading trucks for my dad at four this morning.

He sets the guitar case down, gently, like it’s made of glass and his will to live is not.

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**

That warehouse is a hundred and ten degrees. The trucks are hotter. The kegs sweat. And when the kegs sweat, they slip.

(beat)

I nearly decapitated myself with a case of Miller High Life.

**DAVENPORT**

Jesus.

**KATHY**

That sounds like a Final Destination death. Ohio edition.

**JEFF**

You okay?

**JEREMY**

Yeah. Just… not.

(beat)

But I’m here. Let’s make some fucking noise before I forget how to feel things.

**SOUND:** The air hums again — a collective shift. Everyone sees it: **JEREMY’s** cooked. His eyes are bloodshot. His shirt’s half untucked. His hands are raw. But he showed up.

**KATHY** (quietly, sincerely)

Respect.

**JIM**

You’re a goddamn soldier, Evans.

**DAVENPORT**

And here I was about to whine about my synth cable being tangled.

**JEREMY** lets out a breath. Not a laugh — something closer to a long exhale of shared misery.

He plugs in his guitar. No preamble. No warm-up. Just a slow, deep power chord.

It rings out, ragged and perfect.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**

I didn’t know if I could still move my fingers. I just knew I had to. Music was the only thing I had left that didn’t ask for a punch card or steel-toed boots.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – LATE AFTERNOON**

The room is filled with the low drone of warming amps. Everyone’s tweaking knobs, shifting straps, adjusting mics.

**GILLEY**, shirtless again — somehow both sweat-slick and smug — strolls over to **KATHY**, who’s adjusting the knobs on her battered distortion pedal. She doesn’t look up. Not at first.

He leans in just enough to hover in her space, a little too close, like he’s always almost going to kiss someone but never quite does.

**GILLEY**

You know, if you keep glaring at that pedal like that, it might start behaving out of fear.

**KATHY** (still focused)

If only that worked on people.

**GILLEY** (smile creeping in)

You talking about me?

She doesn’t look up. But the corner of her mouth twitches — a smile that isn’t quite a smile.

**KATHY**

If the boot fits, **GILLEY**.

**GILLEY**

Boot fits just fine. I’m more curious if you’d like to try walking in ‘em again.

**KATHY** (finally looking up)

That was a long walk. And I remember the blisters.

Their eyes lock for a beat too long.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**

I’m not really in the market for reruns.

**GILLEY** (shrugging, cocky)

Nah, this wouldn’t be a rerun. This would be the remastered edition.

**KATHY** (smiling now)

Uh-huh. Dolby surround and everything?

**GILLEY**

Only the best.

She chuckles — involuntary. It’s quick, it’s soft, but it’s genuine.

**KATHY**

I’ve got riffs to write, **GILLEY**. Not time to babysit your libido.

She bends to adjust her amp, hair falling forward to hide her face. But she’s still smiling. He knows it. He watches her for a beat, still smiling, then strolls off like a man who’s planted a flag.

**ACROSS THE ROOM**

**JEFF** saw all of it.

He’s half-hunched behind his bass, pretending to adjust his tone knob that he’s already fixed twice. His face is neutral — too neutral. His jaw clenches once.

**JEFF (V.O.)**

It didn’t mean anything. Probably. Just… old sparks. Whatever.

(beat)

But she smiled. She doesn’t smile like that at me.

He glances up. **KATHY** catches it — just barely — and quickly looks away.

The tension’s back. Not loud. Not spoken. But loud as hell all the same.

**JIM**

Alright. Can we play before we all start fucking each other again?

**DAVENPORT**

Don’t threaten me with a good time.

Everyone laughs — the air cracks just enough to let some levity in. But it doesn’t erase what just happened.

Not even close.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – EARLY EVENING**

The band’s just taken a break. The garage is thick with the smell of sweat, dust, and stale amp heat. **KATHY** and **JIM** have stepped outside to smoke. **GILLEY**’s off somewhere ranting about setlists to nobody in particular.

**JEFF** is alone at the back of the garage, sitting on a milk crate, plucking his bass strings like they’re a stress ball. He’s staring at the concrete floor like it might give him advice.

**BILL** walks over, wipes his hands with a bandana, then sits down across from him. No warning.

**BILL**

You always do this.

**JEFF**

Do what?

**BILL**

This. The… brooding, the staring, the emotionally constipated bass-player-in-a-high-school-movie routine.

(beat)

Man, are you just messed up in the head, or what?

**JEFF** blinks, startled.

**JEFF**

What the hell, **BILL**?

**BILL**

I mean it. Are you, like, missing a card in the deck? Was your “connect to people” gene left on the assembly line?

(beat)

**KATHY** wants to fuck you, man.

**JEFF** freezes. His fingers stop moving on the bass entirely.

**BILL (CONT’D)**

She’s not even being subtle. And that’s saying something because **KATHY** doesn’t throw that energy around lightly. You know it, I know it, **GILLEY** knows it. Hell, probably Mr. **GILLEY** knows it.

**JEFF** (lowering his voice)

Jesus, keep your voice down.

**BILL**

Why? Afraid she’ll hear the truth?

(beat)

Look, I get it. You’re smart. You live in your own head. You want everything to be logical. You want to understand your own feelings before you risk expressing them.

**JEFF**

It’s not that simple.

**BILL**

It is. You’re scared. So instead of stepping up, you’re stewing. Boiling in your own head like you’re gonna solve the equation of “do I like her” before she loses interest.

(beat)

Spoiler alert? She already knows you like her. She’s just waiting for you to get your head out of your ass and confirm it.

**JEFF**

I don’t want to screw it up.

**BILL**

You already are. By doing nothing.

(beat)

What are you waiting for, **JEFF**? Permission? An engraved invitation? Or do you just like feeling miserable?

**JEFF** doesn’t answer. He looks down at the floor again, jaw tight.

**BILL** (softening just slightly)

You’re not broken, man. But damn if you aren’t making this harder than it has to be.

**BILL** stands up, dusts off his hands, and walks away — leaving **JEFF** alone with his silence.

**JEFF (V.O.)**

It was easier when people thought I was just weird. At least that gave me cover.

(beat)

But he wasn’t wrong.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF** is still sitting on the crate, eyes on the floor, the sting of **BILL**’s words still echoing in the garage air.

**BILL** walks away — but only gets a few steps before a voice cuts through the room like a blade.

**JEREMY EVANS (O.S.)**

The hell did you just say to my brother?

Everyone turns. **JEREMY’s** in the doorway, arms crossed, drenched in post-labor grime, guitar strap still over his shoulder. His face is red — not from heat this time, but anger.

**BILL** (defensive, arms up)

I was just telling him what everyone’s thinking.

**JEREMY**

Don’t.

(steps forward, voice low but ice-cold)

Don’t ever come at **JEFF** like that again.

**BILL**

Come on, man. I’m not trying to start anything. I’m just saying he’s gotta quit stewing and actually do something about—

**JEREMY** (stepping between them)

I said don’t.

(beat)

You don’t get it, and you sure as hell don’t get to talk about him like he’s broken. He’s not.

(beat)

He was born this way. He just… processes things differently. He doesn’t show shit like you do. Doesn’t mean he doesn’t feel it. Doesn’t mean he’s defective.

**BILL**

I never said he was—

**JEREMY** (voice rising now)

But you meant it. You implied it.

(beat)

He’s the smartest goddamn person I know. He’s got more empathy in his pinky finger than half the guys in this school. He doesn’t talk fast. He doesn’t flirt well. But he gives a shit in a way you don’t even understand.

(beat)

So yeah. You will respect him.

(stepping in, now face-to-face with **BILL**)

Or I’ll kick your fuckin’ ass.

**SILENCE**.

The air is sharp. Heavy. **BILL**’s posture stiffens. He’s not afraid, but he’s stunned. For a second, everyone just stops.

Then—

**JEFF** (quietly)

Jer.

**JEREMY** glances back. **JEFF**’s still sitting, his face flushed, somewhere between embarrassed and moved.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**

It’s okay. He’s not wrong. Not all the way.

**JEREMY**

He’s still outta line.

**JEFF**

Maybe. But he’s not wrong.

**BILL** exhales and slowly nods. Not backing down. Just… backing off.

**BILL**

Okay. Fair.

(beat)

But you got people who care about you, **JEFF**. Don’t forget that.

He walks away this time for real — toward the synth, toward noise, toward the safe haven of sound.

**JEREMY** stays where he is, watching him go.

Then looks back to **JEFF**.

**JEREMY**

(softer now)

Don’t let him get in your head.

(beat)

You’re not broken. You’re just… you.

He pats his brother’s shoulder once, then moves off to tune up, like nothing happened.

**JEFF (V.O.)**

I wanted to say something. Anything. But the words never came out right.

(beat)

So I picked up my bass. And I let it talk for me.

**EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – LATE EVENING**

The sun is finally dipping behind the trees. The heat has broken, but the air still clings like guilt.

**JEFF** stands outside the garage, fidgeting with his pick in one hand, the other resting on the hood of his faded blue Ford Escort — the kind of car that’s earned every dent.

He takes a breath. Pops the hatch. Digs under a pile of crumpled notebook paper, cables, and an old denim jacket.

**JEFF** stands at the back of his beat-up Ford Escort, hatch open, rooting around like he’s not sure what he’s looking for — until he finds it:

A CD. Still new. Still sealed.

"Uptown Avondale – The Afghan Whigs."

He holds it gently, like it’s made of glass and implication.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

She gave it to me a week ago. Said, “You might like this. They're from Cincy. They’re doing something interesting.”

(beat)

I listened once. Then hid it under a mess of receipts and cables. Like I wasn’t ready to hear it yet.

(beat)

Guess I am now.

He shuts the hatch and heads for the garage.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE –** MOMENT**S LATER**

The air’s thick with the drone of idle amps. **KATHY**’s perched on an amp sipping warm Coke. **JIM** is tapping out quiet rhythms with the tips of his sticks. **BILL** is hunched over his synth, fiddling with settings like he’s cracking a safe.

**JEFF** walks up to him — no preamble, no apology. Just holds out the CD.

**JEFF**

Thought you might want to hear this.

**BILL**

(skeptical)

What is it?

**JEFF**

Uptown Avondale. Afghan Whigs. Brand new. Cincy guys.

(beat)

**KATHY** gave it to me. Said it was doing something different. Soul meets post-punk. Dirty grooves. Real emotion.

(beat)

Not Seattle. Not synth-pop. Something… in between.

**BILL** takes it, flips it in his hands.

**BILL**

You finally listened?

**JEFF**

Today. After everything.

(beat)

Thought maybe… it was worth sharing.

**BILL**

You trying to bury the hatchet?

**JEFF**

I’m trying to hand you something I didn’t write.

(beat)

See what we can learn from it.

(beat)

That’s what you wanted, right? Not to clone anything. To be us.

**BILL** nods slowly. Peels off the plastic wrap with his thumbnail.

**BILL**

You bringin’ this to me now because you want to talk music? Or because your brother nearly punched me into next week?

**JEFF**

Bit of column A. Bit of **JEREMY** Rage.

**KATHY**

(sipping her Coke, casual)

Still think it’s a great CD.

**JEFF** glances at her — not long. Just enough.

**BILL** crosses the garage and pops the CD into a battered boom box.

SOUND: “Band of Gold” begins — dark, slow, soulful. The kind of track that simmers before it burns.

The garage goes quiet. Everyone listens.

Even **GILLEY**, half-muttering lyrics to himself, stops and cocks an eyebrow.

**KATHY**

(softly)

Told you it had teeth.

**BILL**

Yeah. This isn’t grunge. This is… something else.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

It wasn’t just music. It was a bridge. From her to me. From me to **BILL**. From this garage to somewhere bigger than Bethel Township.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS

SOUND: The last soft, echoing groove of “Band of Gold” fades out, leaving nothing but the hum of amps and the stunned silence of five people trying to process what the hell they just heard.

No one moves.

**JIM** stands near the kit, mouth slightly open, like he’s staring at a ghost that told him a secret.

He slowly sets his drumsticks down on the snare like they’re holy relics.

**JIM**

Holy shit.

(beat)

That wasn’t music.

(beat)

That was the voice of God.

SILENCE. Nobody laughs. Nobody rolls their eyes. Because they feel it, too.

**DAVENPORT**

Okay, yeah. That was serious.

**KATHY**

Welcome to what I’ve been trying to tell you for a week.

**JEFF** looks at her — not directly, but enough. She doesn’t look back, just smiles into her Coke can like she knew.

Then, from the corner, wiping sweat from his brow with the hem of his shirt, **JEREMY** Evans speaks.

**JEREMY EVANS**

(plain, no hesitation)

I’d take **JEREMY** **GILLEY** five times a week and twice on Sunday if he ever sang like that.

Everyone turns.

**GILLEY**, who’s been stretching his shoulders and humming some off-key half-song, freezes mid-movement.

**GILLEY**

Wait, what?

**JIM**

(choking on laughter)

Oh my God—

**DAVENPORT**

Get in line, bro. He’s got backup singers now.

**KATHY**

**GILLEY**, that voice you just heard? That’s what you think you sound like when you’ve had three beers and start quoting Bowie.

**GILLEY**

I do sound like that after three beers.

**JEREMY EVANS**

You sound like a guy choking on a harmonica.

Laughter explodes in the room, loud and unfiltered. The ice is broken. The spell has lifted, but the effect lingers.

**JEFF (V.O.)**

For once, nobody was talking about the future. Or the past. Or who liked who.

(beat)

We were just six idiots in a garage, hearing something we weren’t sure we deserved.

**INT. BEER WAREHOUSE – NOON**

The inside of the warehouse feels like a kiln. Dust floats through the shafts of light like it’s too tired to settle.

**JEREMY** EVANS is mid-lift, hoisting a keg onto a wooden pallet with the limp strength of a man who’s been doing this since sunrise. His shirt clings to him like regret. His palms are raw. His shoulders ache.

Across the floor, standing beside a clipboard and a half-wrecked forklift, is **MR. EVANS** — late fifties, beer-gut functional, voice like gravel in a steel coffee mug. He's not watching **JEREMY** closely — just enough to make sure the work keeps moving.

**MR. EVANS**

You scrub the men’s bathroom today?

**JEREMY**

Not yet.

(beat)

Why, something explode in there?

**MR. EVANS**

Might’ve. Or someone died in it. Hard to say. But if you get in there after this shift — really get in there, knees-on-the-tile kind of job — I might be able to scrounge something up for you.

**JEREMY** pauses, arm draped over a keg.

**JEREMY**

What kind of “something”?

**MR. EVANS**

Tickets.

(beat)

Four of ‘em. Bogart’s. Week and a half from now.

**JEREMY** squints. This could be a trap. Or it could be real.

**JEREMY**

Who’s playing?

His dad flips through a sheet tacked to a clipboard, squints at something written in chicken-scratch handwriting.

**MR. EVANS**

That band your brother was talking about the other day. The… uh. Afghanistan Whigs?

**JEREMY**

Afghan Whigs.

**MR. EVANS**

Yeah. Those guys. Sound like they gargle with gravel and heartbreak. Real cheerful.

**JEREMY** stands upright, sweat dripping from his chin, eyes wide now.

**JEREMY**

You’re serious?

**MR. EVANS**

I don’t joke about free tickets, boy. Especially not ones I could sell for beer money.

He tears a note off the clipboard and holds it up like a sacred text.

**MR. EVANS** **(CONT’D)**

You want ‘em? Then get in there and make that bathroom sparkle like the Vatican on Easter.

**JEREMY** grabs a rag off a nearby shelf and salutes with it, mock-military.

**JEREMY**

You got it, General.

**MR. EVANS**

Better use bleach. And don’t just light a match and hope.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

It was hot. My spine felt like rope. My soul had sunstroke.

(beat)

But four tickets to see the Afghan Whigs? That was salvation.

And more importantly, that was something I could hand to **JEFF** without saying a goddamn word.

**INT. MEN’S BATHROOM – BEER WAREHOUSE – LATE AFTERNOON**

The buzzing fluorescent light overhead flickers like it’s giving up on life.

**JEREMY** EVANS is crouched next to a rusted toilet, holding a brush that’s lost most of its bristles and a bottle of industrial-grade bleach that smells like it could burn through regret.

His knees ache. His back is damp. His soul is one flush away from detachment.

SOUND: The harsh slosh-scrub of effort, the occasional drip from a sink that’s seen better decades.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

This is the price I pay.

(beat)

Four tickets to Bogart’s. Sixty bucks worth of sweaty joy and soul-grit.

In exchange for scrubbing human wreckage off tile grout.

He leans back, breathing through his shirt, blinking the sting out of his eyes.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**   **(CONT’D)**

But it hit me, right there in the ammonia haze:

(beat)

There’s six of us.

Six people.

Four tickets.

(beat)

And I’m no math whiz, but that dog don’t hunt.

He looks around at the ruined battlefield of a bathroom — cracked urinal, graffiti carved into the mirror, ancient soap caked in the dispenser.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

I mean, could we get all six of us 55 miles down I-75 and into Bogart’s without losing a limb or a piece of our dignity?

(beat)

Actually… yeah. I think we could.

(beat)

But not with four tickets.

He stands up, stretches his back, flushes the toilet with a faintly vindictive look.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

Someone’s gotta be left out. Or someone’s gotta step up.

(beat)

So I did what any emotionally avoidant little brother would do:

I decided to pester the shit out of my dad.

INT. LOADING BAY – MOMENTS LATER

**MR. EVANS** is checking the inventory sheet, Sharpie tucked behind one ear. **JEREMY** walks up, hands still damp from the worst war zone in Ohio plumbing history.

**JEREMY**

Hey, Dad?

**MR. EVANS**

(mutters)

If you ask me for gas money, the answer’s no.

**JEREMY**

Can you get two more tickets?

(beat)

Same show. Same band. Afghan Whigs. You said four, but there’s six of us.

Mr. Evans looks up, eyes squinting.

**MR. EVANS**

Christ, what is this, a field trip?

**JEREMY**

More like group therapy. But loud.

(beat)

Come on. If we’re gonna do it, we should do it together.

Mr. Evans grunts. Glances at the paper again.

**MR. EVANS**

I’ll make a call.

(beat)

But if they say no, you’re picking who stays home. I’m not playing favorites.

**JEREMY**

Deal.

(beat)

And hey… I did the bathroom.

Mr. Evans just nods once, like that’s the bare minimum for breathing in his warehouse.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

I wasn’t sure if he’d come through.

But I knew I’d just scrubbed the floor of hell for the possibility that we could all be in the same place, at the same time, for once.

(beat)

And if that’s not worth a little bleach in the lungs, I don’t know what is.

INT. LOADING BAY – MOMENTS LATER

**JEREMY** stands, still catching his breath from Toilet Duty Apocalypse. His dad is finishing a note on a clipboard, scribbling with the same Sharpie he’s probably used since 1983.

**MR. EVANS**

(still scribbling)

What are you getting out of it?

**JEREMY** blinks, sweat running into his eyes.

**JEREMY**

Getting out of what?

**MR. EVANS**

The tickets. You want two more. That puts me in the hole.

**JEREMY** frowns.

**JEREMY**

I thought you said you’d make a call?

**MR. EVANS**

I can. But let’s not pretend I’ve got the Pope on speed dial.

(beat)

Cincinnati’s tight. That rep down there? He traded me those four tickets in exchange for an extra Zima allocation.

(beat)

You know what kind of moral compromise that is?

**JEREMY**

(squinting)

Zima?

**MR. EVANS**

Zima.

(grim)

That’s a reputation killer. I’ve spent decades in this industry building up a reputation as a man who doesn’t traffic in clear malt beverages.

(beat)

Then some rep comes crawling with Whigs tickets and desperation, and what do I do?

(beat)

I give him Zima. I barter with the enemy. And now you want me to crawl back for two more?

**JEREMY**

I didn’t realize this was international diplomacy.

**MR. EVANS**

It’s beer, son. Everything’s international diplomacy.

He clicks the Sharpie shut with one hand. Looks **JEREMY** over.

**MR. EVANS** **(CONT’D)**

Dayton Air Show’s coming up.

**JEREMY** groans. Not just with his voice — with his whole body.

**JEREMY**

No. Come on.

**MR. EVANS**

You want two more tickets? You’re gonna give me a crew.

**JEREMY**

A crew?

**MR. EVANS**

For the flight line chalets. VIPs, vendors, military brass with no tolerance for warm beer.

(beat)

We’re talking kegs, hauling, sweating, security wristbands, maybe a golf cart if you don’t screw it up.

**JEREMY**

(sighing)

So you’re telling me this is a ticket-for-keg labor arrangement?

**MR. EVANS**

It’s called quid pro quo. Look it up. And bring a friend who can lift with his legs.

**JEREMY** leans back against a pallet, wipes his hands on his jeans, and stares up at the flickering warehouse lights.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

There’s always a price.

(beat)

But maybe… this time, it’s worth it.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – LATE AFTERNOON

The amps hum lazily. The vibe is low-energy. Practice hasn’t really started — **KATHY**’s noodling through scales, **GILLEY**’s on his back smoking a cigarette through a box fan, **JIM**’s doing rudimentary stick rolls on the snare rim like his brain is elsewhere, and **BILL** is tweaking a synth filter with increasing frustration.

**JEFF** sits off to the side, head low, tuning his bass with methodical boredom.

Then the garage door creaks open hard.

**JEREMY** EVANS strides in, sweat-dried and amped up, waving a folded paper in one hand like it’s a golden ticket. Which, technically, it is.

**JEREMY**

Alright, shut up and listen. I got news.

(holds it up)

Four tickets. Afghan Whigs. Bogart’s. Week and a half from now.

Immediate reactions:

**KATHY**

Hell yes.

**GILLEY**

That’s what I’m talkin’ about.

**BILL**

Finally. Culture.

**JIM**

Do they serve drinks there? Real ones?

**JEREMY** holds up a finger.

**JEREMY**

Bad news: we’ve only got four. For now.

**GILLEY**

What, they run outta bands?

**JEREMY**

Cincy rep only coughed up four in exchange for my dad throwing his soul into a crate of Zima. He’s trying to pull two more out of Dayton, but… there’s a catch.

The garage goes still.

**KATHY**

Always a catch.

**JEREMY**

He needs help at the Dayton Air Show next week. Keg runs. VIP chalets. Hotter than hell and you will smell like Coors for three days.

(beat)

So if I’m gonna try to get those other two tickets… I need a volunteer.

**JIM**

(laughs darkly)

Oh god. I’ve done that gig. You haven’t lived until you’re dragging a keg through a sea of sweaty dads screaming at fighter jets.

**GILLEY**

I went two years ago. My feet got heat blisters through my shoes.

**JEREMY**

I never said it was a good gig.

He looks to **JEFF**, hopeful.

**JEREMY** **(CONT’D)**

**JEFF**?

**JEFF** shakes his head slowly, eyes still on his bass.

**JEFF**

Can’t. I’ve got surgery next week.

**JIM**

Surgery?

**JEFF**

Tympanoplasty.

(looks up)

I’m getting a new eardrum.

**KATHY**

You’re just now telling us this?

**JEFF**

Didn’t think it mattered.

(beat)

Had hearing damage from when I was a kid. Getting it fixed.

The room goes quiet. Nobody quite knows what to say.

**BILL**

Well… that’s terrifying and weirdly impressive.

**GILLEY**

Do they put a new one in with, like… tweezers?

**JEFF**

Laser and scalpel. Local anesthesia. Very punk rock.

**JEREMY** looks at his brother for a beat — no sarcasm, no comment — then back to the group.

**JEREMY**

Alright. So **JEFF**’s out. That leaves **GILLEY**, **JIM**, **BILL**… **KATHY**?

**KATHY**

I’ll do it if the other option is someone crying because they didn’t make it in.

**JIM**

You realize this means we’re working the Air Show. Like, actually working.

**GILLEY**

Guess we better start hydrating now.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

One ticket costs sweat. The other costs hearing. Somehow that felt fair.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS

The air is charged now. **JEREMY** has barely finished his pitch and already the room has turned into a garage courtroom, where tickets are currency, and sweat is the tax.

**KATHY**

Alright, let’s get this over with: who’s gonna be a soldier of light and lager?

**JIM**

Look, I’ve done the Air Show. Twice. That should automatically qualify me for some kind of medical exemption.

**GILLEY**

And I went the year it hit 103 degrees. I came back with sun poisoning and a concussion from a folding chair.

**BILL**

I’ve never gone. Which means I should be protected under the Endangered Species Act.

**KATHY**

You’re not a species, you’re a synth player. No one’s ever endangered you.

**JEREMY**

Y’all need to realize one thing: my dad don’t care about your traumas. He cares about biceps and a willingness to push heavy things in direct sun.

**JEFF**

(still tuning his bass, low-key)

Should we draw straws?

**JIM**

We’d need actual straws for that. And a system that doesn’t immediately devolve into violence.

**GILLEY**

Okay. Real talk. Who deserves to go to this show?

**BILL**

Deserves? I introduced half of you to this band!

**KATHY**

That’s true. But I gave **JEFF** the CD.

**JEREMY**

And I got the tickets in the first place.

**GILLEY**

And I’m the front man, so technically if one of us gets famous off this night, it’s probably gonna be me.

**KATHY**

You wish.

**JIM**

Can’t we just sell a kidney and buy two more?

**JEFF**

We’re too broke for black market organ trafficking.

**BILL**

Then we settle this the way the gods intended.

(beat)

Battle of the Bands. Air Show Edition.

**JEREMY**

No. Absolutely not. That is the dumbest—

**GILLEY**

No, no, hold on. I like where he’s going.

**KATHY**

We are not turning sweat labor into a tournament.

**JIM**

We are broke, though. Like, dangerously broke.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

We weren’t debating about tickets.

We were debating who’d pay the price for keeping this band alive.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – MINUTES LATER

The garage is now the stage for **GILLEY**’s one-man circus. He stands on an overturned milk crate like a manic emcee, shirtless again (of course), twirling a drumstick like a baton.

**GILLEY**

Alright! It’s settled. We’re doing this the only way I know how:

Merit. Pain. And poorly constructed performance metrics.

**BILL**

(sighing)

Oh Jesus Christ.

**KATHY**

Why are we letting him lead?

**JIM**

Because somehow, no one else had the energy to stop him.

**JEFF**

(softly, almost apologetically)

I’m exempt.

**GILLEY**

Yes you are, Cochlear Bionic Man. Godspeed and good luck.

(beat)

But the rest of you? You’re in the Thunderdome now.

**JEREMY**

Please tell me this doesn’t involve running.

**GILLEY**

No. It involves initiative, willpower, and an extremely questionable series of mini-challenges I made up in the back of my skull.

**KATHY**

You’ve had this planned, haven’t you?

**GILLEY**

Honestly? Since last summer. I just never had the stakes before.

(beat, grinning)

Let’s call it: **GILLEY**’s Gauntlet of Honor and Suffering.

**BILL**

I already regret this.

**GILLEY**

Great! That’s step one.

He hops off the crate, starts moving gear out of the way, creating “lanes” with cables and amp cases like a kid building an obstacle course out of garbage.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**

Event One: Speed Coil Wrapping. Fastest to wrap three twenty-foot cables without knots or tangles wins.

**JIM**

This is rigged. I’ve got drummer hands.

**KATHY**

You mean useless flippers?

**BILL**

I’m gonna wrap a coil around your neck if I lose.

**GILLEY**

That’s the spirit!

**JEREMY** leans over to **JEFF**, who’s sitting on the amp like a bemused king watching the court descend into chaos.

**JEREMY**

You know, when I woke up this morning, I really didn’t think the fate of concert tickets would come down to garage Olympics.

**JEFF**

Me either.

(beat)

But this feels… right.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Sometimes you don’t lead a band. Sometimes you survive it.

And somehow, that’s enough.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – MOMENTS LATER

The air is stifling. Sweat beads on every surface. The garage is half-cleared, transformed into a makeshift battleground, complete with improvised barriers, amp-case hurdles, and a “scoreboard” drawn in Sharpie on a pizza box.

**GILLEY** stands in the center, shirt tied around his head like a bandana, holding a broken mic stand as a scepter of authority.

**GILLEY**

Ladies and degenerates: welcome to the first and possibly last **GILLEY**'S GAUNTLET OF HONOR AND SUFFERING.

**KATHY**

You can’t even spell “gauntlet.”

**GILLEY**

I don’t need spelling. I have vision.

EVENT ONE: CABLE WRAP RACE

SOUND: **BILL**’s synth loop playing like a deranged carnival track in the background.

Each contestant stands in front of three tangled cables. **GILLEY** lifts his arms.

**GILLEY**

On my mark…

Get set…

WRANGLE!

Everyone starts.

**BILL** takes a meticulous, surgical approach — perfect loops, smooth pulls.

**KATHY** goes fast and loose, nearly snapping a cable in half.

**JIM** somehow manages to get two wrapped around his ankles and trips into a cymbal stand.

**JIM**

I’M IN HELL!

**JEREMY** cheats immediately, swapping a cable out for one already wrapped behind a speaker.

**GILLEY**

CHEATING IS ENCOURAGED BUT MUST BE CREATIVE. POINTS TO EVANS.

EVENT TWO: GUITAR STRAP LIMBO

An amp cord is stretched across the garage at chest height.

**GILLEY**

Get under it. Wearing your instrument. Backwards. While humming “Come As You Are.”

One by one they attempt it.

**KATHY** glides under like a cat burglar and smiles on the other side.

**BILL** fails halfway through, knocks over a mic stand, blames “spatial energy interference.”

**JIM** just belly-flops under and screams “I’M A STARFISH” for no reason.

**JEREMY** walks around the limbo cord.

**GILLEY**

Disqualified for cowardice! Minus one Bogart!

EVENT THREE: FREESTYLE SOLO-OFF

**GILLEY**

Alright, this one’s for humiliation. Give me 10 seconds of the most unholy solo your ego can produce.

**KATHY** plays something that sounds like a guitar crying while being seduced.

**JIM** solos on a hi-hat and a pizza box.

**BILL** uses every synth effect at once. Sirens. Choirs. Fart noises. He bows when he finishes.

**JEREMY** starts a heartfelt guitar line, messes up a note, panics, and turns it into “Smoke on the Water.”

**GILLEY**

Bonus points for the meltdown. Classic Ohio crumble. We love to see it.

EVENT FOUR: COOL-OFF STAREDOWN

Everyone has to stand in a circle, arms folded, and stare at each other without smiling, blinking, or speaking. **GILLEY** paces like a camp counselor on a power trip.

Within seconds, **JIM** cracks and makes fart noises with his armpit.

**KATHY** loses it laughing.

**BILL** tries to hold composure, but **KATHY** laughs harder and he breaks.

**JEREMY** and **GILLEY** are the last two, locked in an absurd, sweaty battle of wills.

**GILLEY**

(gritting teeth)

You blinked.

**JEREMY**

No I didn’t.

**GILLEY**

You twitched.

**JEREMY**

I have sweat in my corneas, man.

**JEFF** (O.S.)

He wins. You’re the one yelling.

Everyone turns. **JEFF**’s been sitting quietly the whole time, watching like a tired game show judge. One leg propped on an amp, an untouched soda can sweating beside him.

**JEFF** **(CONT’D)**

**JEREMY** wins. For dignity. And cheating creatively.

**GILLEY**

(beat)

Fair.

(beat)

Fine.

(raises hands)

THE WINNERS:

**KATHY**. **JEREMY**.

And… **JIM**.

**JIM**

Wait, me?!

**GILLEY**

Yeah. You made me laugh, and you bled during cable wrap.

**JIM**

I DID. I BLED FOR TICKETS.

**BILL**

This is rigged.

**KATHY**

You tried to synth fart your way to victory. Accept your shame.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

It was chaos. It was dumb. It was perfect.

(beat)

I couldn’t hear half of it.

(beat)

But I could feel it.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – EVENING, SWEAT-SLICK & UNHINGED

EVENT FIVE: THE "STAGE DIVE" SIMULATION

**GILLEY**

Final challenge: trust fall onto the couch cushions. Bonus points for style. Negative points for screaming “**MOM**” mid-air.

A pile of three ratty couch cushions is stacked on the oil-stained garage floor.

**JIM** steps up, crosses himself, yells “GERONIMO,” and jumps. The cushions slip. He lands half-on, half-off. Groans. Flashes a thumbs-up.

**GILLEY**

Pain?

**JIM**

Yeah.

**GILLEY**

Points!

**KATHY** executes a perfect swan dive and lands like a gymnast sticking the dismount.

**GILLEY**

I’m giving you extra points but also docking one for being too good.

**KATHY**

Your entire system is arbitrary.

**GILLEY**

Thank you for noticing.

**BILL** tiptoes up, hesitates, and tries to gently sit backward onto the cushions.

**GILLEY**

BOOOOOO. SIT DIVE?! NEGATIVE POINTS FOR CAUTION.

**JEREMY** gets a running start, does a full spin mid-air, shouts “FOR **JEFF**” and somehow hits the garage wall after missing the cushions entirely.

**JEREMY** (from floor)

I'm… okay.

**JEFF**

That was impressive in the wrong direction.

EVENT SIX: THE LYRICS TRIAL

**GILLEY**

Okay, Karaoke of Death: each of you sings a verse of a Whigs song, from memory, and you have to make eye contact with me the whole time.

**BILL**

I’m out. I don’t do eye contact.

**KATHY**

(locks eyes with **GILLEY**, sings flawlessly)

“Rebirth of the cool…”

**GILLEY**

Jesus Christ.

**JIM** tries and immediately fumbles into what might be Creed lyrics.

**GILLEY**

No. Absolutely not. That’s spiritual contamination.

**JEREMY** goes off-book and turns it into spoken word poetry, arms gesturing like he’s summoning jazz gods.

**GILLEY**

I have no idea what just happened. Points.

AFTERMATH: THE RANKINGS

**GILLEY** stands atop the milk crate again, shirt now tied around his waist, hair slicked with effort and ego.

**GILLEY**

Okay. Based on a deeply flawed, yet passionately executed scoring system, our final standings are:

Tied for first:

**KATHY** – for excellence.

**JEREMY** – for chaos and blood sacrifice.

Third place:

**JIM** – for sheer commitment to being physically destroyed.

**BILL**

Where am I?

**GILLEY**

Nowhere. You didn’t even stage dive.

**BILL**

I contributed! I brought style!

**GILLEY**

You brought synth farts and fear of eye contact.

**JEFF**

You’re lucky this isn’t a democracy.

**BILL**

I will sue you in a garage court.

**KATHY**

You’ll lose. He’s the judge, the jury, and the power strip.

**JIM**

What about **JEFF**’s ticket?

Everyone turns to **JEFF**. He looks up from his spot on the amp, sipping his soda like a man who’s observed a war through a glass wall.

**JEFF**

I’m not going.

(beat)

But if the extra tickets come through… none of this will have mattered.

**GILLEY**

That’s the most **JEFF** thing you could possibly say.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

It was stupid. It was sweaty. It was unfair.

(beat)

And it was one of the best afternoons of my life.

EVENT SEVEN: FINAL TIEBREAKER — THE CHUG OF REGRET

**GILLEY**

Final round. We all knew it would end this way. Garage-warm root beer. Flat. Half-fermented. In a gas station Big Gulp cup. Found in my trunk.

He holds up the cup. It’s sweating. Menacing. Possibly alive.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**

Whoever chugs this most bravely shall be crowned Champion of the Suffering.

**JIM**

I once drank from a puddle at King’s Island. I was eight. Let’s go.

He grabs the cup, takes two gulps, makes a noise like a dying mule, and hands it off.

**KATHY**

(to herself)

This is for art.

She sips once, immediately gags, swears violently, walks away shaking her head.

**BILL**

I’m not drinking that. I know what’s in your trunk.

**JEREMY**

We all know what’s in his trunk.

**GILLEY**

And now, it lives in you.

**JEREMY** shrugs, grabs the cup, finishes it.

**JEREMY**

That was… genuinely awful.

**GILLEY**

We have a winner.

THE FINAL TALLY (WRITTEN IN SHARPIE ON A PIZZA BOX):

    **JEREMY**: 1,000 points (mostly sweat, also trauma)

    **KATHY**: 950 (weaponized eye contact)

    **JIM**: 905 (moonwalk + root beer courage)

    **BILL**: 899 (technical victory, spiritual failure)

    **GILLEY**: Disqualified for running the game

**GILLEY**

Alright, that's it. **JEREMY**, **KATHY**, **JIM** — you get the first three tickets.

**BILL**

What about the fourth?

ALL EYES TURN TO **JEFF**, who’s been silent this whole time, perched on the amp like a wounded monk.

**JEFF**

I’m having my eardrum rebuilt that week.

**GILLEY**

Jesus. You’re like an origin story waiting to happen.

**KATHY**

So who gets the fourth?

**GILLEY**

We fight.

(beat)

Or we wait for Mr. Evans to make another deal with the Zima devil.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – DUSK BLEEDING INTO NIGHT

The sun has died. The overhead bulb flickers like it’s developing PTSD.

**GILLEY**

Next contestant: **BILL** “Synth Farts” Davenport.

**BILL**

(tight-lipped)

I’m going to sing Debonair and I’m not going to enjoy any part of it.

**GILLEY**

Perfect. Make it suffer.

**BILL** stands ramrod straight, closes his eyes, and begins a flat, oddly enthusiastic spoken-word version of the lyrics — somewhere between slam poetry and a hostage tape.

**BILL**

(dead serious)

Hear me now and don’t forget…

I’m not the man my actions would suggest…

**JIM**

I’m uncomfortable.

**KATHY**

You should be. He’s weaponized the lyrics.

**BILL**

(still droning)

A little boy…

**GILLEY**

Okay, okay, you’re done! Jesus. That was like if Leonard Cohen had a sinus infection.

**BILL**

Art hurts.

**GILLEY**

So does listening to it.

EVENT SEVEN: INSTRUMENTAL CHARADES

**GILLEY**

New rule. One of you plays something on your instrument that describes an emotion. The rest of us guess what it is.

**KATHY**

This is performance art for insane people.

**GILLEY**

Correct. You're in the final round.

**JIM** hops onto the drum throne. Slams out a chaotic, uneven blast beat, then stops dead. Looks around, hopeful.

**KATHY**

That was “full bladder during math test.”

**BILL**

Was it “my dad said he was proud of me but I didn’t believe it”?

**JIM**

It was “envy.”

**GILLEY**

Minus two for using a real word.

**JEREMY** plugs in his guitar, cranks the fuzz, and plays a riff so filthy it sounds like a VHS copy of sex.

Everyone stares.

**JEFF**

…Is that “lust?”

**JEREMY**

No. That was guilt.

**KATHY**

My God.

FINAL EVENT: THE ULTIMATE SHAME WALK

**GILLEY**

Okay. Last round. You have thirty seconds to deliver a “thank you” speech for winning a Grammy you did not earn.

Whoever is most delusional wins.

**KATHY**

Oh this is going to be brutal.

**JIM**

(sprinting forward, zero hesitation)

“I wanna thank my third grade teacher for telling me I’d never amount to anything — MISS BURNS, LOOK AT ME NOW. This one’s for every band I ever started that lasted one practice and every pizza I ever bought with coins. We made it. We finally—”

**KATHY**

(softly)

Is he crying?

**GILLEY**

He might be winning.

**JEREMY**

(stumbling into the spotlight)

I’d like to thank caffeine, questionable decisions, and **JEFF**, who once gave me half of his Pop-Tart during gym. This is for the Evans bloodline, which is strong and weird and full of mistakes.

**BILL**

Your speech sounds like a motivational injury report.

**BILL** **(CONT’D)**

My turn.

(steps up, adjusts jacket that doesn’t exist)

“I’d like to thank myself. For enduring. For always knowing I was the smartest person in every room. Especially this one. No one believed I could play 128 MIDI patches in a single night… but I did. This one’s for all the haters.”

**GILLEY**

You’re disqualified. That was too believable.

**KATHY**

(slowly walking up, voice deadpan)

I’d like to thank the ghost of Joan Jett, even though she’s not dead. I’d like to thank **JEFF**’s sock drawer for holding the CD I gave him for six days. And finally, I’d like to thank this garage — for ruining my hearing and saving my soul. Thank you.

Silence.

**JIM**

Wow.

**GILLEY**

Holy shit.

**BILL**

I… I think she won.

**GILLEY**

She transcended.

**KATHY**

I blacked out. What did I say?

**AFTERMATH: FINAL SCORE ANNOUNCEMENT**

Everyone’s sweaty. Broken. A little emotionally raw. **GILLEY** stands on the milk crate again, now holding a crumpled fast food bag like an awards envelope.

**GILLEY**

The results are in.

(beat)

Tied for first:

**KATHY** – for weaponizing poetry and crushing souls.

**JEREMY** – for bleeding, flipping, and existential guitar tone.

**JIM** – for heart. Always heart.

**BILL** – honorable mention for enduring shame with style.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**

And **JEFF**…

**JEFF**

Was never playing your stupid game.

**GILLEY**

Exactly. You win the biggest prize: dignity.

(beat)

Use it wisely.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

We didn’t play to win.

We played to survive each other.

(beat)

And that was enough.

EXT. LOADING DOCK – LATE MORNING – FOUR DAYS LATER

Another scorcher. The kind of heat that bakes through denim and dries your mouth out before you speak. The sound of idling delivery trucks echoes off the cinderblock walls.

**JEREMY** EVANS is hauling another two-keg dolly toward the warehouse when FRANK, one of the beer reps — late 30s, shaved head, gold chain, loud mouth — steps out from under the shade of the loading dock, Diet Pepsi in hand, sunglasses on.

FRANK

Hey Evans!

**JEREMY** grunts, doesn’t slow down.

FRANK **(CONT’D)**

Nah, don’t gimme that “I’m working” face. Lemme ask you something.

**JEREMY** parks the dolly against the ramp and finally wipes his forehead.

**JEREMY**

What.

FRANK

When the fuck are you getting your band into WO Wrights?

**JEREMY** blinks.

**JEREMY**

What?

FRANK

WO Wrights, man. West Ohio. That little college station with the call letters no one can pronounce. They spin everyone. Dayton, Cincinnati, Athens, doesn’t matter. It’s legit. They’re the ones who broke Motel Beds last year.

**JEREMY** stares, brain still catching up.

**JEREMY**

How do you even know about my band?

FRANK

Because Bobby from routing keeps playing your demo tape in the goddamn office, and every time he rewinds it, it sounds like a Chainsaw with feelings.

(beat)

You sound like something, man. But we’re sick of listening to it on that jacked-up cassette he dubbed off the boom box like it’s 1986.

**JEREMY**

It was dubbed off the boom box. In **GILLEY**’s garage.

FRANK

Exactly. Which means it’s either brilliant or a crime against tape heads.

(leans in)

Get it on WO Wrights, Evans. Or we’re gonna have to keep guessing what your band actually sounds like under the static.

**JEREMY** just stares for a beat.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  

We thought no one was listening.

Turns out they were. Just through the worst possible speakers.

INT. **GILLEY**’S KITCHEN – EARLY EVENING

The gang crowds around a cluttered kitchen table. An open yellow pages phone book sits in front of **GILLEY**, who’s barefoot, shirtless, wearing mirrored sunglasses and chewing on a toothpick like he’s about to close a back-alley arms deal.

**GILLEY**

Alright, ladies and weirdos, time to go pro.

**KATHY**

You’re calling a dive bar.

**GILLEY**

Correction: I’m securing a high-profile regional engagement.

**BILL**

You mean cold-calling a bar from a landline.

**JEFF**

Do you even know what you’re going to say?

**GILLEY**

No. And that’s what makes it art.

He grabs the tan rotary phone off the counter, dials the number listed for “W.O. Wrights – Music + Drinks – Dayton” and leans back like he’s about to get a Grammy nomination.

SOUND: Ring… ring… ring… followed by the sound of someone answering mid-cigarette drag.

BAR GUY (V.O.)**  

Yeah?

**GILLEY**

Hey there, this is **JEREMY** **GILLEY**, frontman and booking rep for Arcadia Burning—

(the band stares at him)

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**

—we’re an original act outta Bethel, heavy on soul-grit and low-end fury. I’m calling to see if y’all have an opening for live music.

BAR GUY (V.O.)**  

You a cover band?

**GILLEY**

We could be.

BAR GUY (V.O.)**  

We only do live nights Thursdays. You bring a draw?

**GILLEY**

Oh yeah. Big following. Very grassroots. College kids. Air Force types. Sales reps. Some guy named Frank swears by us.

BAR GUY (V.O.)**  

You got a demo?

**GILLEY**

On cassette. Very raw. Authentic.

BAR GUY (V.O.)**  

Drop it off with Big Ron at the bar. Tell him I said to put it on after darts.

(click)

**GILLEY** sets the phone down with the same expression a man makes when he’s convinced he just sold a car he doesn’t own.

**GILLEY**

Boom.

**KATHY**

Did you just name our band without asking?

**GILLEY**

Arcadia Burning. It’s evocative. Emotional. A little misleading.

**JIM**

Sounds like a Christian metal band.

**BILL**

It sounds like heartburn.

**JEFF**

Do we even have a labeled demo tape?

**JEREMY**

I’ve got one in my glove compartment with “Garage – Side A” scrawled in Sharpie.

**GILLEY**

Perfect. That’s our origin story.

**INT. GILLEY’S KITCHEN – CONTINUOUS**

The phone is still dangling from the cord. **GILLEY** sits smug, feet up, chewing a toothpick. Everyone else is staring at him like he just farted in church.

**KATHY**

Arcadia Burning?

**BILL**

That name sounds like an incense store caught fire.

**JIM**

It sounds like a tragic poetry zine for homeschooled teens.

**JEREMY**

It sounds like something that already opened for Candlebox and broke up before the third song.

**GILLEY**

It was on the spot!

**JEFF**

It was bad.

**KATHY**

We need a name. A real one. Now.

**BILL**

Alright. Brainstorm. Go.

**JIM**

What about Free Beer? That way, it’s always on the poster.

**BILL**

And then no one shows up when they realize they’ve been lied to.

**JEREMY**

The Feedback Loop.

**JEFF**

Too pretentious.

**KATHY**

Half Deaf and Broke.

(everyone pauses)

**JIM**

That’s dangerously close to the truth.

**BILL**

How about Basement Gospel?

**GILLEY**

We don’t even play in a basement.

**JEFF**

We also don’t do gospel.

**KATHY**

Okay then, what about Laundry Fire?

**JIM**

Sounds like my last apartment.

**JEREMY**

Misspent Youth?

**BILL**

Taken. Guaranteed.

**GILLEY**

What about something totally stupid? Something that sticks just because it shouldn’t.

**KATHY**

Like?

**GILLEY**

The Broken Spokes.

**JEREMY**

Too Americana.

**BILL**

Tympanoplasty.

**JEFF**

No.

**JIM**

Hot Lunch?

ALL

NO.

(silence)

**KATHY**

Okay. What do we actually sound like?

**JEFF**

Like if soul music fell down the stairs holding a busted guitar.

**BILL**

And landed on a synth.

**JEREMY**

While **JIM** screamed into a bucket.

**JIM**

You're welcome.

**GILLEY**

We sound like a transmission slipping during prom night.

**KATHY**

We sound like… Ohio on a bad day.

(beat)

**JEREMY**

We sound like Cauterize the Midwest.

ALL

…No.

**KATHY**

Wait.

(beat)

What about This Is a Brick?

(silence)

**BILL**

What?

**KATHY**

No metaphor. No flourish. Just: This Is a Brick. It lands. It hurts. It doesn’t ask questions.

**JEFF**

That’s… kind of beautiful.

**JIM**

It’s stupid. I love it.

**GILLEY**

It’s better than Arcadia Fucking Burning.

**JEREMY**

Alright. Fine. We’re This Is a Brick now?

**KATHY**

Unless someone else says something better right now.

(silence)

**BILL**

…Nope.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

That was it. No epiphany. No lightning bolt.

Just six idiots in a kitchen deciding to name themselves after a building material.

And somehow, it fit.

INT. **GILLEY**’S KITCHEN – EVENING

The yellow light buzzes overhead. A half-empty 2-liter of Mountain Dew sweats next to a pile of failed band names scrawled on receipts, napkins, and a Little Caesars box. No one is speaking. They have broken themselves.

**JIM**

This is purgatory.

**BILL**

This is less than purgatory. This is the waiting room outside purgatory, where they pipe in static and loop “Shiny Happy People.”

**KATHY**

We are six bodies in a Midwestern kitchen, slowly dying under the weight of indecision and **GILLEY**’s bullshit.

**GILLEY**

Okay first of all, I’m sorry for Arcadia Burning. I had, like, five seconds.

**JEREMY**

And you used all of them poorly.

**JEFF**

We’re not even naming a band anymore. We’re just screaming nouns at each other.

**BILL**

I wrote down Thunder Voucher. That’s not a name, that’s a fake gift card.

**JIM**

I had Crate of Dad. That’s a cry for help.

**KATHY**

This Is a Brick sounded okay for a second, then felt like a dare.

**GILLEY**

I still stand by Hot Lunch.

ALL

NO.

(silence)

**JEREMY**

I just… want it to be over. I want the sentence to end. I want the Governor to pardon us. I want Jesus himself to knock on the door and say, “Children. You have suffered enough.”

**BILL**

I’d take Mr. Haddix. Remember him?

**JEFF**

He once cried during a slideshow about Chernobyl. I'd trust that man with my soul.

**JIM**

We’ve served our time. Time served. We are done.

(long beat)

**KATHY**

(quietly, without looking up)

Well then…

(beat)

How about Commuted?

They all freeze.

No one laughs. No one groans.

Just silence. The weight of a name that actually sounds… right.

**JEFF**

Commuted.

**BILL**

Like the sentence. The punishment.

**JEREMY**

Like what we’re begging the universe for.

**KATHY**

It fits.

**JIM**

It’s got a ring to it.

**GILLEY**

It’s… good?

**BILL**

And it’s ours.

They look at each other. Something lands. Heavy, real, true.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

We didn’t find it.

It found us. At the exact Moment we were ready to give up.

(beat)

Commuted.

Our sentence, our sound, our band.

INT. **JEFF**’S BASEMENT – THE NEXT NIGHT

The band is crowded around a clunky old Brother word processor, the kind that still uses green-screen displays and dot matrix printers. **BILL** is typing like he’s hacking into NORAD. The rest of them are spread out, cutting scraps of old show flyers, gluing weird magazine clippings, and arguing about whether lightning bolts are too much.

**JIM**

Should we have a logo?

**KATHY**

We don’t even have a setlist.

**GILLEY**

We need imagery. Something iconic. Like a brick. Or a burning gavel.

**JEFF**

A gavel on fire is definitely a choice.

**JEREMY**

What if we just kept it simple? Black text. White background. Name, date, venue. Done.

**BILL**

Yeah, yeah, fine. No frills. Let me type this up.

(clacking keys)

**BILL** **(CONT’D)**

“LIVE AT W.O. WRIGHTS – THURSDAY NIGHT – DEBUT SHOW OF…”

(he squints, types)

“COMMUTED.”

SOUND: The printer grinds to life. Paper feeds like it’s choking on peanut butter. The band crowds around as the first flyer emerges…

…and in giant bold block letters:

“COMUTED”

**KATHY**

Oh no.

**JIM**

We lost a vowel.

**JEFF**

**BILL**.

**BILL**

What?

**GILLEY**

You spelled it Comuted.

**BILL**

No I didn’t.

**JEFF**

You did.

**JEREMY**

The ‘m’ is there, but the ‘m’ is lonely. It needs a roommate.

**BILL**

Shit.

**KATHY**

How many of these did you print?

**BILL**

Um…

(cut to)

MONTAGE:

– One flyer duct-taped to the door of W.O. Wrights, bold and proud: “COMUTED LIVE!”

– A flyer in the Tecumseh High teacher’s lounge, tacked up next to a “LOST CAT” notice.

– Another at the Speedway, next to the condoms and moon pies.

– One stapled to a telephone pole, flapping in the wind like a sad flag of the underemployed.

– A flyer taped to the inside of the men’s bathroom stall at **BILL**'s Place, right above a “For a good time call…” number.

INT. **GILLEY**’S GARAGE – LATER

The band is staring at the remaining stack of “COMUTED” flyers in silence.

**GILLEY**

So… what’s our name again?

**KATHY**

Apparently? Comuted.

**JIM**

Sounds like a knockoff modem brand.

**JEREMY**

Or a 5th-tier Transformers villain.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

The name didn’t matter. Not really.

The songs mattered.

The sweat mattered.

The six of us?

We were still figuring it out.

(beat)

But now?

We had a gig.

INT. W.O. WRIGHTS – BACK HALLWAY – THURSDAY NIGHT – 8:21 PM

The band stands in a loose, nervous clump — instruments slung, half-sweating, half-jittering. Behind them: the low thump of a jukebox, the clatter of pitchers, and the unmistakable scent of fried mozzarella sticks mixed with despair.

Enter BIG RON: mid-50s, mustache like an outlaw, T-shirt tucked into jeans like he means business. He’s holding a clipboard, a Marlboro Red between his fingers, and a beer gut that speaks of wisdom and authority.

He walks up, looks them over once — like a man checking livestock.

BIG RON

Alright.

(points at **JEREMY**)

You brought me that tape last week. I’ll be honest — I almost tossed it in the fry grease. Thought it was another Creed cover band.

(beat)

But then I played it after darts and I’ll be damned…

(beat)

It wasn’t bad.

**KATHY**

Thank you?

BIG RON

I mean that. Real weird energy. Like if Tom Waits got electrocuted in a strip mall. People were into it. Even Tommy, and Tommy hates everything.

He scratches his neck.

BIG RON **(CONT’D)**

So listen. You keep fifty people in the room past nine o'clock — no bailing to the patio, no barflies ghosting — and I’ll throw you an extra fifty bucks.

**JIM**

That’s like… nine bucks a person.

BIG RON

Exactly. So make 'em stay.

**GILLEY**

What if they start dancing?

BIG RON

Nobody dances here. Not since ’87.

(beat)

Just keep the room hot. Loud. Weird. All covers, and keep it iconic.

**BILL**

We don’t do irony.

**JEFF**

I’m pretty sure all of our music is irony.

BIG RON

Good. Then get in there. Sound guy’s drunk. Don’t touch the monitor knob. It electrocutes.

**KATHY**

Wait—what?

BIG RON

Break a leg, kids.

(beat)

But not on the stairs. Liability waivers don’t kick in until ten.

He walks off, already lighting another smoke.

The band stands in silence for a long beat.

**JEREMY**

Fifty bucks?

**JEFF**

Fifty people.

**GILLEY**

We got this.

(beat)

Right?

**KATHY**

Only if we don’t suck.

**JIM**

Or die.

**BILL**

Same difference.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Nine o’clock. Fifty people. One shot.

No pressure.

INT. W.O. WRIGHTS – STAGE – 9:03 PM

The band is playing. Hard.

**GILLEY**’s shirtless.

**KATHY**’s shredding like it’s therapy.

**JEREMY’s** locked into a riff like it owes him money.

**BILL**’s synth is making alien noises.

**JIM** is hitting the drums like they slept with his ex.

**JEFF**? **JEFF** is counting.

Between bass lines, he scans the room, eyes darting.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Okay, focus. Count the heads. We need fifty. That’s the deal.

He sees:

    Three airmen at the bar, pounding pitchers and nodding politely.

    A table of Wright State kids, half-listening, mostly flirting.

    A guy in a cowboy hat doing that knee-bounce thing.

    Two bartenders.

    A woman in a leather jacket who looks like she could kill someone with a glance.

He mutters numbers under his breath.

**JEFF**

Five… ten… fifteen… twenty…

**KATHY** (while still playing, eyes wide, mouthing)

What’s the count?

**JEFF** shrugs, keeps going.

**JEFF**

Twenty-five… thirty… thirty-five…

Behind the bar, Big Ron is watching. Not smiling. Not frowning. Just… judging.

**JEFF** **(CONT’D)**

Forty… forty-one… forty-two…

**GILLEY**

(into mic)

I wanna hear you, W.O. Wrights!

One guy cheers. Two girls giggle. One dude coughs.

**JEFF**

Forty-three… forty-four… forty-five…

He’s sweating now. Desperation math.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Come on. Come on, come on…

**JEFF** **(CONT’D)**

Forty-six… forty-seven…

He stops counting.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Oh fuck.

**KATHY**

(stepping over mid-solo, shouting)

How bad?

**JEFF**

Forty-seven.

**JIM**

(shouting from behind the kit)

I’m trying to play louder! Maybe people outside will come in!

**BILL**

This is capitalism at its cruelest!

**GILLEY**

I see movement by the pool table!

**JEREMY**

No, that’s the jukebox guy!

**GILLEY**

DAMMIT, RON.

INT. W.O. WRIGHTS – SIDE STAGE – 9:07 PM

The band is still playing. Barely.

The energy is dipping. The clock is ticking.

**JEFF** looks like he’s doing calculus mid-bassline. **GILLEY** is trying to sell enthusiasm like a door-to-door preacher.

They’re still at 47.

**JEREMY** hops off stage mid-breakdown, guitar feedback humming, and ducks into a grimy hallway near the payphone by the men’s room.

He slams a quarter into the slot, punches in the number fast, breathless.

**JEREMY**

(into phone)

**MOM**?

INT. EVANS KITCHEN – INTERCUT – SAME TIME

MRS. EVANS, calm, hair in curlers, holding a cordless phone and a cup of iced tea, answers in her robe.

**JEREMY’s** younger brother (Josiah) is eating Trix directly out of the box.

His sister (Joslyn) is painting her nails at the table.

MRS. EVANS
JEREMY? You okay?

**JEREMY**
I need you to get in the car. Right now. Bring Josiah. Bring Joslyn. Bring… bodies.

**MRS. EVANS**
What?

**JEREMY**
We need fifty people in the bar or we lose fifty bucks. We’re three short. It’s twelve miles down 675. Please. Please. PLEASE.

MRS. EVANS
You want me to bring your teenage siblings to a bar?

**JEREMY**
Technically it’s more of a glorified bunker with nachos. But yes. Just come. Just stand near the jukebox. You don’t even have to clap.

(beat)

I’ll do the dishes for a week.

MRS. EVANS
Make it two.

**JEREMY**
Fine! Please just hurry!

SFX: SLAM.

He hangs up, sprints back toward the stage, panting.

INT. STAGE – MOMENTS LATER

**KATHY**
What did you just do?

**JEREMY**
I called in the Evans Cavalry.

Wave after wave of young airmen, high-and-tight haircuts, fatigues wrinkled, faces sunburned and bleary from a full day hauling gear for the Dayton Air Show. Over 100 of them, loud, laughing, ready to drink, sweat, and scream.

**INT. W.O. WRIGHTS – SIDE OF STAGE – 9:51 PM**

The band huddles, **GILLEY** dripping with adrenaline, **JEREMY** pale from maternal impact, **JEFF** tuning without looking up. Out in the crowd, Mrs. Evans sits stone-faced, sipping from a plastic cup and eyeing the crowd like she’s waiting for a reason to call a health inspector.

She wants Sunday Bloody Sunday.

As in… the actual song?

I know the drum pattern. It’s just snare death march meets Irish angst.

I know the vocals. Sort of. I’ll figure it out. My range is… flexible.

Guys.

This song doesn’t need synth.

**JIM**
Welcome to the theme of the night.

**ONSTAGE – 9:54 PM**

The band clicks in. **JIM** taps out that famous, regimented snare intro — march-like, relentless, perfect. The crowd hushes — even some of the airmen stop shouting.

**KATHY** kicks into the opening chord structure. Sparse. Icy. Controlled.

Then **BILL** enters.

A low, slow-building synth pad rises under it all — subtle and eerie, like a fog rolling in behind the battlefield. He dials in a distant warble, a ghostly echo, something that shouldn’t work but does.

**GILLEY** (singing, surprisingly restrained)
*I can't believe the news today…*

MRS. EVANS watches from the back, arms crossed, one eyebrow raised in maternal evaluation mode.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
*Oh, I can’t close my eyes and make it go away…*

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Somehow, we didn’t butcher it.

(beat)

**BILL** turned his synth into a wounded church organ. **JIM**’s snare cracked like gunfire.
**KATHY** played like she was holding it together with wire.

(beat)

And **GILLEY**, as always… sang like he meant it.

**BACK OF THE ROOM**

Mrs. Evans watches the whole song. Doesn’t clap. Doesn’t react.

**JOSLYN**
Is she… smiling?

No. That’s her “I’m not mad, just surprised” face.

They’re loud. But they’re not bad.

**INT. W.O. WRIGHTS – STAGE – 9:58 PM**

The crowd is still buzzing from “Sunday Bloody Sunday.” Some are drunk. Some are confused. All are weirdly impressed.

PHIL COLLINS!

Doesn’t matter.

He dives into his synth rig. Fingers fly. A bass pad kicks in. The arpeggiator awakens. And suddenly—

SFX: That unmistakable dahhh, duh-da-da-duh-dahhhh starts throbbing through the speakers.

THE CROWD:

A few airmen are thrilled. One guy’s yelling “I LOVE GENESIS!” even though he clearly doesn’t know the difference. Someone’s cousin is moonwalking on beer.

**MRS. EVANS**
Now they’re just showing off.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
We didn’t know the words. We didn’t know the chords. We didn’t know the structure. But for five minutes, we were Phil Collins. And Phil Collins was confused, wherever he was.

**INT. W.O. WRIGHTS – STAGE – 10:07 PM**

The crowd is beyond drunk now. There’s that guy with no shirt making out with a jukebox, two airmen slow-dancing ironically, and Big Mike is actually smiling for once. Somewhere, a pool cue has snapped in half and no one cares.

**BILL** starts pounding out the iconic “*Take On Me*” synth riff — a wall of pure 1985 energy, thin and crisp and utterly perfect.

**KATHY** plays the chords, loose, precise. **JEREMY** and **JEFF** lay in the rhythm like a freight train made of hairspray and heartache.

And then—**GILLEY** leans into the mic.

**GILLEY** (softly, eyes locked on **KATHY**)
*Talking away… I don’t know what… I’m to say I’ll say it anyway…*

But he doesn’t break eye contact.

**KATHY** (strumming, trying to breathe, failing)
Oh no.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
We thought it was just a bit. Just **GILLEY** being **GILLEY**. But he meant every word.

*Take on me… (take on me)*
*Take me on… (take on me)*
*I’ll be gone…*

He tilts his head. Smolders. He does a tiny little hip sway.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**
*…in a day or two.*

**KATHY** (under her breath, panicked but impressed)
What the fuck is happening to me.

She fumbles a chord. Smiles despite herself. Bites her lip.

**JIM** (from the back)
Ohhhh my god it’s working.

This is a state crime.

**JEFF**

CHEERING. SCREAMING. UNSURE WHY. MOVED.

(beat)

**INT. W.O. WRIGHTS – BEHIND THE BAR – 1:02 AM**

The house lights are on. The airmen have mostly staggered out, leaving behind half-drunk pitchers, torn napkins, and one abandoned combat boot. The jukebox is blinking quietly to itself.

The band leans on the bar, fried, glowing, all of them still kind of stunned they pulled it off.

**BIG MIKE** emerges from the back, wiping his hands on a bar towel. He’s got a beat-up cash envelope in one hand and a plastic coffee can in the other.

BIG MIKE
Alright. You did it.

(beat)

Fifty bucks extra, no questions asked. You hit way more than fifty people. You made the airmen scream. You didn’t blow the monitors. Good night.

He drops the envelope on the bar. It’s soft. Folded. Slightly damp. Then he sets down the coffee can with a dull clunk.

BIG MIKE **(CONT’D)**
Half the bonus is in singles. The other half’s in quarters. Dart machine spilled. My loss is your snack bar fund.

**KATHY** (deep breath)
Are we supposed to split that?

**JIM**
I’m taking quarters. I’ve got laundry.

**GILLEY**
I’m gonna buy nachos and cigarettes and die happy.

Don’t spend it all in one parking meter.

He leans forward.

BIG MIKE **(CONT’D)**
Also—

(beat)
You wanna come back? I got an opening two Thursdays from now. Some blues band dropped out. One of ‘em lost a finger in a mower.

**JEFF**
That’s… unfortunate.

BIG MIKE
It’s Dayton. Shit happens.

(beat)

You interested?

The band looks at each other. They don’t even have to speak.

**KATHY**
Yeah. We’re interested.

**GILLEY**
We’re so interested.

**BILL**
Do we have to bring our own quarters?

BIG MIKE
Just bring whatever the hell that was you played tonight.

(beat)

And maybe write your name right on the flyers this time. I still think it said Comuted.

**JEREMY**
We’re working on branding.

BIG MIKE
Good. I like you kids. You’re weird. And loud. And you bring a crowd that drinks.

(beat)

That’s all I need.

He turns, walks into the dark kitchen, and is gone.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
The bar was empty. The night was over.  But somehow, we weren’t. We had quarters, a date, and a name. Even if it was spelled wrong.
