**INT. GILLEY’S KITCHEN – MORNING – 9:06 AM**

The light is harsh and judgmental, slicing through the blinds like a hangover with opinions. The kitchen smells like burnt toast and leftover sweat. The coffee tastes like regret.

**KATHY** stands at the counter, fully dressed — boots laced, keys already in her pocket. She’s wearing last night’s eyeliner like war paint. Her jacket’s zipped, even though it’s not cold. She clutches a chipped mug that says “#1 Dad,” and it burns her hand with every sip, but she doesn’t flinch.

**GILLEY** walks in shirtless, eyes puffy with sleep, hair flattened on one side. He grins. Not sleazy. Not cocky. Just… hopeful. Like maybe he still gets to be part of whatever last night was.

**GILLEY  
** Hey.

**KATHY  
** (flat)  
 We can’t keep fucking.

The smile dies mid-bloom. **GILLEY** freezes, hand half-extended toward the fridge like maybe he was going to offer her juice.

**GILLEY  
** …Okay.

**KATHY  
** No games. No awkward will-they-won’t-they bullshit. Just—no more.

(beat)

I’m not gonna be the girl who sleeps with her bandmate just because the show went well.

**GILLEY  
** You think that’s what this was?

**KATHY  
** I think this was me, full of noise and whiskey and too much skin and too much *yes* when I should’ve said *not tonight.*

(beat)

I think I used you like a smoke alarm I could rip off the wall to stop the beeping in my head.

**GILLEY  
** Jesus.

**KATHY  
** I’m not mad at you.

(beat)

I’m just disgusted at how easy I made it.

**GILLEY  
**You didn’t seem disgusted last night.

**KATHY  
**Don’t do that.

**GILLEY  
**What?

**KATHY  
**Don’t shrink it down to a reaction you can manage.

(beat)

What we did was real. Onstage? That was the best we’ve ever been. Maybe the best we’ll ever be.

(beat)

And offstage… maybe there was something there, too.

(beat)

But I’m drawing the line now. Clean. No fade-out. No encore.

**GILLEY  
**Why not?

**KATHY  
**Because I want to keep playing with you.

(beat)

Because if we cross this line again, I won’t respect you.

(beat)

And worse—I won’t respect me.

He doesn’t nod. Doesn’t argue. Just stands there like someone trying not to wake up fully, because the Moment he does, this becomes real.

She finishes her coffee. Sets the mug down — hard enough to crack it slightly, though she doesn’t notice. Or maybe she does.

**KATHY **(CONT’D)**  
**I’ll see you at practice.

She walks out without looking back.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**    
**She thought she was saving something.  
The band. Herself.  
Maybe even me.

But all I felt was the shape of her leaving.  
The shape of her ass?  A door I thought would stay open just a little longer.

**CAMERA STAYS on GILLEY, alone in the kitchen.  
**The broken mug still sweating on the counter.  
The fridge still humming, oblivious.  
His arms still bare, still cold.

**EXT. GILLEY’S FRONT PORCH – MORNING – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** steps outside, boots crunching on gravel. The door slams shut behind her — sharp, final.

She’s halfway down the steps when it blasts back open.

**GILLEY  
**(shirtless, eyes blazing, voice raw)  
You forgot your fucking bra!

He launches it like a grenade. It arcs in the air — pale, delicate, absurd — and lands in the dew-wet grass with a limp thud.

She keeps walking.

**GILLEY **(CONT’D)**  
**(spitting, almost choking)  
You fucking *cunt!*

The word echoes. Too loud. Too sharp for morning.

Silence.

A bird chirps.

A dog barks two blocks away, then stops.

**KATHY** halts. Mid-step. Back stiff.

Turns.

Slowly.

Her face is unreadable — not calm, not angry. Just *beyond.*

She steps off the walkway. Walks to the bra in the grass. Picks it up between two fingers like it’s contaminated. Like *he* is.

Then she walks back. Not rushing. Not flinching.

Stands below him. Close. Too close. Just out of reach, like something beautiful with venom under the skin.

**KATHY  
** (quiet, razor-edged)  
 You don’t get to call me that.

(beat)

Not on stage.

Not at practice.

Not even in your fucked-up little ego monologue.

(beat)

Grow the fuck up, **GILLEY**.

She doesn’t throw the bra back. She keeps it.

Turns.

And walks away — not for good measure.

For *good.*

**GILLEY** stays frozen in the doorway, shirtless, fists clenched, chest heaving like he’s just sprinted through humiliation and landed in regret.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** That was the Moment he stopped being the frontman.

(beat)

And became the problem.

**INT. GILLEY’S BEDROOM – LATER THAT MORNING – 9:42 AM**

The house is dead quiet. **KATHY**’s long gone.

**GILLEY** sits on the edge of the bed in his boxers, staring at the spot where her bra landed, like it’s cursed ground. His jaw clenches. He breathes deep, once, twice, through his nose.

He doesn't go after her.

He doesn’t clean up.

Instead, he reaches to the floor, fishes around in a pile of receipts, guitar picks, and unmatched socks… and pulls out a tiny spiral notepad, warped from back pocket sweat and time.

The cover says:

“Names / Numbers / Maybe.”

Written in Sharpie.

He flips through the pages. Quick scrawls. Lipstick prints. Hearts. No hearts. Smudged digits. A history of half-baked flirtation and backup plans.

Six names.

Angie – blonde from **GILLEY**’s cousin’s wedding

Trina – beer rep’s niece, liked the synth

"??? – Waffle House?"

Shelly – from darts night, could sing? maybe?

Stacey – airman groupie, had a camo jacket

“Not **KATHY**” – literally written that way

He stares at the last one.

Then tears out the page and drops it in the ashtray.

His finger hovers over the rest.

**GILLEY** (V.O.)**  

Six numbers. Six maybe’s. Six shots at forgetting.

(beat)

Might as well get to work.

He flips back to Trina’s name.

Grabs the phone. Starts dialing.

Halfway through the number, he pauses.

Long beat.

Then hits the last digit.

SFX: The line starts ringing.

**GILLEY**

(casual, into phone)

Hey… this Trina?

This is **GILLEY**.

Yeah, from the show.

(beat)

Nah, I’m not busy.

INT. **GILLEY**’S BEDROOM – MINUTES LATER

The notepad’s still in his lap. The ashtray has a torn piece of paper with “Not **KATHY**” curling at the edges, already burning a black corner.

**GILLEY** flips the pages again.

He lands on a name:

Stacey Dawson.

Big, looping handwriting.

He stares at it longer than the others.

His lip curls. He says it out loud, almost to himself.

**GILLEY**

Stacey Dawson. She might be nice.

(beat)

Wouldn’t it be something if I could say I had **JEREMY** Dawson’s wife in my bed?

(beat)

That’d be a hell of a feather in the cap.

He smiles. But it’s hollow.

**GILLEY** (V.O.)**  

Wasn’t about Stacey.

Wasn’t even about **JEREMY**.

It was about winning something.

Anything.

After losing her.

(beat)

Problem was, he didn’t even know what he’d lost.

INT. **GILLEY**’S BEDROOM – LATER THAT MORNING

**GILLEY**’s still on the bed, one leg crossed, flipping his dog-eared notepad like it’s a catalog of dreams. His finger pauses on Stacey Dawson’s name. Big loops. Little heart.

He grins to himself.

**GILLEY**

(smiling)

Stacey goddamn Dawson.

He leans back against the wall, one arm behind his head.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**

She always laughs when I talk to her. Says I’m bad news. Says I wouldn’t know what to do with her even if I got the chance.

(beat)

She’s probably right.

(beat)

But man, if I ever did?

(he whistles)

That’d be it. Shut it all down. Retire the jersey. Frame the sheets.

He laughs, low and private.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**

Not that I’d ever actually go through with it.

(beat)

Too much work. Too much risk.

Too much… real.

But the idea?

The idea’s gold.

He closes the notebook, taps it twice on his knee like a good-luck charm.

**GILLEY** (V.O.)**  

There was no fire. Not even a spark.

Just a lighter flicking in the dark, waiting for someone to notice.

INT. **GILLEY**’S KITCHEN – EARLY EVENING – THE NEXT DAY

**GILLEY** leans against the kitchen counter, shirtless (again), a bottle of generic soda in one hand and the cordless phone wedged between shoulder and ear. There’s a box of Magic: The Gathering cards open on the table. Decks spread out. Sleeves. Dice. The works.

RING. CLICK.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

Hello?

**GILLEY**

Hey. Stacey. It’s **GILLEY**.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

Oh… wow. Okay. What’s up?

**GILLEY**

So here’s the thing.

Practice is off. **JEFF**’s going in for that ear surgery thing tomorrow. Tympa-something. So the band’s dark tonight.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

Right. The hearing thing. That sucks.

**GILLEY**

Yeah. I mean, I guess we’re all just one weird childhood fever away from becoming lead singers.

(beat)

Anyway—I was sitting here, just thinking… and I thought:

You know who might be fun to play Magic with?

(beat)

Stacey. Fuckin’. Dawson.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

(surprised laugh)

You’re calling me to play Magic?

**GILLEY**

Yes, ma’am.

(beat)

Bring a deck. Or I’ll loan you one. I’ve got this Rakdos build that’s all about chaos and emotional instability. Figured it’d be perfect.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

(half amused, half cautious)

You do realize I’m married, right?

**GILLEY**

Course I do. That’s what keeps the mystery alive.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

You’re such a weirdo.

**GILLEY**

I prefer “charismatic eccentric.”

(beat)

So. You in?

(beat)

Cards. Maybe snacks. Maybe existential dread. Just a little evening magic between friends.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

(pause)

You know what?

(beat)

Yeah. Why not.

But just cards.

**GILLEY**

That’s all I’m offering. Scout’s honor.

STACEY (V.O.)**  

You were never a scout.

**GILLEY**

Still. Honor-adjacent.

**GILLEY** (V.O.)**  

It was never about the game.

Never about the girl.

It was about not being alone.

And tonight, that was enough.

INT. **GILLEY**’S LIVING ROOM – 8:24 PM

The lights are low. A fan hums lazily in the corner. A worn coffee table is covered in sleeves, dice, and two custom-built decks.

Stacey Dawson sits cross-legged on the couch. Black lipstick, black nails, and a smile that’s older than her marriage. She’s holding her hand of cards like a fortune teller with nothing but bad news.

**GILLEY** lounges on the floor, back against the couch, shirtless and barefoot, sipping flat cola from a chipped glass. His cards are color-coded, clean-sleeved, blue deck in perfect order—calculated chaos in his hands.

STACEY

(turning a card)

Swamp.

(places it)

Here we go.

**GILLEY**

Of course you’d go black.

STACEY

Of course you’d go blue.

All control. No commitment.

**GILLEY**

It’s called strategy.

STACEY

It’s called fear.

She summons a creature with a smile. Something dark and skeletal.

STACEY **(CONT’D)**

Let’s see how long you last when the graveyard starts filling up.

**GILLEY**

(playing an island)

Counterspell.

He leans back, smug. But she only smiles wider.

STACEY

That’s what I like about you, **GILLEY**.

**GILLEY**

My stunning command of the stack?

STACEY

Your desperation to interrupt anything that might actually affect you.

**GILLEY**

You say that like it’s a flaw.

STACEY

It is. But it’s charming. In the way stray cats are charming.

She plays another creature. It sticks this time.

**GILLEY** taps two lands. Bounces it back.

STACEY **(CONT’D)**

There it is.

**GILLEY**

I warned you.

(beat)

Besides, you like the dance.

STACEY

Oh, I live for the dance.

But only when it never reaches the bedroom.

She looks up. Lets it sit.

**GILLEY** doesn’t flinch. But his grip on the cards tightens.

**GILLEY**

That’s what makes it art.

STACEY

No. That’s what makes it safe.

(beat)

And we both know—we like safe.

They keep playing. Moves get faster. Hands get smaller. The board stacks up in a slow-burning war of denial and manipulation.

By the end?

Stacey wins.

Just barely.

STACEY **(CONT’D)**

Good game.

**GILLEY**

Yeah.

(beat)

You always win.

STACEY

You always let me.

She stands, smooths her skirt, grabs her keys.

STACEY **(CONT’D)**

Tell the band I said hi. Tell **KATHY** she looked on fire the other night.

**GILLEY**

You noticed?

STACEY

Everyone noticed.

She walks to the door.

Stops.

STACEY **(CONT’D)**

You ever wanna lose again… call me.

She leaves.

Door clicks behind her.

**GILLEY** stares at the board.

**GILLEY** (V.O.)**  

She played black.

I played blue.

Neither of us played red.

(beat)

Maybe that’s why it never burns.

---

**INT. PRE-OP ROOM – DAY – 8:06 AM**

**JEFF** lies on the hospital bed, dressed in a gown, IV in his arm. His hair is covered in a thin blue surgical cap. One sock on, one sock lost somewhere in the past 20 minutes. The room hums with the soft, low rhythm of pre-op preparation: cart wheels, quiet voices, and the sound of distant movement behind sliding glass doors.

The anesthesiologist is nearby, prepping the final sedative — clear fluid in a labeled syringe.

Dr. Goldberg, the ENT surgeon, is glancing over **JEFF**’s chart. Calm, competent. Polite.

**JEFF** looks over at him, a little dazed already from the first round of sedatives. His voice is soft, dry-mouthed, but still weirdly alert.

**JEFF**
Hey, uh…

(beat)

Before I go under, I got a question.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Of course.

**JEFF**
Is it true they use skin from behind your knee to rebuild an eardrum?

**DR. GOLDBERG** (half-smiling, surprised)
That’s… actually a great question.

(beat)
Yes. In some cases. Not always, but yes — we harvest a small graft of fascia, the connective tissue, from behind the ear or sometimes the underside of the thigh or behind the knee. Depends on the size of the repair.

**JEFF**
So like… knee skin in my ear?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Not skin, technically — fascia. But yes.

(beat)
It’s thin, durable, and takes well to the middle ear environment. You won’t notice it.

**JEFF**
That’s so weird.

(beat)
I’ll be hearing through my knee.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Not quite, but I like your enthusiasm.

**JEFF**
Do people ever get… like… phantom knee sounds?

**DR. GOLDBERG** (laughing gently)
Not that I’ve heard.

**JEFF**
They will now.

(beat)
Okay, you can knock me out.

He turns his head slightly toward the ceiling.

**JEFF** **(CONT’D)**
Tell **KATHY** I didn’t cry or say anything weird, okay?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
We’ll tell her you were a model patient.

**JEFF**
Cool.

(beat)
Tell her I was cool.

SFX: the beeping slows slightly as the anesthesia takes hold. **JEFF**’s eyes flutter, then close.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
Knee in the ear. Weird how the body just… borrows from itself.

(beat)
Like a band. Like a garage. All scraps. All stitched together. But somehow —it works.

---

**INT. HOSPITAL WAITING ROOM – 8:22 AM**

Fluorescent lights hum. A vending machine buzzes. The TV is tuned to local morning news no one is watching.

Mrs. Evans sits near the window, knitting something with way too many colors. She looks up when **JEREMY** **GILLEY** walks in — hoodie half-zipped, sunglasses on indoors, coffee in a cup that clearly wasn't paid for. He looks wildly out of place, like a rock show crashed a church potluck.

**MRS. EVANS** (eyebrows raised)
Well. That’s a surprise.

**GILLEY** (grinning)
Morning, ma’am. Don't worry, I’m not here to sell anything.

He sits. Leans back, slouches in the chair like it owes him money.

**MRS. EVANS**
Didn’t expect to see you here. Practice is cancelled. **JEFF** told everyone.

**GILLEY**
Yeah, I know. I’m not here for band business.

(beat)

I’m here because I owe the guy.

**MRS. EVANS**
Owe him?

**GILLEY**
Yeah.

(beat)

Last year — right around July — I had this emergency eye thing. Bad inflammation. Real bad. Couldn’t even look at a night light without wanting to crawl into a grave. Doctor told me no light, no screens, no nothing. So I crawled into the hall closet. Only place dark enough. No window, no bulb, just shoes and coat hangers and darkness.

He sips his coffee. Doesn’t look at her.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**
**JEFF** came over to check on me.  He found out I was in the closet, and instead of, y'know, leaving me to rot in peace?  He crawled in there with me.  Brought a flashlight with the battery half-dead and a deck of cards.  We sat in that damn closet for eight hours.  Played every stupid made-up game we could think of. Didn’t even talk much. Just… was there.

Mrs. Evans watches him closely now. Not smiling. Just listening.

**GILLEY** **(CONT’D)**
Since then… I dunno. Guy’s got a seat in the back of my heart. Unfortunately.

(beat)

So. I’m here. Sitting. Waiting. Paying back a little bit of what I owe.

MRS. EVANS
Well.

(beat)

This is the nicest thing I’ve ever seen you do, **JEREMY** **GILLEY**.

**GILLEY**
Don’t spread it around. I got a reputation.

MRS. EVANS
Too late.

(beat)
But for what it’s worth… that was decent of you.

**GILLEY**
I’m decent when no one’s looking.

(beat)
At my core? I’m a goddamn softy.

MRS. EVANS
Just don’t tell Stacey Dawson. She’ll think you’re evolving.

**GILLEY**
Lady, if I ever evolve, shoot me on sight.

They sit in silence. The kind that doesn’t ask for anything. Just waiting.

---

INT. RECOVERY ROOM – 9:15 AM

Muted tones. Soft beeping. A partition curtain. The smell of antiseptic and grape-scented anesthesia masks.

**JEFF** blinks awake slowly. Eyes dry. Mouth dry. Brain still rebooting like a Commodore 128 PC.

He licks his lips. Everything’s fuzzy. But his body is unmistakably telling him: feed me.

**JEFF** (low, raspy)
…m’sandwich?

A NURSE approaches from the other side of the curtain, smiling with practiced calm.

NURSE
Hey there, welcome back. Everything went fine. Surgery was smooth. You’re in recovery now.

**JEFF** (grumpy)
Yeah okay. Great.

(beat)
Am I allowed to be hungry or is that illegal?

NURSE
We’ll get you something in just a second. Let’s check vitals first.

**JEFF**
Vitals are fine. Vitals want toast.

She chuckles as she checks his blood pressure cuff.

NURSE
Pain?

**JEFF**
Mild.

(beat)
But my thirst is a medical emergency.

NURSE
We’ll start with water. Ice chips first.

**JEFF**
Jesus Christ. It’s like a spa run by prison guards.

NURSE
Your **MOM**’s still in the waiting room. And a… **JEREMY**?

**JEFF** (nods slightly)
Yeah. **GILLEY**. Probably sitting like he owns the hospital.

NURSE
Would you like them to come in?

**JEFF**
Only if one of them brought a sandwich.

She smiles and walks off.

**JEFF** lies back against the pillow. Blinks slowly. His throat is dry but his hearing — even in the ear that was worked on — already feels different. Quieter. Cleaner. Like static had been scraped out.

He closes his eyes for a second. Then opens them again.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
They cut me open.  They rebuilt a piece of me.  Now I’m here.

(beat)
Still **JEFF**. Still grouchy. Still hungry.

(beat)
But maybe…Just a little bit more tuned in.

---

**INT. RECOVERY ROOM – 9:30 AM**

**JEFF** sits upright in the hospital bed, wrapped in white gauze like a cartoon mummy from the neck up. The bandage covers his entire right ear, looping across the top of his head and around his jaw, cinched with medical tape.  He looks like a helmeted squirrel. He also looks mildly insulted by his own condition.

**DR. GOLDBERG** stands at the foot of the bed, professional and calm.

**GILLEY** and Mrs. Evans step in. Mrs. Evans gasps softly. **GILLEY** freezes.

**MRS. EVANS**
Oh honey…

**JEFF** (flatly)
Hi mom.

**GILLEY**
Dude.

(beat)
You look like you lost a fight with a roll of paper towels.

**JEFF**
Thanks for coming.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
The procedure went well. Textbook, actually. But just so everyone’s clear on what we did…

(he gestures toward the head wrap)
We made a small incision behind the ear, sliced the outer ear partially away from the skull…

**GILLEY** (interrupting)
Wait—you sliced his ear off?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Partially. Then we temporarily attached it to the side of his face with surgical adhesive.

**MRS. EVANS** (to JEFF, calmly)
You have an ear cheek.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
We harvested a skin graft from behind the knee, replaced one of the ossicles—the middle ear bones—with a surgical wire, reconstructed the eardrum, stitched the canal, and filled the inner ear with sterile packing material.

**GILLEY**
That is metal as hell.

**JEFF**
I feel like a ham sandwich someone tried to repair.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
He won’t be able to lift anything over ten pounds, avoid any physical exertion for a week, and absolutely no water in the ear.

**GILLEY**
No cannonballs. Got it.

**MRS. EVANS**
And you’ll be staying at my house. No argument. I already made the guest bed and fluffed your pillows. Twice.

**JEFF**
Of course you did.

(beat)
What about music?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
No headphones. No loud noise. And definitely no garage practice.

**GILLEY**
What if we just play really soft, like acoustic blues?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Then he can listen from another zip code.

**JEFF** (nods slowly)
Cool.

**GILLEY**
You know, for a guy who just had a piece of knee installed in his head, you’re holding up pretty well.

**JEFF**
It’s the hospital Jell-O. Gave me powers.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
They sliced my ear.  They wired my bones.  They stitched me together with glue and luck.  But I’m still here. Still grouchy.  Still me.

(beat)
Just a little more patched up than yesterday.

**EXT. FRONT STREET WAREHOUSE – 4:02 AM – SATURDAY**

The street is dark, the air thick and sticky, like breathing through a damp towel. Sodium lights buzz overhead. The warehouse sits like a cold war relic, metal roll-up doors rattling in the early breeze.

A single truck idles nearby, headlights too bright, cutting through the night like an accusation.

**KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** arrive separately—but within seconds of each other, like zombies that accidentally synchronized their shambling.

**KATHY** (muttering)
I hate everything.

**JEREMY**
I hate you for being on time.

**BILL**
I haven’t seen the number 4 this early since I cried through my AP Chemistry exam.

**KATHY**
Shut up, **BILL**.

**BILL**
Respectfully.

They gather near the loading dock. A few other workers—college kids, warehouse lifers, and a guy in jorts eating a boiled egg—nod in sleepy solidarity.

**JEREMY**
Where’s my dad?

**KATHY**
Hopefully still asleep. Like a normal person.

**JEREMY**
No chance. He’s probably already halfway to the flight line, driving a golf cart full of Michelob.

**BILL**
What are we even doing?

**KATHY**
Beer. Kegs. Boxes of napkins. Stuffing corporate chalets full of overpriced vodka and plastic folding chairs so people can watch planes fly over their heads and pretend it's patriotism.

**BILL**
That’s so bleak.

**JEREMY**
Yeah, well, two extra concert tickets don’t appear out of nowhere.

**KATHY**
I’d sell my soul for five more hours of sleep and a Waffle House hashbrown right now.

**JEREMY**
You already sold your soul. Now you’re just working off the debt.

A forklift growls to life somewhere in the dark.  A foreman with a clipboard and the energy of a man fueled entirely by truck stop coffee steps out of the shadows.

**FOREMAN**
Let’s move, crew! You want that ticket, you better earn it!

**JEREMY** (under his breath)
This is indentured servitude with better parking.

**KATHY**
Come on. Let’s go commit war crimes in the name of beer and aviation.

They trudge toward the open bay door, silhouettes against the yellow light of the warehouse.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
While I was healing, they were hauling. While I was doped up, they were sweating in the dawn. We all had our own ways of paying for the music.

**INT. FRONT STREET WAREHOUSE – MANAGER’S OFFICE – MOMENTS LATER**

A door swings open at the top of the steps overlooking the warehouse floor. Out strides Mr. Evans — tall, tucked-in polo shirt, belt clipped with two pagers, and a smile so sincere it borders on aggressive.

**MR. EVANS**

Morning, team!

The crew groans in unison.

**MR. EVANS (CONT’D)**
Come on, now! It’s a beautiful day in the Miami Valley! Sun’s not even up yet, and we’re already ahead of the game.

**KATHY** (quietly to **BILL**)
Why is he like this?

**BILL**
I think he bathes in black coffee and positive reinforcement.

**MR. EVANS**
You ready to head to the airport?

**JEREMY**
Dad, it's four-oh-freaking-seven.

**MR. EVANS**
Exactly! Time waits for no keg! And guess what?

(beat, grinning)

I’m driving.

Everyone pauses. Nervous.

**MR. EVANS (CONT’D)**
That’s right. I brought out the Silver Bullet One.

**KATHY**
Oh no.

**BILL**
You mean that rolling metal coffin with the CB radio and the captain’s chairs?

**JEREMY**
The one with the wolf mural on the side?

**MR. EVANS**
That’s the one. Tires rotated. Tank full. Spirit untouchable.

**KATHY**
Does the passenger door still fall off if you slam it?

**MR. EVANS**
Only if you disrespect it.

**JEREMY**
Dad, are you seriously driving us onto Wright-Patt in that thing?

**MR. EVANS**
Hell yes I am.

(beat)

We’re bringing class, style, and a light aroma of stale menthols to the Dayton Air Show. The crew files out slowly, half-dreading, half-awed.

**EXT. LOADING DOCK – MOMENTS LATER**

There it is. Silver Bullet One. Chrome trim. Slight sag on the rear axle. CB antenna swaying in the breeze. The painted airbrushed wolf on the side panel is faded but majestic, howling at a moon that now resembles a dent. The side door is chained shut with a padlock, for safety. The engine rumbles like a V8 trying to forget Vietnam.

**MR. EVANS**
Everybody in!

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
While I was eating Jell-O and wondering if I still had a functional face…They were climbing into the Econoline of legends.

**EXT. LOADING DOCK – 4:17 AM – MOMENTS LATER**

The crew stands half-slumped in front of the Silver Bullet One, looking like hostages being forced into a community theater version of Smokey and the Bandit. Mr. Evans holds up a laminated badge, clipped to his belt, like it’s an Olympic medal.

**MR. EVANS**
Oh—and just to clarify—Did you mean Dayton International Airport and not Wright-Patt?
Because we can’t get on base. Not without a security clearance, a background check, and a really convincing lie about hauling ice cream.

(beat)

BUT!

(holds up badge with a flourish)

I’ve got an Access All Areas pass. For the van. And for y’all!

**KATHY**
What does that even mean?

**MR. EVANS**
It means—once we drop off those pallets, hook up the taps, and roll out the trash bins—you are unleashed upon the Dayton International Airport grounds.

**JEREMY**
Unleashed like dogs?

**BILL**
Unleashed like interns?

**MR. EVANS**
Unleashed like legends.  Unlimited meal cards. Full staff access. Hangars, chalets, beer tents, break areas, even the tarmac perimeter if you don’t get in the way of the Thunderbirds.

**KATHY**
Do we get a map?

**MR. EVANS**

Improvise.

**JEREMY**
Oh my God.

**MR. EVANS**
This is gonna be an incredible bargain.

(beat)

Two hours of hauling. All day of perks.  Hot dogs. Sodas. Shady spots behind the hangars. You wanna stand under a cargo plane and feel spiritual? Boom—you’re in.

**KATHY**
If this is a scam, it's the most charming one I've ever seen.

**MR. EVANS**
Scams don’t come with free nachos and a folding chair near the flight line.

(beat)

Now get in the van before someone else takes our spot on the fuel truck route.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
While I was recovering from getting a metal wire hammered into my skull…My friends were driving across Dayton in a wolf-painted van, about to work harder than they ever had…In exchange for nachos and freedom.

**INT. SILVER BULLET ONE – 4:26 AM – MOVING**

The interior of the van is lit only by dashboard glow, a cracked dome light, and the faint blue flicker of the CB radio display. Everyone is half-asleep, rattling around in captain’s chairs that lean at varying, suspicious angles.  The road is pitch black, and outside the windshield—it’s just endless Ohio dark.

**JEREMY** (squinting at the road)
Hey Dad?

**MR. EVANS**
Yeah, buddy?

**JEREMY**
Just a thought.

(beat)

Why haven’t you turned the headlights on?

**MR. EVANS** (glancing at the dash, perfectly calm)
Oh, they haven’t worked since Memorial Day.

**KATHY** 
Excuse me what?  I’m sorry—what?

**BILL**
Are we… stealthing our way to the airport?

**MR. EVANS**
It’s not a big deal. There’s just enough streetlight to keep her between the lines. Plus, those reflective stripes on the hood catch enough bounce to let folks know we’re coming.

**KATHY**
Reflective stripes?

**JEREMY**
You mean the duct tape you slapped on in June?

**MR. EVANS**
Exactly. That stuff’s rated for construction zones.

(beat)

We’re good.

**BILL**
We’re gonna die in this van. This is how the band ends.

**MR. EVANS** (cheerful)
If we die, we die legends. With access all areas!

**JEREMY**
You’re insane.

**MR. EVANS**
You say “insane,” I say efficient underfunded logistics.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
While I was sipping broth through a straw and pretending not to feel stitches in my skull…The rest of the band was flying down the highway in a ghost van with no headlights…
Led by a man powered by pure optimism and expired inspection stickers.

**INT. SILVER BULLET ONE – STILL RUMBLING DOWN THE HIGHWAY – 4:31 AM**

The van rattles like a metal drum in a wind tunnel. The windows are fogged. Someone just spilled stale coffee on the CB mic.

**JEREMY** is gripping the passenger seat with both hands, staring straight ahead as his dad navigates a left turn with no headlights and no signal—just vibes and lane guesses.

**MR. EVANS** (O.S.)**
You just gotta feel the road, son. It’s like jazz. Tires tell you where to go.

**KATHY**, slumped in a back seat with her arms crossed, leans over toward **JEREMY**, dry-eyed but too exhausted to filter herself.

**KATHY** (quietly, almost to herself)
Sometimes I can really tell that **JEFF** is your father’s son.

**JEREMY** (eyes still forward)
What’s that supposed to mean?

**KATHY**
Means he’s calm in chaos. Doesn’t flinch. Gets hurt and doesn’t say a word.

(beat)

Doesn’t know when to bail.

**JEREMY**
That’s not fair.

**KATHY**
It’s not mean, **JEREMY**.

(beat)

It’s just… accurate.

**MR. EVANS** (O.S.)**
Hey! I found the high beams! Wait—nope, that’s the horn.

**HONK**!

They jolt as the van blares into the pre-dawn silence.

**BILL**
This is a slow-motion hostage situation.

**KATHY**  (smiling faintly)
Yup.  And **JEFF**’d never complain.  He’d just sit through it. Same way he sat through **GILLEY**. And me.

(beat)

It’s kind of admirable.  And a little sad.

**JEREMY**
He’s not sad.

**KATHY**
No. He’s not.

(beat)

But sometimes, I wonder if he’s tired of being quiet just to keep everyone else okay.

The van rolls on. No one says anything for a long Moment.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
They say we inherit our parents’ bones.  But maybe we also inherit their silences.

**INT. SILVER BULLET ONE – 4:44 AM – APPROACHING THE AIRPORT PERIMETER**

The sky is still pitch black. The horizon is barely starting to hint at pink. Out ahead is the entry gate to Dayton International Airport’s Air Show service entrance, lit by two spotlights and guarded by two uniformed airport police officers standing next to a folding barricade.

Inside the van, tension tightens.

**MR. EVANS**
Alright, team. Time to get tactical and practical.

**KATHY**
Tactical?

**BILL**
Practical?

**MR. EVANS**
**KATHY**, hand me the bag of donuts. Top of the cooler. White bag. It’s my cop currency.

**BILL**
You’re bribing the police?

**MR. EVANS**
I’m incentivizing community relations.

(beat)

The access-all-area passes will get me through the gate, no problem. But they don’t explain why a wolf-painted van with no headlights is creeping up a runway access road at 4:45 AM.

**KATHY**
Jesus Christ.

**MR. EVANS**
So when in doubt—donuts.  And also—

(looks at everyone very seriously)

Try to stay out of sight.

**JEREMY**
Are you smuggling us into the airport?

**MR. EVANS**
Technically, you’re “vendor support specialists.” But the cops don’t know that. I might have left out the part about the… entourage.

**KATHY**
So you lied?

**MR. EVANS**
I omitted for efficiency.

(beat)

Now crouch. And don’t breathe too loud. Cops hate that.

The van creaks as they all hunch down awkwardly behind the seat backs and under tarps. **KATHY** grabs the donut bag. **JEREMY** whispers:

**JEREMY**
This is felonious.

**MR. EVANS**
Nah. This is entrepreneurial logistics.

**BILL**
This is how bad movies start.

**MR. EVANS**
This is how legends start.

The van slows as it rolls toward the checkpoint.  The donuts are in hand. The vibe is pure dumb It’s a Mad, Mad, Mad World.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

They weren’t just sneaking into the airport.  They were sneaking into the memory of a lifetime.  One coffee-soaked donut at a time.

**EXT. AIRPORT SERVICE GATE – 4:48 AM**

The Silver Bullet One rolls to a gentle, hissing stop just before the metal swing gate, its engine rumbling like a discontented bear.

Two airport cops—Officer Nance and Officer Wells, both early fifties and already halfway through their second coffee—stand beside a folding barricade, sipping and chatting like this is just another morning in paradise.

**MR. EVANS** hops out of the driver’s side with military precision, holding up his laminated badge in one hand and a white paper donut bag in the other, like the world’s most diplomatic criminal.

**MR. EVANS**
Morning, officers!

**OFFICER NANCE**
Morning, Evans. You’re early.

**MR. EVANS**
Early is the new on-time. And I brought sugar diplomacy.

He hands over the donut bag. Nance peeks in—Maple bars. Jelly. A lone cruller. The smile spreads.

**OFFICER WELLS**
Same van as last year?

**MR. EVANS**
Silver Bullet One. Still running strong. She may rattle, but she’s got heart.

**OFFICER NANCE**
Still no headlights?

**MR. EVANS**

Don’t need ‘em. I’ve got God and duct tape.

**OFFICER WELLS** (grinning)
Hell, same difference.

They wave him through.

**OFFICER NANCE**
You know the drill. Load at Chalet 3, then check in at the Red Zone tent. Don’t block the service loop like last time.

**MR. EVANS**
Wouldn’t dream of it.

He hops back in the van, gives the officers a friendly salute.  As the swing gate opens, Silver Bullet One rolls forward, slowly, confidently, into the maze of aircraft, fencing, porta-johns, and corporate-sponsored chalets.

**INT. VAN – MOVING THROUGH AIRPORT – MOMENTS LATER**

**JEREMY**, **KATHY**, and **BILL** slowly rise from their hiding spots like confused raccoons emerging from a trash can.

**JEREMY**

We’re in?

**MR. EVANS**

Like Flynn.

**BILL**

I didn’t even hear you lie.

**KATHY**

He didn’t have to. That was all… vibe.

**MR. EVANS**

Son, I’ve been sweet-talking local law enforcement since before you were born.

(beat)

Now let’s go move some beer.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Some people break rules.

Some people bend them.

Dad just winks at the rules…

…and the rules let him through.

MONTAGE – “THE COORS CREW COMETH”

EXT. AIR SHOW GROUNDS – 5:12 AM – INTO THE MORNING

[SHOT: **KATHY** peels out in a Coors-branded golf cart, a crate of Coors Light kegs rattling in the back.]

She’s driving like it’s a Mario Kart deathmatch. **JEREMY** clutches a seat handle like it’s a parachute cord.

**JEREMY**

This is why Dad doesn’t let you drive anything with brakes!

**KATHY**

Tell your dad he shouldn’t give me the keys unless he wants the job done fast.

[SHOT: **BILL** attempts to unload a keg off a pallet. The keg rolls, nearly takes out a vendor’s feet. The vendor shouts.]

VENDOR

Watch it! That almost hit me!

**BILL**

It’s Coors, not Bud. You’d have been blessed.

[SHOT: **JEREMY** opens a cooler and finds Bud Light cans.]

He gags.

**JEREMY**

Ugh. What is this, Michigan tailgate runoff?

[SHOT: **KATHY** at Chalet 3. She delivers the kegs, deadpan and authoritative.]

**KATHY**

Here’s your cold beer. Accept no substitutes. If anyone asks for Bud, tell them to grow taste buds.

BEER REP (squinting at the label)

This is all Coors?

**KATHY**

All day. All gold. We don’t deliver horse piss.

[SHOT: Mr. Evans rolls up with a clipboard and that dangerous early-morning sparkle in his eye. He sees a tent with Budweiser signage. Stops dead.]

**MR. EVANS**

**JEREMY**. Please tell me you didn’t unload product here.

**JEREMY**

We didn’t.

**MR. EVANS**

Good. This tent reeks of regret and St. Louis beer piss.

[SHOT: **BILL** finds a snack tent. Reaches for a soda. Sees it’s stocked with Bud-branded water bottles. Stops. Walks away in protest.]

[SHOT:    **th**              whips around a corner in the golf cart, Coors banners fluttering off the side. A Blue Angels rating points and whistles.]

**BLUE ANGELS GUY**

Now that’s a delivery.

**KATHY**

Coors only, baby.

SHOT: The crew regroups under the wing of a C-141, drenched in sweat, holding a stack of empty water cups and a half-eaten pretzel the size of a hubcap. They collapse onto a pallet like war heroes.

**MR. EVANS** (offscreen)**

That’s how we do it. Team Coors. No shortcuts. No Bud.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

While I sat half-mummified in my **MOM**’s guest room…

My friends became beasts of burden, under the watchful eye of a man who believed in two things:

Cold Coors and no compromises.

**EXT. BEHIND CHALET 3 – 7:16 AM**

The crew is catching their breath. Pallets are stacked, kegs are in place, and **KATHY** is chugging water like it’s a punishment. **BILL**’s lying flat on a patch of grass, quietly dying. **JEREMY** is wiping his face with a Coors-branded towel, trying not to vomit from effort.

Mr. Evans strolls up, hands on hips, looking completely unbothered. Not a drop of sweat on him. He surveys the scene, clearly proud of his sweaty, mildly traumatized crew.

**MR. EVANS**

That, my friends, is what we call “crushing it.”

**KATHY**

That’s what I call workers’ comp waiting to happen.

**BILL**

If I die, just put a Coors in my hand and let me be free.

**MR. EVANS**

(grinning)

You kids did good. I mean it.

(beat)

Let me tell you the secret to staying alive in this business… in any business, really.

(leans in, mock-conspiratorial)

It ain’t a crime if no one drops a dime.

**KATHY**

Jesus Christ.

**BILL**

That belongs on a t-shirt sold out of a bootleg fireworks stand.

**JEREMY**

You told me that when I was nine.

**MR. EVANS**

And it’s still true.

**KATHY**

How are you not in jail?

**MR. EVANS**

Because I know how to move quietly, work fast, keep the beer cold… and bribe airport security with donuts.

(beat)

Welcome to middle management.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Mr. Evans ran on charm, loopholes, and a weird kind of wisdom you couldn’t Google.

It wasn’t legal.

It wasn’t ethical.

But damn if it didn’t work.

**EXT. BACKSIDE OF THE MAIN CHALETS – 11:02 AM**

The sun is up. Blazing. Oppressive. The sky is mercilessly clear. Jet trails carve long scars overhead as another fighter jet rips across the horizon with a thunderous roar.

**KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** are leaning against a half-empty pallet of water bottles, sweaty, salt-streaked, and praying for death—or at least lunch.

In the near distance, they spot Mr. Evans, standing next to a man in aviators and a tight polo, both of them gesturing enthusiastically at a massive, humming white freezer truck parked near a loading dock.

**JEREMY**

(tilting his head)

Tell me he’s not doing what I think he’s doing.

**KATHY**

He’s not.

(beat)

…Is he?

**BILL**

He’s definitely saying “freezer truck.” I heard it. Three times.

**KATHY**

No. No no no. I refuse to do freezer truck work. That’s where dignity goes to die.

**JEREMY**

That’s where fingers go to die.

They watch Mr. Evans gesture animatedly toward them, then do that awful “thumbs-up while pointing” thing dads do when they volunteer you for something you didn’t agree to.

**KATHY**

Oh my God he’s bartering us.

**BILL**

We’re currency now.

**JEREMY**

We should’ve walked.

**KATHY**

We can’t. He’s our ride. That van has the only keys. And air conditioning.

**BILL**

We’re trapped. We’re going into the box.

**JEREMY**

You think they’ll even give us gloves?

**KATHY**

No. They’ll give us attitude and a crate of frozen hamburger buns.

**They watch as Mr. Evans and Clipboard Guy shake hands. It’s done. A deal is struck. Mr. Evans starts walking back, wiping his hands like a man who just closed a merger.

**JEREMY**

What could we possibly be doing in a freezer truck?

**KATHY**

Nothing good.

(beat)

This is a fresh hell.

And it's 28 degrees inside it.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

While I was sipping soup through a bendy straw and watching Price is Right reruns…

My friends were about to get stuffed in a truck full of ice cream sandwiches and despair.

(beat)

Dad called it “a favor.”

They’d remember it as The Cold Shift.

**EXT. BACKSIDE OF THE MAIN CHALETS – 11:05 AM**

**KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** are still slumped against the pallet, resigned to their freezer-truck fate, when Mr. Evans strolls up like he’s returning from the winner’s circle at the Indy 500.

**MR. EVANS**

Now before you yell at me—hear me out.

**KATHY**

Oh we’re way past yelling.

**JEREMY**

Dad, did you just sell our bodies to the frozen meat gods?

**MR. EVANS**

I just struck the best deal since I got your sister those Elton John tickets in '87.

**BILL**

(weakly)

That was a felony, wasn’t it?

**MR. EVANS**

Focus up.

(beat, dramatic pause)

How would you guys like SIX tickets… to see DEF LEPPARD… at Riverfront Coliseum… in September?

They blink. Slowly. Processing.

**KATHY**

Are you screwing with us?

**MR. EVANS**

And, because I am, in fact, the greatest middle manager in this or any timeline—

Backstage passes.

**BILL**

Back… stage?

**MR. EVANS**

That’s right. Meet and greet. Access to the green room. You might even smell the drummer.

**JEREMY**

You bartered us for Def Leppard?

**MR. EVANS**

I bartered you for rock immortality.

**KATHY**

What’s the catch?

**MR. EVANS**

Just a few hours of freezer truck work. Help the catering crew with cold storage logistics. Maybe break down a pallet or two. Light lifting. Minimal frostbite.

**BILL**

You said no more lifting.

**MR. EVANS**

I said no more keg lifting. Now it’s just… crates of frozen pretzels.

They stare at him.

**MR. EVANS** **(CONT’D)**

Come on. Def Leppard. “Pour Some Sugar on Me.” “Photograph.” One-armed drummer.

**JEREMY**

(beat)

…I’m in.

**KATHY**

I hate how fast I caved.

**BILL**

I would strip for those passes.

**MR. EVANS**

That’s the spirit!

He claps his hands, already walking toward the freezer truck, which sits ominously under the blazing sun like a white tomb of dreams and discount burritos.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

While I counted ceiling tiles and wondered if I’d ever hear stereo again…

My friends were walking into a freezer for rock and roll.

And somehow…

It felt fair.

**EXT. FREEZER TRUCK – 11:09 AM**

The sun is blistering. The air is thick with heat shimmer, and the white metal side of the freezer truck glows like it’s holding radioactive secrets.

Mr. Evans stands beside it, beaming, clipboard in hand, like a man about to change the world through logistical optimism and child labor.

**MR. EVANS**

Alright, crew. Good news. This one’s simple.

(beat)

You’re just moving a small pile of ice.

**JEREMY**

Okay, what’s the catch?

**MR. EVANS**

No catch!

(beat)

Well. You do have to get the ice from inside the freezer truck.

**BILL**

Oh, no. Oh no no no. I just got warm again.

**KATHY**

Define “small.”

**MR. EVANS**

Fifteen—

**KATHY**

—hundred?

**MR. EVANS**

Thousand. Fifteen thousand pounds.

**BILL**

(deadpan)

Are we bagging glaciers now?

**KATHY**

Do you have any idea how much 15,000 pounds of ice is?

**MR. EVANS**

Of course! That’s like… 1,875 8-pound bags.

(cheerful)

But they’re all stacked already! You just haul ‘em out, load ‘em into carts, send ‘em off to the chalets.

**JEREMY**

(bleakly)

Like we’re ice gnomes in some capitalist fairy tale.

**MR. EVANS**

You want to see Def Leppard, don’t you?

**KATHY**

Do I have to die to see them?

**MR. EVANS**

It’s a simple exchange. Work fast, get done fast.

**BILL**

You say that like we won’t emerge with hypothermic hand syndrome and emotional damage.

**MR. EVANS**

Just wear gloves! I left three pairs in the backseat of the van. They’re in decent shape. A little wet, maybe.

**JEREMY**

We’re gonna be cold. We’re gonna be wet. We’re gonna be trapped in a truck full of ice for hours.

**MR. EVANS**

And when you’re done?

(beat)

All-access passes. Unlimited hot dogs.

Backstage with Def Leppard.

(beat)

You’ll be legends.

The trio stares into the open maw of the freezer truck. It breathes fog like a sleeping beast. Inside, mountains of bagged ice wait… unbothered. Unmoved. Eternal.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Fifteen thousand pounds of ice.

Trapped in a meat locker on wheels.

In exchange for music and nachos.

Somewhere between bravery and madness, they said yes.

Because that’s what friends do.

Even when it’s freezing.

**INT. FREEZER TRUCK – HELL O’CLOCK – SAME DAY**

It’s 34 degrees Fahrenheit. Fog swirls with every breath. The light above flickers faintly, casting everything in a sickly blue glow. The walls glisten. The air bites.

And the bags of ice. Oh God, the bags.

Stacked like the bones of ancient frost giants.

Over and over and over again, the three of them move bags from the far back of the truck to the front. From there, a barely-awake Air Show volunteer grabs them and tosses them into golf carts like precious, cursed cargo.

**KATHY**

(shivering, soaked)

This is war.

**JEREMY**

(frost in his eyelashes)

This is how people die in the mountains.

**BILL**

This is how I die in Ohio.

**KATHY**

My ass is on ice.

**JEREMY**

I can’t feel my kneecaps. They’re just… gone.

**BILL**

There’s crushed ice in my shoes, **KATHY**. In my socks. Do you understand what that does to a man?

**KATHY**

I don’t even blink anymore. My face is frozen in this expression of rage and resignation.

**BILL**

Why did we do this? Why did we say yes?

**JEREMY**

Because my dad said “Backstage Def Leppard,” and we’re all idiots.

They pass another bag. Then another. Their gloves are soaked. Their fingers are numb. Every bag lands like a curse from a frozen god.

**CUT TO: EXT. NEAR THE VIP CHALET – SAME TIME**

Mr. Evans, parked in a folding chair under a small awning, is living the dream. A walking taco in one hand, a sloppy joe in the other. A giant Coors Light-branded cup of Pepsi rests by his feet. His sunglasses reflect the tarmac.

**MR. EVANS**

(to himself, mouth full)

God bless this great American tradition.

He looks out at the jets in the distance.

**MR. EVANS** **(CONT’D)**

Cold beer. Hot food. Air superiority.

(beat)

And motivated youth.

INT. FREEZER TRUCK – 54 MINUTES IN

**KATHY**

My soul is wet.

**BILL**

My lungs are wet.

**JEREMY**

My hope is wet.

They each grab one more bag. One more trip. One more step toward the van. Toward warmth. Toward salvation. Or at least, dry socks.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

While I healed in peace,

They suffered in silence.

In the cold.

In the wet.

In the hell that is fifteen thousand pounds of commercial-grade ice.

All for the love of music.

And the terrible, contagious charisma of a man with a clipboard and no conscience.

EXT. AIR SHOW LOADING ZONE – 12:23 PM

The freezer truck door swings open, groaning like a tomb.

**KATHY**, **JEREMY**, and **BILL** stumble out like war refugees, soaked, stiff, and hunched like cold-stunned raccoons. Their shirts cling. Their socks squish. Their gloves are biological weapons.

**KATHY**

(hoarse, furious)

If I die today…

Put Mr. Evans in the casket with me.

**JEREMY**

He’s your ride home.

**KATHY**

Then we’re all going down together.

**BILL**

I think I just passed a bag of ice through my bloodstream.

**MR. EVANS**

(cheerfully approaching)

There they are!

The Champions of Chill!

**KATHY**

We are damp. We are broken. We are legally no longer people.

**MR. EVANS**

Oh, come on—it wasn’t that bad! Builds character! Plus…

(He whips a plastic shopping bag off a nearby table, dramatic as hell.)

**MR. EVANS (CONT’D)**

Ta-da!

Commemorative Dayton Air Show T-shirts!

He tosses them out one by one—like he’s Santa Claus, if Santa were powered by Coors Light and toxic optimism.

They’re stiff, boxy Gildan shirts, one-size-fits-nobody, printed with an F-16 and the words "Catch the Thunder!" across the chest.

**KATHY**
You think this will keep me from testifying?

**JEREMY**
I want to burn this.

**BILL**
I’m going to wear mine every day. As a warning.

**MR. EVANS**
You kids were incredible. You did the work. You showed grit. And now?  You’re legends.

(beat)

Now go find somewhere dry and think about what you’re gonna wear to meet Def Leppard.

**KATHY**(sotto, dead-eyed)
A towel. A towel and vengeance.

They trudge away, holding their shirts like cursed relics.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
While I napped and healed, they faced frost and humiliation. They earned t-shirts, trauma, and backstage passes. And somehow…They'd do it all again.

(beat)

Because we were all a little stupid for the right reasons.

**EXT. DAYTON INTERNATIONAL AIRPORT – SHOW CENTER – 1:15 PM**

The sun is high, merciless and blinding. The air smells like hot asphalt, jet fuel, and stale nachos. The trio—**KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY**—are sprawled on the grass behind a VIP tent, t-shirts still damp, hands aching, legs half-numb from cold and work.

And then—a deep, growing rumble.

**JEREMY**
You hear that?

**KATHY** (shielding her eyes)
No. But I feel it.

**BILL**
Like a train made of war.

Suddenly, like a blade slicing through the sky—an F-15 EAGLE. Screaming past show center. 500 knots. 150 feet off the deck. The nose tips up. The jet claws into the sky. And then—it accelerates straight vertical, like physics just got mugged in broad daylight.

The sound hits them a second later.

**A THUNDERCLAP OF RAW POWER.**

Everything shakes—the ground, their ribs, their inner ear bones. It’s not a sound. It’s a full-body event. They’re silent. Eyes wide. Jaws slack. The Eagle climbs, disappearing into the haze, and just as it’s about to crack the sound barrier—It stops. Just short. 
Dancing at the edge of transonic insanity. Holding it.

Mr. Evans stands nearby with a lemonade in one hand and a half-eaten churro in the other. His sunglasses reflect a dot in the sky.

**MR. EVANS**
Now that…

(beat)

That’s the sound of dominance.

No one responds. They can’t.  The ringing hasn’t stopped.

**KATHY** (wide-eyed)
I think it just rewired my brain.

**BILL**
I saw God.

**JEREMY**
God is very loud!

**MR. EVANS**
God flies an F-15 with twin Pratt & Whitney engines and a top speed of Mach 2.5.

(beat, smiling)

And he’s on our side.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
While I lay in bed, listening to the hum of air conditioning and my mother clicking through her crosswords…They were watching angels made of titanium scream into the sky. And for once…They didn’t think about pain. They just looked up and remembered why you endure the stupid shit. Because sometimes? You get to feel this.

**EXT. DAYTON AIR SHOW GROUNDS – 1:30 PM TO 4:00 PM – TIME LAPSE MONTAGE**

The trio finds a shaded patch of grass, feet kicked out, souvenir sodas in hand, faces turned upward. They are sunburned, sore, and smiling in that dazed, post-trauma kind of way.

SHOT: TORA! TORA! TORA! show. The sky fills with smoke. Pyrotechnics explode along the flight line. Re-enactors in vintage planes buzz the crowd in a WWII recreation of the Pearl Harbor attack. **KATHY** flinches. **JEREMY** instinctively ducks. **BILL** applauds with both arms full of nachos.

**KATHY**
This is the loudest historical education I’ve ever had!

**JEREMY**
I think I just learned what fear smells like. It’s burnt gasoline and hot dogs.

**BILL**
I feel patriotic and nauseous.

SHOT: A gorgeous, sleek RF-4C Phantom arcs across the sky, camera ports gleaming.

**ANNOUNCER (V.O.)**
Ladies and gentlemen, your United States Air Force RF-4C Phantom II—capturing a high-resolution reconnaissance photograph of all you fine people right now!

**KATHY**
Smile for Big Brother.

**JEREMY**
I blinked.

**BILL**
They’ll know.

SHOT: F-14 Tomcat demonstration. The crowd erupts. Goose and Maverick fever sets in. The Tomcat does a high-speed pass, then a slow, gear-down, flaps-out dirty roll. Every Navy veteran in a 1000-yard radius salutes involuntarily.

**BILL**
This is the sexiest thing I’ve ever seen that doesn’t involve Joan Jett.

**KATHY**
You’re in public.

Kids with earmuffs on their heads. Old guys in lawn chairs filming on camcorders. Babies crying. Beer sloshing. The heat is real. The energy is rising.

**TIME: 3:58 PM**
The announcer says nothing. But everyone knows. The crowd starts shifting toward the fence. Cameras raised. Babies handed off. Beer clutched tighter. There’s a buzz in the air—not just noise, but expectation.

**KATHY**
This is it.

**BILL**
We survived the ice.

**JEREMY**
Now we get the fire.

They all look up.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
They had been through sweat. They had been through frost. They had hauled kegs and dodged golf carts and gotten scammed by a man with a clipboard and a smile. But at 4:00 PM…They were just faces in a crowd. Waiting for gods with afterburners.

**EXT. DAYTON INTERNATIONAL AIRPORT – 4:00 PM**
The airshow crowd is still. Silent. Phones raised. Children on shoulders. Every eye locked skyward.

**ANNOUNCER (V.O.)**
Ladies and gentlemen… the United States Air Force Thunderbirds.

SFX: ROAR.

SIX F-16 FIGHTING FALCONS explode into view from behind the hangars, blasting low over the runway in perfect delta formation, vapor trails etching geometry into the sky.

The trio reacts in unison:

**KATHY**
Jesus FUCKING CHRIST!.

**BILL**
That’s not flying. That’s fucking incredible!.

**JEREMY**
That’s geometry at Mach .95

**MANEUVER #1: THE BOMB BURST**
At show center, the six jets split wide in a massive arc, shooting outward like a starburst of thunder. The air shakes. A beat later—each jet rolls separately, peeling in opposite directions, tracing corkscrews of smoke across the sky. The crowd screams.

**BILL**
How are they real?

**KATHY**
They’re not. We’re hallucinating. This is the heat talking.

**MANEUVER #2: THE DIAMOND 360**
Four jets return in diamond formation, tight as teeth, no more than inches apart, circling show center at 400 knots, wings level, as if glued together by physics and arrogance.

**JEREMY**
I can’t even merge lanes that smoothly!

**BILL**
This is better than sex.

**KATHY**
Excuse me?

**BILL**
It is! It’s louder. It’s faster. And I don’t need permission.

**MANEUVER #3: OPPOSING SOLO PASS**
Two jets, coming from opposite ends of the field, converge at show center in a high-speed pass. One flies inverted, the other knife-edge. They cross within 50 feet of each other at nearly 1,000 mph. The sonic pressure slaps the crowd in the chest. Kids cry. Adults cheer. Beer gets launched skyward.

**KATHY** (laughing through shock)
That was illegal.

**JEREMY**
We cheered for a potential mid-air collision!

**BILL**
America! Fuck yeah!

**MANEUVER #4: VERTICAL ROLL CLIMB**
Solo #5 pulls vertical, rolls upward, spinning like a drill bit into the stratosphere, trail of white vapor behind it. It disappears into the haze, then drops like a dart, flipping end-over-end and recovering inches above the runway.

The crowd *LOSES*. *THEIR*. *MINDS*.

**ANNOUNCER (V.O.)**
Give it up for your United States Air Force Thunderbirds!

All six jets return in formation, soaring overhead in a perfect delta, wingtips glowing in the late-day sun. They arc into the blue like a single body made of light and speed and noise.
The trio just stands there. Still. Silent. Nothing left to say.

**KATHY**
I mean…It’s a good day.

**BILL**
It’s the best day. Even if I can’t feel my balls anymore.

**JEREMY**
Totally worth the trauma.

They look up one last time as the jets vanish into the horizon, leaving only smoke trails, ringing ears, and something they’ll never quite be able to explain.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
You think you know what awe feels like. Then the Thunderbirds show you otherwise. It’s not just flying. It’s proof that sometimes—just sometimes—humans earned their place in the sky.

**EXT. PARKING LOT – DAYLIGHT – 7:14 PM**
The sky is still blazing blue, not a hint of dusk yet. No golden hour for another hour. No relief. More hours of full-force sun, bouncing off windshields and heating the pavement until it smells like rubber and hot dogs.

**KATHY**, **JEREMY**, and **BILL** are trudging across the parking lot toward Coors Force One, sweat reactivating with every step, but grinning all the same—sunburned, stiff, and stupidly proud.

The van, with its peeling wolf mural and duct-taped CB antenna, gleams in the afternoon sun like a holy relic of poor decisions.

**JEREMY**
I’m gonna sleep in the shower.

**BILL**
I’m gonna write a will before I go unconscious.

**KATHY**
You both better live long enough to brag, because I’m not letting the others off the hook.

(beat)

They missed it.

**JEREMY**
Big time.

**BILL**
Like, they’ll never understand missed it.

**KATHY**
I want Jeff to hear everything. All of it.

Every jet. Every ice bag. Every bag of regret.

**JEREMY**
They sat at home. We got a goddamn aerobatics baptism.

**BILL**
We made memories. We earned t-shirts. We saw God and He flew an F-15.

They reach the van. Mr. Evans is already in the driver’s seat, sipping something out of a red Solo cup and humming “Rock of Ages” to himself.

**MR. EVANS**
Coors Force One is wheels-up in five, folks. If you didn’t bleed for beer and burn fo JP-4 today, I don’t want you in this van.

They collapse inside. Doors slam. The van rumbles to life.

**KATHY** (Softly, to no one)
We won.

**BILL**
And Def Leppard is just the victory lap.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
I didn’t see the Thunderbirds. Didn’t feel the shockwave. Didn’t taste the sweat or the cold or the nacho cheese dust on Bill’s chin.  But when they came home, glowing and broken, I understood something deep: Sometimes the best part of the band…Is when they come back with stories. And save one just for you.

**EXT. I-70 WESTBOUND ON-RAMP – 7:41 PM**

Coors Force One creeps forward, inch by painful inch. All around them: a sea of brake lights, minivans, lawn chairs tied to roofs, and sunburnt faces behind windshields. The aftermath of the Dayton Air Show is a traffic jam of patriotic regret.

**KATHY** (leaning her head back)
We survived fifteen thousand pounds of ice… for this.

**JEREMY**
At least it’s warm now.

**BILL**
My ass is soup.

**MR. EVANS** (grinning)
Traffic builds character.

**KATHY**
Everything builds character with you.

**MR. EVANS**
Look at my boys, child!

**EXT. I-70 – 8:05 PM**
After twenty-four minutes of hell at 3 mph, the van finally breaks free. They merge onto I-70 westbound—open highway ahead. The windows roll down. The breeze rushes in. The radio crackles, sputters, then finally lands on a half-decent station.

“Photograph” by Def Leppard starts up, grainy but perfect through cheap, wheezing speakers. They all look at each other. Laugh. Not big laughs—just that tired, knowing kind.

**KATHY**
Now this is the good stuff.

**BILL**
Turn it up. Blow the cones.

**MR. EVANS**
Only if the tape deck doesn’t eat it.

The van rattles along, the mural wolf howling at nothing, Dayton fading behind them, the music just good enough, the wind loud, the company better.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
They were sore. They were half-dead. They were half-melted and half-buzzed from jet fuel and bad nachos. But for that stretch of highway? With the windows down, and the summer air punching through the cab, and rock and roll clawing its way through the static…All was right in their world.

**EXT. PARKING LOT – 8:27 PM**
The sun is still up, but starting to think about calling it. The trio stands near their cars, plastic bags with soggy t-shirts in hand, still half-covered in dust, salt, and glory. They’ve just done a full day of physical punishment, patriotism, and propellant—but now, reality’s creeping back in.

**BILL** (stretching, groaning)
Alright, I gotta bail. I’ve got work in the morning. Early shift.

**JEREMY** (shrugs)
Yeah. I should head out too. I don’t really care about my brother that much. I’ll see him tomorrow anyway.

(beat)

It’s like, his ninth ear surgery or whatever. We’re used to it.

**KATHY** (firing off, sharp but true)
Somebody’s gotta do it.

(beat)

So… see ya.

Somebody’s gotta see ya. That lands. Not heavy. But real.

**JEREMY** looks at her, quiet for a second. Then just nods.

**BILL**
Alright then. Good day. We’ll talk soon.

They scatter. Keys jingle. Engines start. Brake lights glow in the fading light.

**JEFF (V.O.)**

You spend enough time with people, you figure out how they say what they mean…Even when they don’t say it at all.

**EXT. JEFF’S HOUSE – 8:56 PM**

A McDonald’s bag dangles from **KATHY**’s hand, grease already soaking through the corner. She stands on the porch in a faded Air Show t-shirt, sunburned and tired, her hair still slightly damp from sweat and freezer burn. She doesn’t knock at first. Just stands there for a second, eyes up at the door like it might ask her why she came.

She exhales. Then knocks. Twice.

INT. **JEFF**’S HOUSE – MOMENTS LATER

The door opens slowly. **JEFF** stands there, still in recovery mode. Head bandaged, one ear wrapped like a Halloween mummy, pajama pants, one sock.

He blinks, surprised, then gives her that wry half-smile he reserves for when he’s too tired to ask questions but still glad to see you.

**JEFF**

Let me guess.

McRib season?

**KATHY**
Don’t act like you don’t know.

(holds up the bag)

Sauce and soft bread solve most things.

**JEFF**
You come here to tell me about the jets?

**KATHY**
Later. First we eat the sandwich. Then we speak in tongues.

**JEFF**
Come on in. You smell like sunscreen and national defense.

**KATHY**
And freezer trauma. Don’t forget that.

She steps inside.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Sometimes the people who see you coming are the ones worth letting in.

Even when they show up with barbecue sauce and jet fumes.

**INT. JEFF’S LIVING ROOM – 9:06 PM**

The TV is on but muted. Bob Barker gestures silently at a Showcase Showdown. The air is still. There’s the smell of fries and sauce.

**KATHY**’s curled up on the edge of the couch, cross-legged, half-wrapped in a throw blanket that used to belong to **JEFF**’s childhood bed. **JEFF** sits nearby, ear bandaged, holding half of a McRib like it’s a science experiment.

**JEFF** (taking a bite, chewing)
Okay. You’re gonna have to explain to me what you meant by freezer trauma. Because I don’t understand.

**KATHY** 
(smiling, but tired)
You ever move fifteen thousand pounds of ice?

**JEFF**
In what world would I do that?

**KATHY**
Exactly.

(beat)

We were in a freezer truck. All three of us. No breaks. No gloves that worked. **JEREMY** was delirious. **BILL** swore he saw his ancestors. I couldn’t feel my femurs.

**JEFF**
That sounds illegal.

**KATHY**
It was! Your father called it “a favor.” Which is dad-code for “you’re gonna suffer and I’m gonna eat a sloppy joe while you do it.”

**JEFF**
Jesus.

**KATHY**
We were soaked. Freezing. Hauling bags out for hours while the air outside hit triple digits. My fingers went full popsicle. I haven’t been warm since noon.

**JEFF**
I missed all that?

**KATHY**
Yes. And you’re lucky. And also? You missed everything.

**JEFF**
That’s a hell of a sentence.

**KATHY**
I saw an F-15 scream vertical, **JEFF**. I felt it in my ovaries.We worked, we suffered, we earned it. And you weren’t there.

**JEFF**
My ear was kind of… off.

(taps the bandage)

And being reattached to my skull.

**KATHY**
Fair.

She leans her head back on the couch. Closes her eyes.

**KATHY** **(CONT’D)**
Still wish you were there.

**JEFF**
Yeah. Me too.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
Sometimes you miss the best day of someone’s life. And they bring you a sandwich anyway.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 9:13 PM

The room is dim, lit only by the muted TV glow and a little lamp in the corner.

The McDonald's bags sit crumpled on the table, fries long gone.

The McRibs are half-devoured.

**KATHY** takes another bite, chews slowly.

**JEFF** mirrors her, quiet, content.

They eat in silence. Not an awkward silence—just easy, earned. The kind that means you don’t have to perform.

After a while, **KATHY** leans back, wipes her fingers on a napkin, and glances at **JEFF**.

**KATHY**
You know…You look okay.

**JEFF** (lifts an eyebrow)
You mean for someone with his ear taped to his face?

**KATHY**
Exactly. You look… better than I expected.

**JEFF**
Thanks.

(pause)

You smell like smoke and jet fuel and… barbecue sauce.

**KATHY**
You’re not wrong.

**JEFF**
It suits you.

She smiles, just barely. Turns her head toward him.

**KATHY**
You’re smarter than people think.

**JEFF**
You’re tougher than people realize.

They sit there. Letting that land. Then they go back to their sandwiches. Quiet. Together. Everything else… can wait.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
Sometimes the best conversations don’t say much. Just enough to know you’re still seen.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 9:24 PM

The wrappers are balled up now. The McRibs are gone. **KATHY**’s curled into one corner of the couch, arms loose around her knees. **JEFF** shifts a little in his seat, like he’s thinking about something but trying to casually bring it up.

**JEFF**
So, uh…Doctor says no heavy lifting.

**KATHY** (smiling)
I’d hope so. Your ear’s stitched together like a Frankenstein puppet.

**JEFF**
Yeah. He said bass guitar probably counts as “heavy lifting.”

**KATHY**
Definitely. That thing’s half a tree.

**JEFF**
Anyway. Was thinking maybe Monday night… if you’re not busy… maybe we could get together and write? You know. Lyrics. Chords. Stuff I can’t lift.

**KATHY** (pauses, watching him)
You asking me to babysit the wounded?

**JEFF**
No. I’m asking you to show up.

**KATHY** (more softly)
Yeah. Okay. Monday night. We’ll write.

**JEFF**
Cool.

**KATHY**
You’ll owe me fries.

**JEFF**
You already owe me a new eardrum.

She smiles again. The silence comes back—calm, warm, mutual.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

No loud confessions.

No lines drawn in the sand.

Just a quiet invitation.

And someone who didn’t flinch.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 9:31 PM

**JEFF** is still on the couch, angled toward her, saying nothing, but not looking away. His wrapped ear makes him look even more vulnerable—softened, somehow.

And yet… still unreadable.

**KATHY** watches him.

Not openly. Not with a stare. Just little glances.

The kind that measure silence.

She thinks:

**KATHY** (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)

Okay.

He asked me to come over.

Brought up Monday night.

Asked me to write. That’s not nothing. That’s… something.

But he didn’t say why.

Didn’t say “I missed you.”

Didn’t say “Stay.”

He’s sitting here with me,

bandaged up, post-op,

eating a McRib like it’s a sacrament.

So… what’s the move?

Do I reach out?

Touch his hand?

Ask a real question?

Say something raw?

Or do I go nuclear?

Do I unzip his fly and settle this with my mouth and not my heart?

Would he stop me?

Would he flinch?

Would he… even know what to do?

Because I swear to God, if he says “thanks” I’m walking into traffic.

But maybe—

Maybe he’s waiting for me.

Maybe he’s scared.

Maybe he’s just trying not to push.

Maybe I am too.

She looks up.

**JEFF** catches her eyes for a Moment—just long enough to register that she’s thinking something big.

But as always… he says nothing.

Just that small, safe smile.

**KATHY** (INTERNAL)

This would be easier if he were a jerk.

If he were selfish. Or cocky. Or obvious.

But he’s not.

He’s **JEFF**.

And that’s the problem.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 9:36 PM

**JEFF** leans back on the couch, half-wrapped in a blanket, eyes on the muted TV, still catching **KATHY** in the corner of his vision.

She’s been… twitchy.

Not in a bad way. Just… agitated.

Like something’s buzzing under her skin.

And he doesn’t get it.

**JEFF** (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)

She seems… off.

Not in a bad way. Just jumpy.

Tense.

I don’t think I did anything.

I mean—I’m glad she came. I’m glad she stayed.

This is… honestly, this is one of the best nights I’ve had in weeks.

She brought me dinner.

She sat here. She listened. She made fun of my ear bandage.

In a nice way.

It’s good. This is good.

She’s good.

So why’s she acting like she’s about to bolt?

Or jump me?

Or both?

(beat)

Maybe she’s tired.

Or maybe she’s thinking too hard.

She does that sometimes. Goes quiet in a way that feels loud.

(beat)

Maybe I should say something.

He glances at her. Still close, still present. But yeah—something’s ticking in her head. He doesn’t push.

Instead?

He smiles, soft.

**JEFF**

Hey.

Reds are on at ten-oh-five. In San Francisco.

Wanna stick around and watch with me?

He says it like it’s nothing.

But he means everything.

Because this? This is a good night.

And he wants to keep it going.

**JEFF** (INTERNAL)

Don’t go yet.

Please don’t go yet.

Just sit with me a little longer.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 9:37 PM

**JEFF** looks at her from the couch, his voice casual, his face calm.

    “Reds are on at ten-oh-five. In San Francisco.

    Wanna stick around and watch with me?”

**KATHY** freezes. Not visibly. Just inside.

**KATHY** (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)

Is… is that the best he can do?

(beat)

Yeah.

Yeah, it is.

That’s his version of asking me to stay.

Of asking me to be here.

No hint. No angle.

Just baseball.

Just company.

God, it’s so soft it hurts.

I’ve been listening to **JEREMY** more.

Not just hearing him, but really listening.

The way he talks about **JEFF**… it’s different.

He doesn’t say “weird.”

He doesn’t say “off.”

He says,

“He’s just wired another way.”

And yeah. He is.

**JEFF** doesn’t flirt.

He doesn’t chase.

He doesn’t corner you into feelings.

But he opens a door.

And if I want in—

I have to walk through it.

So maybe I stop waiting for a sign.

Maybe I stop playing this like a game.

Maybe I just say—

**KATHY**

Yeah.

I’ll stay.

**JEFF**

(quietly pleased)

Cool.

She settles a little deeper into the couch. Not closer. Not further. Just… there.

**KATHY** (INTERNAL)

One game.

One night.

One more chance to learn how he works.

Because maybe that’s what love looks like with someone like **JEFF**.

Not lightning.

Not explosions.

Just a chair.

A quiet TV.

And a really, really good night.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 10:36 PM

The Reds are down by two in the third inning. The game drones softly from the TV.

**KATHY** and **JEFF** sit side by side—not touching, but close enough that the couch doesn’t feel empty between them.

She hasn’t said much in the last inning.

Then, quietly, she speaks.

**KATHY**

Can I ask you something?

**JEFF**

Always.

**KATHY**

How do you do it?

**JEFF**

Do what?

**KATHY**

Write lyrics like that.

Like you feel everything. Like you’ve lived everything. Like your chest is a cathedral and all the doors are open.

(beat)

And then… in real life…

You barely say a word.

You don’t show it.

You barely hint at it.

You just… fold in on yourself.

(beat)

How does that make sense?

**JEFF**

(pause)

It doesn’t.

Not to most people, anyway.

He shifts slightly, as if the question itself is something heavy he’s learning how to carry.

**JEFF** **(CONT’D)**

Writing’s different.

There’s time.

There’s space.

There’s no one looking at you.

I can think it through.

Rewrite it.

Cut the parts that don’t make sense, or feel too loud, or come out wrong.

It’s like…

(he shrugs)

It’s like building a bridge out of wood you’re still growing.

In real life, there’s no draft.

No second take.

Just people looking at you, waiting for you to say something,

and you don’t even know what you’re supposed to say.

(beat)

So you say nothing.

Because nothing feels safer than the wrong thing.

He doesn’t look at her as he says it. He just keeps his eyes on the screen—a batter fouls one off into the stands.

**KATHY** watches him. Really watches him.

**KATHY**

So the lyrics… they’re the right thing?

**JEFF**

They’re the only thing that comes out right.

(beat)

They’re the parts of me I wish I could just…

walk around with.

But I can’t.

Not yet.

The TV drones on. The Reds load the bases.

**KATHY** doesn’t say anything right away.

Then—

**KATHY**

Thanks for telling me that.

**JEFF**

Thanks for asking.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Some people speak in poems.

Some people speak in silence.

And sometimes, when you're lucky—

They meet in the middle.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 10:52 PM

A commercial break hits. The room dips into silence, lit only by the glow of the muted TV and the faint hum of the floor fan.

**KATHY** shifts, looking over at **JEFF**. A new thought in her head.

**KATHY**

Hey—did you hear about Tim?

**JEFF**

Tim who?

**KATHY**

Tim Wright. From high school.

He finally got a ship assignment.

**JEFF**

Wait—really?

**KATHY**

Yeah. He finished his corpsman training.

He’s getting deployed to the USS Iwo **JIM**a.

**JEFF**

No shit.

(beat)

I ran into him earlier this summer. Just randomly. He was back in town.

**KATHY**

Yeah?

**JEFF**

I didn’t even recognize him.

Swear to God, I thought he was someone’s older brother.

**KATHY**

I heard he dropped a ton of weight.

**JEFF**

But eighty pounds?

Eighty.

He’s not even the same human being. He was the soft, doughy guy who used to fail gym just for existing.

Now?

(beat)

He looks like he can break ribs on purpose.

**KATHY**

That’s what happens when you let the Navy own your ass for a year and a half.

**JEFF**

Yeah, well—he cleaned up.

Still weird seeing it, though.

Like seeing a childhood stuffed animal come back with a six-pack and military discipline.

**KATHY**

Tim, the plush bear turned war medic.

**JEFF**

Exactly.

The game flickers back.

Bases cleared. Reds down by one.

They turn back to it.

But the conversation has softened something, brought the world back in, just enough to remind them they’re still in it.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Time doesn’t just change people.

It redraws them.

Sometimes you see it.

Sometimes you feel it.

And sometimes… you sit beside someone

and realize it’s happening to you, too.

INT. **JEFF**’S LIVING ROOM – 11:08 PM

The Reds are rallying. Barely.

**KATHY**’s not watching the game anymore.

She’s watching **JEFF**’s side profile—still, calm, locked in on the screen.

One sock on. Blanket around his legs. Head wrapped in white gauze like a war hero who reads poetry.

**KATHY** (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)

If anything is going to happen, it has to be me.

That’s just… the truth.

He’s not going to make the move.

Not tonight.

Not Monday.

Maybe not ever.

Because he doesn’t operate like that.

He needs space. He needs time. He needs to be sure.

But me?

I don’t want to keep waiting.

I’ve been waiting since before the McRib.

So I have three options:

I do it now.

Tonight. In the soft part of the night, when everything’s quiet and real and we’re close enough to breathe in sync.

Or I wait until Monday.

When we’re writing. When it’s safe. When we can hide behind lyrics and chords and deflection.

Or…

I don’t.

I let this stay whatever it is.

Comfortable. Sweet. Distant. Safe.

And I go home.

And I lie awake.

And I scream into my pillow about what could’ve happened.

But if I do it now—

What is it?

A kiss?

A hand touch?

A blunt “do you want me?”

Or just curling closer on the couch and letting that be enough?

Jesus. Why can’t he just make a move?

No. That’s not fair.

This is the move.

This night. This couch. This version of him.

This is the best he can do.

And I either meet him halfway…

Or I don’t.

She looks at him again.

He shifts just slightly, eyes still on the game, but there's a little something in the way his body angles toward her. Like he's waiting, without knowing he's waiting.

**KATHY** (INTERNAL)

Now or Monday or never.

That’s the choice.

And whatever I pick…
