Not when it might change something for you.

I don’t want to betray his confidence.

But I can’t disrespect yours.

He stops there. Looks at her fully now. No dodging. Just… present.

**JEFF**

I trust you to do what you need with that.

**KATHY** (after a long pause)

You’re telling me because it’s true.

Not because you’re jealous.

Not because you’re trying to win something.

Just because I’m… worth telling.

**JEFF**

Exactly.

Another beat.

**KATHY** breathes in through her nose.

Nods once—short, sharp, but not angry.

**KATHY**

Okay.

I hear you.

And that’s all she says—for now.

But her voice is clear. Her eyes are still on him.

And nothing broke.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Sometimes being honest means holding a match in your hand—

And trusting the other person not to think you’re setting fire to the room.

**INT. JEFF’S LIVING ROOM – SUNDAY MORNING – 8:49 AM**

**KATHY** is finally sitting upright, legs crossed, one hand on her coffee mug, watching **JEFF** with that half-curious, half-intense stare she reserves for when something important is on the line—but she doesn’t want to show it.

She asks it plain:

**KATHY**

Do you consider me your friend, **JEFF**?

**JEFF** doesn’t answer right away.

He frowns. Not because he’s upset, but because he’s thinking—

actively calculating the emotional math.

**JEFF**

Yes.

(beat)

I now have three good friends.

**GILLEY**.

You.

And Jeff **CREMEANS**.

**KATHY** raises an eyebrow. She knows **GILLEY**. She obviously knows herself. But **CREMEANS**?

**KATHY**

**CREMEANS**?

**JEFF**

Yeah.

(beat)

He might make you nervous.

He’s… not like the rest of us.

**KATHY**

Not like how?

**JEFF**

He’s…

How do I say this?

**CREMEANS** is either going to be a local legend or a cautionary tale.

He’s a genius in bursts and a hazard the rest of the time.

He once duct-taped a toaster to a skateboard and called it a protest.

**KATHY** blinks.

**KATHY**

Of what?

**JEFF**

His father.

Capitalism.

The cafeteria.

I never really figured it out.

(beat)

But he’s loyal.

And weird in the kind of way I recognize.

**KATHY** smiles—just barely. That quiet, amused grin she gives when **JEFF** says something that is 100% on-brand and also deeply honest.

**KATHY**

So, I’m one of three.

**JEFF**

You’re the most recent, but not the least.

That line—"not the least"—lands with more weight than **JEFF** realizes.

**KATHY** holds his gaze just a Moment longer than usual.

**KATHY**

Thanks, **JEFF**.

**JEFF**

For the record, you’re easier to explain than **CREMEANS**.

**KATHY**

Not a high bar.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

Friendship doesn’t come naturally to me.

But when I know it’s real, I keep track.

Not because I don’t trust it—

But because I do.

**INT. JEFF’S LIVING ROOM – SUNDAY MORNING – 8:56 AM**

**JEFF** and **KATHY** sit on opposite sides of the coffee table now. Coffee cooling. Sunlight climbing through the blinds.

**JEFF** runs a hand through his hair—gingerly, around the bandage—still trying to put the last twelve hours into a framework he can explain.

He glances out the window, seemingly to nowhere in particular.

**JEFF**

**CREMEANS** would be on his way to the Baptist church right about now.

The one over by the Taco Bell near the mall.

**KATHY**

Right. The holy quadrant.

**JEFF**

No boozing.

No cards.

No dancing.

And definitely not any late-night BJs.

**KATHY** snorts into her mug. Low, sharp. Almost a choke.

**KATHY**

Christ, **JEFF**.

**JEFF**

Just saying.

That’s not a judgment. That’s a schedule.

He pauses, lifts his eyes just enough to look at her—really look at her.

**JEFF** **(CONT’D)**

Last night was…

off the grid.

For me.

**KATHY** softens again. Her fingers curl tighter around the coffee mug, but not because she’s cold.

**KATHY**

It was off the grid for me too.

Even if I don’t have a **CREMEANS** to compare it to.

They both smile.

Quiet.

Content.

Still feeling the aftershocks of what they’ve done, and what it might mean.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

There’s the world you live in…

And then there’s the one that starts when someone sees you.

Last night wasn’t just new.

It was mine.

**INT. JEFF’S LIVING ROOM – SUNDAY MORNING – 9:04 AM**

The coffee’s gone lukewarm. The light is no longer soft—it’s sharp, slicing cleanly through the blinds. Daylight’s in charge now.

**KATHY** sets her mug down on the table with a soft clink. She stretches.

**KATHY**

I should go.

Need to shower before I head over to my **MOM**’s.

She gets twitchy if I show up looking like I’ve been up to something.

**JEFF**

(soft laugh)

You have been.

**KATHY**

Exactly.

She rises, smooths her shirt, checks for any visible signs of their night together—the kind of reflex you don’t admit out loud but always do anyway.

**JEFF** stays seated. His tone shifts—not sad, just real.

**JEFF**

I’ve gotta dig into my Ohio History text anyway.

**KATHY**

On a Sunday?

**JEFF**

Got an exam Tuesday.

Summer class.

I fell behind on the graduation plan. Too much work. Too much band.

Had to cram this one in to catch up.

**KATHY** pauses mid-button on her jacket. There’s no pity in her eyes—just understanding.

**KATHY**

You really do juggle a lot.

**JEFF**

Not always well.

(beat)

But I’m trying.

She steps over to him, puts a hand on his shoulder—not dramatic, not romantic, just a connection before the day starts pulling them in different directions.

**KATHY**

Well. Read your history.

Tuesday comes fast.

**JEFF**

So does Monday night.

That makes her smile.

Not sly. Not wicked. Just warm.

**KATHY**

Yes, it does.

(beat)

You remember your assignment?

**JEFF**

Condoms.

And maybe lyrics.

**KATHY**

In that order.

She heads toward the door. **JEFF** watches her go—not wistfully, not sadly. Just grateful.

Still wrapped in the glow of something new.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  

The world didn’t stop for us.

But it shifted.

And now, even Ohio History has to compete with the thought of her—

Monday night,

and all the things we haven’t written yet.

**INT. KITCHEN – KATHY’S MOM’S HOUSE – SUNDAY, 12:17 PM**

It’s a cozy little space—sunlight coming in through the gingham curtain above the sink, a light jazz record humming through an old stereo in the corner.

**KATHY** and her mother are side by side at the counter, prepping Sunday lunch the way they always do. Tomatoes being sliced, green beans snapped, a casserole in progress.

There’s an ease in their rhythm—two women who’ve done this a hundred times before.

**MOM**

You’re cutting those like you’re in a commercial.

**KATHY**

I had practice. Last night I sliced a tomato with a plastic knife while sleep-deprived and mildly dehydrated.

**MOM**

Ah. The seasoning of youth.

They share a laugh.

**KATHY** leans in to grab the salt.

Her hair is clean, still damp at the ends, and her skin has that unmistakable post-shower brightness. She’s in a fresh T-shirt and jeans. Casual, but intentionally pulled together.

Her mother notices.

Of course she does.

But she doesn’t ask right away.

She just stirs the sauce and smiles a little to herself.

**MOM**

So.

Did the power come back on at your place, or did you just decide to rejoin the ranks of the freshly bathed?

**KATHY**

(mildly caught)

Rude.

**MOM**

Just an observation.

You look nice today.

Refreshed. Like you chose to look nice.

Not like you had to fake it for brunch with a cousin you hate.

**KATHY** smiles and shrugs like it’s no big deal, but the faint blush creeps into her cheeks.

**KATHY**

Maybe I just wanted to smell good for my **MOM**.

**MOM**

Mm-hmm.

There’s a quiet pause as they both chop and stir and move around each other like clockwork.

Then:

**MOM** **(CONT’D)**

He a good one?

**KATHY** stops just short of reaching for the garlic powder.

Doesn’t look up. Doesn’t flinch.

But her lips curl slightly—a real smile, small and unguarded.

**KATHY**

He’s a weird one.

But yeah.

I think he might be.

Her **MOM** doesn’t push.

She just pats her daughter’s shoulder, briefly, on the way to the oven.

**MOM**

Good.

Weird lasts longer than handsome.

They go back to cooking.

The room feels lighter than it has in a long time.

**KATHY** (V.O.)**  

She knew.

Of course she knew.

**MOM**s don’t need details.

Just a clean head of hair

and a real smile

on a Sunday afternoon.

**INT. KITCHEN – KATHY’S MOM’S HOUSE – SUNDAY, 12:26 PM**

**KATHY**’s pouring salad into a mixing bowl. Her **MOM** is transferring the green bean casserole into a ceramic baking dish. The whole kitchen smells like comfort.

They’re in rhythm again—food, conversation, soft jazz, and observation.

Then—

**MOM**

By the way, just so it’s on record—

I’m not ready to be a grandmother.

Let’s say… ten years. Minimum.

Maybe twelve.

**KATHY** freezes, spoon in hand, eyebrow raised.

**KATHY**

Did you just bring up grandkids while I’m still trying to figure out if he knows how to use a calendar?

**MOM**

Timing is everything.

Also—

(passively, like it’s the weather)

Please pass the ranch.

**KATHY**

(sighs, grabs the bottle from the fridge)

This is why I don’t bring people home.

**MOM**

I didn’t ask to meet him. I asked for dressing.

**KATHY** hands over the bottle.

**MOM** gives a subtle nod of satisfaction.

**MOM** **(CONT’D)**

This is the Midwest, Katherine.

Ranch goes on everything.

Salads. Pizza. Questionable life choices.

**KATHY** laughs despite herself, shaking her head as she finishes mixing the salad.

**KATHY**

You terrify me sometimes.

**MOM**

That’s how you know I’m good at this.

They clink their forks together and keep prepping lunch.

No big emotional speech. No pressure. Just ranch, and warnings, and love, Midwest-style.

**KATHY** (V.O.)**  

She said it like a joke.

But she meant it.

And somehow…

that made me feel safe.

Even if I’m not sure where this is going.

Yet.

**EXT. PUTT-PUTT COURSE – LATE SUNDAY AFTERNOON – 5:12 PM**

The sun’s still blazing, but lower now—casting long shadows across poorly-maintained astroturf and chipped fiberglass volcano holes.

**JIM**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** Evans are on hole 12. Someone's ball is floating in a water trap shaped like a pirate ship.

There are bees.

There are Mountain Dew bottles.

There is so much cussing.

**JIM**

That’s bullshit. I didn’t even hit it that hard.

**BILL**

You bounced it off the clown’s uvula, **JIM**.

**JIM**

That clown’s got a vendetta.

**JEREMY** lines up a putt with the focus of a man who’s seen too much ice in too short a time.

He sinks a two-stroke.

**JEREMY**

That’s right. Precision.

Not power.

They finish the hole and head inside for some arcade time before dinner.

**INT. ARCADE – 5:32 PM**

The NBA Jam cabinet is glowing like a religious icon.

The announcer’s voice is a nonstop fever dream of 90s basketball lingo.

NBA JAM ANNOUNCER (CABINET)

MIKE IUZZOLINO!

CAN’T BUY A BUCKET!

FROM DOWNTOWN!

HE’S ON FIRE!

**BILL**

Did anyone ever figure out who Mike Iuzzolino was?

**JIM**

That man has haunted my dreams since forever.

**JEREMY**

He's the reason I fear Italians.

They slap buttons, scream, shove each other at just the right moment. It’s glorious.

But after a brutal slam dunk…

**JIM**

(eyes narrowed)

Alright.

How bad was the airshow?

**JEREMY**

You mean the labor camp?

**BILL**

Have you ever been waterboarded with crushed ice?

**JIM**

That bad?

**JEREMY**

We were in a freezer truck for over an hour. **KATHY** almost punched a colonel.

And we got T-shirts.

**BILL**

It was hell. But then the Thunderbirds flew.

**JIM**

So you’re saying I missed everything.

NBA JAM CABINET

MIKE IUZZOLINO!

BOOMSHAKALAKA!

**JEREMY**

You missed the pain. You missed the glory.

You missed the meat sweats.

But the rest of the band’s gotta pull their weight. Airshow crew next year?

**JIM**

Let me finish dunking on this pixelated fucker, and then we’ll talk.

They laugh.

The machine flashes.

Somewhere, a child is crying because the skee-ball tickets jammed.

Everything is exactly as it should be.

**JIM** (V.O.)**  

They survived something.

And now I gotta catch up.

Preferably without the frostbite.

**INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 6:41 PM**

The fluorescent lights hum overhead. Everything smells like meat dust and fake citrus cleaner.

**JIM**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** sit in the corner booth by the window—the one with the view of the Baptist church and its judgmental parking lot signage.

Empty Mountain Dew cups and half-eaten Crunchwraps are scattered between them.

**JIM**  (leaning back, eyeing **JEREMY** sideways)
I still don’t get how your dad can just conjure tickets out of thin air.  I mean—Def Leppard? Backstage? That sounds fake.

**JEREMY**
It’s never thin air. It’s quid pro quo.

**BILL**
Latin at Taco Bell. We’re doomed.

**JEREMY**
Sometimes a sales guy gets comped tickets—arena box, pavilion, whatever—but doesn’t have a client to impress that night.  So what does he do? He trades. Maybe he needs an early morning keg drop-off. Maybe he wants an extra pallet of Zima. Maybe he wants to swap a Thursday morning delivery for Wednesday at 4:00 a.m. because he’s got a tee time. Boom. We get the tickets.

**JIM**
That’s… depressingly logical.

**JEREMY**
That’s the game. I’ve been getting comped tickets since I was in braces. I didn’t know people paid to go to concerts until high school.

**BILL**
My dad paid for us to see Huey Lewis in '87.

**JEREMY**
And that was his first mistake.

They all laugh. The kind that comes from exhaustion, salt, and familiarity.

**JEREMY** crunches a taco, then points vaguely toward the Baptist church across the lot.

**JEREMY** **(CONT’D)**
You see that? That’s the Baptist Quadrant. No drinking. No cards. No dancing.  No fucking.

**JIM**
No fun.

**BILL**
No grace.

**JEREMY**
Meanwhile, three hundred yards west, we’ve got tacos and the barter-based black market of Dayton’s liquor distribution.

**JIM**
Alcohol is the universal solvent.

**JEREMY**
And barter is the universal currency.

They raise their cups in mock reverence—clinkless, plastic, full of ice water and regret.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  
The economy doesn’t run on money. It runs on favors. On knowing who wants what. 
And having what someone else needs. Even if all you’ve got is Zima and a truck with no brakes.

**INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 6:53 PM**

The post-putt-putt feast is winding down. **JIM**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** are working through their fourth Mountain Dew refills and talking trash like it's their actual job. Then the door opens.

**JEFF** **CREMEANS** walks in. And the energy? It shifts. Like someone just cast a spell on the place. **CREMEANS** is decked out in full Sunday Best. Pressed khakis. Button-down shirt. Tie slightly loosened but still perfectly centered. Hair combed like he’s in a debate round. He walks to the soda fountain, stone-faced.

**JIM**
Oh my God. Is that…?

**BILL**
**CREMEANS**.

**JEREMY**
Yep. Fresh outta the First Baptist Fortress of Purity, and right into the Taco Bell Temple of Regret.

They watch him. And then, it happens.

**CREMEANS** picks up a styrofoam cup. Fills it. Not with Mountain Dew. But with sweet iced tea.

**JIM**
Wait—

**BILL**
No. No, no, no.

**JEREMY**
…That’s not right.

**JEREMY** leans forward, deadly serious.

**JEREMY** **(CONT’D)**
If **CREMEANS** ever drinks anything besides Mountain Dew—Assume he’s been replaced by a pod person. Tell no one. Shoot him on sight.

**BILL**
Like, no hesitation?

**JEREMY**
None. We can’t risk it.

They stare as **CREMEANS** calmly sips his iced tea, unbothered by the cosmic rupture he’s just caused. And then—the girl enters. Late teens. Pink sundress that’s a scandal in three counties. She walks with full Sunday-night youth group confidence, struts right up to **CREMEANS**, and plants a soft kiss on his cheek.

**JIM**
Okay. What the hell is happening?

**BILL**
Who is she?

**JEREMY**
Marcy. Youth choir soprano. President of Fellowship of Christian Athletes. Came in second at State Science Fair and wanted a recount.

**JIM**
Are they dating?

**JEREMY**
They pray together. But…it’s complicated.

**CREMEANS** turns, sees them watching. He gives a nod.  Raises his iced tea.  Smiles like he’s already five steps ahead in the conversation.  Then turns back to Marcy.  Totally unshaken.

**JIM** (V.O.)**  
Some people are made to be explained.  **CREMEANS**?  **CREMEANS** is made to be witnessed.  And possibly stopped.  If he drinks the wrong beverage.

**INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 6:56 PM**

The guys are still frozen, mid-taco, mid-lifetime moment.  **CREMEANS**, without a word, hands the iced tea to Marcy, who accepts it like it’s a goblet of holy water.  Then, with methodical precision, he pours himself a Mountain Dew—the correct drink, the only drink.

He turns toward the guys. Winks. Then slides into a booth with Marcy like he’s about to recite Psalms and split a Crunchwrap Supreme.

**BILL**
Okay, false alarm. Tea wasn’t for him.

**JIM**
Which means he’s still **CREMEANS**.

**JEREMY**
Yeah, but the optics…Jesus.

They all turn to study the table.  Marcy’s laughing at something he said, leaning in. She’s got the kind of build that triggers youth pastor warnings and side-eyes from church moms.
She’s not just attractive, she’s composed, sharp, and clearly all in on this interaction.

**CREMEANS** is cool as ever, eating with post-righteous confidence.

**JIM**
You think he’s ever tapped that?

They all look at each other. The pause is instant. The answer comes together like a silent unanimous vote.

**ALL THREE**
No.

**BILL**
And not unless he marries her.

**JIM**
Church wedding. Full choir. Handwritten vows.

**JEREMY**
And only then.  Once.  On a Wednesday.

**BILL**
Lights off. Shoes on. Missionary. And then a full debrief with his youth pastor the next day.

**JIM**
He’s not just waiting until marriage. He’s waiting until the second hymn after communion. They crack up. Quietly. Carefully. They don’t want **CREMEANS** to sense the irreverence.
Because if anyone can hear across planes of reality—it’s **CREMEANS**.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**  
There’s regular weird.  And then there’s **CREMEANS** weird.  And somewhere between the Mountain Dew, the choir girl, and that wink…You just know something’s happening—
But you’ll never get the full story unless you roll a 20 on Perception.

**INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 7:11 PM**

**CREMEANS** and Marcy are deep in their own private sermon two booths down.

The guys are leaning in a little now. Their food’s mostly gone. The sun’s lower through the plate-glass windows. **JIM**’s been quiet. Then, without a setup—

**JIM**
Hey.  How well do you guys really know **CREMEANS**?

**BILL**
Better than we want to. Why?

**JIM**
I’ve got two classes with him this summer. Business electives at Wright State. Intro to Finance, Organizational Theory.  He’s…

(pause)

Otherworldly.

**JEREMY**
As in, good?

**JIM**
As in, untouchable.  He doesn’t raise his voice. He doesn’t argue.  But everything the professors say, he already knows. He breaks down case studies in minutes.  I saw him fix a presentation one-handed while eating an Egg McMuffin.

**BILL**
Jesus.

**JIM**
And the wild part?  He’s bored by it. You can see it. He doesn’t even blink. It’s like his mind is running four versions of the class in parallel just to stay engaged.  

They all sit with that for a second.  Watching **CREMEANS** now with a slightly different lens.  And then **JIM** softens. Lowers his voice.

**JIM** **(CONT’D)**
It kinda made me think.  What the hell am I doing?  I mean—I’m taking classes I don’t care about.  Trying to stay on a path I never really chose.  And then there’s the garage. The band. You guys.  If we could get this thing out of **GILLEY**’s garage? Get it moving?
On the road?

He looks at them now. Really looks. For once, not joking.

**JIM** **(CONT’D)**
I’d be a real musician.  I’d be living the dream.

A long beat.

The only sound is the quiet shuffle of napkins and the faint crackle of someone filling a soda across the room.

**JEREMY** breaks the silence.

**JEREMY**
You think we can get there?

**JIM**
I don’t know.  But I’m thinking about not going back.

**BILL**
Because of **CREMEANS**?

**JIM**
Because of us.  Because maybe this isn’t just screwing around anymore.

They sit with that. Three guys.  Two tacos, one dream.  And the uncomfortable possibility that they might actually be able to pull it off.

**JIM** (V.O.)**  
**CREMEANS** might build empires out of business plans.  But me?  I just want a van. A gig. A setlist that slaps. And one shot to be more than the kid who didn’t try.

**INT. TACO BELL – SUNDAY EVENING – 7:18 PM**

The fluorescent lights above flicker once like the Taco Bell gods are weighing something big.  **JIM**’s just dropped the “maybe I don’t go back to school” bomb.  Silence has crept in.
Then, **JEREMY** speaks—measured, rare for him.

**JEREMY**
Alright. Serious question.

**BILL**
Oh shit.

**JEREMY**
I’ve been gaming with **CREMEANS** for years.  Hundreds of hours. Tabletop, basement RPGs, weird-ass campaigns where we argue about whether you can legally cast a spell while pinned under a Soviet tank.

**JIM**
Sounds scary.

**JEREMY**
It is. And I’m telling you—He’s weird, yeah. But he’s honest. Approachable. Focused.  
I’ve never seen him flake once.  Not once.

He glances over at the booth where **CREMEANS** and Marcy are now sharing a cinnamon twist like it’s holy sacrament.

**JEREMY** **(CONT’D)**
Think he’d be a good guy to manage our act?

**BILL**
Like… manage us? Like a real band?

**JIM**
Set lists. Scheduling. Promo.  Phone calls. Paperwork.

**BILL**
Okay. But how would we even pay him?  If we’re talking trucker rules—ass, grass, or gas—well…

(smiling)

We're gonna have to spend our money buying shit for him.  And I don’t know what you buy for a guy who looks like he tithes and moonlights as a dungeon master.

**JIM**
We made sixty bucks each at W.O. Wright's.  I spent mine on drumsticks and Taco Bell.  We’re not exactly flush with options.

**JEREMY**
But think about it. **CREMEANS** doesn’t need the cash. He needs a project. He’d probably do it just to write out a three-year touring logistics plan on graph paper and color-code our emotional arcs per setlist.

**BILL**
So… you're saying he'd be our Dungeon Manager?

**JIM**
Honestly? Could work.  He’s weird enough to follow us into the fire.  And smart enough to book the gig before we get there.

The three of them look at each other.  Then over at **CREMEANS**, who raises his cup of Mountain Dew as if he heard everything.

**JIM** (V.O.)**  
Bands don’t start with fame.  They start with a booth at Taco Bell.  And the crazy idea
that maybe we’re not a joke after all.

**EXT. BETHEL TOWNSHIP FARMLAND – DAY – MID-OCTOBER 1990**

Wide shots of the Bethel Township landscape. Fields of corn stalks stand golden brown, ready for harvest. Trees are ablaze with color – reds, oranges, yellows. The air is crisp and cool, a stark contrast to the oppressive heat of summer. Farmers drive combines through the fields, kicking up dust that catches the autumn sunlight.

**(SOUND:** The rustling of corn stalks in the wind, the distant hum of farm machinery, the chirping of crickets.)

**EXT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – DAY**

The garage door is wide open, letting in the cool autumn air and the colorful view. The workbench has been moved back against the wall, leaving more space for the band. **JEFF**, **BILL**, **JIM**, and **GILLEY** are gathered in the center of the garage, their breath misting slightly in the cool air. **JEFF** is animated, gesturing with his hands as he speaks.

**SOUND:** The distant sound of leaves crunching underfoot, the muffled sound of the band setting up their equipment.

**JEFF** (His voice matter-of-fact, almost clinical) I have generally crossed the t’s and dotted the i’s in life, and being devious, if not deviant, has been rare because I color inside the lines. Mostly. I think the silliest deviant thing I’ll admit happened towards the end of my freshman year at Wright State. I worked in the typing lab at a Work Study job.

**GILLEY** (Grinning) The typing lab? Jesus, **JEFF**, that’s about as deviant as a goddamn church picnic.

**BILL** (Chuckling) Yeah, what’d you do? Rearrange the alphabet on the keyboards?

**JEFF** (Ignoring them, continuing his story) The transition from the typing lab to the computer labs had been well underway for years. Sometimes we would go for an entire week with no one showing up. We had a basic daily checklist of stuff to do, but most days it took ten minutes to complete. Then there was another three hours to go. I got a lot of homework done and talked quite a bit with my coworkers. One October afternoon, at the end of the day, the conversation with one of the ladies turned to our respective sex lives…

**GILLEY** (Leaning forward, his eyes widening) Whoa, whoa, whoa. Hold the goddamn phone. What lady? Was she hot?

**BILL** (Nodding eagerly) Yeah, details, man! We need details! Was she a librarian type? Glasses? Tight bun?

**SOUND EDITING POSSIBILITIES:**

- **Layered Sound Effects:** Enhance the intimate atmosphere by layering soft ambient sounds—like distant music from the band practicing and the subtle rustling of fabric—as the montage unfolds. This creates a rich soundscape that immerses the audience in the Moment.
- **Echoing Vocals:** Use sound editing to echo **KATHY**’s voiceover, creating a haunting effect that emphasizes her internal conflict. This could give the impression of her thoughts lingering in the air long after she speaks.
- **Dynamic Volume Control:** Adjust the volume of “Just Like Heaven” to create Moments of intimacy. For instance, during the kiss, the music could soften to allow the audience to hear the characters’ whispers, then swell back up as the laughter and joy return.
- **Musical Cues:** Intertwine specific lyrics with visual Moments for dramatic effect. For example, as they tumble onto the bed, the line “Just Like Heaven” can coincide with their laughter, reinforcing the euphoric feeling of the Moment.
- **Transitional Sounds:** Use sound transitions that mimic the emotional shifts in the scene. For instance, a crescendo leading into **KATHY**’s voiceover can heighten the tension, signaling the audience to shift from joy to introspection.

**ARTISTIC CHOICES & COMMENTARY:**

- **Lighting & Blocking:** The lighting is soft, creating an intimate atmosphere while ensuring the characters are treated as ordinary individuals. The blocking focuses on their physical closeness, giving the audience a voyeuristic glimpse into their dynamic.
- **Tone & Mood:** The positive, upbeat tone juxtaposes the underlying self-destructive behaviors, setting the stage for the chaos to follow. Emphasizing their chemistry allows the audience to become emotionally invested in their relationship.
- **Nudity Approach:** Frontal nudity is introduced with care, focusing on the beauty and vulnerability of the characters rather than sensationalizing. This artistic choice serves to humanize them, contrasting their future media portrayals.
- **Voiceover Integration:** **KATHY**’s voiceovers provide insight into her inner conflict, enhancing the emotional depth of the scene. The use of The Cure’s lyrics creates a poetic connection between her past and present, setting up the narrative tension for Act 2.

**INT. W. O. WRIGHT’S COLLEGE BAR - NIGHT – LATE JANUARY 1991**

The usual boisterous atmosphere of W. O. Wright’s is muted. The bar is still crowded, but the energy is subdued. The usual cacophony of sports commentary and cheers is absent. Instead, every large-screen television is tuned to CNN, showing grainy footage of explosions and military briefings from the Persian Gulf. The faces on the screens are grim.

**(SOUND:** The low murmur of conversations, occasionally punctuated by the somber tones of the CNN news anchors. The faint, distorted sound of static and breaking news reports. The clinking of beer glasses.)

**JEFF** and **JIM** sit at a small table near the back, two half-empty bottles of beer in front of them. They’re both dressed casually, but there’s a noticeable tension in their posture.

**JEFF** (Grinning) Two bucks a head! Can you believe it?

**JIM** (Nodding, a wide smile on his face) That’s insane! We’re gonna make a killing!

**JEFF** (Pulling out a napkin and doing some quick calculations) If we get… say… four hundred people… that’s… eight hundred bucks! Just from the door!

**JIM** (Whistling) Plus the thousand we’re getting for the gig! That’s… eighteen hundred dollars!

**JEFF** (Laughing) We’re gonna be rich!



**JEFF (V.O.)** Rich. Of course, “rich” for us meant we could finally afford new guitar strings and maybe a decent microphone stand. But at the time, it felt like we were about to hit the big time.

**JIM (V.O.)** Eighteen hundred dollars. That's a lot of beer.

**JIM** (Nodding, his smile fading) Yeah.

They both look at the television screens, their faces becoming more serious.



**JEFF (V.O.)** All those guys… over there…

He thinks of the dozens of guys from their high school who are now serving in the Gulf.

**JEFF (V.O.)** Tim…

**JIM (V.O.)** Tim Wright.

**JIM** (Nodding, his voice equally low) Me too.



**JIM (V.O.)** Tim was always a good guy. Quiet. Kept to himself. But… a good guy.

He raises his bottle.

**JIM (CONT'D)** To two bucks a head!

**JEFF** hesitates for a Moment, then raises his bottle as well.

**JEFF** (His voice subdued) To two bucks a head.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on **JEFF** and **JIM**, their faces etched with worry as they stare at the television screens, the images of war flickering across their faces.

This scene highlights the contrast between the band's excitement and the somber backdrop of the war. The use of voiceover and quick cuts emphasizes the underlying anxieties of **JEFF** and **JIM**, creating a poignant and memorable Moment.

**(SOUND:** The music swells again, the chorus returning. The TV static is present but not overwhelming.)

**BEAT 13 The music crescendos as they move together.**

**(SOUND:** The full force of the song, the drums, guitars, and vocals reaching a peak. The TV static blends with the music, creating a chaotic and unsettling mix. The artillery fire is not present.)

**BEAT 14 GILLEY notices the condom has broken but grins, unbothered.**

**KATHY**’s face falters for a split second.

**(SOUND:** A sharp, discordant note cuts through the music. The TV static intensifies, a news report breaking through the music: “…ground offensive has begun…” Very faint sound of artillery fire.)

**BEAT 15 The rhythm quickens, urgency building.**

Close-up on **KATHY**’s face as she tries to maintain control.

**(SOUND:** The music becomes faster, more frantic. The TV static is almost overwhelming, the sound of artillery fire is not present.)

**BEAT 16 As GILLEY climaxes, KATHY’s expression shifts dramatically.**

**RILEY (V.O., echoing a line from "Just Like Heaven"):** "And just like that, reality crashes in."

Her smile fades, replaced by a look of dawning horror.  She should not be sensing **GILLEY**’s hot semen inside her.

**(SOUND:** The music cuts out abruptly, leaving only the sound of their heavy breathing and the loud, clear sound of a news report: “…coalition forces are advancing into Kuwait…” The distinct sound of artillery fire is now very loud and clear.)

**END MONTAGE**

The scene cuts back to the bar, the joyous facade shattered by the looming consequences.

**INT. W. O. WRIGHT’S COLLEGE BAR - NIGHT / INT. CRAMPED BATHROOM - NIGHT - INTERCUT**

**(SOUND:** The scene opens with the muffled sound of Def Leppard’s “Animal” fading out, abruptly replaced by the low, somber tones of CNN news reports about Operation Desert Storm in the bar. Simultaneously, a low, buzzing hum of a fluorescent light and the faint drip of a leaky faucet are introduced in the bathroom.)

**JEFF** is now animated, gesturing with his hands as he outlines his newfound understanding of communication.

**JEFF** (His voice earnest) 
So, what I need to do is… actively listen. You know? Really listen to what they’re saying. Not just… wait for my turn to talk.

**(SOUND:** The news report briefly mentions the potential for casualties, then fades back into a low murmur.)

**INT. CRAMPED BATHROOM - CONTINUOUS**

The bathroom is small and dingy, lit by a harsh, neon blue light emanating from a digital clock on the wall. **KATHY** stares at her reflection in the cracked mirror, her face etched with regret.

**(SOUND:** The buzzing hum of the fluorescent light intensifies, punctuated by a distinct *drip… drip… drip…* of the leaky faucet. No other sound.)

**KATHY (V.O.)** (Her voice low and filled with self-reproach) 
I knew it. I knew it was a mistake.

**INT. W. O. WRIGHT’S COLLEGE BAR - CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF** (Continuing) 
And I need to… ask questions. You know? Show that I’m… interested. In what they’re thinking, what they’re feeling.

**(SOUND:** A faint cheer erupts from another part of the bar, quickly dying down as the news report resumes.)

**INT. CRAMPED BATHROOM - CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY (V.O.)** (Her voice becoming more desperate) 
What was I thinking?

**(SOUND:** The buzzing hum and the dripping faucet continue, creating a claustrophobic atmosphere.)

**INT. W. O. WRIGHT’S COLLEGE BAR - CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF** (Continuing) 
And I need to… pay attention to their… body language. You know? Their facial expressions. Their… tone of voice.

**(SOUND:** A brief, distorted guitar riff, almost like a memory of “Animal,” cuts through the bar noise. The news report continues.)

**INT. CRAMPED BATHROOM - CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY (V.O.)** (Her voice cracking) 
It was just… sex. It didn’t mean anything.

**(SOUND:** The buzzing hum intensifies, the dripping faucet becomes more rapid, creating a sense of growing anxiety.)

**INT. W. O. WRIGHT’S COLLEGE BAR - CONTINUOUS**

**JIM** (Looking at **JEFF**, a look of surprised approval on his face) 
Wow, **JEFF**. That’s… actually… pretty good.

**JIM (V.O.)** Maybe… maybe there’s hope for him after all.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **JIM**’s face, a genuine smile spreading across his lips.

**INT. CRAMPED BATHROOM - CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY (V.O.)** (Her voice filled with despair) 
But… it felt like it meant something. To me.

**(SOUND:** The buzzing hum and the dripping faucet reach a crescendo, creating a sense of overwhelming hopelessness.)

**INT. W. O. WRIGHT’S COLLEGE BAR - CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF** (Continuing, his voice gaining confidence) 
I think… I think I can do this. I think I can… be a better communicator.

**JEFF (V.O.)** I’m going to try. I’m really going to try.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **JEFF**’s face, his expression now determined and hopeful.

**INT. CRAMPED BATHROOM - CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** looks at her reflection, tears welling up in her eyes.

**KATHY (V.O.)** (Her voice barely a whisper) 
I’m so… lost.

The buzzing hum and the dripping faucet suddenly cut out, leaving only the sound of **KATHY**’s soft sobs. The news report from the bar fades almost entirely, becoming a distant, muffled echo.

**(FINAL SHOT):** A split screen, one side showing **JEFF**, looking hopeful and determined, the other side showing **KATHY**, her face filled with despair. The contrast is stark, highlighting the diverging paths they are now on.

**EXT. PARK LAYNE DRUGSTORE PARKING LOT - DAY – LATE JANUARY 1991**

The parking lot is bleak and windswept, a few bare trees shivering in the cold winter air. Patches of dirty snow cling to the edges of the asphalt. Across the street, the familiar golden arches of McDonald’s loom large, a stark reminder of her recent encounter with **JEFF**.

**(SOUND:** The wind whistling through the bare trees, the distant rumble of traffic on the nearby road, the crunch of gravel under **KATHY**’s feet.)

**KATHY**’s beat-up car, a rusty, faded color, sits in the parking lot. She gets out, slamming the door with more force than necessary. Her face is set in a determined expression, her eyes fixed on the drugstore across the lot.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **KATHY**’s boots as she walks across the parking lot, the crunch of gravel under her feet amplified in the sound mix. Then a quick cut to the McDonald's sign across the street.

**INT. PARK LAYNE DRUGSTORE - CONTINUOUS**

The drugstore is brightly lit and sterile, a stark contrast to the bleakness outside. **KATHY** strides confidently down the aisles, her eyes scanning the shelves.

**(SOUND:** The generic Muzak playing softly in the background, the muffled sounds of other shoppers, the beeping of a cash register in the distance.)

She approaches the pharmacy counter, where a bored-looking pharmacist stands waiting.

**KATHY** (Her voice clear and direct) 
How do I get morning‑after pills?

The pharmacist points to a beige wall‑phone without making eye contact.

**PHARMACIST**  
Call this number. Have them fax the prescription.

Kathy dials Planned Parenthood, plants her hip against the Formica, and waits.  
The fluorescent hum creeps under her skin; the same Muzak loop restarts for the fourth time.

Two hours later…

**PHARMACIST (droning)**  
Any questions or concerns? Would you like the—

**KATHY**  
No. I’m done.

She pays, pockets the kit, and breezes outside.  The pharmacy’s neon cross flickers, one tube dead, mirroring the half‑lit arches across Dayton-Lakeview Road.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
Just like buying a pack of gum.

**EXT. PARK LAYNE DRUGSTORE PARKING LOT - CONTINUOUS**

Back in her car, **KATHY** sits for a Moment, staring straight ahead. She opens the bag, takes out the pills, and swallows them dry, without even a sip of water.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **KATHY**’s hand as she swallows the pills. The camera then focuses on her face, her expression blank and emotionless.

**(SOUND:** The sound of **KATHY** swallowing the pills, amplified slightly in the sound mix. Then, the sound of a cassette tape being ejected from a car stereo.)

She reaches over and ejects a cassette tape from the car’s stereo. The tape, a homemade demo, lies on the dashboard. She’s been listening to it on the drive over, but now she’s not in the mood for music.

**KATHY (V.O.)** 
Is this a good day to skip practice?

She considers the question for a Moment, her eyes fixed on the McDonald's across the street.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on the McDonald's sign, then slowly zooms out, showing **KATHY** sitting alone in her car in the bleak parking lot.

**(SOUND:** The wind whistling through the trees, the distant rumble of traffic. A faint, distorted guitar riff, almost like a ghost of “Animal,” plays briefly, then fades away.

**(FINAL SHOT):** **KATHY** sits in her car, her face a mask of uncertainty and regret. The camera slowly pulls back, emphasizing her isolation in the vast, empty parking lot. The McDonald's sign looms large in the background, a stark reminder of the events that led her here.

---
**EXT. GILLEY’S FAMILY DRIVEWAY - DAY – CONTINUOUS**

Ten minutes later, **KATHY** pulls into **GILLEY**’s driveway. Other band members' cars are already there. The garage door is open, and she can hear the sounds of movement and muffled conversation.

**(SOUND:** The crunch of tires on the gravel driveway, the distant sound of power tools from a nearby house, the muffled voices of the band members.)

As **KATHY** gets out of her car, she sees Mr. Rick **GILLEY**, **GILLEY**’s father, at the end of the driveway, checking the mailbox. She remembers his words of encouragement from the past, his belief in her talent.  Mr. **GILLEY**’s face as he checks the mailbox. Then a quick cut to **KATHY**’s face, a flicker of recognition and then a look of sudden understanding.

**KATHY (V.O.)** He believed in me. And I… I just…

She realizes the extent of her recklessness, the lack of control she’d allowed herself to have.

**KATHY (V.O.)** It’s my body. My responsibility. Never again.

A newfound resolve hardens her expression. She closes her car door and strides towards the garage.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE - CONTINUOUS**

The band members are amid rearranging equipment, preparing for practice. **JEFF** is talking animatedly to **JIM**, probably still rehashing the previous night’s events. **GILLEY** is conspicuously absent.

**(SOUND:** The clatter of equipment being moved, the muffled conversations of the band members.)

**KATHY** enters the garage, her presence immediately commanding attention. She pointedly ignores **JEFF**, her gaze settling on **GILLEY** who is now present. She gives him a simple, almost imperceptible shake of her head "no". **GILLEY** nods slightly back to her.

She walks over to **JIM**.

**KATHY** (Her voice clear and direct) 
JIM, I need your help.

**JIM** (Surprised) 
With what?

**JIM (V.O.)** No one ever asks me for help with instruments.

He’s intrigued, even a little flattered.

**KATHY** 
I need a piano.

**JIM** (Blinking) 
A piano?

**KATHY** 
Yeah. I’m going to learn to play. I want to add it to our sound.

**BILL**, who is tinkering with his synthesizer, looks up, perplexed.

**BILL** 
But… I play keyboards.

**KATHY** (Turning to **BILL**, her voice gentle but firm) 
You play whatever the song requires, **BILL**. You’re a master of so many instruments. Restricting you to your Casio is limiting.

She looks back at **JIM**.

**KATHY (CONT'D)** Can you find me one?

**JIM** (A wide grin spreading across his face)
I’ll see what I can do.

**JIM (V.O.)** This is a challenge. I like challenges.

**KATHY** (Turning back to **BILL**) 
Can you play violin?

**BILL** (Shrugging) 
Yeah. I haven’t played in, like, three years, since high school.

**KATHY** 
JIM will buy one next payday.

She says it with such confidence that no one questions it.

**BILL (V.O.)** 
What the heck just happened?

**KATHY** then turns her attention back to **JIM**.

**KATHY** 
So, how did the negotiations go at W.O. Wright’s?

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE - CONTINUOUS**

The garage is still cluttered, the lingering scent of sweat and guitar strings hanging in the air. The howling of the neighborhood dogs has subsided, leaving a strange quiet. **JEFF** and **JIM** are putting away the last of the equipment, while **KATHY** stands slightly apart, lost in her thoughts.

**(SOUND:** The clatter of equipment being packed away, the low murmur of conversation between **JEFF** and **JIM**, the distant rumble of traffic.)

**JEFF**, noticing **KATHY**’s distant expression, turns to her, a hopeful look on his face.

**JEFF** (His voice hesitant) 
Hey, **KATHY**… I was wondering… would you maybe want to… take a ride?

He gestures towards his beat-up Ford Escort parked in the driveway.

**KATHY (V.O.)** 
He’s still trying.

She recognizes the effort he’s making, the attempt to connect. A small, almost involuntary smile touches her lips.

**KATHY** (Her voice gentle) 
Thanks, **JEFF**. But… I think I’m just going to go home.

**JEFF**’s face falls slightly, but he nods understandingly.

**JEFF** (His voice a little disappointed) 
Oh. Okay.

He reaches into his backpack and pulls out a cassette demo. He holds it up, a slightly mischievous grin spreading across his face.

**JEFF (CONT'D)** 
But… check this out.

**KATHY** looks at the cassette, her curiosity piqued.

**JEFF (CONT'D)** 
I scored a demo.

He hands her the cassette. The cover is simple, almost stark: a grainy black and white photo of a topless man sitting in a chair, wearing sunglasses indoors. The title, “*Uptown Avondale*,” is printed in a simple, sans-serif font.

**KATHY** (Examining the cassette)
“*Uptown Avondale*”?

**JEFF** (Nodding enthusiastically) 
Yeah! It’s The Afghan Whigs.

**KATHY** (Frowning slightly) 
The Afghan Whigs? I’ve heard of them. They’re from… Cincinnati, right?

**JEFF** (Nodding) 
Exactly! This is their demo. Before they were… you know… *The* Afghan Whigs.

**JEFF (V.O.)** This is a big deal. The Afghan Whigs were… they are different. Raw. Intense. They are… real.

**JEFF** (Continuing, his voice filled with excitement) 
It’s called “*Uptown Avondale*.” Avondale’s this… industrial suburb in Cincinnati. It’s… rough. GE builds airplane engines there. But there’s something… beautiful about the name. You know?

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on the plastic cover, the grainy photo of the topless man. Then a quick cut to **KATHY**’s face, her expression now a mixture of curiosity and intrigue.

**JEFF** (Continuing) 
I think you’ll really dig it. It’s… it’s like something we could do.

**KATHY** looks at the cassette again, turning it over in her hands.

**KATHY (V.O.)** He’s actually… thoughtful.

She considers the offer again. The idea of listening to this demo, this glimpse into the raw, early work of a band she respects, is suddenly appealing.

**KATHY (V.O.)** Maybe… maybe it wouldn’t be so bad.

But the memory of the previous night, the conflicting emotions, the feeling of being used… it’s all still too fresh.

**KATHY** (Her voice gentle but firm) 
Thanks, **JEFF**. Really. But… I just need to go home.

She hands the box back to him.

**JEFF** (His voice a little disappointed, but understanding) 
Okay. No problem.

The camera lingers on the cassette in **JEFF**’s hand, then slowly zooms out, showing **KATHY** turning to leave the garage.

**(FINAL SHOT):** **KATHY** walks away, leaving **JEFF** standing in the cluttered garage, the “*Uptown Avondale*” demo clutched in his hand. The setting sun casts long shadows across the room, emphasizing the quiet solitude of the Moment.

**EXT. GILLEY’S FAMILY DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** trudges down the driveway toward her car, the cold January air biting at her face. She’s grateful for her thigh-high leather boots, which, while hot during practice, now provide welcome warmth and traction on the icy surface.

**(SOUND:** The crunch of **KATHY**’s boots on the icy driveway, the wind whistling through the bare trees, the distant rumble of traffic.)

She reaches her car, a thin layer of frost coating the windows. She pulls out an ice scraper and begins scraping the frost off the windshield, then moves around the car, clearing each window in turn.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **KATHY**’s hand scraping the frost, the sound amplified in the mix. Then a quick cut to her face, her breath misting in the cold air.

She gets into the car, shivering, and turns on the engine. She directs the heated air from the vents towards her hands, trying to warm them. She flips on her headlights and is startled to see **JIM** standing just outside the driver’s side door.

**(SOUND:** The engine turning over, the whoosh of the car’s heater, the sudden, sharp intake of **KATHY**’s breath.)

**KATHY** tries to roll down the window, but it’s frozen solid. She sighs in frustration and opens the door slightly.

**JIM** (His voice low and urgent) 
What the fuck was that?

**KATHY (V.O.)** Not now, Jim.

**KATHY** (Her voice tired) 
Jim, this is a bad time. I’m tired.

**JIM** (His voice insistent) 
No, this is important. Jeff…he doesn’t get it. He doesn’t understand women. He *definitely* doesn’t understand *you*.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **JIM**’s face, his expression serious and concerned. Then a quick cut to **KATHY**’s face, her expression a mixture of fatigue and frustration.

**JIM (CONT'D)** 
You weren’t exactly subtle, Kathy. You’ve been practically throwing yourself at him for weeks.

**KATHY** (Her voice defensive) 
I wasn’t…

**JIM** (Interrupting her) 
Yes, you were. And he missed every single goddamn signal.

He lowers his voice, leaning closer to the open car door.

**JIM (CONT'D)** 
We talked last night. He was… he was actually trying to figure things out. He was determined to… improve himself. He was talking about listening.

**KATHY (V.O.)** Listening.

**JIM** (Continuing, his voice becoming more emphatic) 
But listening works both ways, **KATHY**.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on Jim’s eyes, his gaze intense and direct.

**KATHY** (Her voice barely a whisper) 
Is it… too late?

**JIM** (Shaking his head) 
With Jeff? You could restart a conversation with him that started five years ago, and he’d pick right back up where you left off. He wouldn’t even notice.

**JIM (V.O.)** The guy’s got the emotional intelligence of a goddamn toaster oven.

**JIM** (Continuing, his voice becoming more serious) 
But…if he ever *does* figure it out…if he ever develops some goddamn empathy…then this…this little retreat of yours…it’s not going to go over well.

**JIM (V.O.)** 
She needs to understand. This is a one-time pass.

**JIM** (Looking directly at Kathy, his voice firm) 
Be grateful for his…behavior this time, Kathy. Because he’s completely unaware of how he’s *supposed* to react. But when he figures it out…then we’re all going to have to change how we deal with him.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on Kathy’s face, her expression a mixture of understanding, apprehension, and a dawning realization of the complex dynamics at play. The wind continues to whistle through the trees, a constant reminder of the cold, harsh reality of the situation.

**EXT. GILLEY’S FAMILY DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY**’s tears fall silently, her voice barely a whisper.

**KATHY** (Her voice trembling) 
Jim… I… I’m so sorry. I’m… I’m such a mess.

**JIM** looks at her, his expression filled with concern. He reaches out to touch her shoulder, but she flinches away.

**KATHY** (Her voice rising slightly) 
Don’t touch me. Please.

**JIM** withdraws his hand, a look of hurt crossing his face.

**JIM** (His voice soft) 
Kathy…

**KATHY** (Interrupting him) 
Just… leave me alone, please.

She turns away, her voice thick with emotion.

**JIM** (His voice gentle but firm) 
Kathy…

**KATHY** (Cutting him off) 
I said leave me the fuck alone!

She slams the door shut on **JIM**.

**JIM** stands there for a moment, his face etched with a mixture of confusion, hurt, and a lingering sense of hope. He knows she’s hurting, but he also knows he can’t help her.

**INT. KATHY’S CAR - CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** sits in her car, her head resting against the steering wheel. She’s crying uncontrollably, her sobs echoing through the empty driveway.

**KATHY (V.O.)** (Her voice muffled by her sobs) 
I’m such a mess. I’m so… weak.

She wipes her tears away, but they continue to flow freely.

**KATHY (V.O.)** 
I’m so sorry, Jeff. I’m so sorry, Jim.

She takes a deep breath, trying to control her emotions.

**KATHY (V.O.)** 
I just need some time. Some time to… figure things out.

She starts the car and drives away, leaving behind the quiet suburban street and the empty garage.

**INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE - LATER**

**JEFF** and **JIM** are packing up the rest of their equipment, their conversation subdued. The incident with **KATHY** has left a lingering awkwardness in the air.

**JEFF** (His voice low and hesitant) 
Is she okay?

**JIM** (Shaking his head) 
I don’t know.

**JEFF** (Sighing) 
She’s going through a tough time right now.

**JIM** (Nodding) 
Yeah. She is.

There’s a long pause, both men lost in their thoughts.

**JEFF** (Breaking the silence) 
Hey, Jim…

**JIM** (Looking up) 
Yeah?

**JEFF** (Hesitating for a Moment) 
Can I… can I talk to you about something?

**JIM** (Surprised) 
Sure, Jeff. What’s up?

**JEFF** (His voice low and earnest) 
It’s about… Kathy.

**JIM** (His eyebrows raising)
Kathy?

**JEFF** (Nodding) 
Yeah. I… I think I might… like her.

**JIM** (Chuckling) 
Finally!

**JEFF** (His face turning red) 
No, I mean… I really like her. I… I think she’s amazing.

**JIM** (Smiling) 
Well, that’s good to know.

**JEFF** (His voice becoming more serious) 
But… I’m not sure if she… feels the same way.

**JIM** (Shrugging) 
You’ll never know unless you ask.

**JEFF** (Hesitating) 
I don’t know if I can…

**JIM** (Placing a hand on **JEFF**’s shoulder) 
Hey, it’s okay. Just be yourself.

**JEFF** (Taking a deep breath) 
Okay.

He turns towards the door, a newfound determination in his eyes.

**JEFF (CONT'D)** Thanks, Jim.

**JIM** (Smiling) 
No problem.

**JEFF** leaves the garage, leaving **JIM** alone with his thoughts. He watches **JEFF**’s retreating figure, a sense of hope and optimism filling him.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on **JIM**, a gentle smile on his face. He knows **JEFF** is about to embark on a journey, a journey that will change him forever.

**INT. GILLEY'S ROOM - NIGHT**

The room is dimly lit, a single lamp with a low-watt bulb casting long, distorted shadows across the walls. Instruments and posters are visible, but slightly out of focus, creating a sense of claustrophobia.

**(SOUND:** The opening chords of U2’s “So Cruel” begin, Bono’s voice filled with raw emotion and a sense of desperation. The sound is slightly muffled, as if coming from a nearby room, adding to the intimate atmosphere.)

**MONTAGE**

**BEAT 1 KATHY and GILLEY are entangled on the bed.**

**GILLEY** is on his back, **KATHY** straddling him. He’s insistent on skipping the condom. The camera is positioned low, looking up at **KATHY**, emphasizing her dominance in this initial Moment.

**(SOUND:** The driving drumbeat of “So Cruel” kicks in. The muffled sound of the television continues in the background, a reminder of the world outside.)

**KATHY (V.O., echoing a line from "So Cruel"):** “You’re dangerous, you’re beautiful.”

**BEAT 2 KATHY hesitates, her face flickering with indecision.**

Close-up on her face, her eyes darting nervously.

**(SOUND:** A distorted guitar riff from the song. The television static briefly intensifies, a news anchor’s voice cutting through: “…ground offensive…” then fades back down.)

The camera lingers on a crumpled condom wrapper on the floor, a stark reminder of the previous encounter.

**(SOUND:** A percussive beat from the song. A subtle sound effect of fabric rustling.)

She arches her back, her posture deliberately provocative.

**(SOUND:** The chorus of “So Cruel” begins, Bono’s vocals soaring. The television static is constant.)

Close-up on his hands, his touch confident and assured.

**(SOUND:** A distorted guitar chord. A subtle sound effect of skin on skin.)

The falseness of her expression is subtle but perceptible.

**(SOUND:** A high-pitched vocal cry from Bono. The TV static is slightly louder.)

**BEAT 7 They switch positions, KATHY now on top.**

The camera angle shifts, now looking down on **GILLEY**, emphasizing **KATHY**’s attempt to regain control.

**(SOUND:** A heavy drumbeat and distorted guitar riff. The television static becomes more prominent.)

**BEAT 8 Close-up on KATHY’s hands gripping GILLEY’s shoulders.**

Her nails dig into his skin, a hint of desperation in her grip.

**(SOUND:** A sharp, discordant note cuts through the music. A subtle sound effect of fingernails scratching skin.)

**BEAT 9 GILLEY whispers something in KATHY’s ear.**

Close-up on **KATHY**'s ear and the side of her face.

**GILLEY** (Whispering) You like it rough, don’t you?

**(SOUND:** The music continues. The TV static is still present.)

**BEAT 10 Their intimacy is framed by the window.**

Moonlight highlights the sheen of sweat on their bodies. Brief, tasteful glimpses of frontal nudity are shown, focusing on the curves of their bodies and the play of light and shadow.

**(SOUND:** A softer, more melodic section of the song plays. The TV static fades slightly. Very faint sound of artillery fire.)

**BEAT 11 KATHY’s movements become more mechanical.**

Close-up on her face, a flicker of frustration crossing her features.

**(SOUND:** The music continues, the drumbeat driving the scene forward. The TV static is still present.)

**BEAT 12 The music swells, masking the silence between them.**

**KATHY** throws her head back, eyes closed, faking ecstasy.

**(SOUND:** The music reaches a crescendo, the drums and guitars pounding. The TV static is almost overwhelming.)

**KATHY (V.O., echoing a line from "So Cruel"):** "And you cut me up, and you cut me down."

**BEAT 13 GILLEY reaches climax.**

Close-up on his face, his expression a mixture of pleasure and relief.

**(SOUND:** A sharp, discordant note cuts through the music. The TV static intensifies, a news report breaking through: “…coalition forces…” Very faint sound of artillery fire.)

**BEAT 14 KATHY bites her lip, forcing a smile as he relaxes beneath her.**

Close-up on **KATHY**'s face.

**(SOUND:** The music softens slightly. The TV static continues.)

**BEAT 15 As they separate, KATHY’s facade drops** Moment**arily.**

Close up on **KATHY**'s face, her eyes wide with a mix of despair and confusion.

**(SOUND:** The music fades out abruptly, leaving only the sound of their heavy breathing and the loud, clear sound of a news report: “…advancing into Kuwait…” The distinct sound of artillery fire is now very loud and clear.)

**KATHY (V.O., echoing a line from "So Cruel"):** "I'm so cruel."

**BEAT 16 KATHY lies beside him, her smile a mask.**

The camera lingers on her face, capturing the complexity of her emotions—satisfaction, despair, and confusion.

**(SOUND:** The low murmur of the television resumes, the distant sound of fighter jets and artillery fire a constant reminder of the world outside. Very faint sound of a heartbeat.)

**END MONTAGE**

**INT. GILLEY'S ROOM - NIGHT**

The room is dimly lit, but not in a romantic way. More like a cheap motel room after a long tawdry night. A single, bare bulb hangs precariously from the ceiling, casting harsh shadows that accentuate the mess. The air is stale, thick with the smell of sweat, cigarettes, and cheap cologne. The camera slowly pans across the room, taking in the details: a half-empty bottle of whiskey on the nightstand, a pile of crumpled clothes on the floor, and a discarded condom wrapper lying near the edge of the bed like a forgotten cigarette butt.

**(SOUND:** The faint, tinny sound of a late-night radio station playing a bluesy guitar riff. The sound of heavy breathing gradually returning to normal.)

**GILLEY** removes a used condom, dropping it carelessly onto the floor. He reaches over, giving **KATHY**’s breast a gentle shake, more like nudging a sleeping animal than an affectionate gesture.

**GILLEY (His voice casual, almost bored)** 
Hey, **KATHY**… I think this is the last time.

**GILLEY (V.O.)** 
Like a spent firecracker. Fizzled out. Time to light another one.

**KATHY (V.O.)** 
He treats me like a stray dog he picked up off the street. Fed me, gave me a place to sleep for the night, now it's time to kick me back out.

**KATHY**, still enveloped in a post-orgasmic haze, barely registers his words.  She blinks slowly, her eyes unfocused.

**GILLEY (Leaning closer, his voice soft yet firm, like a salesman closing a deal)** Seriously, we can’t keep doing this.

**KATHY (V.O.)** Keep doing what, exactly? Screwing? Or pretending this means something?

**KATHY** blinks again, her mind slowly catching up.  A flicker of annoyance crosses her face.

**KATHY (Her voice laced with sarcasm)** 
Not good enough for you? Or maybe you just want something… *different*?

**GILLEY (V.O.)** 
Different is always good. Keeps things interesting.

**GILLEY** gets out of bed and begins to pace, naked, speaking candidly, as if discussing the weather.

**GILLEY (Shrugging)** 
It's not that, **KATHY**. It’s just… I like the chase. This… this could ruin us before we even get started.

**KATHY** props herself up on her elbows, her eyes following **GILLEY**’s movements. Her gaze is a mix of confusion and a growing sense of anger.

**KATHY (Her voice rising slightly)** 
Then why did we just *fuck*?

**KATHY (V.O.)** 
Good question. Maybe I should ask him that again, but slower. And louder.

**GILLEY** stops pacing, turning to face her with a sheepish grin, like a kid caught with his hand in the cookie jar.

**GILLEY** (Shrugging again) 
Honestly? Didn't hit me until after.

**KATHY**’s brows knit together, processing his words with growing disbelief.

**KATHY** (Her voice incredulous) 
Is that… *normal* for guys?

**GILLEY (V.O.)** 
Normal is overrated.

**GILLEY** shrugs again, a hint of humor in his tone, as if this is all a big joke.

**GILLEY (Grinning)** 
Pretty hard to lie right after.

**INT. GILLEY'S ROOM - NIGHT - CONTINUOUS**

**(SOUND:** The faint, tinny sound of the late-night radio station continues. The sound of heavy breathing has subsided, replaced by an unsettling silence punctuated by the occasional rustle of sheets.)

**BEAT 9 KATHY shifts, sitting up fully now, pulling the sheet around her. Her expression is a mix of intrigue, disbelief, and a growing sense of unease.**

**KATHY** (Her voice laced with a bitter edge) And… how was it… *for you*?

**(Tarantino-esque Inner Monologue – KATHY):**

**KATHY (V.O.)** Like I don’t already know the answer to that.



**GILLEY (V.O.)** Mission accomplished.

**(Zalman King Glamour Shot - Countered by Verhoeven):**

*King:* A close-up of **KATHY**’s bare shoulders and the curve of her neck, the soft light highlighting her delicate features.

*Verhoeven:* The camera focuses on the goosebumps on her arms, the slight tension in her neck muscles. The shot is not about beauty; it’s about vulnerability and discomfort.

**BEAT 10 GILLEY nods, acknowledging the obvious with a smug look that he tries to pass off as sincerity.**

**GILLEY** (His voice smooth, oozing with false sincerity) Great. Could get addictive.

**(Tarantino-esque Inner Monologue – GILLEY):**

**GILLEY (V.O.)** Already is. For her, anyway.



**KATHY (V.O.)** Addictive for who?

**BEAT 11 Silence fills the room, the tension now thick enough to cut with a knife. KATHY’s expression shifts from a forced attempt at nonchalance to a mix of resolve and resignation.**

**(Zalman King Glamour Shot - Countered by Verhoeven):**

*King:* A wide shot of the bed, the tangled sheets and the two bodies creating a visually arresting image of post-coital intimacy.

*Verhoeven:* The wide shot is messy and unglamorous. The sheets are rumpled and stained. The bodies are not intertwined in a romantic embrace; they are simply lying apart, the space between them a visual representation of their emotional distance.

**(SOUND:** The radio station begins to play a slow, melancholic blues song, the music mirroring the growing tension in the room.)

**BEAT 12 KATHY swings her legs over the side of the bed, beginning to dress hurriedly, as if she can’t get out of there fast enough.**

**KATHY** (Her voice flat, devoid of emotion) So… just pretend this never happened?

**(Tarantino-esque Inner Monologue – KATHY):**

**KATHY (V.O.)** Like I could ever forget this.



**GILLEY (V.O.)** Easy for me.

**BEAT 13 GILLEY watches her, his features softening slightly, a hint of genuine regret flickering in his eyes for a fraction of a second, before it's replaced with his usual mask of indifference.**

**GILLEY** (His voice low, almost a whisper) Yeah. Already have.

**(Zalman King Glamour Shot - Countered by Verhoeven):**

*King:* A close-up of **GILLEY**’s face, his eyes filled with longing as he watches **KATHY** dress.

*Verhoeven:* The close-up is unflattering, the harsh light revealing the lines around his eyes and the slight puffiness of his face. The longing is not romantic; it’s more like a fleeting Moment of self-reflection.

**(SOUND:** The volume of the radio station increases slightly, the blues guitar becoming more prominent.)

**BEAT 14 KATHY pauses, buttoning her shirt, processing the finality of his words. Her face is a canvas of disappointment, anger, and a deep, gnawing sense of emptiness.**

**(Tarantino-esque Inner Monologue – KATHY):**

**KATHY (V.O.)** Just like that. Gone. Erased. Like it never even happened.



**GILLEY (V.O.)** Next.

**BEAT 15 She finishes dressing, standing by the door with an air of defiance, her posture rigid, her eyes fixed on some point beyond GILLEY.**

**KATHY** (Her voice cold and distant) Fine. See you at practice.

**(Zalman King Glamour Shot - Countered by Verhoeven):**

*King:* A shot of **KATHY** framed in the doorway, the light from the hallway creating a halo around her, emphasizing her beauty and strength.

*Verhoeven:* The shot is stark and unflattering. The light from the hallway casts harsh shadows on her face, making her look tired and worn. The framing emphasizes her isolation and vulnerability.

**(SOUND:** The radio station abruptly cuts to static, followed by a brief news bulletin about the war. The sound of artillery fire is heard faintly in the background.)

**BEAT 16 KATHY exits, leaving GILLEY alone in the dimly lit room. He exhales deeply, running a hand through his hair, then sits on the edge of the bed, his expression now completely blank, as if he’s already moved on to the next thing.**

**(Tarantino-esque Inner Monologue – GILLEY):**

**GILLEY (V.O.)** Time to find some breakfast.



**KATHY (V.O.)** I hate him. I hate myself.

**(VISUAL):** The camera lingers on the empty bed, the rumpled sheets, and the discarded condom wrapper, a stark reminder of the fleeting and ultimately meaningless encounter.

**(SOUND:** The radio station returns, now playing a upbeat pop song, completely incongruous with the emotional weight of the scene.

**END SCENE**

**EXT. W.O. WRIGHT’S - LOADING DOCK - FRIDAY MORNING**

The grey light of a January morning illuminates the back of W.O. Wright’s. A large beer delivery truck is backed up to the loading dock, its engine idling roughly. **JEREMY** Evans, looking bleary-eyed and miserable, sits in the passenger seat, dressed in a worn-out work jacket and gloves. The driver, a burly man with a permanent five o’clock shadow, climbs out of the cab.

**(SOUND:** The rumbling of the truck’s engine, the hiss of air brakes, the crunch of ice and snow underfoot.)

The driver hands **JEREMY** a stack of papers.

**DRIVER** 
Alright, kid. Here’s the damage.

**JEREMY** takes the papers and his eyes widen. Instead of the usual single page, he’s holding three densely printed sheets.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on the delivery sheets, the sheer volume of text and numbers emphasizing the size of the order.

**JEREMY** (His voice incredulous) 
What the…

He scans the bottom of the last page, his eyes settling on a number: $23,900.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
Twenty-three *thousand* nine hundred?

**DRIVER** (Whistling)
Looks like someone had a hell of a party. They ordered about three times as much as usual. This is gonna take us an hour to unload.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** 
Six AM on a Friday. Twenty-four grand worth of beer. This is not how I envisioned my rock and roll lifestyle.

**EXT. W.O. WRIGHT’S - LOADING DOCK / INT. W.O. WRIGHT’S - CONTINUOUS**

A montage begins, showing **JEREMY** and the driver making repeated trips between the truck and the bar’s storage area, using hand dollies piled high with cases of beer. The work is backbreaking, their breath misting in the cold air.

**(SOUND:** The heavy thud of cases of beer being loaded onto the dollies, the creaking of the dollies’ wheels, the grunts and heavy breathing of **JEREMY** and the driver.)

**(VISUAL):** Quick cuts: close-ups of **JEREMY’s** straining muscles, the dollies’ wheels bumping over uneven surfaces, cases of beer being stacked haphazardly in the storage area.

Inside the bar, the only people present are the manager, a harried-looking man in a stained apron, and a couple of kitchen staff preparing pizza dough. The usual lively atmosphere is replaced by a sense of exhaustion and frantic activity.

**JEREMY** and the driver finally wheel the last dolly into the storage area. **JEREMY** wipes sweat from his brow, looking at the sheer volume of beer they’ve just unloaded.

**JEREMY** (To the manager, his voice incredulous) 
What the fuck happened?

**JEREMY (V.O.)** 
I mean, seriously. Did a goddamn fraternity throw a convention in here or something?

The manager looks at him, not recognizing him from the band.

**MANAGER** (His voice frazzled) 
Tuesday night. Live show. We got… *wiped out*.

**JEREMY** (Confused) 
Wiped out? You ran out of beer?

**MANAGER** (Nodding emphatically) 
Ran out of *everything*. Every tap. Every bottle. We were scrambling to find anything to serve.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** 
Ran out of beer? At W.O. Wright’s? That’s like… running out of oxygen at a goddamn oxygen bar.

**DRIVER** (Chiming in, rubbing his aching back) 
Tell me about it. I just unloaded a couple tons of beer. My back’s killing me.

**MANAGER** (Looking at the stacks of beer, a calculating look in his eyes) 
With the markup… that’s closer to a sixty-thousand-dollar delivery you just hauled in, boys. From the ice and snow.

**JEREMY’s** eyes widen.

**JEREMY** (His voice a mixture of disbelief and awe) 
Sixty *thousand*?

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **JEREMY’s** face, his expression a mixture of disbelief and dawning realization. Then a quick cut to the stacks of beer cases, now seen in a new light – as a vast quantity of money.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera pans across the bar, now empty and quiet, then back to **JEREMY**, his mind reeling from the revelation of the bar’s financial success. The contrast between the mundane reality of his job and the surprising profitability of the bar is stark and unsettling.

**INT. BEER WAREHOUSE - LATER**

The beer truck is now empty, parked amidst rows upon rows of towering pallets stacked high with cases of beer. The warehouse is vast and cavernous, lit by harsh fluorescent lights that hum overhead. The air is cool and smells faintly of hops and yeast. The workday is ending, and drivers and sales representatives are hurrying to clock out, eager to escape.

**(SOUND:** The echoing clang of metal as dollies are parked, the chatter of tired workers, the distant sound of a forklift beeping as it reverses, the low hum of the fluorescent lights.)

**JEREMY** fights against the tide of departing workers, pushing his way through the crowd. He’s determined to find his dad, the warehouse manager.

The camera follows **JEREMY** as he moves through the crowd, the other workers appearing almost like extras in a vast, industrial landscape. The camera focuses on the sheer scale of the warehouse, the endless rows of beer stretching into the distance.

He spots his dad near the central computer station, a cluttered desk piled high with paperwork.

**JEREMY** (Calling out) 
Dad!

His dad looks up, a tired but warm smile spreading across his face.

**DAD** (His voice gruff but affectionate) 
Hey, kiddo. Long day?

**JEREMY** (Nodding wearily) 
You have no idea. That W.O. Wright’s order… it was insane.

**DAD** (Chuckling) 
Yeah, I heard. What’s up?

**JEREMY** (His voice incredulous) 
It was like… a Wal-Mart order. Or a Kroger order. How does a bar go through that much beer?

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
I delivered enough beer today to float a goddamn battleship.

His dad shrugs.

**DAD** 
Beats me. But I can tell you exactly how much they ordered. Thanks to this baby.

He pats the computer monitor.

**JEREMY** (His voice insistent) 
Did they really order… like… four times as much as usual?

His dad types a few commands into the computer, then looks up, his eyebrows raised.

**DAD** (His voice surprised) 
Five times as much, actually.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on the computer screen, showing the sales figures for the W.O. Wright’s account. The numbers are large, monochrome green and imposing.

**JEREMY** (His voice incredulous) 
Five times?

**DAD** (Nodding)
Yeah. Look at this.

He points to an ASCII graph on the screen, showing the W.O. Wright’s order history over the past few months.

**DAD (CONT'D)** 
They buy a decent amount, consistently. But… look at these spikes.

He points to several sharp peaks in the graph.

**DAD (CONT'D)** 
They have a really… spiky purchasing pattern.

**JEREMY** (Frowning) 
Why?

**DAD** (Shrugging) 
That’s a question for the sales guy. He’d know more about their business.

**JEREMY** (Looking around the warehouse) 
Has he left yet?

His dad points to the far end of the warehouse, where a lone figure is still packing up his briefcase.

**DAD** 
There he is.

**JEREMY** nods, a determined look on his face.

**JEREMY** (His voice resolute) 
I’m gonna go talk to him.

He turns and heads towards a nearby forklift. He climbs into the driver’s seat, starts the engine, and with a sudden burst of speed, takes off across the warehouse floor, the forklift’s horn blaring, scattering the remaining workers.

The camera follows **JEREMY** as he drives the forklift, the vastness of the warehouse and the speed of the vehicle creating a sense of almost surreal movement. The other workers scatter out of his path, looking on in a mixture of amusement and alarm.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on the salesman at the far end of the warehouse, his back to **JEREMY**, unaware of the approaching forklift. The sound of the forklift’s horn grows louder and louder, creating a sense of impending confrontation.

**INT. BEER WAREHOUSE - CONTINUOUS**

**JEREMY** brings the forklift to a screeching halt just a few feet from the salesman, who turns around, startled but quickly recognizing **JEREMY**. The salesman is impeccably dressed in a crisp, button-down shirt, a tie, and neatly pressed slacks – a stark contrast to **JEREMY’s** dirty work clothes.

**(SOUND:** The screeching of the forklift’s tires, the sudden silence as the engine cuts off, the echoing sound of their voices in the vast warehouse.)

**JEREMY** (Shouting over the lingering echo)
Dude!

**SALESMAN** (Shouting back, a wide grin spreading across his face) 
Dude!

Without hesitation, they perform a brief, slightly awkward chest bump, the salesman Momentarily wincing as **JEREMY’s** dirty work jacket contacts his clean shirt.

**JEREMY** (His voice slightly breathless from the forklift ride) 
You got a second?

**SALESMAN** (Adjusting his tie slightly) 
For you? Always. I owe you one, remember? That time you got me those backstage passes to… what was it… Slaughterhouse Five?

**JEREMY** (Waving his hand dismissively) 
Don’t worry about it. This is… more of a professional inquiry.

He gestures vaguely towards the direction of the loading dock.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
W.O. Wright’s. What the *hell* is going on over there?

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
I feel like I just single-handedly restocked the entire state of Ohio’s beer supply.

The salesman raises an eyebrow, a knowing smile playing on his lips.

**SALESMAN** (His voice smooth and professional) 
You haven’t noticed? They’ve increased their orders… *significantly*.

**JEREMY** (Rubbing his aching back) 
Notice? My back and knees can tell you exactly how significant. I just delivered enough beer to fill Lake Erie. What’s the explanation?

**JEREMY (V.O.)** I needed answers. And I needed them now. My lower back was demanding them.

**SALESMAN** (Leaning in slightly, lowering his voice as if sharing a secret)
It’s the bands, man. The live music.

**JEREMY** (Frowning)
The bands?

**SALESMAN** (Nodding) 
Yeah. They’ve been booking some really popular local acts. Drawing in huge crowds. They’re selling beer like it’s going out of style.

He pauses, then adds with a wink:

**SALESMAN (CONT'D)** 
Especially on Tuesdays, apparently.

**JEREMY** (His eyes widening slightly) 
Tuesdays?

He remembers their gig from the previous Tuesday.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** Wait a minute…

**JEREMY** (His voice now a mixture of realization and disbelief) 
You’re saying… because of… *us*?

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on the salesman’s face, his smile widening as he nods slowly, confirming **JEREMY’s** suspicions. The vastness of the warehouse and the mundane setting suddenly take on a new significance, as **JEREMY** realizes the unexpected impact their music has had on the bar’s business.

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - EVENING**

The sun is setting, casting long shadows across the **GILLEY**’s driveway. The band members are finishing up packing their gear back into their respective vehicles after a grueling practice session.

**(SOUND:** The clatter of instrument cases being closed, the slamming of car doors, the low murmur of conversation, the distant sound of crickets chirping.)

**JEREMY**, looking serious, addresses the group.

**JEREMY** Hey, guys… could I talk to you for a sec after we finish up?

**KATHY**, adjusting her jacket, gives a quick, dismissive wave.

**KATHY** (Her voice casual) Can’t. Got a date.

**JEFF**, already loading his guitar case into **JIM**’s car, chimes in.

**JEFF** Yeah, **JIM** and I gotta head downtown. Got a meeting about another gig.

**GILLEY**, without a word, simply turns and walks into the house, closing the garage door behind him.

**(VISUAL):** Quick cuts: **KATHY** adjusting her jacket, **JEFF** loading his guitar, **GILLEY** disappearing into the house. The quick, dismissive actions emphasize their lack of interest in what **JEREMY** has to say.

**JEREMY** is left standing with **BILL** and **JIM**.



**JEREMY (V.O.)** Well, that went well.

Once the others have driven off, **BILL** turns to **JEREMY**, a sly grin on his face.

**BILL** (His voice low and suggestive) 
No bra today. That’s a… *date*. If you know what I mean.

He winks, nudging **JEREMY** in the ribs. **JIM** snorts with laughter.



**JIM (V.O.)** These guys were so far from maturity, they were practically still in the goddamn primordial soup.

**JEREMY** sighs, shaking his head.

**JEREMY** (His voice serious) 
Guys, I’ve got something more important than speculating about **KATHY**’s sex life.

**BILL** and **JIM** exchange a look, their interest piqued slightly.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
You remember how I had to work today? Delivering beer?

**BILL** (Shrugging) 
Yeah, so?

**JEREMY** (His voice gaining intensity) 
So… I just unloaded twenty-four *thousand* dollars worth of beer at W.O. Wright’s.

**BILL** and **JIM** exchange another look, this time with a hint of confusion.

**JIM** (His voice skeptical) 
Twenty-four thousand?

**JEREMY** (Nodding emphatically) Twenty-four thousand. Just from *our* distributorship. Miller and Coors. The sales guy told me the Budweiser distributor probably hauled in at least three and a half times that much.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **JEREMY’s** face as he delivers the information, then quickly cuts to **BILL** and **JIM**, their expressions shifting from disinterest to surprise.

**JEREMY** pauses for dramatic effect, letting the information sink in.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
That’s… eighty-four thousand dollars, give or take. In beer. At one bar. In one week.

He looks at **BILL** and **JIM**, his eyes wide.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
Any guesses how that happened?

**JEREMY (V.O.)** I could see the gears turning in their heads. Slowly, but surely, the pieces were starting to fall into place.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on **BILL** and **JIM**, their faces now etched with a mixture of disbelief and dawning realization. The crickets continue to chirp in the background, the mundane setting now contrasting sharply with the extraordinary information they’ve just received.

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

The crickets continue their chirping chorus, oblivious to the Momentous conversation unfolding in the driveway. The setting sun casts long, dramatic shadows.

**(SOUND:** The crickets chirping, the distant rumble of traffic, the sudden, sharp intake of breath from **JIM**.)

**JIM** is the first to react, his voice exploding in a mixture of disbelief and awe.

**JIM** (His voice loud and incredulous) 
Jesus holy fuck shitnuggets! Eighty-four *thousand*?! We sold *how much* beer? How the *fuck* do you know this crap, dude?

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **JIM**’s face, his eyes wide, his jaw dropped. The camera then quickly cuts to **JEREMY**, who looks slightly overwhelmed by **JIM**’s outburst.

**BILL**, still struggling to process the information, looks from **JIM** to **JEREMY**, his brow furrowed.

**BILL** (His voice confused)
