Yeah, seriously. How *do* you know this stuff?

**BILL (V.O.)** My brain’s short-circuiting. Numbers are hard.

**JEREMY** sighs, rubbing his temples.

**JEREMY** (His voice patient, but slightly exasperated) 
My dad showed me the delivery data from his computer. He’s the warehouse manager, remember? And then I talked to the sales guy. He was so fucking pleased, he’s talking about getting a car phone.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** A car phone. That’s how you knew you’d made it back then. You were practically Gordon Gekko with a Motorola.

**BILL** still looks lost, his eyes darting back and forth between **JEREMY** and **JIM**.

**BILL** (His voice confused) 
A car phone? What does that have to do with…

**JIM**, realizing that **BILL** still isn’t grasping the connection, steps in, his voice slow and deliberate.

**JIM** (His voice patient, as if explaining something to a small child) 
*We* sold the beer, **BILL**. W.O. Wright’s was just the… the *middleman*.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **BILL**’s face as the realization dawns on him. His eyes widen, his mouth opens slightly, and his jaw drops.

**BILL (V.O.)** Oh.

**BILL** (His voice a plaintive whistle, followed by a slow, drawn-out profanity) 
Oh… *shit*.

**JIM (V.O.)** The lightbulb finally went off. It was a slow burn, but it finally happened.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on the three band members, their faces illuminated by the fading light of the setting sun. **JIM** is grinning, **JEREMY** looks relieved, and **BILL** is still processing the information, his expression a mixture of awe and disbelief. The crickets continue their chirping chorus, the mundane sounds of suburban life now juxtaposed with the extraordinary revelation they’ve just shared.

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

The crickets continue their evening chorus, the suburban setting now a backdrop to a growing sense of disillusionment.

**(SOUND:** The crickets chirping, the distant hum of traffic, the rustling of leaves in the light breeze.)

**JEREMY**, seeing the stunned expressions on **JIM** and **BILL**’s faces, starts to feel a pang of guilt. He knows they’re excited about the apparent financial windfall, and he hates to burst their bubble.

**JEREMY** (His voice hesitant, apologetic) 
Guys… I know you think this is… like… our biggest payday ever… and I really appreciate you and **JEFF** hustling to get us the gig…

He pauses, taking a deep breath.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
But… we only made eighteen hundred dollars.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **JIM** and **BILL**’s faces as they process this new information. Their expressions shift from awe to confusion, then to a dawning sense of disappointment.

**JIM** (His voice confused) 
Eighteen hundred? But… you said they sold eighty-four thousand dollars worth of beer!

**JEREMY** (Nodding grimly) 
Yeah. They did. But… we only get eighteen hundred. Split six ways.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** Three hundred bucks a guy. For a night’s work. It wasn’t bad, exactly. But compared to what they were making… it felt like we were getting robbed blind.

**BILL** (His voice incredulous) 
Three hundred bucks? That’s… that’s it?

**JEREMY** (Shrugging, his voice laced with frustration) 
That’s it.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** It was like we were working for tips. Except the tips were pre-determined, and ridiculously low.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
The bar’s making off like a bandit. They’re selling our music, using it to draw in crowds, and they’re keeping almost all the profit.

He gestures emphatically with his hands.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
And it’s not just W.O. Wright’s. It’s probably the same at all the other places we play. They’re all taking us for a ride.

**(VISUAL):** The camera slowly zooms out, showing the three band members standing in the driveway, the setting sun casting long, ominous shadows. The suburban setting now feels oppressive, a symbol of the limitations and frustrations they face.

**JIM** (His voice now laced with anger) 
So… we’re getting screwed.

**JEREMY** (Nodding grimly) 
Pretty much.

**JIM (V.O.)** I felt a slow burn start in the pit of my stomach. Not just anger. But… a sense of betrayal.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on the three band members, their faces now etched with a mixture of anger, frustration, and a dawning realization of their situation. The crickets continue their chirping chorus, now sounding almost mocking, as the band faces a new challenge – the realization that their musical dreams are intertwined with the harsh realities of the music business.

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

The band members stand in the driveway, the weight of **JEREMY’s** revelation hanging heavy in the air. As they talk, a dark blue Ford Escort drives slowly past the **GILLEY** residence, heading down the street. It pulls into the driveway of the **CREMEANS**’ house, two doors down.

**(SOUND:** The crickets chirping, the distant rumble of traffic, the soft hum of the Ford Escort’s engine as it passes, the crunch of tires on the **CREMEANS**’ driveway.)

**JIM** watches the Escort pull in, a look of sudden clarity washing over his face. He’s struck by a simple, yet profound realization.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **JIM**’s face as the Escort drives by, the light from the setting sun glinting off his glasses. Then a quick cut to the **CREMEANS**’ house as the car pulls into the driveway.

**JIM** (His voice calm and resolute, a stark contrast to his earlier outburst) 
We need a manager.

**JIM (V.O.)** It was like a switch had flipped in my head. Suddenly, everything was clear. We couldn’t keep doing this on our own.

**BILL** snorts, his skepticism immediately surfacing.

**BILL** (His voice dismissive) 
A manager? That’s how bands get ripped off.

**JEREMY** nods in agreement.

**JEREMY** (His voice echoing **BILL**’s sentiment) 
Yeah, exactly.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** Managers. They were like the used car salesmen of the music world. Always trying to screw you over.

**JIM** shakes his head, his voice firm.

**JIM** (His voice confident) 
I’d agree with you… normally. But I’m not talking about just any manager. I’m talking about… **CREMEANS**.

**BILL** and **JEREMY** look at each other, a flicker of recognition in their eyes.

**BILL** (His voice questioning) 
**CREMEANS**?

**JIM** (Nodding) 
Yeah. **JEFF** **CREMEANS**. He’s about to graduate from Wright State with a degree in business.

**(VISUAL):** The camera briefly focuses on the **CREMEANS**’ house, then cuts back to **JIM**, his expression now determined.

**JIM (CONT'D)** 
We can trust him. He’s one of us.

**JEREMY** (His voice thoughtful) Yeah… I guess.

**BILL** (His voice still skeptical) But… he’s not… you know… an industry insider. He doesn’t have any experience.  And for fuck's sake, he's another *Jeff*!  Two Jeff's in one place!  That's a disaster waiting to happen.

**JEREMY** (His voice emphatic) 
Bill, we already have two Jeremys in the same place at the same time!  Haven't you noticed?  No one has died yet.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)**
Trust is the most important thing, **BILL**. And **CREMEANS** is impeccably trustworthy. He’ll pick up the music business stuff fast. Plus… he’s entrepreneurial. He doesn’t want to report to “The Man.” He only recognizes the Lord as worthy in his personal chain of command.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** **CREMEANS** was… different. He had this unwavering faith, this almost naive optimism. But he was also smart, driven, and fiercely independent.

**BILL** (His voice still hesitant) 
But… would he even listen to us? And is he too much of a… you know… *holy roller* for this kind of business?

**BILL (V.O.)** The music business. It was a den of sin and temptation. Would **CREMEANS** be able to navigate those treacherous waters without getting his soul tarnished?

**JIM** smiles confidently.

**JIM** (His voice reassuring) 
He’ll be fine. Trust me.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on the three band members, their faces now reflecting a mixture of hope and uncertainty. The crickets continue their chirping chorus, the suburban setting now a backdrop to a pivotal Moment in the band’s history. The decision to bring **CREMEANS** on board will irrevocably change their trajectory, for better or for worse.

---

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - LATER**

The band members look at **CREMEANS**, a mixture of curiosity and mild amusement on their faces.

**(SOUND:** The clatter of instrument cases, the distant sound of birds chirping, the gentle rustling of leaves in the winter breeze.)

**KATHY**, never one to miss an opportunity for a jab, throws a playful barb at **CREMEANS**.

**KATHY** (Her voice teasing, with a pointed glance at **GILLEY**) I can count on **GILLEY**’s dick the same number of times you’ve shown any interest in our… *musical endeavors*.

**(VISUAL):** Quick cuts: a close-up of **KATHY**’s playful smile, a quick cut to **GILLEY** looking slightly uncomfortable, then back to **CREMEANS**, who remains unfazed.



**KATHY (V.O.)** I was trying to goad him. Get a rise out of him. But **CREMEANS**… he was like a goddamn Teflon frying pan. Nothing ever stuck to him.

**CREMEANS** simply chuckles softly, unfazed by **KATHY**’s comment.

**CREMEANS** (His voice even and good-natured) Oh, I wouldn’t say that.

**JEFF**, ever the man of few words, gives **CREMEANS** a quick high five.

**JEFF** **JEFF**.

**CREMEANS** (Returning the high five and the curt acknowledgement) **JEFF**.



**(V.O. – JEFF)** It was a ritual. A sacred, unspoken ritual. They’d been doing it since middle school. It was their way of saying, “I acknowledge your existence, fellow human. And I find this exchange mildly amusing.”

**CREMEANS** chuckles again, finding the exchange genuinely funny.

**(VISUAL):** The camera lingers on **CREMEANS**’ face as he chuckles, his amusement seemingly genuine and unforced.

**CREMEANS** then shifts his attention to the group as a whole.

**CREMEANS** (His voice now more direct) Actually, I was invited over.

**GILLEY**, who had been quietly observing the interaction, looks confused.

**GILLEY** (His voice puzzled) Invited? My dad didn’t say anything about that.

**GILLEY (V.O.)** What the hell was going on?

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera focuses on **CREMEANS**, the Mountain Dew bottle still firmly in his grip, as he looks at the band members, a hint of mystery in his eyes. The tension in the air has shifted slightly, from playful banter to a sense of anticipation. The band is clearly intrigued, wondering what **CREMEANS**’ unexpected visit is all about.

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

The band members exchange uneasy glances, the atmosphere shifting from mild curiosity to a more palpable tension.

**(SOUND:** The clatter of instrument cases, the distant sounds of suburban life, the faint sound of **CREMEANS** taking another sip from his Mountain Dew bottle.)

**CREMEANS** looks at the group, his expression polite but firm.

**CREMEANS** (His voice even and direct) Well, that’s just it. Half the band missed last night’s meeting. I was wondering why.

**(VISUAL):** The camera pans across the faces of the band members, lingering on each one as they react to **CREMEANS**’ question.

**GILLEY** shrugs, avoiding eye contact.

**GILLEY** (His voice casual, dismissive) I was tired. Went to bed early. We’ve got a killer schedule this weekend.

**GILLEY (V.O.)** Truth was, I was exhausted from… other activities. But I wasn’t about to share that with ***CREMEANS***.

**KATHY** shifts uncomfortably, her eyes darting nervously between **CREMEANS** and the other band members.



**(V.O. – KATHY)** Oh, Jesus. Here we go.

**KATHY** (Her voice strained, trying to sound nonchalant) I… had something to do.

**KATHY (V.O.)** “Something to do.” As if “something to do” involved writhing naked with **GILLEY** in his sweaty bedroom. I was so full of shit.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **KATHY**’s face, her discomfort palpable. The camera then quickly cuts to **JEFF**, who looks equally uncomfortable.

**JEFF** clears his throat, adjusting his glasses.

**JEFF** (His voice slightly flustered) I… had a paper due. For my political science class. Had to… read and write. You know.

**JEFF (V.O.)** It was a complete and utter lie. But it was the best I could come up with on the spot.

**JEREMY**, ever the straight shooter, simply tells the truth.

**JEREMY** (His voice straightforward) I was talking to **BILL** and **JIM** about the… financial situation.



**(V.O. – JEREMY)** Honesty. It was always my downfall.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **CREMEANS**’ face as he listens to each explanation, his expression remaining polite but subtly scrutinizing.

**CREMEANS** nods slowly, taking another sip from his Mountain Dew.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)** Something wasn’t adding up.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera lingers on the group, the tension in the air now more pronounced. **CREMEANS**’ presence, combined with the band’s evasive answers, has created a sense of unease. The stage is set for a confrontation, or at least a very awkward conversation.

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

The band members look at **CREMEANS**, a mixture of surprise and skepticism on their faces. The bright winter sun glints off **CREMEANS**’ glasses as he takes another sip of his Mountain Dew.

**(SOUND:** The distant sound of traffic, the rustling of leaves in the winter breeze, the faint sound of **CREMEANS** swallowing his Mountain Dew.)

**CREMEANS** clears his throat, setting the Mountain Dew bottle down on the hood of **GILLEY**’s car.

**CREMEANS** (His voice calm and professional) **JIM**, **JEREMY**, and **BILL** approached me last night. They suggested… that I manage you guys. More… professionally.

He looks directly at **JEFF**, **KATHY**, and **GILLEY**, his gaze steady and direct.

**CREMEANS (CONT'D)** I’m willing to take the helm… if you three are on board. It’s a simple majority vote.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on each of the three band members – **JEFF**, **KATHY**, and **GILLEY** – as **CREMEANS** speaks, capturing their individual reactions.

**CREMEANS** then proceeds to explain the reasoning behind **JIM**’s suggestion.

**CREMEANS (CONT'D)** **JIM** pointed out that you’re… leaving a lot of money on the table. Money you don’t even realize you *could* be demanding.

**JEFF**, ever practical, raises a valid point.

**JEFF** (His voice hesitant) But… you haven’t even graduated yet.

**CREMEANS** (His voice confident) This would be a part-time job. Just like the rest of you have part-time jobs. And some of you go to college. I can handle it.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)** I pulled an all-nighter last night. Scoured every book, every article, every website I could find about managing a band. In the land of the blind, the one-eyed man is king.

**CREMEANS** then launches into his vision for the band’s future, his voice gaining enthusiasm.

**CREMEANS (CONT'D)** I’m talking about setting up a corporation. For tax purposes. To manage your assets, your intellectual property. To pay your taxes and **BILL**s properly. To claim business expenses. You’re inadvertently paying more taxes than you should without structuring yourselves as a business.



**CREMEANS (V.O.)** Incorporation. It sounded so… official. So… *legit*. Like we were about to become the goddamn Rolling Stones.

**KATHY**, ever focused on the creative aspect of the band, interjects.

**KATHY** (Her voice slightly dismissive) The purpose is to make music, **CREMEANS**.

**CREMEANS** nods, his voice becoming more emphatic.

**CREMEANS** (His voice passionate) Exactly! And the purpose of this… this *structure*… is to allow you to *do* that. To structure your lives so that making music *supports* your lives. So you can devote yourselves to music, to writing, to touring.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **CREMEANS**’ face as he speaks, his eyes shining with conviction. Then a quick cut to the band members, their expressions now a mixture of intrigue and dawning respect.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** He sounded… smarter than he actually was. But in that Moment, it didn’t matter. He had a vision. And it was starting to sound… pretty damn good.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera lingers on **CREMEANS**, the Mountain Dew bottle now forgotten on the car’s hood, as he looks at the band members, his expression confident and determined. The stage is set for a new chapter in the band’s history, one that could lead them to either great success or spectacular failure.

**EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE - DRIVEWAY - CONTINUOUS**

The band members look at each other, a mix of confusion and amusement on their faces. The bright winter sun continues to glint off **CREMEANS**’ glasses.

**(SOUND:** The distant sound of traffic, the rustling of leaves, the faint sound of a dog barking in the distance.)

**JEFF**, never one to shy away from a complex analogy, steps forward, clearing his throat.

**JEFF** (His voice serious, as if delivering a lecture) Okay, so… hear me out. The band… it’s a democracy, right? Of course. But we can’t operate like it’s… you know… *now*. Like under the Constitution.

He pauses for effect, adjusting his glasses.

**JEFF (CONT'D)** We need to operate like it was *after* Independence. You know… the Articles of Confederation?

**(VISUAL):** A brief, stylized flashback to a black and white image of the signing of the Declaration of Independence, then quickly back to **JEFF**.

**JEFF (V.O.)** I’d been reading up on early American history. It seemed… relevant. Somehow.

**JIM**, always eager to support **JEFF**’s intellectual pursuits (no matter how obscure), nods enthusiastically.

**JIM** (His voice encouraging) 
Yeah! The Articles! I remember that!

**JIM (V.O.)** 
**JEFF** could spin a yarn about anything. And most of the time, it was entertaining as hell.

**KATHY** rolls her eyes, but a small smile plays on her lips.

**KATHY** (Her voice dry) 
You mean… consensus?

**JEFF** waves his hand dismissively.

**JEFF** (His voice insistent) 
No, no. Not exactly. Under the Articles, votes in Congress had to be… *unanimous*.

**BILL**, ever the pragmatist, interjects.

**BILL** (His voice matter-of-fact) 
Yeah, and that’s why it didn’t work. America didn’t really function smoothly until 1789 and the adoption of the Constitution.

**JEFF** points a finger at **BILL**.

**JEFF** (His voice triumphant) 
Partially correct!

**JIM** (His voice enthusiastic) 
Partially correct is the best kind of correct!

**(VISUAL):** 
A quick zoom in on **JIM**’s face as he delivers this line, emphasizing his enthusiasm.

**GILLEY**, who had been quietly observing the exchange, suddenly chimes in, a mischievous grin on his face.

**GILLEY** (His voice suggestive) 
Partially correct… rhymes with… partially erect. I’m liking this **CREMEANS** guy’s advice already. And I like **JEFF**'s point about unanimity.

**GILLEY (V.O.)** 
Any excuse to talk about erections was a good excuse in my book.

**JEFF**, emboldened by **GILLEY**’s support, continues his historical tangent.

**JEFF** (His voice gaining Momentum) 
And you know what else happened under the Articles? Ohio achieved statehood!

**JEREMY** groans, rubbing his temples.

**JEREMY** (His voice exasperated)
Enough, **JEFF**! You’re just piling on now.

He turns to **KATHY**.

**JEREMY (CONT'D)** 
**KATHY**, are you on board with this?

**KATHY** hesitates, a look of uncertainty on her face.

**KATHY** (Her voice thoughtful)
I… have a specific vision for where I want this band to go.

**KATHY (V.O.)** A vision that probably involved far more sex, booze, and loud music than **CREMEANS** could handle.

**CREMEANS**, sensing her hesitation, steps in.

**CREMEANS** (His voice reassuring) I understand. And I’m sure your vision involves far more sex, booze and loud music than I can stand. But let’s just get the legal structure in place for now. We can revisit the… *creative direction*… in three months. After we get the corporation set up.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on **CREMEANS**’ face as he delivers this line, his expression a mixture of seriousness and a hint of amusement. Then a quick cut to **KATHY**, her expression softening slightly.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The band members look at each other, a tentative agreement forming in the air. The setting sun casts long shadows across the driveway, symbolizing the long road ahead. The decision to bring **CREMEANS** on board has been made, and the band is about to embark on a new and uncertain journey.

**MONTAGE SEQUENCE – THE RISE**

**(SOUND:** A driving, energetic rock song begins, reflecting the band’s growing Momentum. Snippets of crowd noise, applause, and the clinking of glasses are interspersed throughout.)

**(VISUAL):** Rapid cuts, jump cuts, and quick zooms create a sense of frenetic energy, mirroring the band’s hectic schedule.

**INT. CREMEANS’ KITCHEN – NIGHT**

(SOUND: A clock ticks. A faucet drips. Muffled television voices hum behind a closed door.)

**CREMEANS** sits hunched at the table — elbows sharp, brow furrowed — lit only by a buzzing overhead light that makes the scene look jaundiced. The yellow legal pad before him is half-filled with tight, precise handwriting. Cities, numbers, margins scrawled and crossed out.

**CAMERA: EXTREME CLOSE-UP on the pad.  
“Dayton – $200”  
“Cincinnati – $600?”  
“Shoe rental? WTF is ‘backline’?”

Next to the pad: a battered calculator, a receipt from Speedway, and a warm pop sweating in a foam koozie.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
It started simple. Dates. Dollars. Drive times.  A plan. Or what passed for one.

**CAMERA: PULL BACK to reveal the full table.  
Covered in takeout bags, loose coins, a cracked phone with voicemail blinking. The chaos of someone just barely holding Momentum together.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
But a yellow pad only takes you so far.  Eventually, you need… infrastructure.

He underlines *“Indianapolis”* twice, draws a crude triangle connecting cities. He nods to himself, mouth set like a man preparing to move contraband across state lines.

**VISUAL STYLE ():**  
Jump cuts to different angles of the same table, same night — the pad growing more chaotic, the handwriting more frantic, the Mt Dew replaced by a gas station coffee. Same man, getting less sleep.

---

**BEAT 2: THE KNITTING DESK**

**INT. CREMEANS’ LIVING ROOM – LATE NIGHT – MAY 1991**

(SOUND: A box fan whirs in the window. Frogs croak outside. Somewhere in the house, an old refrigerator buzzes like a dying wasp.)

**CREMEANS** kneels at his mother’s antique knitting desk, now buried under a massive plotter calendar, push pins, and empty Diet Rite cans. The desk creaks under the weight of the future he’s trying to build.

**CAMERA: OVERHEAD SHOT  
**The calendar is a battlefield — red and blue ink scrawled across every day:  
“Bogart’s – 3800”  
“Canal St. – 2000 (door cut!)”  
“WRIGHT STATE FESTIVAL – THIS ONE MATTERS” circled in black marker, twice.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
My mother used to knit here. Baby booties. Christmas mittens.  Now it’s where I plan small-scale financial domination.

**VISUAL STYLE (TARANTINO-ESQUE DIALOGUE & PACE):  
**Quick cuts:  
– **CREMEANS** slapping a sticky note onto a date.  
– Grabbing a phone and dialing.  
– Scribbling numbers while mouthing, _“No, we can’t play a freaking brunch.”  
_– Sipping a flat can of soda like it’s bourbon.  
– Muttering, *“Thirty percent door if we bring our own mic cables? Who do they think they’re dealing with?”*

**WIDE SHOT:**
The desk, once delicate and doily-lined, now looks like the war room of a very broke general. A single half-finished scarf droops off the side like a white flag.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
The desk didn’t like it.  Neither did she.  But empire doesn’t care about heirlooms.

**BEAT 3: THE GIGS**

**MONTAGE – VARIOUS VENUES – LATE MAY 1991**

(SOUND: A dirty, distorted riff kicks in. It’s half adrenaline, half feedback — something like the bastard child of Pixies and Mudhoney. The crowd roars under it, half-drunk and half-awake.)

**RAPID CUTS – VERHOEVEN-STYLE FRENZY:**

— **INT. VFW HALL – TROTWOOD  
****KATHY** hurls her head in time with the beat, a snarl on her lips. Her fingers blur across the fretboard. Sweat flies off her temple like shrapnel.

— **EXT. BOGART’S – CINCINNATI – NIGHT  
**The marquee flickers: *COMMUTED + GUESTS* in black plastic letters. A crowd crushes forward, sloshing beer and shouting names.

— **INT. CAMPUS SHOW – WRIGHT STATE  
**A fluorescent-lit stage**. **GILLEY** howls into the mic, veins bulging. A couple of frat guys up front are losing their shit. A girl flashes the stage. **KATHY** doesn’t blink.

— **INT. CANAL STREET TAVERN – DARK, SWEATY  
**Smoke coils through stage lights.  JIM’s** snare cracks like a gunshot. A kid in the front row pukes into his shoe, still clapping.

**CAMERA: CLOSE-UPS**  
— **KATHY**’s face — focused, feral.  
— **GILLEY**’s mouth — open, screaming.  
— **CREMEANS** in the wings — fists pumping, eyes manic, mouthing the lyrics like a prophet.  
— A tipped-over drink soaking a power strip.  
— A kid crowd-surfing in a Minor Threat shirt.  
— A bouncer pulling two people apart mid-fight.

**SLOW-MOTION SHOT:  
****KATHY** mid-leap off a monitor, boots airborne, hair backlit like a halo made of static.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
It wasn’t tight. It wasn’t clean.  But Jesus, it *moved*.

**FINAL SHOT:  
**A sea of hands raised toward the lights. The band a blur. The crowd a blur. The noise becoming joy.

---

**BEAT 4: THE SCHEDULE**

**MONTAGE – MAY INTO JUNE 1991**

(SOUND: The ticking of a wall clock — steady at first, then speeding up into a manic, metallic tempo overlaid with distorted guitar.)

**VISUAL STYLE – VERHOEVEN FRENZY**

**RAPID CUTS – CALENDAR PAGES:**

— *May 10: Dayton VFW Hall – 8PM  
— May 12: The Clubhouse, Springfield – 10PM (door split)  
— May 14: Yellow Springs Pizza Basement – “Pay in Pies” written in red ink  
— May 18: Bogart’s, Cincinnati – $3800 circled three times  
— May 21: Wright State Spring Fest – “DO NOT BE LATE” in block caps*

**CAMERA: OVERHEAD SWEEP of the same calendar**  
The entries multiply. Gig after gig, weeknights and weekends, no gaps. Pen lines blur together like a nervous breakdown on paper.

**FLASH CUTS – BETWEEN DATES:**

— **KATHY** asleep across amp cables, cigarette in her lips, guitar still on.  
— **CREMEANS** on the phone, pacing, barking “Yes we have monitors now, no we’re not bringing our own dang stage.”  
— **JIM**’s drum heads with tape crosses and blood smudges.  
— **GILLEY** backstage, shirtless, downing a warm Pabst, eyes wild.

**SOUND BRIDGE:**  
Calendar page flipping turns into drum hits — *thwack-thwack-thwack-thwack* — syncing to the chaos.

**QUICK ZOOM on a date in June:  
***JUNE 22 – INDIANAPOLIS – CLUB RETINA – FIRST HEADLINE SHOW*

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
At some point we stopped asking if we could play.  We just started showing up and daring people to say no.

**FINAL IMAGE:  
**A wall calendar in **CREMEANS**’ room — covered in scribbles, tape, Sharpie corrections — completely full. A sticky note at the top reads:  **“IF YOU SLEEP, YOU MISS THE VAN.”**

**BEAT 5: THE VAN**

**EXT. CREMEANS’ DRIVEWAY – DAY – JUNE 1991**

(SOUND: Distant lawnmower. A garage radio plays WING-AM, fading in and out between baseball scores and CCR.)

**CREMEANS** stands beside the Ford Econoline like it’s a monument. One hand rests on the hood. His other arm is raised like he’s just won a local election.

The van is a faded blue-gray beast, long enough to park a crime scene in. One panel is primer-gray. Another has the ghost of a plumbing company logo barely scraped off.

**CAMERA: LOW ANGLE, HERO SHOT  
****CREMEANS** grinning, sweating, posing like he’s conquering Everest. Behind him: suburban Ohio sameness. In front of him: destiny with rust on the wheel wells.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
Transportation.  Not glamorous. Not sexy.  But you don’t take the hill without getting to the battlefield together…

**VERHOEVEN-STYLE CAMERA MOVEMENT:  
- A slow, circling pan around the van, showing:  
- A cracked rearview mirror duct-taped back in place.  
- One tire that’s clearly been patched twice.  
- A torn seat visible through the window.  
- A sticker on the bumper that reads *“I’m not drunk, I’m just avoiding potholes.”*

**CUT TO – INTERIOR:  
**CREMEANS** throws open the back doors. Inside: a chaotic but functional Tetris of gear — amps, cabs, drum cases, a cooler of ice-melted Mountain Dew, and a box of tangled extension cords.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
You can’t control the crowds.  You can’t control the sound guy.  But you *can* make sure your stuff arrives in one piece.

**WIDE SHOT:  
**CREMEANS** stands back, admiring the van like it’s the last thing standing between them and irrelevance.

**GILLEY (O.S.)**  
It smells like feet and broken dreams in here.

**CREMEANS (without looking)**  
That’s the smell of progress.

---
**BEAT 6: THE WAREHOUSE**

**INT. DAYTON AIRPORT PERIMETER – SMALL INDUSTRIAL WAREHOUSE – DAY**

(SOUND: A pen scratches across paper. A hangar door groans open. Somewhere in the distance, a plane taxis by, oblivious.)

**CREMEANS** signs the lease like he’s launching a coup — back straight, jaw set, hair sticking to his forehead. The property manager hands over the keys like she’s giving him a loaded weapon. She doesn’t smile.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
Storage. Rehearsal space.  And eventually… world domination headquarters.

**VISUAL STYLE – VERHOEVEN CAMERA MOVEMENT:  
**The doors swing open. **CREMEANS** steps into the echo chamber of his dreams.

**CAMERA: SLOW PAN ACROSS THE SPACE**  
The warehouse is enormous for what they need — dusty, dim, full of potential. An old metal desk sits crooked in the corner. There’s graffiti from God knows when on one wall. A single dangling lightbulb sways above.  But there’s power.  And it’s theirs.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
It didn’t matter that the bathroom was condemned.  Or that there was a beehive in the south wall.  We had *space.*

**MONTAGE – FIRST MOVES:  
- **KATHY** drags in a mic stand with electrical tape around the base.  
- **JEFF** sets up drums on bare concrete.  
- **JEREMY** opens a fold-out chair and immediately crushes a Miller Lite.  
- **CREMEANS** draws a crooked band logo on the wall in red Sharpie:  *“COMMUTED HQ – TRESPASSERS WILL BE SHOT, RE-BOOKED, AND PAID IN COINS”*

**WIDE SHOT – STATIC CAMERA**
The four of them inside the empty space.  Tiny. Loud. Insanely hopeful.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
We didn’t just want to play shows.  We wanted a base.  A myth.  A place to be loud without apology.

---

**BEAT 7: THE BLOW JOB**

**INT. BACK ROOM – POST-GIG – NIGHT**

(SOUND: Muffled bass thumps through a cinder block wall. A car alarm chirps once, then stops. Somewhere, laughter and a bottle breaking.)

The room is barely lit — one bare bulb swings overhead. Everything is yellowed and damp-looking. The walls are stained. The air smells like beer and bleach.

**KATHY** kneels, silent, in front of a man we never fully see.  Just hands on his hips. Belt undone. The logo on his shirt is some forgettable band she won’t remember in ten minutes.

**CAMERA: EXTREME CLOSE-UP on KATHY’s face.**  
Expression flat. Eyes unfocused. Her lips move, but there’s no sensuality in it. No heat. It’s not even routine. It’s subtraction — of self, of sound, of context.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
This was becoming regular.  Not fun.  Not sexy.  Just… quiet.  And quiet was the closest thing I had to peace.

**BRIEF FLASHES — VERHOEVEN-STYLE DETAIL:  
- The flicker of her necklace hitting her collarbone.  
- The man’s hand awkwardly brushing her hair aside.  
- Her fingers curled into the shag carpet like she’s anchoring herself.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
The stage was loud.  The van was loud.  Even my fucking thoughts had reverb.  
But this…This was muted.

**CAMERA: OVER-THE-SHOULDER SHOT**  
We glimpse a flyer for the show stuck to the wall. Bright colors. Cartoon flames. *COMMUTED LIVE!*

**KATHY** looks pale by comparison. Desaturated. Like she’s been cut and pasted in from a black-and-white film.  She finishes. Stands. Doesn’t speak. Doesn’t make eye contact. She adjusts her jacket. Wipes his cum on her sleeve, and leaves.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
Color was for other people.  I just needed quiet.

---

**BEAT 8: THE TOAST**

**INT. WAREHOUSE – NIGHT – JUNE 1991**

(SOUND: Music blasting — a cassette demo of one of their own tracks, raw and half-mixed, but *theirs*. Laughter. Amp buzz. Bottles clinking.)

The warehouse is lit with a dozen half-working string lights. Someone dragged in a cheap patio set. Pizza boxes, empty tallboys, and fast food bags litter the floor. The air is warm with beer breath and spilled adrenaline.

**CLOSE-UPS – VERHOEVEN-STYLE:**

- **KATHY**, cheeks flushed, laughing harder than she has in weeks, mid-sip from a red Solo cup.  
-  **JIM** doing fake drum fills on a pizza box with two drumsticks.  
- **BILL**, still in partial stage gear, eyeliner smeared, shirt open, hair soaked, eyes wide like he’s just seen God and liked what he saw.  
- **CREMEANS** — standing tall, in cargo shorts and a sweat-stained *KINKO’S ROCKS* tee — raising a 20 oz. bottle of Mountain Dew like it’s the Stanley Cup.

**CREMEANS (loud, almost preaching)**  
To loud amps, late nights, and *never* asking for permission.

**BAND (in chaotic unison)**  
***TO COMMUTED!***

THEY CLINK — whatever they’re holding.  Plastic cup. Dew bottle. Tallboy. A random socket wrench.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
This wasn’t supposed to happen.  Not to us.  Not here.

**WIDE SHOT – PULLING BACK SLOWLY:**  
The whole warehouse — now alive. Lit with possibility.  A spray-painted backdrop. A pile of tangled cords. A thrift store couch.  These kids — reckless, half-broke, completely convinced the future belongs to them.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
But somehow, it was.  And for one night, one stupid, beautiful night —  
We believed it.

---

**MONTAGE SEQUENCE – ROCKETING TO THE STARS**

**(SOUND:** The opening synth chords of Peter Schilling’s “Major Tom (Coming Home)” begin, immediately establishing a distinct 80s atmosphere. The song’s driving beat and soaring vocals provide a perfect backdrop for the band’s rapid rise.)

**(VISUAL):** Rapid cuts, jump cuts, and quick zooms, but with a slightly more stylized, almost music video-esque feel. Think early MTV, with a touch of Verhoeven’s signature visual flair.

**BEAT 1: COUNTDOWN BEGINS**

**INT. CREMEANS’ KITCHEN – NIGHT – EARLY JUNE 1991**

(SOUND: The opening synths of *“Major Tom (Coming Home)”* by Peter Schilling swell in — crisp, cold, glorious. The beat hits. The mission begins.)

The kitchen table is a war zone of paper: folders with curled corners, photocopied contracts, flyers marked up in red Sharpie. The yellow legal pad — once humble — now sprawls like a holy manuscript, pages curling with exhaustion.

**CAMERA: VERHOEVEN-STYLE STYLIZATION  
**— A CLOSE-UP on a cheap digital wall clock.  
_9:48:35… 9:48:34… 9:48:33…  
_The numbers blur, counting down faster than time should.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
**Ground control to Major Tom…  
The mission is a go.

**INSERT SHOTS – MTV-STYLE CUTS:  
**— His finger jabs a calculator like he’s launching a missile.  
— A date circled on a laminated map of Ohio: _“INDIANAPOLIS – GO TIME”  
_— A roll of duct tape and a pack of Sharpies with *“DO NOT DARE LOSE”* scribbled across them.

**CAMERA: ZOOM ON CREMEANS’ FACE  
**Beads of sweat on his temple. Jaw tight. He’s not stressed. He’s *dialed in.*

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
I wasn’t managing a band.  I was plotting trajectories.  Fueling boosters.  Scheduling liftoff.

**JUMP CUT – CLOCK AGAIN:  
***9:47:59… 9:47:58…*

He stands suddenly, knocking over a half-empty mug that says *“World’s Okayest Boss.”*

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
**They had the noise.  I had the blueprint.

**SOUND CUE – SCHILLING’S VOICE HITS:  
***“This is Major Tom to Ground Control…”*

**VISUAL: CREMEANS throws open a folder marked “Q3 TOUR – MASTER PLAN”  
**Inside: More calendars. Receipts. Names of clubs.  But also: ambition, written in highlighter.

**BEAT 2: LIFT OFF (JEFF’S POV)**

(SOUND: Peter Schilling still thumping, fading under dialogue. Phones ringing. Pens scratching. Pages flipping like rotor blades.)

**JEFF** stands in the doorway, holding a half-eaten bag of Funyuns, watching the scene like he’s stumbled into a Cold War ICBM launch simulation gone indie.

**CREMEANS** is planted at the antique knitting desk like it’s NORAD. The desktop plotter calendar dominates everything — sprawling over the desk, taped to the wall, spread onto the floor like it’s growing.

**CREMEANS (on the phone, animated)  
** No, *net* door, not gross. Yeah. We *split* the tips. Yes, even if it’s all quarters.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** I don’t know what he was doing exactly.   But I was pretty sure NASA had less paperwork.

**VISUAL STYLE – VERHOEVEN MEETS EARLY MTV:  
** — A CLOSE-UP of **CREMEANS**’ Sharpie circling dates with brutal precision.  
 — Each venue name flashes on screen in bold, glitchy 80s fonts:  
*“Indianapolis: $3200 – IGNITION!”  
“Bogart’s: $3800 – BLAST OFF!”  
“Columbus: $5000 – WE HAVE LIFTOFF!”  
“Canal Street Tavern: $2000 – STAGE ONE SEPARATION!”  
“Wright State Spring Festival: $3700 – ENTERING ORBIT!”*

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
It was like watching someone plan a war they secretly hoped would go nuclear.

**CREMEANS** hangs up, grabs another flyer, dials again, already mid-sentence.

**CREMEANS**  
Hey, it’s **CREMEANS**—yeah, again. Look, here’s the deal—

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**I didn’t understand half the numbers then.  But I could see it in his eyes.  He thought we were going to the moon.  And God help me, I started to believe him.

**CAMERA: PUSH IN** on JEFF’s face.  Half grinning. Half horrified. All in.

**BEAT 3: ACCELERATION (GILLEY’S POV)**

(SOUND: “Major Tom” crescendos behind the noise — synths crash with snare hits, lights flare in time with the beat.)

**GILLEY** steps into the spotlight, and the world makes *sense*.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**    
Some people need years to grow into it.  To build confidence.  To fake it till they make it.  Me?  I was born for this shit.

** / GLAM-ROCK DREAMSTATE:**

- Smoke machines belch fog across a tiny bar stage like it’s Madison Square Garden.  
- Flashing lights illuminate **GILLEY** from behind, turning sweat into shimmer.  
- A close-up of his face mid-scream, eyeliner running slightly, but it looks intentional.  
- The crowd is a blur of motion — hands up, heads banging, mouths open, but all *faceless*. He’s not looking at them — they’re looking at *him*.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**    
Every stage felt like déjà vu.  Like I’d already lived this, just… waiting to catch up to it.

**INSERT SHOTS – RAPID FIRE:**

- **GILLEY** grabbing a mic stand and spinning it like a preacher in a tent revival.  
- **KATHY** beside him, locked in, not even glancing his way — _but there.  
-  A sea of sweaty kids shouting lyrics they barely know, but shouting anyway.  
- **GILLEY** shirtless, backlit, arms raised like a resurrection.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**    
You can’t fake presence.  You *either burn or you don’t.*

**CAMERA: PUSH IN ON GILLEY’S FACE**  
Eyes wild. Smiling. Breathing heavy. *Alive.*

**GILLEY (V.O.)**    
This wasn’t a climb.  It was a *return.*

---

**BEAT 4: BREAKING THE SOUND BARRIER (JEREMY’S POV)**

**MONTAGE – VARIOUS LOCATIONS – MAY INTO JUNE 1991**

(SOUND: Calendar pages whipping like chopper blades. A rising synth pulse undercuts it — tense, bright, urgent.)

**JEREMY** leans against the Econoline, flipping through the latest scribbled itinerary, grease on his hands, a rolled-up Miller High Life tucked in his back pocket.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
**First, it was a weekend thing.  Then it was a “Thursday too” thing.  Then it was *every* night.

** VISUAL STYLE:**

CALENDAR PAGES flip at an unnatural pace.  Venue names streak across the screen with stylized graphics:  
-  Columbus: $5000 – *Hyperburn*”  
- “Bogart’s: $3800 – *Plasma Entry*”  
- “Dayton Spring Fest: $3700 – *Max Capacity Achieved*”

Behind the glowing fonts, quick flashes of gear being loaded, cords tangled, back doors of venues slamming shut. **JEREMY’s** fingerprints are on every frame.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
I’d haul amps all night, then kegs at the warehouse by day.  But somewhere in there, I stopped dreading the late shift.  Started *liking* the noise.

**FLASH CUT – JEREMY LIFTING A CABINET onto the stage.**  
He grins, nods at the sound guy, gets a half-hearted nod back.  It feels like *something*.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**  
I couldn’t play. I didn’t write.  But I could move mountains in flight cases.

**ONE FLASHING DATE – JUNE 22 – INDIANAPOLIS – “HEADLINING” appears in blinking red.**

**JEREMY** sees it written in bold on the whiteboard in the warehouse, underlined twice.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
Maybe I didn’t have to push beer forever.  Maybe there was *another* way to make the grind matter.

**SOUND: WHIP-PAN to the next calendar page.**

---

**BEAT 5: REACHING ESCAPE VELOCITY (JIM’S POV)**

**EXT. PARKING LOT OUTSIDE THE WAREHOUSE – LATE AFTERNOON**

(SOUND: A tape deck clicks on. “Major Tom” is fading into the chorus. The wind kicks up a plastic bag and the smell of hot blacktop.)

**JIM** squints into the sun. There it is.

The Ford Econoline. No longer a ghost-gray rust bucket. Now a matte black beast with a DIY spray-paint job — a stylized rocket ship arcing through a cassette-shaped moon. *COMMUTED* stenciled across the side in jagged lettering like it was scratched in with a knife.

**JIM (V.O.)**    
Holy shit.  It had *room.*

**CAMERA: VERHOEVEN-STYLE CIRCULAR PAN around the van**  
The blurred background gives the illusion that it’s already moving. Already *gone.*

**CREMEANS (V.O., in a mission-control tone)**
We’re leaving the atmosphere.

**JIM** walks toward it like he’s approaching a spaceship. He slides open the side door.

**INSIDE THE VAN:**
- Amps neatly stacked.  
- Folded tarp over a milk crate of cables.  
- An entire corner cleared out, clearly measured… just for him.

His drum kit.  All of it.  All the *extra* pieces — the mis-matched toms, the octobans, the garbage can lid with the duct-taped clamp — it *fits.*

**JIM (V.O.)**  
You know what it’s like to be the drummer?  To always be in someone else’s way?

**He runs his hand across the paneling like it’s velvet.**

**JIM (V.O.)**    
Not here.  This van?  This van was *designed* for chaos.  For misfit parts.  
For loud motherfuckers with too much gear and too many opinions.

He pulls out a pad and starts sketching a new setup — wider, weirder, dumber. And he grins.

**JIM (V.O.)**    
I could finally build the monster right.  And this time?  It’s coming with us.

**BEAT 6: ESTABLISHING ORBIT (BILL’S POV)**

**CREMEANS** signs the lease agreement for the warehouse space, which is now filled with the band’s equipment, posters, and other merchandise. It looks like a makeshift command center.



**INT. DAYTON AIRPORT WAREHOUSE – LATE AFTERNOON**

(SOUND: A key turns in the lock. The giant metal door *clanks* open, echoing like a shotgun blast in a canyon. “Major Tom” is now in full chorus. The synths float.)

**BILL** steps inside, and stops.

Sunlight slices through the upper vents. Dust dances in midair like glitter caught in floodlights. The place is *huge* — open, ugly, perfect. It smells like oil and concrete and cold metal.

**BILL (V.O.)**    
**You could fit three garages in here.  
And it sounds like a goddamn airplane hangar.  
*This is gonna slap.*

**CAMERA: VERHOEVEN PAN — SLOW, PURPOSEFUL SWEEP**

 Drum kit in the far corner.  
— **KATHY**’s rig stacked high, cords coiled like snakes.  
— **GILLEY**’s mic stand is duct-taped to a cinder block base.  
— Posters slapped haphazardly on one wall — half curling off, all loud.

There’s a table with band shirts (two sizes, both wrong), a coffee pot that doesn’t work, and a broken stool **CREMEANS** insists is a “meeting chair.”

**CREMEANS** claps his hands together.

**CREMEANS  
**Welcome to mission control.

**BILL (V.O.)**    
**The reverb alone’s gonna make every riff sound like Zeppelin at Knebworth.  
You could whisper and it’d echo for *days*.

He walks the room slowly, clapping once, then again. The echo answers like applause.

**BILL (V.O.)**    
**This wasn’t a rehearsal space.  
It was an _amplifier.  
_For everything.  
The music.  
The noise.  
The mess.

He drops his gear by the wall, already planning mic placements in his head.

**BILL (V.O.)**    
**God help the neighbors.  
This place is gonna *scream.*

**BEAT 7: ASTRONAUT’S HOLIDAY (KATHY’S POV)**

**INT. BACKROOM OF BAR – NIGHT – POST-GIG**

(SOUND: Distant reverb from the stage. A snare hit echoes like it's coming from underwater. Someone laughs far away. Muffled. Unreachable.)

The lighting is soft, sepia-toned but desaturated — *not* warm. Dust hangs in the air like snow that forgot how to fall.

**CAMERA: VERHOEVEN-STYLE SURREALISM  
**— Close-up on **KATHY**’s face in profile, slightly out of focus.  
— Her eyes are glazed, not closed. Looking somewhere beyond the wall.  
— The man’s face never shown. Just the edge of a boot. A hand. Belt buckle. Forgettable pieces of someone she won't remember.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
**Floating in space.  
Untethered.  
No ground.  
No gravity.

Her hands move with muscle memory, not intent. She blinks slowly, like time has forgotten to move forward.

**CAMERA: PULLS BACK SLIGHTLY  
**The shadows of gig posters shimmer on the wall behind her — warped and ghosted by a spinning fan. One reads: *“COMMUTED – ONE NIGHT ONLY”*

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
**He said thank you.  
Like I gave him something.  
But I didn’t feel less empty.  
Just… quieter.

She finishes. Wipes her mouth. Adjusts her shirt. Doesn’t look up. She stands, zipping her jacket like it’s armor, not clothing.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
**People think space is cold.  
But it’s not.  
It’s _nothing.  
_And that’s worse.

**CAMERA: STATIC SHOT as she leaves  
**The door swings shut. The posters flutter slightly.

The room is silent.

**BEAT 8: MISSION ACCOMPLISHED (JEFF’S POV)**

(SOUND: “Major Tom” surging into final chorus — *“Coming home…”* — while the warehouse explodes with celebration.)

Confetti drifts like snow from the ceiling insulation someone poked with a broom. Lights flash, strobe-like, powered by a jerry-rigged surge strip duct-taped to a floor tom. The warehouse looks like a low-budget prom met a space shuttle launch and got drunk.

**CAMERA: CLOSE-UP – CREMEANS’ HAND  
**Raises a plastic bottle of Mountain Dew. A tiny red-and-silver rocket ship sticker wraps around the label.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**Thus according to prophecy.  
Behold: the Dew of Destiny.

**THE TOAST – ALL VOICES TOGETHER  
***“TO COMMUTED!”*

**CAMERA: CLOSE-UPS – FACES CAUGHT IN CELEBRATION**

— **KATHY** laughing with a mouthful of pizza.  
— **GILLEY** doing a fake slow-motion guitar solo with a broom.  
— **JIM** spinning a drumstick like a baton.  
— **BILL** saluting the Mountain Dew bottle like it's the American flag.

**CREMEANS** grins like a cult leader whose spaceship finally arrived.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**This was supposed to be dumb.  
Supposed to be a side hustle.  
A reason to drink and yell and maybe get free nachos.

**POP!  
**Someone opens champagne. Simultaneously:  
**POP!  
****CREMEANS** cracks his Dew like he’s christening a warship.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**But it was _working.  
_Not clean. Not safe.  
But real. Loud. Ours.

**CAMERA: SLOW ZOOM OUT – WIDE SHOT OF THE WAREHOUSE**

Everyone’s toasting. Posing. Yelling over each other.  
The cheap party lights flare like booster rockets.  
The confetti settles on amps, wires, cracked cymbals, and open beer cans.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**We weren’t coming home.  
We were just learning how to leave.

**FINAL SHOT:  
**The camera pulls back like a satellite feed — the warehouse glowing with noise, joy, chaos — shrinking into the dark.

The last note of *“Coming home…”* fades into ether.

**INT. DOWNTOWN SPRINGFIELD – BANQUET HALL – AUG 1991 NIGHT**

(SOUND: *Bruce Springsteen’s “Dancing in the Dark”* is pounding through rented speakers. Laughter bubbles like champagne, silverware clinks, heels scuff the parquet dance floor. A full slice of Midwestern joy… all happening under a huge, rented chandelier.)

The room is pristine. Overdone. Like a wedding exploded and arranged itself just so. White chair covers. Twinkling lights. Ice swans. A DJ in a tuxedo t-shirt. The dance floor is a mosaic of high heels and polyester suits grinding to Springsteen’s heartbreak anthem.

** VISUAL**: The camera glides over it all — glittering shoes, fake smiles, distant uncles with cheap cameras — until it lands on **KATHY, JIM, and BILL**, spinning each other around, faces glowing with sweat and joy. They look like 80s movie stars in a late-night MTV video: artificial, magnetic, *too* happy.

**V.O. – THE DANCERS (Collective):  
**They weren’t dancing for fun.  
They were dancing to forget.  
To deflect.  
To drown out the other half of the band sitting at the bar like they were at a funeral.

**AT THE BAR – JEFF & GILLEY**

Slouched in matching ill-fitting rental tuxes. Shirt collars limp. Faces sour. Hands wrapped around sweating whiskey glasses. Neither looking at the dance floor. Neither looking at each other.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**We were ghosts in a dream we didn’t believe in.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**    
**A thousand-dollar party for a five-dollar mistake.

The clink of a glass. The camera cuts close — **JEFF slams his empty down**, loud, sharp, wrong for the room. No one notices. Except **JEREMY**.

**JEREMY  
**(Half-drunk, glowing, beaming, bride somewhere else.)  
Hey, guys! You having a good time?

**GILLEY  
**(Deadpan.)  
Highlight of my fucking year.

**JEFF  
**(Smiles. Ugly.)  
Just peachy.

**V.O. – JEREMY  
**They weren’t happy.  
They weren’t subtle.  
And I was too dumb, or too in love, to care which.

**JEREMY  
**(Oblivious, cheerful)  
Ceremony went great, right? I mean, for Springfield? The caterer even got the chicken right. And no fights! That’s gotta be a record.

**GILLEY  
**No fights *yet.*

**JEFF  
**(Casual. Too casual.)  
We need to talk.

**MUSIC LOWERS SLIGHTLY — The World Tilts**

They’re still in the banquet hall, but suddenly it doesn’t feel like a wedding. It feels like a confrontation in a Western. Three men, one bar, no happy ending.

**JEFF  
**I checked my bank account.

**CLOSE-UP: His eyes. Cold. Focused.**

**JEFF (CONT'D)  
**I also checked plane tickets.  
Acapulco.  
Mexico.  
Round trip. For three.

**GILLEY nods, not smiling.  
**Like they’ve practiced this.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**We needed an out.  
Not just from the band.  
From *everything.*

**JEREMY  
**(Thrown, disbelieving)  
You’re not serious.

**GILLEY  
**Dead serious. We leave tonight.

**FLASH CUT – VERHOEVEN-STYLE FANTASY SHOT  
**Sun-soaked Acapulco beach.  
Cheap motel sign flashing.  
Empty stage on sand.  
The dream of escape, flickering like film stuck in the projector.

**JEFF  
**Two-diamond hotel. With a pool.  
**MOM**’s AAA card got us 12% off.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
**It wasn’t even the words.  
It was the *look* in their eyes.  
Like they already left, and were just waiting on me to realize it.

**JEREMY  
**I just got married.

**GILLEY  
**Exactly.

**JEFF  
**You don’t belong here either, man. You know it.

**JEREMY (Rising, pissed)  
**Are you guys insane?! This isn’t a game! I’m starting a *life* here!

**GILLEY  
**No. You’re quitting the band. You’re quitting *us.*

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
**They didn’t want to rescue me.  
They wanted to drag me back down with them.

**MUSIC: “Dancing in the Dark” hits the line — *“You can’t start a fire, You can't start a fire without a spark…”***

**JEFF (Cold)  
**We’re leaving. You’re either in or you’re not.

**FINAL SHOT: THE THREE AT THE BAR**

A triangle of tension. Static and still while the rest of the world spins and celebrates behind them. The camera slowly *zooms out* — the party growing distant, hollow.

The beat of the song becomes taunting.  
The laughter now sounds like mockery.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**We weren’t a band anymore.  
We were in the wreckage.

**INT. DOWNTOWN SPRINGFIELD - BANQUET HALL - NIGHT**

(SOUND: The music has stopped. A record player needle hiss would be fitting, but it’s just the dead silence of a reception between songs. Distant laughter. Clink of a fork. A cough.)

The mood is fractured. Guests sense something wrong, but can’t place it. A few glance toward the bar.

**AT THE BAR – JEFF & GILLEY & JEREMY  
**The tension is armor-thick. **JEFF** and **GILLEY** are squared off emotionally, **JEREMY** still in the eye of the storm.

Then:

**TIM WRIGHT enters, cutting the room in half.**

Dressed in **US Navy Service White Dress**, medals glinting. Clean. Pressed. Regal. The only man in the room who looks like *he has a plan and a backup plan.*

** VISUAL**: The camera follows Tim’s entrance from *knee-level*, the white of his uniform glowing like a holy figure — except he walks like a predator. Rigid. Determined.

**TIM  
**(Voice booming with Navy confidence)  
Hey. What’s the hold-up?

The bar trio turns slowly. **JEFF**’s jaw clenches. **GILLEY** exhales through his nose.

**V.O. – JEFF  
**Tim was the kind of guy who never left his ship.  
He just brought it with him.

**JEFF  
**(Flat)  
This is a private function, Tim.

**GILLEY  
**(Dry)  
Yeah. Beat it.

**TIM  
**(Grinning, not listening)  
Met your bride, **JEREMY**.

Beat.

**TIM (CONT'D)  
**Cunt.

A sonic blast in the silence. No music to hide behind. The word hits like a slap across a ballroom.

**VERHOEVEN CLOSE-UP**: **JEREMY** blinks like he’s been shot. **JEFF** and **GILLEY**… *smile.*

Not joy. Not approval.

*Permission.*

**JEFF  
**(Low, amused)  
Yeah, she is.

**GILLEY  
**(Same)  
A real cunt.

**V.O. – TIM  
**They were joking. I think.  
But something cracked right then.  
Like they were cutting the line and letting me drift.

**TIM  
**(Confused, edge creeping in)  
What the hell are you guys talking about?

**JEFF  
**(Quiet menace)  
None of your goddamn business.

**GILLEY  
**(Stepping forward)  
So beat it.

Tim’s fists clench. Ribbons twitch on his chest as his body shakes with anger.

**TIM  
**What the *fuck* did you say to me?

**JEFF  
**I said: beat it.  
*Naval etiquette should cover that.*

**GILLEY  
**Let it go, Tim.

Beat.

**TIM  
**(Low)  
You think you’re tough, huh?

**GILLEY  
**(Lower)  
I think I don’t need the uniform to be respected.

The words *cut*. And in that Moment, it’s clear:

They’re not brothers anymore.

**JEREMY**
(Desperate, placing a hand on Tim’s arm)  
Tim. Stop. Please. It’s my wedding.

**ZOOM**: On Tim’s face. Anger folding into resentment. Resentment melting into *loss.*

**TIM**  
(Final, muttered)  
Fine. But don’t forget… I’m always watching.

**V.O. – JEFF**  
He didn’t mean it like a threat.  But it *was* one.  Because he wasn’t our brother anymore.  He was a man in a white uniform…And we were in black.

**CAMERA: WIDE SHOT – RECEPTION CONTINUES**

Guests laughing again. “Shout” plays. No one saw it. No one cared.  But at the bar?  Three men stare at the space Tim left behind. And none of them move.

**INT. PLANNED PARENTHOOD CLINIC – DAY**

(SOUND: Soft humming of fluorescent lights. The low murmur of voices beyond the door. A printer quietly spits out paperwork.)

**NURSE JOHNSON**, mid-50s, professional but warm, sits across from **KATHY**, who looks… not broken, but hollow. Hoodie zipped up halfway. Eyes a little glassy. She’s trying to hold it together and mostly succeeding.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
(Smiling gently)  
 Let’s talk birth control options. You mentioned the IUD?

**KATHY**  
(Nods, voice dry)  
Yeah. Something long-term. Low maintenance.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
**Perfect. We can schedule you for an insertion. How’s next Thursday morning?

**KATHY**  
(Without hesitation)  
That works.

**VISUAL**: A close-up on Nurse Johnson flipping her appointment book, fingers steady. Then to **KATHY** — shoulders squared. Chin lifted half an inch higher than when she walked in.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
You’ll want to take some ibuprofen an hour before. And ideally, you’re not on your period that day. I’ll walk you through the rest.  
(Pause)  
We’ll also need a quick STI screen and some history.

**KATHY**  
(Straightforward, no drama)  
Twelve.

**NURSE JOHNSON**
(Pauses ever so slightly, then nods)  
In the last twelve months?

**KATHY**
(Still calm)  
Yes.

**FLASH**: A blink-and-you-miss-it twitch in Nurse Johnson’s eyes. The faintest spark. But her voice remains steady.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
Thanks for your honesty. It helps us do this safely. That’s what matters.

**KATHY (V.O)**  
She didn’t ask why.  Didn’t raise an eyebrow.  Didn’t offer a lecture.  She just kept moving, like I wasn’t broken, just… in progress.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
(Handing over a slim packet of pamphlets)  
This explains the procedure and aftercare. Call us if you have questions or change your mind.

**KATHY** takes the papers. Her hand is steady. She almost says “thank you,” but doesn’t. Instead, she nods. It’s enough.

**VERHOEVEN-STYLE VISUAL**: **KATHY** exiting through automatic doors. Harsh sunlight floods her as the door whooshes shut behind her. The pamphlets are clutched in her hand like a hall pass.

**KATHY (V.O)**  
It wasn’t a fix.  It wasn’t redemption.  It was just… a line in the sand.  Not this. Not again. Not like that.

**(BRIEF FLASH MONTAGE)  
- **KATHY** reading the pamphlet under a lamp, biting her thumbnail.  
- **KATHY** tuning a guitar with new strings.  
- **KATHY** walking past a bar she used to duck into at 1 a.m. without even glancing sideways.  
- **KATHY** laughing — genuinely — at something **JEREMY** says off-camera, unaware of the laugh until it’s already out.

**KATHY (V.O)**
I didn’t even know what the next right thing was.  But I knew what the next *wrong* thing was.  And for the first time in a long time, I wasn’t doing that.

**FINAL SHOT**: **KATHY** walking down the sidewalk. The sun's in her face now. No triumphant music. Just footsteps. Just movement

**KATHY (V.O.)** I didn’t know it then, but that appointment… it changed me. It gave me something I’d never had before: agency. And with that came something else: a complete and utter lack of fucks to give about what anyone else thought.

**(FINAL SHOT):** **KATHY** walks down the street, the pamphlets clutched in her hand, a new sense of confidence radiating from her. The setting sun casts long shadows, symbolizing the long journey ahead, but **KATHY** is ready. She has taken the first step. The scene dissolves. 

---

**The Ford Econoline van and JEFF’s Escort barrel westward under a low, cloud-heavy sky. Their headlights cleave through the dark, desolate stretches between Dayton and Chicago. Refineries blink in the distance. Transmission towers loom like skeletal monoliths.**

**SOUND:** The constant low grind of rubber on concrete. The van's overworked suspension rattling. The Escort's tape deck murmuring the tail end of a worn-out mixtape — half-music, half-static.

** VISUAL:** Alternating cuts between both vehicles. Long aerial shots. Tight close-ups. Everything is dim, metallic, unnatural. Gary, Indiana is a graveyard of smokestacks and busted windows — more haunted than inhabited.**

---

**INT. FORD ECONOLINE VAN – CONTINUOUS**

BILL balances the fraying road atlas on his knees.

**BILL**  
 (half-muttered)  
 Gary’s up next. Then we cut north to the Skyway.

**BILL (V.O.)** 
 We weren’t tourists anymore. We were a band with a van. The kind you see parked behind every dive bar in every dying city.

GILLEY, hands gripping the wheel like it’s trying to buck loose, stares dead ahead.

**GILLEY (quietly)**  
 Place looks like hell coughed it up and forgot to swallow.

**The van jolts as they hit a pothole the size of a baptismal font.**

---

**EXT. HIGHWAY – CONTINUOUS**

**They pass the sign: “Welcome to Gary, Indiana” — bullet holes in the metal, rust chewing at the corners. A collapsed overpass looms to the right like the skeleton of ambition.**

** VISUAL:** The sign flashes behind them in the rearview. A child’s broken tricycle lies in a median.

---

**INT. FORD ESCORT – CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF** stares straight ahead, jaw set. **JEREMY** is folded over a clumsy, trifold map of Chicagoland.

**KATHY** is sprawled in the back. Hood pulled halfway up, face damp with sweat, her arm clenched across her abdomen.

**JEREMY (frustrated)  
 This doesn’t make any damn sense. Why does every road change names three times?

**JEREMY (V.O.)**   
** Chicago didn’t invite you in. It just… absorbed you. No welcome mat. Just concrete, exhaust, and noise.

**KATHY  
** (strained, barely audible)  
 Bathroom. Now.

---

**INT. FORD ESCORT VAN – CONTINUOUS**

**GILLEY** glances into the mirror, sees **KATHY** curled into a comma in the Escort.

**GILLEY**  
 She doesn’t look good.

**BILL ** 
(nods)  
 This part of the drive doesn’t look good either.

**BILL (V.O.)    
 Gary’s like a cancer that metastasized out of Chicago and kept growing. No heart. No skyline. Just scars.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
 I thought I was tough. One little coil of copper and progesterone shouldn’t feel like someone’s jabbing a corkscrew through my guts. But it did.

**KATHY**  
(bitterly)  
 This thing’s trying to murder me from the inside out.

**JEFF**  
(concerned but clueless)  
 Should we pull over? Maybe a rest stop or something?

**KATHY**  
(snarling through the pain)  
 Unless the rest stop has a morphine drip and a gynecologist, no.

** VISUAL:** Close-up on **KATHY**’s clenched teeth, then to **JEFF**’s face, blank and helpless. **JEREMY**, frozen between compassion and panic.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
I’d forgotten to take the ibuprofen this morning. Classic fuck-up. Rookie move.   But this?   This was hell in a bucket seat.

---

**INT. FORD ECONOLINE VAN – CONTINUOUS**

The Sears Tower appears like a spike against the sky — distant and surreal.

**BILL**  
(excited)  
There! Sears Tower!

**GILLEY** (flat) 
That's twenty-five miles away. Downtown’s not even waving at us yet.

**BILL (V.O.)**    
Chicago wasn’t just big. It was planetary. And we were just specks on the windshield.

---

**INT. FORD ESCORT – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** moans again, curled into herself. **JEREMY** fumbles for a bottle of water. **JEFF** white-knuckles the wheel.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
We were on an adventure. Supposed to be, anyway.   But **KATHY**… she was living her own subplot. A solo act in a torture chamber.

---

**FINAL SHOT – EXT. SKYWAY BRIDGE – NIGHT**

The van and Escort crest the rise of the bridge. The city sprawls before them, neon haze and infinite possibility.

** VISUAL:** The skyline glows ahead like Oz. But in the back seat of the Escort, **KATHY** closes her eyes — not from wonder, but from pain.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
All I wanted was to not bleed.  And all I got was pain.  Maybe that’s the trade.  Maybe that’s just what it costs to start fixing yourself.

The Escort presses through the night like a tired animal, the city lights of Chicago a faint shimmer ahead. Inside: claustrophobic, silent but for static and pain.

**(SOUND:)** The steady hum of the engine, flickers of static from the half-tuned radio, and KATHY’s faint, involuntary whimpers.)

They pass a gaudy **BILL**board hawking a personal injury lawyer. "HURT? CALL BART!" The suited man grins with too many teeth.

**(VISUAL):** The board burns unnaturally bright against the dark industrial sprawl—garish, grinning, indifferent.

**INT. FORD ESCORT – CONTINUOUS**

**JEREMY** fidgets with the map, trying not to look back. **JEFF** stares dead ahead. **KATHY** lies curled in the backseat, not apologizing anymore—just enduring.

**JEREMY**  (softly)  
So… **KATHY**… this morning. Were you… I mean, were you told what to expect?

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
Every word was a tightrope walk. She didn’t need pity. She didn’t need jokes. She needed space—and maybe, honesty.

  
**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
Briefed.” Christ. Like we were storming the beach.

**KATHY**  
(flat, dry)  
I was briefed. Yeah. They just forgot to mention the part where it feels like a bear trap's going off inside you.

A beat. She adjusts herself, winces.

**KATHY **(CONT’D)**  
And I forgot to take anything this morning. I was in such a rush… stupid.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
This wasn’t their fault. It wasn’t even the IUD’s fault. It was mine—rushing, half-asleep, skipping the painkillers like a rookie. But I didn’t want sympathy. I just wanted to survive the next few hours.

**JEFF**  
Maybe we should stop at the—

**KATHY**  (cutting, but calm)  
Don’t.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on **KATHY**’s face. Tired, clammy, but composed. Not snapping. Just asking for silence. A beat of respect passes between them.

---

**INT. FORD ESCORT – LATER**

Chicago is a little closer. The road stretches on, endless. Static sputters from the radio.

**JEREMY  
**(thoughtful)  
Man… if we had a car phone, this would be so much easier. Just call **CREMEANS** and tell him we’re behind.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
Car phones. Like laserdiscs and flying cars—cool until you remember the price tag.

**(VISUAL):** Flash: a shimmering fantasy shot of a sleek mobile phone glowing like a prop from *Star Trek*. Back to the dusty, taped-up Escort.

**JEFF**
(disbelieving scoff)  
A car phone? What a waste. I’d rather have tires with tread.

  
**JEFF (V.O.)**    
Mobile phones. Like beepers and gold chains. Things guys bought when they needed strangers to know they were important.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
Still can’t believe **CREMEANS** got that pager. As if Quincy Jones is gonna page him for a collaboration.

**(OBSERVATION – JEFF):  
JEFF (V.O.)**    
** A pager. Status symbol for exactly five seconds. Now it just beeped to remind you that nobody was calling.

**JEREMY  
**(laughs)  
 Remember how smug he looked? "Don’t want to miss any important messages." Yeah, sure, dude.

**(VISUAL):** Brief flashback—**CREMEANS** flashing the pager like a Rolex. Back to the Escort: laughter fading.

**KATHY  
**(softly, weakly)  
Guys… please.

They both go silent.

**  
**KATHY (V.O.)**    
**I didn’t want sympathy. I didn’t want jokes. I just wanted to get there… to anywhere that wasn’t this goddamn back seat.

**(OBSERVATION – COLLECTIVE):  
V.O. (collective)  
**None of us knew what we were doing. Not really. But that night, the road became a mirror—showing us all the cracks.

**(VISUAL):** The Escort cuts forward through the dark. The city glows faintly ahead, like a finish line you can never quite reach.

**(FINAL SHOT):  
** The road stretches, cold and indifferent. The car presses on—tired bodies, fraying nerves, and one silent promise: just get there.

---

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – TUNNEL – NIGHT**

The band, followed by **CREMEANS**, emerges from the mouth of their journey into the cathedral of their ambitions. A long concrete tunnel yawns ahead, bleak and vast, swallowing sound, light, and nerves.

(SOUND: Footsteps echo with military rhythm. A low wind whistles through concrete gaps. Somewhere far away, the hollow thump of a mic check.)

( VISUAL): The camera tracks behind them, long lens, their figures shrinking as the tunnel stretches. The lights flicker cold, industrial. Each shadow is a reminder of what could go wrong.

**KATHY** limps, clutching her abdomen. She’s gritting her teeth. Her body’s no longer betraying her—it’s punishing her.

(OBSERVATION – **KATHY**):  
 **KATHY (V.O.)**  
 This wasn’t cramping. This was revenge. My uterus was staging a full-blown insurrection.

  
 **KATHY (V.O.)**  
 If collapsing dramatically on the stadium floor was an option, I would’ve taken it. Might even get a sympathy article in the student newspaper.

**CREMEANS** stops. Turns. Looks at her with something approaching alarm.

**CREMEANS** You okay? You look like you’ve been shot.

( VISUAL): His concerned face, lit like a detective in a noir—half shadow, half dread.

**KATHY** (weakly)  
 Fine. Just… playing through the pain.

She takes another step. Almost folds.

  
 **JEREMY (V.O.)**  
 She wasn’t okay. We all knew it. But none of us knew what to do.

**CREMEANS** leans in.

**CREMEANS** You don’t have to do this. We can—

**KATHY** (sharp, breathless)  
 We are doing this. Shut up.

  
 **CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
 I was out of my depth. Tour manager? Sure. Medic? Hell no.

They continue walking. The tunnel yawns open to a distant glow—Dyche Stadium’s field, pulsing like the promise of a dream.

---

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – TUNNEL – LATER**

The group pauses. The buzz of distant sound checks and crew chatter rises faintly. **CREMEANS** checks his watch, then checks it again, as if it might offer wisdom.

**CREMEANS** We’re up at two tomorrow. That’s thirteen hours. What’s the plan?

( VISUAL): Close-ups of each face, reacting to “plan” like it’s a foreign concept.

**JEFF** (thoughtfully)  
 I plan to infiltrate the Northwestern library, dismantle the Western Canon, and maybe—if time allows—punch Derrida in the teeth.

**JEFF (V.O.)** Or hit the first dive bar and drink until I'm fluent in existential despair.

**BILL** (deadpan)  
 Pizza. Phone. Girls. Not in that order.

**BILL (V.O.)** Nourishment. Nostalgia. Nookie. The holy trinity.

**KATHY** (smiling through pain)  
 Frat house. No underwear. Maybe steal a beer keg and sing “Piece of My Heart” on their roof.

**KATHY (V.O.)** If I’m going to bleed, I might as well make it memorable.

**JIM** (grinning)  
 Party 'til I black out. Then find a second party to wake up at.

**JIM (V.O.)** If chaos were a vitamin, I’d be overdosing.

**JEREMY** (shrugging)  
 Call my wife. Remind her I’m not dead.

**JEREMY (V.O.)** I wasn’t ready to admit it, but I missed her already. More than I should’ve.

**GILLEY** (conspiratorial)  
 Scoreboard. Christmas lights. “69.” No notes.

( VISUAL): A surreal cutaway of **GILLEY** perched on the scoreboard, haloed by blinking digits.

**CREMEANS** (staring, defeated)  
 You’re… all serious.

**CREMEANS (V.O.):** We were twelve hours away from our biggest gig ever. And they were planning frat raids and pizza orgies. I was managing a band. They were managing their own disaster.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):** **CREMEANS** clutches his Mountain Dew like it’s a holy relic. Around him, the band buzzes with anticipation and exhaustion. Behind them, the tunnel. Ahead, the stadium—waiting to be conquered.

---

**JEFF'S ZOO STATION MONTAGE**

**(SOUND:** The opening distorted guitar riff of U2's "Zoo Station" explodes as the band members scatter in six different directions. The music's driving beat and chaotic energy perfectly mirror **JEFF**'s descent into madness.)

**(VISUAL):** Rapid cuts, jump cuts, and distorted camera angles create a sense of disorientation and chaos. Think early MTV meets Verhoeven, with a dash of internet meme humor.

**SCENE 1: THE LIBRARY (INITIAL DECEPTION)**

**INT. NORTHWESTERN UNIVERSITY LIBRARY – NIGHT**

*(SOUND: The distorted, grinding riff of “Zoo Station” kicks hard — as if the song itself has kicked in the doors.)*

A tracking shot glides over rows of clean, well-lit bookshelves. Students, quiet, composed, highlight textbooks. The library breathes quiet purpose.

*Then — smash cut.*

**JEFF** enters like a man on a mission of deceit. Blazer, collared shirt (untucked), glasses that might not be prescription. He moves with exaggerated seriousness, scanning the spines.

( VISUAL): The camera warps slightly as he walks, the lens ever-so-slightly fish-eyed. Fluorescent lights buzz too loud. Students seem hyperreal, twitchy in their stillness.

He plucks a thick tome from the shelf:  
 **“Post-Structuralist Literary Theory: A Reader.”**

**JEFF** flips it open to a page titled _“Hyperreality and the Death of Meaning.”  
_ He nods solemnly. Yawns. Deeply.

Then, without breaking eye contact with the text, he slides a flask from inside his blazer.

(OBSERVATION – **JEFF**):

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** Immersion in local culture. Phase one complete.

He tips the flask, takes a long pull. His eyes water, but he swallows it like gospel. A slow smile crawls across his face.

*Cut to: the book now used as a coaster on a side table near a quiet group study pod.*

**JEFF** walks past, whispering to a startled freshman:

**JEFF (hushed)  
** Baudrillard is my co-pilot.

---

**SCENE 2: THE REAL IMMERSION**

**EXT. EVANSTON STREET – OUTSIDE A DIVE BAR – HOURS LATER**

*(SOUND: "Zoo Station" now fully roaring — distorted, frenetic. Every snare hit sounds like a brick thrown through a window.)*

**JEFF** tumbles out of a narrow, neon-lit door. His tie is a noose hanging off one shoulder. His hair? Some combination of electroshock and karaoke-induced wind shear.

He’s holding a *half-empty bottle of tequila,* dancing awkwardly with it as if it were his date for the evening.

Behind him, the bouncer yells:

**BOUNCER  
** That’s it! No *Springsteen* in German ever again!

**JEFF** shouts back:

**JEFF  
** *“Ich bin der Boss, motherfucker!”*



**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** Turns out, “local culture” involves a lot of cheap tequila and questionable karaoke.

He stumbles into the alley, takes a shaky bow to an invisible crowd. From somewhere deep in the bar, the garbled echo of a drunken rendition of “Like a Prayer” drifts out.

**JEFF** raises the bottle in solemn salute. Then slips on a wet pizza box and vanishes out of frame.

*Smash cut to black. Bassline pulses like a heartbeat made of regret.*

SCENE 3: THE UNDERGRADUATES (UNSUSPECTING VICTIMS)

EXT. NORTHWESTERN UNIVERSITY LIBRARY – NIGHT

*(SOUND: “Zoo Station” hums underneath like a malfunctioning machine — pulsing, glitching, threatening to explode.)*

Two undergrads — earnest, bespectacled, carrying tote bags full of expensive textbooks — exit the library. They talk in hushed tones about something deeply academic. Or maybe Star Trek.

Enter **JEFF** from frame left, stage-tilting, tequila bottle in hand, arms flailing like semaphore flags in a windstorm.

( VISUAL): The camera *whips* into close-ups of the undergrads’ faces — wide eyes, twitching mouths, the unmistakable look of prey spotting a wounded predator with nothing left to lose.

**JEFF** You guys! *You guys.* I have cracked Derrida. I *killed* the author. With this. *(He waves the tequila bottle like Excalibur.)*

One of the undergrads takes a half step back. The other tightens his grip on his backpack.

UNDERGRAD #1  
 Uh… we have a seminar in the morning…

**JEFF** Perfect! I’ll audit! But only if I can scream about Lacan during attendance.



**JEFF (V.O.)**    
 I was Socrates with a drinking problem. Diogenes with better shoes. And they… they were my unsuspecting disciples.

He stumbles closer, begins to recite — not Derrida — but *lyrics* to “Sister Christian,” misattributing them to Roland Barthes.

**JEFF** “Motoring… what’s your price for flight?” *(beat)* That’s *punctum*, right? That’s the wound.

---

SCENE 4: THE DEBATE (A DISASTER)

INT. CAMPUS QUAD – LATER

A folding chair. A trashcan podium. A lone lamppost casting harsh white light.

**JEFF** stands on an overturned recycling bin, addressing… no one. Except a raccoon nearby and a couple walking briskly by, choosing fear over confrontation.

(SOUND: “Zoo Station” now a throbbing migraine of synth and guitar stabs.)

A MONTAGE:

- **JEFF** spills tequila on his shirt as he passionately argues the meaning of “différance.”
- He points at the raccoon like it's a tenured professor and yells, _“You get it, don’t you? You little semiotic fuck!”  
      
      
    _
- He starts singing *“Every Rose Has Its Thorn”* — off-key, voice cracking — using the tequila bottle as a mic.  
      
      
    
- He attempts to climb onto a bike rack to make a stronger rhetorical point, but falls, knocking over a trash can.  
      
      
    
- He sits in the grass, eyes glassy, telling the raccoon:  
     **JEFF** (slurred)  
     You’re the *only one* who understands me, Roland.  
      
      
    

(OBSERVATION – **JEFF**):

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
 The debate… it was… spirited.

*Cut to a security light blinking overhead, casting intermittent flashes over **JEFF** passed out beneath a student activities poster advertising “Mindfulness Yoga.”*

SCENE 5: THE TEQUILA-FUELED EPIPHANY

EXT. UNIVERSITY PARK – VERY LATE NIGHT

The quad is nearly empty. A mist rolls low over the trimmed grass. A flickering streetlamp buzzes overhead like it's considering quitting. **JEFF** slumps on a bench, half-empty bottle of tequila resting in his lap like a security blanket.

(SOUND: “Zoo Station” distorts into a wailing, decelerated breakdown — slowed and dragged like an old cassette unraveling.)

Across from him, a squirrel perches on a garbage can, nibbling a sandwich crust. **JEFF** locks eyes with it.



**JEFF (V.O.)**    
 The squirrel… it understood. It *all* understood.

( VISUAL): The camera pushes *hard* into **JEFF**’s dilated pupils, then cuts to a surreal, slow-motion shot of the squirrel chewing, lit like a deity in a shampoo commercial. The crust crumbles. It’s beautiful. It’s meaningless. It’s everything.

**JEFF** You get it, right? There’s no center. No original. Just… text. Just… tail.

He laughs, then weeps. Then laughs while weeping. It's unclear where one ends and the other begins.

---

SCENE 6: THE SQUIRREL (AN UNWILLING PARTICIPANT)

EXT. UNIVERSITY PARK – CONTINUOUS

**JEFF** slides off the bench with drunken purpose and approaches the squirrel slowly, reverently, like he’s about to address a forest tribunal.

**JEFF** Let’s *talk*, okay? Just two sentient beings… trapped in a meat grinder of signifiers… parsing what’s real…

He crouches, holding the tequila bottle out like a peace offering.

**JEFF** (CONT'D)  
 You ever read Baudrillard?

The squirrel freezes. Assesses. Then bolts into the nearest bush.

( VISUAL): A shaky, disorienting POV shot from **JEFF**’s perspective as the squirrel vanishes, accompanied by a Doppler-shifted skittering sound that echoes like a philosophical rejection.

**JEFF** (yelling after it)  
 COWARD! FACE YOUR ONTOLOGY!

(OBSERVATION – **JEFF**):

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
 And just like that… it was gone. The only creature that ever truly listened.

*Final shot: **JEFF** alone on the grass, surrounded by discarded pamphlets and empty mini liquor bottles. “Zoo Station” sputters, then cuts out completely.*

  
  

**(VISUAL):** Slow-motion shot of the squirrel fleeing in terror, accompanied by dramatic music.

**EXT. EVANSTON RESIDENTIAL NEIGHBORHOOD – NIGHT**

**JEFF** stumbles down a quiet, tree-lined street, tequila bottle still in hand, now mostly empty. Victorian-style homes rise like polite phantoms in the mist. Porch lights glow like interrogators. He squints at a street sign and nods with unearned confidence.

(SOUND: The echoing *clack* of his shoes on pavement, the soft *ting* of wind chimes, the occasional bark of a distant dog.)

(OBSERVATION – **JEFF**):

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** Navigation… it was never my strong suit. Even sober, a map looked like a Jackson Pollock painting. And tonight? Well, I was painting with tequila and hubris.

( VISUAL): A high, Dutch-angle crane shot follows **JEFF** as he zigzags past manicured hedges and confused cats on windowsills. Streetlights flare like overexposed stars, flickering as though rejecting his presence.

He pauses in front of a mailbox labeled “HENDERSON,” salutes it, and mutters something about deconstruction. Then he walks into a hedge.

---

**SCENE 8: THE AWAKENING**

**EXT. HENDERSON FRONT LAWN – EARLY MORNING**

Dew glistens on the grass. Birds chirp. A gentle sprinkler arcs back and forth across a well-maintained lawn… and onto **JEFF**, who is sprawled facedown in a pile of damp leaves. His shirt is open, his tie around his head like a disillusioned bandanna.
