(SOUND: The rhythmic *chhh-chhh* of the sprinkler. One bird lands on a nearby bush, assesses **JEFF**, and flies away.)

The sprinkler hits him squarely in the face. He sputters awake, blinking against the water, looking around like a man who just got dropped into a foreign film mid-scene.



**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** Turns out, “local culture” also involves sleeping on strangers’ lawns. With sprinklers. In your goddamn face.

( VISUAL): A tight, spinning overhead shot of **JEFF** as he sits up, dazed, the grass stained on his clothes, leaves in his hair, mascara-smudged book still clutched in his hand. His flask clinks against his hip as he slowly realizes: he's utterly, completely… not at the stadium.

*Final frame: He mutters something unintelligible and topples over again as the sprinkler hits him once more. Cut to black.*

---

**SCENE 9: THE WALK OF SHAME**

**EXT. EVANSTON – LAKESIDE BIKE PATH – EARLY MORNING**

**JEFF** shuffles along the sidewalk, a picture of self-inflicted ruin. His shirt is buttoned wrong, his tie now limp around his neck like a noose of poor decisions. His shoes are mismatched. Leaves cling to his hair like nature’s judgment.

He passes a **cluster of early-morning joggers**, their pristine Nike gear and energized strides a cruel contrast. One woman slows, eyes narrowing as she assesses the staggering wreckage.

( VISUAL):  
 Slow-motion shot as **JEFF** slouches past the joggers. Their steps seem choreographed, angelic in rhythm. **JEFF** moves like a film reel out of sync—his limbs trailing just behind the beat. The distorted intro of “Zoo Station” deconstructs into a melancholic instrumental echo. The camera lingers on **JEFF**’s eyes: bloodshot, sunken, aware that he is now the joke.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** This was no longer satire. This was my biography.

---

**SCENE 10: THE REUNION (A DISASTER)**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE TUNNEL – MINUTES LATER**

The band huddles with **CREMEANS**, who’s pacing, clipboard in one hand, pager in the other. The midday sun filters harshly through the stadium entrance.

**JEFF** lurches into view, silhouetted against the concrete light like a war casualty. He’s still swaying. The tequila bottle is gone, but the *stench* of the night clings to him like bad poetry.



**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** Ground control to Major Tom… we have a problem. And that problem smells like well tequila, barf, and post-structuralist regret.

The rest of the band stares. Silence. Then **JIM** breaks it with a single, dumbfounded blink.

**JIM  
** Holy shit. He made it.



**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** Maybe post-structuralism wasn’t the best topic for a tequila-fueled debate. But that squirrel… it *got* me, man.

( VISUAL):  
 Wide-angle, static frame of the band clustered in one corner, clean and ready to perform. **JEFF** stands opposite, shadowed, slouched, a walking warning sign. The tension is thick as the opening chords of their first song start to soundcheck from the field.

---

**FINAL SHOT**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BLEACHERS –** MOMENT**S LATER**

**JEFF** sits alone, the stadium now slowly coming to life around him. Rows and rows of empty seats stretch to the heavens. His clothes still damp, his posture defeated.

(SOUND: The last faded echo of “Zoo Station,” now distant and ambient. No dialogue. Just breath. Stadium reverb. Regret.)



**JEFF (V.O.)**    
** It started as a joke. But the punchline? That was all mine.

(Camera slowly pulls back, higher and higher, until **JEFF** is a single figure dwarfed by the architecture of the stadium—a dot, a mistake, a cautionary tale.)

**TEXT ON SCREEN:**  
**DYCHE STADIUM – EVANSTON, IL – 10:13 AM**

**RICO'S SCOREBOARD SAGA MONTAGE**

**(SOUND:** The opening spoken-word intro of Gerardo's "Rico Suave" begins as the band members scatter. "Suave… suave… Rico… Suave…" The music's infectious Latin beat and over-the-top machismo provide the perfect soundtrack for Rico's escapade.)

**(VISUAL):** Rapid cuts, jump cuts, and exaggerated camera angles create a sense of frantic energy and comedic exaggeration. Think a blend of action movie tropes and slapstick comedy.

**SCENE 1: THE MISSION BRIEFING (SELF-DELUSION)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – PARKING LOT – NIGHT**

**GILLEY**, now fully immersed in his alter ego “RICO,” strikes a heroic pose beside the band van. His shirt is half-unbuttoned, aviator shades on (despite it being night), and he’s chewing gum with militant precision.

(SOUND: The opening lines of **Gerardo's "Rico Suave"** — *"Suave…suave…Rico…Suave…"*)

( VISUAL):  
Dutch angles, lens flares, and artificially enhanced wind dramatically ruffle his hair. The parking lot looks like a music video battlefield. A nearby cat screeches and runs off.

**OBSERVATION – RICO (V.O.)**    
** Operation: 69. A mission of vital importance. A mission only Rico Suave could handle. The stakes? Monstrous. The risk? Erotic. The reward? Eternal scoreboard glory.**

**GILLEY** nods solemnly to himself, slaps a pair of novelty sunglasses on over the aviators, and jogs toward the stadium perimeter with purpose.

---

**SCENE 2: THE INFILTRATION (A COMICAL CLIMB)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – PERIMETER FENCE – NIGHT**

Rico scans the wall like a Navy SEAL—who’s been drinking. He mutters action clichés under his breath.

**RICO (V.O.)**    
Stealth was key. Or at least, it would have been… if I hadn’t tripped over that goddamn garbage can.

(SOUND: Loud metallic *CLANG* as Rico faceplants over a tipped trash bin. Gerardo’s beat doesn’t stop.)

He scrambles up, dramatically somersaults to nowhere, and begins climbing. He grabs at bricks that aren’t handholds, jams his sneaker into a storm drain, and somehow *succeeds* through pure, undeserved luck.

( VISUAL):  
Exaggerated close-ups: sweat beads on his forehead, the glint in his eyes, his fingers slipping, his shirt riding up. A security camera watches silently, lens slowly zooming in as if confused.

**OBSERVATION – RICO (V.O.)**    
The wall was 30 feet of pure concrete hostility. No ladder. No plan. Just Rico. And one very stretched hamstring.

(FINAL BEAT OF SCENE):  
Rico hauls himself over the edge and collapses like a sack of lawn clippings—flat on his back, panting, but somehow triumphant.

**SCENE 3: THE SECURITY GUARD (AN UNWITTING ACCOMPLICE)**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – SECURITY OFFICE – NIGHT**

A PAUNCHY SECURITY GUARD sits slumped in a swivel chair, the glow of a *black-and-white television* flickering on his face. The sound of a late-night infomercial echoes from the small set.

(SOUND: “And *you* too can own a set of commemorative Civil War chess pieces for only three easy payments of $29.99!”)

**( VISUAL):  
 The camera lingers on the guard’s slack jaw, his eyes half-lidded in a trance. Sweat trickles down his temple. An untouched sandwich sags beside him. The world outside his booth doesn’t exist.

Behind the glass, we catch glimpses of movement: **Rico**, hunched behind an **obnoxiously large plastic ficus**, tiptoeing across the hallway like a cartoon criminal.

He moves two steps… freezes.  Moves again… freezes.  Spins the plant to face a different angle, for no reason whatsoever.

**RICO (V.O.)**    
Most people see a ficus. I see a goddamn invisibility cloak.

**(TARANTINO-ESQUE VISUAL):**  
Sudden whip zoom to Rico’s eyes peering through the leaves, cut with close-ups of the guard’s glazed eyes blinking out of sync with reality.

Rico edges past the booth and disappears around the corner. The guard remains utterly oblivious, now reaching for his sandwich with dramatic, lazy suspense.

---

**SCENE 4: THE TUNNEL CRAWL (A TIGHT SQUEEZE)**

**INT. STADIUM MAINTENANCE VENTILATION DUCT – NIGHT**

**Rico**, now stripped down to a tank top, squeezes himself through a **dust-choked** ventilation shaft barely wider than his shoulders. Each inch is a struggle.

(SOUND: Labored breathing, the grind of fabric scraping metal, and the occasional squeak of a poorly placed elbow.)

**(OBSERVATION – RICO (V.O.)):  
Turns out, I’m not as suave when I’m covered in dust bunnies. Or when my boxers are riding up somewhere only God and my chiropractor can see.

He stops mid-crawl and looks deadpan into the middle distance. A **single cobweb drapes across his forehead** like a cursed veil.

**( VISUAL):  
Extreme close-up on Rico’s eye twitching, cut with a flash frame of a taxidermy raccoon from some long-forgotten promotional display. The duct trembles under his weight.

**RICO (V.O.)**    
But Rico never quits. Rico never surrenders. Rico… just… really needs some Gold Bond.

He army-crawls onward, his dignity crumbling like plaster in the vents behind him.

**SCENE 5: THE SCOREBOARD ASCENT (A DANGEROUS STUNT)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – SCOREBOARD STRUCTURE – NIGHT**

The hulking frame of the stadium scoreboard looms like a black monolith against the night sky. Crickets chirp in the distance. The structure groans slightly in the wind.  Rico, clad in fingerless gloves and a harness he definitely doesn't know how to use, stares up at it with manic glee.

(SOUND: A heroic orchestral swell crashes into the gritty synth break of “Rico Suave.”)

  
**RICO (V.O.)**    
 Adrenaline was pumping. My heart was racing. I was Rico Suave, conquering the heights!   It was Everest. It was the Berlin Wall. It was that jungle gym I got stuck on in second grade—only now I had tequila and hubris.

( VISUAL):  
Dramatic low-angle shot as Rico begins his ascent: rope slung over one shoulder, belt full of zip ties, mouth full of gum.   He climbs, slips, recovers.   Climbs, dangles, curses.   At one point, he’s literally crawling across a ledge using only one shoe and his forehead for leverage.  A bird squawks from its nest above him. Rico flips it off without looking.

---

**SCENE 6: THE CHRISTMAS LIGHT ACQUISITION (A SHADY DEAL)**

**INT. STADIUM STORAGE ROOM – NIGHT**

Rico kicks open a rusted door to a forgotten utility closet deep beneath the bleachers. Dust billows out like a magician’s smoke.

Inside: a single shelf of ancient holiday decor—a sad string of tinsel, a cracked Santa head, and a tangled box of Christmas lights.

(SOUND: The faint electric hum of one flickering fluorescent bulb overhead.)

( VISUAL):  
 Close-up on Rico’s eyes narrowing like a thief in a diamond vault. The box glows faintly under the flickering light.  He lifts the tangled mess reverently, like Indiana Jones with the idol.

**RICO (V.O.)**
Red or green. Passion or envy. Love or rage.   But then it hit me… this isn’t a funeral. This is a celebration.

Quick cut: Rico pulls out a multicolored strand and kisses it.

**RICO (CONT’D) (V.O.)**    
Multi-color. The party starts now.

(TARANTINO-STYLE INSERT SHOT):  
Rico jams the lights into his backpack, slams the door shut behind him, and sprints back toward the looming scoreboard, eyes burning with psychotic Christmas spirit.

**SCENE 7: THE WIRING (A COMICAL ELECTROCUTION SCARE)**

**EXT. SCOREBOARD CATWALK – NIGHT**

Rico is hunched in a precarious position on the metal catwalk behind the scoreboard. He’s got the Christmas lights strung out like a chaotic tangle of glowing spaghetti, one end wrapped in duct tape, the other dangling near a battered power box labeled “HIGH VOLTAGE – AUTHORIZED PERSONNEL ONLY.”

(SOUND: The zippy buzz of fluorescent light mixed with Gerardo’s synth-heavy chorus.)

Rico squints. In one hand: a pair of wire strippers he probably stole from the janitor’s closet. In the other: a live wire he definitely shouldn't be touching.

( VISUAL):  
Extreme close-up of Rico's sweaty face, then jump cut to a spark explosion as he accidentally bridges two terminals.  He convulses comically—Looney Tunes style—his hair frizzing out in all directions, lit briefly like a human sparkler.
  
**RICO (V.O.)**    
Turns out, I’m not as good with electrical wiring as I thought.  I was aiming for “Bond villain,” but what I got was “shocked raccoon.”

CUT TO: Rico staggering backward, smoke rising from his fingertips. He grins anyway, teeth glowing faintly blue.

---

**SCENE 8: THE MESSAGE (A MOMENT OF TRIUMPH)**

**EXT. STADIUM FIELD – NIGHT**

Wide overhead shot. The stadium is dark and empty. But on the colossal scoreboard?  “69” glows in glorious, multicolored incandescent lights.

(SOUND: Gerardo’s “Rico Suave” hits the chorus. The beat drops hard.)

  
**RICO (V.O.)**
Mission accomplished. Rico Suave had left his mark on the world.  One number. Two digits. Infinite stupidity.

( VISUAL):  
A crane shot swoops past Rico—arms outstretched, shirt flapping in the wind like a flag of pure idiocy.   Below him, the entire stadium is bathed in tacky holiday cheer, a single blazing “69” twinkling like a cosmic joke.

FINAL IMAGE: Rico silhouetted against his glowing masterpiece.  A bottle of Mountain Dew in hand.   Eyes misty.   Sweat glistening.   America.

**SCENE 9: THE SECURITY GUARD’S RETURN (A SUDDEN INTERRUPTION)**

**INT. STADIUM CONTROL ROOM – NIGHT**

The room is dim and cluttered with ancient equipment and a plate of half-eaten nachos. The **flickering glow of the scoreboard** washes over the walls.

**(SOUND: A low buzz, followed by a mechanical beep.)**

A blinking red light on an ancient control panel suddenly grabs attention.

**( VISUAL):**  
The camera zooms slowly toward the guard's face, catching every twitch as he squints at the monitor.

**Cut to:**  
The security cam feed showing Rico on the scoreboard, arms raised like a maniacal mascot, with a glowing **“69”** behind him.

**The guard’s face transforms.** From **dull fatigue**, to **stunned disbelief**, to **pure annoyance**.

**SECURITY GUARD (flatly):**  
Mother of God…

He mutters into a walkie-talkie that’s clearly never been used for anything this ridiculous.

---

**SCENE 10: THE DESCENT (A HILARIOUS FALL)**

**EXT. SCOREBOARD STRUCTURE – CONTINUOUS**

Rico sees the guard through the distance. His eyes widen. He spins around and yells:

**RICO (panicked)**  
**Abort! ABORT!**

He makes a break for the catwalk—legs flailing, wires trailing. In his haste, he **trips over one of his own cords**, flips forward like a stuntman in a bad sitcom, and **plummets off a short ledge.**

(SOUND: Comedic drum sting followed by a loud WHUMP.)

**( VISUAL):**  
The fall is captured in glorious slow motion. Rico’s limbs flail like a malfunctioning marionette. Christmas lights explode around him like confetti. The scoreboard still reads “69,” winking suggestively.

**RICO (V.O.)**    
Gravity. The ultimate party crasher.

**FINAL IMAGE:**  
Rico sprawled face-up in a pile of discarded foam padding, blinking at the stars.  From somewhere above: the scoreboard buzzes, then shorts out in a small, sad fizzle.

**SOUND: One last “Rico… Suave…” echoes as the lights die.**

**RICO (V.O.)** 
Turns out, gravity is a real bitch.

**SCENE 11: THE APPREHENSION (A COMICAL ARREST)**

**EXT. SCOREBOARD BASE – NIGHT**

Rico lies tangled in a snarl of multicolor Christmas lights, blinking like a crash-landed UFO. He’s trying to untangle himself with the dignity of a drunken ballet dancer.

**(SOUND: Static-laced walkie-talkie and slow, deliberate footsteps.)**

The security guard approaches with a pair of cuffs and the unhurried menace of a man who has absolutely had it.

**( VISUAL):**  
A low-angle shot of Rico squinting up at the guard from the floor, surrounded by broken light bulbs, empty Mountain Dew cans, and a twisted extension cord like a noose.

**SECURITY GUARD (deadpan):**  
You got a permit for that public art installation?

**RICO (V.O.)**    
Even in handcuffs, Rico Suave never loses his cool.

(He winks. The guard doesn’t flinch.)

Cut to: Rico being gently hauled to his feet, still entangled in the lights, stumbling as he tries to strut in zip ties.

---

**SCENE 12: THE MORNING AFTER (A HANGOVER AND A HEADACHE)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM PARKING LOT – MORNING**

**(SOUND: Birds chirping. Distant L-train rattling. Rico groaning.)**

Rico sits on the curb, head in hands, sunglasses too large and too late to hide the damage. A bottle of Pedialyte rests beside him like a sacred offering.

**( VISUAL): ** 
Camera pulls up from Rico’s slumped form to the scoreboard now advertising **"Kraft Singles Family Night – Friday at 7!"** The "69" is gone—erased like it never happened.

**RICO (V.O.)**    
They say glory fades. But hangovers? Those linger.

**(FINAL SHOT):**  
Wide shot of the stadium’s empty lot.  Rico—still dressed like a knocked-off Bond villain—sits alone, a man basking in the memory of his own idiocy. He adjusts his collar, winces, and leans back with a sigh.

**SOUND: Gerardo’s “Rico Suave” outro hums faintly from a distant passing car.**

**JEREMY'S HONEYMOON PHONE CALL FROM HELL MONTAGE**

**(SOUND:** The iconic opening piano riff and vocal sample of *"Gonna Make You Sweat (Everybody Dance Now)"* blast as the band scatters. The song's energetic beat and suggestive lyrics create a hilariously awkward backdrop for **JEREMY**'s conversation.)

**SCENE 1: THE PAYPHONE (A LONELY OUTPOST)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – OUTER WALL – NIGHT**

**JEREMY** stands under the sickly yellow glow of a flickering streetlight, dwarfed by the looming concrete of the stadium. The only sign of life: a battered PAYPHONE box buzzing faintly with static.

He fumbles a wad of coins from his pocket—quarters, dimes, a Canadian penny, and what might be a button.

**( VISUAL):**  
Harsh close-ups: the smeared plexiglass of the phone booth, **JEREMY’s** sweaty hands clutching the change, a neon bug crawling across the receiver.

 
**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
Gonna make you sweat… gonna make you… call your wife.

He exhales, steels himself, and steps into the booth like it’s a confession box.

---

**SCENE 2: THE DIAL TONE (ANTICIPATION)**

**INT. PAYPHONE – CONTINUOUS**

The camera zooms in tight on **JEREMY’s** index finger as it slowly punches the numbers. Each button click echoes like a gunshot in the booth’s tinny acoustics.

**(SOUND):** The mechanical *click* of each digit. Then… the dial tone. Loud. Flat. Menacing.

**( VISUAL):  
** A rapid montage:**  
 – **JEREMY’s** nervous gulp.  
 – His wedding ring glinting in the payphone’s harsh light.  
 – A brief cutaway to his wife back home, brushing her hair in slow motion, totally unaware.  
 – The coin-drop spinning like a roulette wheel.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
This was it. The Moment of truth. The first phone call of married life.

He closes his eyes, braces for whatever awaits on the other end.

**SCENE 3: THE RING (AWKWARD SILENCE)**

INT. PAYPHONE – NIGHT

The phone rings. Once. Twice. Three times.  **JEREMY** stands rigid in the booth, breathing shallow, his eyes darting like a fugitive’s.

( VISUAL):  
 *Rapid cuts*:  
 – **JEREMY’s** hand tightening around the receiver, knuckles white.  
 – Sweat dotting his upper lip.  
 – His foot jittering in an arrhythmic tap, hitting the metal phone base.  
 – A flickering bulb overhead, buzzing louder with each ring.

(SOUND):  
 The ring tone blends with the still-looping beat of "Gonna Make You Sweat" in his head, creating a warped, anxious rhythm.

---

SCENE 4: THE ANSWER (THE WIFE’S VOICE)

A click.

**WIFE (V.O.)**   _(groggy, surprised)  
_ Hello?

**JEREMY** freezes. Then, like a reflex—possibly from panic, possibly from tequila-laced idiocy—he blurts:

**JEREMY** (overly chipper)  
*Everybody dance now!*

(SOUND):  
The beat from the song stops cold.

**JEREMY** (V.O.)**    
Wrong song for this situation.  Definitely the wrong song.

( VISUAL):  
**JEREMY’s** face in a Moment of horror.   A bead of sweat falls.   The silence on the other end stretches, long enough to feel like a cosmic punishment.

**SCENE 5: THE SMALL TALK (A DISASTER)**

INT. PAYPHONE – NIGHT

**JEREMY** leans against the scratched plexiglass wall of the booth, still clutching the receiver like it’s the last lifeline to normalcy. He tries to recover.

**JEREMY** So, uh… how was your day?

(SOUND):  
 The faint echo of “Everybody dance now!” pulses in his mind like a toxic mantra.

( VISUAL):  
 – Close-up: **JEREMY** mouthing “Everybody dance now!” with exaggerated intensity.  
 – Cut to: **JEREMY** attempting a suave wink at the reflection in the phone glass.  
 – Cut to: An errant pigeon outside the booth staring directly into the camera.

WIFE (V.O.)**   _(soft, longing)  
_ It was okay. I just… miss you.

**JEREMY** _(grinning like a game show host)  
*Gonna make you sweat!*

He raises his eyebrows. A beat too long.

  
 **JEREMY** (V.O.)**    
 Subtlety is overrated. Timing is everything.   I had neither.

---

SCENE 6: THE HONEYMOON RECAP (TOO MUCH INFORMATION)

Now full-throttle, **JEREMY** barrels through the conversational guardrails.

**JEREMY** Remember that time on the beach? When the umbrella blew away and you chased it in your swimsuit?

(SOUND):  
 He breaks into an impromptu, off-key falsetto of the chorus. His shoulders shimmy in time with some internal, inappropriate rhythm.

**JEREMY** _(mouthing)  
**Gonna make you sweeeaat…**

WIFE (V.O.)**   (horrified, whispering)  
**JEREMY**! There are other people in the house!

  
 **JEREMY** (V.O.)**    
 Details. It was all about the details. And the nudity.   But mostly the details.

( VISUAL):  
 – The camera slowly rotates around **JEREMY** as he pantomimes scenes from the honeymoon, including a fully-clothed recreation of him applying sunscreen.  
 – Quick insert: a moth flies into the payphone light and dies. Symbolic? Maybe.

**SCENE 7: THE BAND UPDATE (A GROSS MISCALCULATION)**

INT. PAYPHONE – NIGHT

**JEREMY** straightens up, switching gears, trying to sound like a Big Deal. The payphone crackles. He speaks louder, gesturing as if the street needs to hear his success.

**JEREMY** We’re playing in front of fifteen thousand people!

(SOUND):  
 *BOOM – “Everybody dance now!” smashes back into his head like a club anthem.*

( VISUAL):  
 – A slow-motion cut of **JEREMY** throwing his arms wide as if addressing a cheering crowd.  
 – Reality check: He’s alone. A rat scurries past the booth.

WIFE (V.O.)**   _(deadpan, distant)  
_ That’s great, honey. But I really need to go.

  
 **JEREMY** (V.O.)**    
 I was losing her. Fast.  
 The emotional equivalent of a mic drop — except the mic was me, and I was falling into a dumpster fire.

---

SCENE 8: THE DESPERATE PLEA (A COMPLETE FAILURE)

**JEREMY** clutches the phone tighter. His tone cracks like a cheap wineglass at a wedding toast gone wrong.

**JEREMY** I miss you so much! I can’t wait to see you again!

(SOUND):  
 The beat drops. **JEREMY** can’t resist. He mouths it again—only this time, he commits.

**JEREMY** (Mouthing, with exaggerated hip thrusts)  
 Gonna make you sweeeat…

( VISUAL):  
 – The camera zooms in fast and tight on **JEREMY’s** face, his eyes wide, pupils dilated from a mix of anxiety and late-night sugar crashes.  
 – Intercut with flashes of his honeymoon: mismatched socks, spilled wine, and a seagull stealing their lunch.

  
 **JEREMY** (V.O.)**    
 I had officially gone off script. The wrong movie, the wrong genre…  
 And no one was yelling “cut.”

  
  

**SCENE 9: THE HANG UP (A DEVASTATING BLOW)**

**INT. PAYPHONE – NIGHT**

The line goes dead with a sharp *click*. **JEREMY** stares at the receiver like it just shot him.

**(SOUND):  
** The music warps and distorts—“Everybody daaaaance…” slurring into dissonance.

**  
**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
** Ouch. That hurt.  
 Like getting ghosted with a dial tone.

**( VISUAL):  
** – The flickering streetlight above him dies with a sputter.  
 – **JEREMY** drops the receiver. It swings back and forth, tapping like a metronome of shame.

---

**SCENE 10: THE REPLAY (A** MOMENT **OF SELF-AWARENESS)**

**EXT. PAYPHONE – NIGHT / DAWN APPROACHES**

**JEREMY** leans against the booth, eyes closed. The events rewind in his mind like a bad highlight reel—every hip thrust, every lyric mouthed, every cringe-inducing line.

**(SOUND):  
** The C+C Music Factory chorus fades into a low, distorted echo.

 
**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
** Maybe “Gonna Make You Sweat” wasn’t the best soundtrack for a romantic phone call.  
 Maybe I should’ve gone with “I Just Called to Say I Love You.”  
 Or maybe… I should’ve just kept my damn mouth shut.

**( VISUAL):  
** – A wide shot: **JEREMY**, small and alone, silhouetted by the first hints of dawn.  
 – The empty street around him feels massive. The receiver dangles. The only other sound: a passing garbage truck.

---

**SCENE 11: THE DEJECTED WALK (A WALK OF SHAME)**

EXT. STREET OUTSIDE DYCHE STADIUM – EARLY MORNING

**JEREMY** walks away from the payphone, shoulders slumped, head down. The flickering streetlight above finally gives out.

( VISUAL):  
 – Slow-motion: **JEREMY’s** form receding into the emptiness of the street.  
 – Trash skitters past his feet. The city wakes around him—delivery trucks, joggers, sprinklers. But **JEREMY** is moving through a world all his own.  
 – The music slows to a crawl, echoing in half-time—“Everybody dance now…” becomes a dirge.

---

SCENE 12: THE REALIZATION (A HARD TRUTH)

EXT. PARK BENCH – NEAR STADIUM – CONTINUOUS

**JEREMY** sits, slumped, on a bench. He fidgets with his wedding ring, twisting it slowly. His hangover collides with emotional clarity.

  
 **JEREMY** (V.O.)**    
 Marriage.  
 It wasn’t just another party.  
 It was a whole different kind of dance.  
 And I was definitely stepping on her toes.

  
 **JEREMY** (V.O.)**    
 In that Moment, the tequila wore off. The bravado wore off.  
 All that was left… was me.

(SOUND):  
 The music is gone. Replaced by the sound of birds, distant traffic, and **JEREMY’s** long, labored sigh.

---

FINAL SHOT

WIDE – THE BENCH, THE PAYPHONE BEHIND HIM

**JEREMY**, small against the backdrop of the vast stadium and the looming payphone, stares at nothing. The device behind him glows dimly in the daylight, a cold, metallic monument to poor timing and worse judgment.

TITLE CARD (optional):  
 “Dyche Stadium. Evanston, Illinois. The morning of the gig.”

**SOUND:  
** The screeching synth intro of **The Prodigy's "Firestarter"** erupts like a lit fuse. The camera whip-pans across the group as the band members split in all directions. **KATHY** veers off like a rocket aimed at chaos.

---

**1. THE MISSION (SELF-DESTRUCTION)**

**EXT. NORTHWESTERN CAMPUS – NIGHT**

**KATHY** stomps across the quad like a woman with a score to settle. She rips open a packet of ibuprofen with her teeth, downs the pills dry, then chugs the last two inches of warm malt liquor from a plastic bottle.


**KATHY (V.O.):** *I was done negotiating with pain. It wanted war? It had it.*

**  
**KATHY (V.O.):** *This wasn’t about fun. This was about revenge. On my insides. On the patriarchy. On the whole goddamn concept of “quietly suffering.”*

**VISUAL STYLE:  
** A jump cut to her feet—chunky combat boots stomping across the campus. Another to her hand, knuckles white around a flask. Her hair’s wild, her mascara’s already halfway down her face. She’s not just going to the party—she’s going to detonate it.

---

**2. THE ENTRANCE (A GRAND ARRIVAL)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – NIGHT**

**(SOUND:)** The beat drops as **KATHY** slams open the front door. Bass hits like a body blow. The living room is a neon warzone of sweaty dancers, shirtless bros, and scattered Solo cups.

**( VISUAL):  
** The camera goes handheld—shaky, fast, chaotic. A strobe light freezes her every few seconds in wild, angular poses as she stalks through the crowd like a glam-rock Terminator.

**SLOW-MOTION INSERT:  
** As **KATHY** steps inside, the music Momentarily distorts—*“I’m the bitch you hated / Filthy, faded, educated…”*—and a passing frat boy spills beer on her boot.

**FREEZE FRAME:  
**KATHY** glares down at her soaked boot.  
 **(V.O.):** *Wrong move, Chad.*

**3. THE INTRODUCTION (A BOLD STATEMENT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT**

**KATHY** pushes her way through a knot of shirtless bros attempting an ironic conga line. She climbs atop a half-broken ping pong table and grabs the mic off a nearby karaoke setup mid-chorus.

**KATHY (shouting, unhinged):  
** **“I’M THE FIRESTARTER! TWISTED FIRESTARTER!”**

The crowd freezes. The music doesn’t. Her voice slices through the room like a serrated blade, turning heads and silencing beer pong mid-serve.

**(OBSERVATION – THE FRAT BOYS):  
** **(V.O. – collectively):** *Who the hell is this chick? And why do I want her to be my major?*

**( VISUAL):  
** The mic screeches with feedback as **KATHY** rips her jacket off, throws it into the crowd, and strikes a pose like she’s about to lead a revolution—or a mosh pit.

A solo cup flies across the frame. Someone yells “YEAH!” Someone else trips over a keg. The party's no longer theirs. It's hers.

---

**4. THE DANCE FLOOR (A WILD DISPLAY)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – DANCE FLOOR – NIGHT (LATER)**

**(SOUND:)** The track slams into overdrive—“Hey! Hey! Hey!” **KATHY** hits the floor like a cyclone, her boots pounding in rhythm to the chaos.

**(RAPID-FIRE MONTAGE):**

- **KATHY** twerking on a broken recliner.
- **KATHY** spinning on the floor, beer flying in all directions.
- **KATHY** locking eyes with a stunned sophomore and flipping him off mid-dance.
- **KATHY** doing windmills in combat boots.

**CLOSE-UPS:  
** Her eyes gleaming with manic joy.  
 Her lipstick smeared.  
 Her teeth bared in a full-on primal grin.

**(TARANTINO-ESQUE DIALOGUE – V.O.):  
**KATHY:** *My pain? Gone. Replaced by something bigger. Louder. Dirtier. Unapologetic hedonism with a splash of rage and a chaser of don’t-fucking-touch-me.*

**( VISUAL):  
** Strobe lights fracture her form, turning her into a mythic, punk rock goddess in a sea of half-dressed, clueless frat kids.

**5. THE BEER PONG TABLE (A COMPETITIVE SPIRIT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – BEER PONG ROOM – NIGHT**

A group of bros are mid-game, cocky and loud, red Solo cups lined up like sacrificial offerings. **KATHY** pushes through the crowd, picks up a ping pong ball without asking, and sinks a perfect shot.

**KATHY (deadpan):  
** “That one was for Roe v. Wade.”

**( VISUAL):  
** Hyper-speed shots:

- Ping pong balls bounce in slow motion, then cut rapidly to splashes of foamy beer.  
      
      
    
- **KATHY** sniping cup after cup like she’s taking out targets on a sniper range.
- The bros’ confident smiles melting into confused awe.  
      
      
    

**(OBSERVATION – THE FRAT TABLE):  
** **(V.O. – collectively):** *She didn’t just come to party. She came to dominate.*

One frat bro wipes his forehead like he’s in a shootout. Another whispers “Bro… she’s like… really good.”

---

**6. THE CONVERSATIONS (A SERIES OF INAPPROPRIATE COMMENTS)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – VARIOUS LOCATIONS – NIGHT (LATER)**

**(MONTAGE):**

- **KATHY** corners a finance major and leans in with drunken intensity:  
     **KATHY:** “I’m a firestarter, man. I burn things down.”  
     **FRAT BOY:** “Uh… cool?” (backs away slowly)
- She confesses to an ROTC pledge:  
     **KATHY:** “I once faked a psych eval just to avoid a math final. Wanna make out?”  
     **FRAT BOY:** “I—I have a girlfriend…”  
      
      
    
- She tries to seduce a philosophy major by quoting Nietzsche. Backwards.  
      
      
    


**KATHY (V.O.):** *I was on a mission. A mission to forget. A mission to obliterate every thought I’d had that day. And maybe a few brain cells while I was at it.*

**( VISUAL):  
** Jump cuts between **KATHY**’s increasingly outrageous one-liners, frat boy reactions, and her own triumphant, defiant grin. The energy’s chaotic, combustible—and she’s loving it.

---

**7. THE SHOT GLASSES (A RAPID DESCENT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – KITCHEN/DRINKING STATION – NIGHT**

The crowd chants: “**KATHY**! **KATHY**! **KATHY**!”

**KATHY** slams down shot after shot like she’s in a competitive eating contest. Her hand is steady at first, then progressively more erratic.

**(VISUAL):**

- **Close-ups**: shot glasses being slammed onto sticky countertops, the liquid inside rippling like mini-explosions.  
      
      
    
- The visuals start to **blur and tilt**—colors oversaturate, lights flare.  
      
      
    
- Quick **jump cuts** show her wobbling slightly, laughing too loud, eyes gleaming with adrenaline and recklessness.  
      
      
    


**KATHY (V.O.):** *This was the* Moment *the pain took a back seat. And the tequila took the wheel.*

---

**8. THE KARAOKE MACHINE (A VOCAL ASSAULT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT (LATER)**

**KATHY** snatches a mic from a stunned frat guy mid-ballad. She scrolls, selects, and *bam*—“Firestarter” begins blasting.

**(VISUAL):**

- **KATHY** stands center stage (coffee table), backlit like a punk-rock deity.
- The lights strobe. The crowd cringes as she *screams* into the mic, off-key but utterly commanding.  
      
      
    
- A bro drops his red cup in slow motion.  
      
      
    

**  
**KATHY (V.O.):** *Pitch? Irrelevant. Presence? Off the charts.*

**KATHY (screaming):  
** “I’M THE BITCH YOU HATED—FILTH INFATUATED!”

**(OBSERVATION – THE CROWD):  
** **(V.O. – collectively):** *We didn’t know whether to cheer… or call campus security.*

**9. THE NEAR-NAKED RUN (A** MOMENT **OF MADNESS)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – VARIOUS ROOMS – NIGHT**

A blinding flash of red and white streaks down the hallway. **KATHY** sprints, nearly nude, draped only in a **stolen Delta Gamma flag** like a toga.

**(SOUND: The bass from “Firestarter” drops into a distorted, echo-heavy loop.)**

**(VISUAL):**

- Shaky cam tracking shot of **KATHY** blazing past startled frat bros.  
      
      
    
- Overexposed flashes of strobes hit her like paparazzi bulbs.  
      
      
    
- One guy drops a bong mid-rip. Another gasps, “IS SHE—?”  
      
      
    

**(OBSERVATION – THE FRAT BOYS):  
** **(V.O. – collectively):** *We were stunned. We were confused. We were also kind of impressed.*

---

**10. THE CRASH LANDING (A COMICAL FALL)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY**, triumphant and topless under the flag, rounds a corner—and goes airborne over a slick patch of spilled beer and crushed Solo cups.

**(VISUAL):**

- **Slow-motion fall**: **KATHY**’s arms windmill as the room stretches in warped fisheye.  
      
      
    
- **Comical sound effect**: a deep “WHOOMP” as she collapses into a beanbag, legs flailing like a ragdoll.  
      
      
    
- The flag flutters downward, _comically draping back over her like a curtain call.  
      
      
    _

**KATHY (V.O., deadpan):  
** *I stuck the landing. Mostly.*

---

**11. THE MORNING AFTER (A HANGOVER AND A MYSTERY)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – MORNING**

The camera opens on **KATHY’s face**, half-buried in a couch cushion. Her **mascara is smeared**, her hair looks like it lost a fight with a leaf blower, and a half-eaten corn dog rests beside her cheek.

**(SOUND: The faint clink of beer cans shifting as someone snores nearby.)**

**  
**KATHY (V.O.):** _What the hell happened last night?  
_ She blinks at her surroundings: a frat boy is curled up like a cat on the armrest. Another is passed out in the open fridge, holding a bottle of ranch dressing like a teddy bear.


**KATHY (V.O.):** *Everything hurt. My head. My pride. My liver was typing up its resignation letter.*

---

**12. THE ESCAPE (A HASTY RETREAT)**

**EXT. FRAT HOUSE – FRONT LAWN – MORNING**

**KATHY** tiptoes across the grass, **still wrapped in the fraternity flag**, now stained and trailing like a battle-worn cape. She glances around nervously as joggers and students eye her with confusion and thinly veiled judgment.

**(VISUAL):**

- **Long tracking shot** from behind: the flag drags behind her across the dewy lawn.
- Students part like Moses and the Red Sea. One frat bro waves from a window. She flips him off without turning around.  
      
      
    

**(SOUND: “Firestarter” fades into silence. Now it’s just birds chirping. A lawn sprinkler sputters to life. KATHY groans.)**

**(FINAL SHOT):  
** A **wide shot**: **KATHY** limps down the block, the frat house looming behind her like a war-torn fortress. The flag catches the breeze one last time—her own tattered banner of the night before.

**1. THE PHONE BOOTH (A SHRINE TO LONELINESS)**

**EXT. STREET CORNER NEAR STADIUM – NIGHT**

**BILL** stands outside a battered, graffiti-tagged **payphone booth**, bathed in the flickering glow of a red neon sign that reads **“OPEN 24 HOURS.”** A strip of duct tape barely holds the booth’s door in place. The wind howls like it knows something he doesn’t.

He **pulls out a fat roll of quarters** like a blackjack dealer, grinning with misplaced confidence.

**(SOUND: Stevie Ray Vaughan’s “Voodoo Chile” kicks in with that raw, bending guitar riff. Feedback howls like a banshee.)**

**(OBSERVATION – BILL):  
**BILL (V.O.):** *Well, I stand up next to a mountain… and I chop it down with the edge of my hand…*

**  
**BILL (V.O.):** *My mountain of loneliness. My hand… my phone. Let’s dial some demons, shall we?*

---

**2. THE FIRST CALL (A BAD IDEA)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

**BILL** dials with swagger. His eyes narrow. His grin sharpens. He leans against the glass like a man calling a bookie, a priest, and an ex-girlfriend all at once.

**SPLIT SCREEN MONTAGE** — rapid-fire flashes of:

- An answering machine clicks: “*Hi! You’ve reached Becky and I’m not—*” _Click.  
      
      
    _
- A woman in a nightgown answers: “*It’s 1:45 in the goddamn morning.*”  
      
      
    
- A guy picks up: “*She moved out, man. Months ago.*”  
      
      
    

**(VISUAL):**

- **BILL**’s face distorts through the greasy glass.  
      
      
    
- The camera whips and spins as he dials again and again, each call more desperate than the last.  
      
      
    
- The neon sign outside buzzes ominously like it’s judging him.  
      
      
    

**(OBSERVATION – BILL):  
**BILL (V.O.):** *First call was a disaster. But you don’t climb a mountain without slipping on a few ex-girlfriends.*

**  
**BILL (V.O.):** *I had a list. A glorious, stupid list. Half of them wouldn’t remember me. The other half would wish they didn’t.*

---

**3. THE HANG UP (A BRUTAL REJECTION)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

**BILL**, lips parted mid-sentence, suddenly hears the *click* of disconnection.

**(VISUAL):**

- **EXTREME CLOSE-UP** of the **receiver slamming** down on the other end.
- Hard jump-cut to **BILL’s stunned expression**, mouth slightly open, the receiver still to his ear.  
      
      
    
- The **buzz of the dead line** fills the booth like a vacuum.  
      
      
    
- Outside, the neon **"24 HOURS"** flickers **off** for a Moment—**ominous symbolism.  
      
      
    **

**  
**BILL (V.O.):** *She hung up so fast, I could still hear the echo of my own dignity hitting the floor.*

---

**4. THE SECOND CALL (A HIGH SCHOOL SWEETHEART)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT (LATER)**

**BILL** exhales hard. He dials again, slower this time. Hope's still in there, somewhere between bravado and bad choices.

**RING.  
**RING.  
**CLICK.**

A warm, familiar female voice answers—**older**, **tired**, but unmistakably her.

**VOICE 2 (V.O.):** *Hello?*

**BILL (Trying to sound suave, still echoing the lyrics):  
** *And I chop it down… with the edge of my hand…*

**Pause. Then—**

**VOICE 2 (V.O.):** ***BILL****? Is that you? It’s been… years. I’m married now. With two kids.*

**(OBSERVATION – BILL):  
**BILL (V.O.):** *Damn. Forgot about the whole “married with kids” thing. Also forgot about her husband being a cop.*

**(VISUAL):**

- A brief **flashback montage**: prom night, a flask in a tuxedo pocket, a poorly executed slow dance.  
      
      
    
- Cut back to **BILL**, one eye twitching slightly, gripping the phone like it’s a sinking ship.

**5. THE THIRD CALL (A WRONG NUMBER)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT (LATER STILL)**

**BILL** wipes his forehead with his sleeve, growing more desperate. Another number, another shot in the dark.

**RING. RING.**

**GRUFF MALE VOICE (V.O.):** *Yeah?*

**BILL (Riffing like a drunken bard):  
** *Well, I pick up all the pieces… and make an island…*

**GRUFF MALE VOICE (V.O.):** *Wrong number, you idiot!*

**  
**BILL (V.O.):** *My island of loneliness was starting to look more like a deserted rock. No coconuts. No volleyball. Just shame.*

**(VISUAL):**

- **Close-up** of **BILL**’s face under harsh fluorescent light, eyebrows twitching.
- Smash cut to a black screen with the words: **“DO YOU EVEN KNOW WHO YOU’RE CALLING?”** in flashing red.  
      
      
    

---

**6. THE FOURTH CALL (A DISCONNECTED LINE)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH –** MOMENT**S LATER**

Now trembling slightly, **BILL** dials again, his hands a blur. A robotic voice breaks the silence.

**RECORDED MESSAGE (V.O.):  
** *We’re sorry. The number you have dialed has been disconnected.*

**(VISUAL):**

- The **camera pushes in fast** on **BILL**’s blank face.  
      
      
    
- **Close-up** on the **coin return**: a lone quarter clangs back out with _metallic disdain.  
      
      
    _

**(OBSERVATION – BILL):  
**BILL (V.O.):** *She changed her number. Changed her life. Left my ass back in '88 with a mixtape and a boner.*

**7. THE FIFTH CALL (A CONFUSED GRANDMOTHER)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT (STILL LATER)**

**BILL** slouches deeper into the grimy booth, his voice now a slurry blend of lyrics and longing. He dials without checking the number.

**RING. RING.**

**GRANDMOTHER (V.O.):  
** *Hello? Who is this? Is this my grandson, **BILL**y?*

**BILL (Still mumbling, channeling Stevie Ray):  
** *Might even raise a little sand…*

**(OBSERVATION – BILL):  
**BILL (V.O.):** *Close enough.*

**(VISUAL):**

- **Tight shot** on the receiver, slowly rotating in **BILL**’s hand as he stares blankly into the neon-lit void.
- **Insert shot** of a confused elderly woman in a doily-covered living room, peering suspiciously at a rotary phone.

---

**8. THE SIXTH CALL (A POLICE OFFICER)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH –** MOMENT**S LATER**

**BILL**, now hunched and glassy-eyed, dials another number with the reckless confidence of a man whose self-respect has fully evaporated.

**CLICK. RING.**

**POLICE OFFICER (V.O.):  
** *Evanston Police Department, what is your emergency?*

**BILL (Voice barely audible):  
** *'Cause I'm a voodoo chile…*

**  
**BILL (V.O.):  
** *My emergency? My complete and utter failure to connect with another human being.*

**(VISUAL):**

- The booth’s fluorescent bulb buzzes ominously as **BILL** stares up at it, as if it holds the answers.  
      
      
    
- **Quick flashback montage** of all six failed calls, edited like a boxing knock-out reel.

**9. THE HANG UP (A HASTY RETREAT)**

**EXT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

The Moment “Evanston Police Department” registers in his whiskey-soaked brain, **BILL**’s eyes widen like a cartoon character.

**SOUND: A SLAM.  
** He smashes the receiver down and bolts from the booth with the grace of a drunken linebacker.

**(VISUAL):**

- **Fast-motion wide shot** of **BILL** sprinting under the harsh glow of sodium-vapor streetlights, the booth’s neon buzzing like a bug zapper.
- **Dutch angle close-up** of his sneakers flopping against the pavement, one untied.
- **Jump cut** to the booth behind him, flickering like a haunted relic.

---

**10. THE EMPTY POCKETS (A FINANCIAL DISASTER)**

**EXT. SIDEWALK –** MOMENT**S LATER**

**BILL** skids to a stop, panting. He reaches into his pockets—left, right, inside-out. Nothing. Not even a lint-covered mint.

**(OBSERVATION – BILL):  
**BILL (V.O.):  
** *Spent all my quarters, spent all my dignity. Guess we’re even now.*

**  
**BILL (V.O.):  
** *Note to self: never chase love through payphones. They only return change, not feelings.*

**(VISUAL):**

- **Extreme close-up** of two empty, turned-out pockets flapping like sad little flags of surrender.
- A coin rolls away in slow motion down a crack in the sidewalk—his last quarter abandoning him like everyone else.  
      
      
    

**(OBSERVATION – BILL):**

**BILL (V.O.)** My island was now completely devoid of resources.

---

**11. THE DEJECTED WALK (A WALK OF SHAME)**

EXT. EVANSTON STREETS – EARLY MORNING

**BILL** shuffles back toward the stadium. His boots scuff the pavement, the glow of neon signs giving way to the soft, gray light of dawn.

( VISUAL):

- Slow-motion tracking shot as **BILL** trudges past empty storefronts, his silhouette drooping under invisible weight.  
      
      
    
- Insert shot: A passing jogger eyes him with judgmental disdain.  
      
      
    
- Close-up: His hair is matted, his shirt untucked, one sleeve wet from something he doesn’t remember encountering.  
      
      
    

(SOUND):  
 The blistering blues of “Voodoo Chile” slow to a drawn-out, dirge-like riff, distorted and warped like a warped cassette tape on its last breath.

---

12. THE REALIZATION (A HARD TRUTH)

EXT. PARK BENCH NEAR DYCHE STADIUM – MOMENTS LATER

**BILL** drops onto the bench with a heavy grunt. The stadium looms in the distance like a stone monolith, indifferent and unimpressed.

  
 **BILL** (V.O.):  
 *Maybe “Voodoo Chile” wasn’t the best theme song for a series of awkward phone calls. Should’ve gone with something quieter. Like… “The Sound of Silence.”*

(OBSERVATION – **BILL**):  
 **BILL** (V.O.):  
 *I came to conquer hearts. All I conquered was a payphone and my pride.*

(SOUND):  
 The music fades into silence, leaving only the rustling of trees, a few birds chirping, and **BILL**’s tired sigh.

(FINAL SHOT):  
 A wide shot reveals **BILL**, small and slumped on the bench, dwarfed by the empty street and distant stadium—a man out of luck, out of quarters, and out of delusions. The camera slowly zooms out until **BILL** is just another anonymous figure in the morning haze.

**1. THE SEARCH (A DESPERATE QUEST)**

EXT. EVANSTON STREETS – NIGHT

**JIM** barrels down a sidewalk, eyes wide, grinning like a man on a mission from Satan. He grabs a group of undergrads exiting a Chipotle.

**JIM** (Frantic, panting)  
 Have you seen the Sandman? He owes me a shot of Jaeger!

( VISUAL):

- The camera spins around **JIM** in a dizzying 360-degree blur as the intro riff of “Enter Sandman” begins.  
      
      
    
- Random flashes of student faces: confused, frightened, entertained.  
      
      
    
- A poster for a local rave whips past in the wind. **JIM** chases it for half a block.  
      
      
    

(OBSERVATION – **JIM**):  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *Hush little baby, don’t say a word… Mama’s gonna buy you a mockingbird… and Daddy’s gonna spike it with Everclear.*

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *I wasn’t just looking for a party. I was hunting it. Like it was Bigfoot. And I was armed with nothing but a liver and a bad idea.*

---

2. THE FALSE LEADS (A SERIES OF DEAD ENDS)

MONTAGE – VARIOUS LOCATIONS

- EXT. LIBRARY – NIGHT  
     **JIM** pounds on the glass doors. A lone librarian stares from inside, unimpressed.  
     **JIM**  
     Where’s the bass drop, Dewey!?  
      
      
    
- INT. COFFEE SHOP – NIGHT  
     **JIM** bursts in. People reading. Jazz music playing. He sniffs the air.  
     **JIM** (Disgusted)  
     Smells like decaf and disappointment.  
      
      
    
- EXT. DESERTED PARK – NIGHT  
     **JIM** stumbles into a playground, sees a raccoon near the swings.  
     **JIM**  
     Even you left the party!?  
      
      
    

( VISUAL):

- Harsh cuts between **JIM**’s wild-eyed frustration and the echoing emptiness of each space.  
      
      
    
- The lights seem colder, harsher. The music drops to a distorted, slowed riff as **JIM** spins in circles, increasingly unhinged.  
      
      
    

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *Every door was a disappointment. Every closed sign, a personal insult. But I wasn’t stopping. Not until I found that sandman—and punched him in the face with a beer bong.*

**3. THE FRAT HOUSE (A GLIMMER OF HOPE)**

**EXT. FRAT HOUSE – NIGHT**

**JIM** stops dead in his tracks. A thumping beat pulses through the air. Colored lights spill from the windows like a beacon from Valhalla. He squints through the open door and sees **KATHY** mid-dance, spinning in a cyclone of sweat and rebellion.

(OBSERVATION – **JIM**):  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *And if that mockingbird don’t sing… Mama’s gonna buy you a diamond ring…*

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *And that ring? It was forged in the fires of keg-fueled debauchery. A diamond ring of pure, unadulterated party.*

( VISUAL):

- High-speed dolly zoom as **JIM** zeroes in on the front door.  
      
      
    
- Quick flashes of students stumbling, drinks flying, and **KATHY** locking eyes with him, giving a subtle nod—_"bring the chaos."  
      
      
    _

---

**4. THE CRASHING (A GRAND ENTRANCE)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – CONTINUOUS**

**JIM** SLAMS through the door, arms spread wide like a prophet of noise. The crowd parts Momentarily, stunned. He bellows at the top of his lungs:

**JIM** (Over the pounding music)  
 Enter Sandman!

( VISUAL):

- Slow-motion: Beer mist sprays across the air as **JIM** leaps onto a couch.  
      
      
    
- His manic grin dominates the frame as the bassline of “Enter Sandman” drops heavy and hard.  
      
      
    
- Students cheer, some laugh, some cower. One guy immediately hands him a beer. Another offers a funnel.  
      
      
    

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *I didn’t knock. I didn’t ask. I didn’t care. The sandman had arrived—and he brought hell with him.*

**5. THE DANCING (A WILD DISPLAY)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT**

**JIM**’s on the makeshift dance floor, surrounded by flashing lights and reverb-soaked music. His dance style is a blend of flailing limbs, mosh pit aggression, and the gracelessness of a marionette with broken strings.

( VISUAL):

- Jump cuts: Spilled beer splashes across the camera lens.  
      
      
    
- Close-up: **JIM** knocks over a stereo speaker mid-spin.  
      
      
    
- Distorted angle: A girl screams as her drink is knocked out of her hand.  
      
      
    

(OBSERVATION – THE FRAT BOYS):  
 (V.O. – collectively):  
 *Who invited this guy?*

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *My moves? Unholy. My rhythm? Nonexistent. My impact? Devastating.*

---

6. THE BEER PONG (A COMPETITIVE SPIRIT)

INT. FRAT HOUSE – KITCHEN – MOMENTS LATER

**JIM** slams his palms on the beer pong table, swaying slightly, eyes bloodshot but gleaming.

**JIM** (Challenging)  
 Next. I got this. I’m a goddamn sandman.

He grabs a ping pong ball and hurls it… directly into a potted plant.

( VISUAL):

- Close-up: The ball bounces off a guy’s forehead.  
      
      
    
- Slow-motion: Red Solo cups fly as the table gets bumped.  
      
      
    
- Wide shot: The frat boys groan in unison.  
      
      
    

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *Exit light… enter night… take my hand… we’re off to never-never land… and maybe a few minor concussions.*

**7. THE CONVERSATIONS (A SERIES OF BIZARRE ENCOUNTERS)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – VARIOUS LOCATIONS – NIGHT**

**JIM** floats from room to room like a party ghost, latching onto anyone within range. His conversations make no sense and are delivered with apocalyptic sincerity.

**JIM** (Grabbing a frat guy by the shoulders)  
 Have you seen the Sandman? He’s got the good stuff. The *real* stuff.

FRAT BOY  
 (Recoiling)  
 Dude, are you okay? Like… medically?

( VISUAL):

- Tight close-ups of horrified and confused partygoers.  
      
      
    
- Sudden fisheye lens of **JIM**’s manic, sweaty face filling the frame.  
      
      
    
- A cutaway to a beer tap hissing like a pressure valve about to blow.  
      
      
    

(OBSERVATION – **JIM**):  
 **JIM** (V.O.):  
 *Never-never land… it was starting to look a lot like this party. Except louder. And somehow stickier.*

---

8. THE MISTAKEN IDENTITY (A COMICAL CASE OF WRONG PERSON)

INT. FRAT HOUSE – STAIRCASE LANDING – LATER

**JIM** spots a girl with dark hair and combat boots from behind. In his booze-addled brain, that’s enough. It’s **KATHY**.

He swaggers up, slurring the opening lines of “Enter Sandman” like it’s a love ballad.

**JIM** (Singing off-key, heartfelt)  
 Hush little baby, don’t you cry…

The girl turns around.

GIRL  
 (Backpedaling)  
 I… I don’t know you.

( VISUAL):

- Freeze frame on her expression: confusion curdling into alarm.  
      
      
    
- Insert shot of **JIM** offering a fistful of beer-soaked confetti.  
      
      
    
- A dolly zoom as **JIM** blinks in slow realization.  
      
      
    

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):

**9. THE STAGE DIVE (A DISASTROUS ATTEMPT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT**

**JIM** spots a wobbly table being used as a DJ booth and clambers up like it’s Madison Square Garden.

**JIM** (Arms outstretched, triumphant)  
 ENTER NIGHT!!

He leaps.

No one even looks up.

He crashes flat onto the beer-soaked tile floor with a *THWUMP*.

  
 **JIM** (V.O.):

**12. THE ARRIVAL (A DISAPPOINTING SIGHT)**

The elevator dings. The glass doors slide open. One by one, the band members shamble in—**KATHY** still half-wrapped in a fraternity flag, **JEREMY** looking haunted, **JEFF** caked in grass stains, **BILL** missing a shoe, **JIM** still humming Metallica under his breath, and Rico dragging a tangled bundle of Christmas lights.

**CREMEANS** closes his novel with a gentle *thwap*, stands, straightens his collar, and surveys the wreckage before him.

**  
**CREMEANS (V.O.):

He sighs—just once—then takes a slow sip of his cold coffee, already pivoting mentally to damage control.

**(SOUND):

**TITLE CARD:  
**Evanston, Illinois. Late Morning. Dyche Stadium Calls.**

**INT. HOTEL LOBBY – DAY**

The hotel lobby gleams with faux opulence—polished marble, fake plants, and the antiseptic scent of too much lemon cleaner. Morning sunlight pours through tall windows, cutting like a judgmental spotlight.

**CREMEANS** stands dead center, pristine, sipping a fresh Mountain Dew like it’s a sacrament.

(SOUND: A Muzak version of “Tainted Love” plays, offensively cheerful.)  
 The band straggles in, a rogue’s gallery of hangovers, bad decisions, and questionable hygiene.

( VISUAL):

**CREMEANS** smiles. It’s tight. It’s weaponized.

**CREMEANS** (with the calm of a man seconds from a meltdown)  
 Good morning, team. I trust your… evening endeavors were productive?

  
 **CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
 “Productive.” That’s one way to describe spiritual collapse.

He surveys the carnage—each band member a personal affront to order and decency.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)** Would someone care to explain exactly what went down during the nine hours you were *supposed* to be resting?

**  
 CREMEANS (V.O.)** It was like herding cats. If the cats were blackout drunk. And on fire.

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

**CREMEANS** moves with practiced resolve. Over to the bathroom.

The band has moved on. The wreckage remains. But so does **CREMEANS**—armed with a Mountain Dew, a dog-eared Bible, and just enough hope to get them to showtime.

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – DAY**

The backstage is chaos incarnate: clanging cases, snapping cables, roadies barking in staccato rhythms. **CREMEANS** navigates it like a man possessed—one part manager, one part battlefield medic.

(SOUND):  
 The dull roar of the crowd bleeds in from the stadium. Water bottles crack open like gunshots. Gaffers tape sticks to skin and steel. It's organized madness.

( VISUAL):  
 The camera trails **CREMEANS** in a series of whip pans and crash zooms—he materializes from frame to frame like a caffeinated phantom, slinging hydration and authority.

(OBSERVATION – THE BAND):

 Where the hell is he getting all this water?

**CREMEANS** spins to face the band like a drill instructor who’s read too much Sun Tzu.

**CREMEANS** (His voice brisk, clipped)  
 Alright, we’re live in one hour. Ten minutes to set up. Forty minutes to burn it down. Ten to disappear. Like ghosts. Efficiency is survival.

  
 **CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
 In rock and roll, as in war, timing is everything. Miss a cue, miss a shot.

He holds up his clipboard like it’s sacred scripture.

**CREMEANS** (CONT'D)  
 Setlist: “Not Taken Kindly.” “The Left Hand.” “Payment in Kind.” The holy trinity of smut and sentiment. These tracks will be the spine of *69 Reasons*.

( VISUAL):  
 Close-up on the clipboard: bold Sharpie titles, coffee stains, a tiny sketch of a demon with a tambourine.

**CREMEANS** (CONT'D)

**KATHY** cocks her head, eyebrow raised.

**KATHY** (Sardonically)  
 So, we open with a song about blow job critiques, move into something about voyeurism, and close on transactional sex. Is there a thesis statement I missed?

(OBSERVATION – **KATHY**):  
 **KATHY** (V.O.)**    
 Our lyrics were… emotionally raw. In a "Dear Penthouse" kind of way.

  
 **KATHY** (V.O.)**    
 This band was like if Tennessee Williams wrote for Joan Jett.

**CREMEANS** exhales like a man who's already lost the argument.

**CREMEANS** I don’t write the songs, **KATHY**. I just keep the wheels from falling off.

Then, quieter. Sincere.

**CREMEANS** (CONT'D)  
 But today—today, you need to sell it. Like it’s truth. Because someone’s watching who can change everything.

His eyes flick to the shadowed corner.

( VISUAL):  
 Nick Stewart. Island Records. Immaculate suit. Arms crossed. Face unreadable. A sphinx with a clipboard.

(FINAL SHOT):  
 The band stares at **CREMEANS**. Nervous. Hungover. Wired. The adrenaline is rising. This is the last deep breath before the plunge.

One hour to go.

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The energy backstage hums like a live wire. The band huddles amid a storm of coiled cables, cracked snare heads, and scuffed amp cases. Outside, the crowd’s roar swells, shaking the air like a brewing thunderstorm.

(SOUND):  
 The persistent murmur of a waiting crowd. Clinks of metal. Gaffer tape tearing. A faint feedback squeal. **CREMEANS**’ voice cuts through it all like a conductor keeping a deranged orchestra in tune.

( VISUAL):  
 Sweeping shots of tension: a trembling cymbal, a bead of sweat trickling down **BILL**’s neck, **CREMEANS**' clipboard held like a holy relic.

**BILL** raises a hand, uncertain.

**BILL** (Anxiously)  
 So… how are we closing the show?

(OBSERVATION – **BILL**):  
 **BILL** (V.O.)**    
 The closer. The last note. The thing they’d talk about on the ride home. Or never forget at all.

  
 **CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
 The closer wasn’t just a song. It was the shot that rang out after the credits rolled.

**CREMEANS** steps forward, resolute.

**CREMEANS** (Deadpan, deliberate)  
 The same way you always do. “Come Inside Me.”

**JEREMY** flinches at the memory of the sprawling final act.

**JEREMY** (Wincing)  
 But… it’s long. Like… *long* long.

( VISUAL):  
 A stopwatch click. The red digits blink. Smash cut to the crowd—a surging sea of anticipation, chanting, vibrating.

**CREMEANS** is unshaken.

**CREMEANS** (Crisp, precise)  
 Which is why you modulate it. Build it, break it, rebuild it. Stretch or squeeze it depending on the clock. Today? You ride that sucker to the buzzer.

He gestures toward a small light rig near the wings.

**CREMEANS** (CONT'D)  
 Yellow lamp: two minutes left. Red: you’re out. That’s your signal to end *loud*.

He scans their faces. Locking eyes. No wiggle room.

**CREMEANS** (CONT'D)  
 Does that work for everyone?

(OBSERVATION – THE BAND):  
 (V.O. – everyone except **BILL**)  
 Yeah.

**BILL** shifts uncomfortably, still chewing the idea.

**BILL** (Softly)  
 I just… I don’t know if—

**CREMEANS** (Cutting him off, voice like steel)  
 No room for subtlety, **BILL**. Not today.

  
 **CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
 Subtlety is for monks and memoirists. This? This had to hit like a truck.

He claps his hands once—sharp, final.

**CREMEANS** (CONT'D)  
 Let’s load in.

(FINAL SHOT):  
 The band disperses, heads nodding, hearts pounding. **CREMEANS** turns back toward the shadow where Nick Stewart still watches, arms folded.

The game is about to begin.

---

**CREMEANS (CONT'D)  
** Alright, let’s go make some noise!

*The band moves toward the stage entrance. The crowd’s roar swells—no longer sound but pressure, like a storm surge behind a levee.*

Just before stepping into the light, **GILLEY** leans in toward **KATHY**, mischief weaponized in his grin.

**GILLEY** _(low, sly)  
_ Hey… about that toga…  
 Any chance I could… borrow your panties?

**( VISUAL):  
**Close-up** — **KATHY**’s face. Equal parts amusement and exasperation.  
 She’s heard worse. She’s *said* worse.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
** The band, **CREMEANS** at the front, assembles just offstage.  
 The crowd’s roar hits them like a freight train.  
 Lights dim.  
 A single chord from the previous act lingers in the air like ozone.  
 It's nearly 2 PM. Showtime.  
 *Chicago, Illinois.*

---

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

Backstage churns with motion—runners hustling, roadies shouting, techs mumbling into headsets.  
 The crowd’s muffled roar is constant, like surf crashing miles away.

**CREMEANS** is locked in, clipboard clutched, voice sharp.

**(SOUNDS):  
** The ambient thunder of the crowd.  
 Metal clanging.  
 Water bottles snapping open and draining fast.

**( VISUAL):  
** The camera tracks **CREMEANS** pacing like a general mid-campaign.  
 No sleep. No coffee. Pure adrenaline.

**CREMEANS** _(clipped, focused)  
_ Okay—moving on. Number four:  
 *“Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar.”*

---



**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** It’s a crowd-pleaser. High tempo. Dirty charm.  
 Perfect opener after the warm-up act deflates.

---



**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** And let’s be honest—after last night, you degenerates probably feel *right at home* in a dive bar.

***KATHY*** *raises an eyebrow, that wry, seen-it-all smile locked and loaded.*

**KATHY** _(bone-dry)  
_ Actually, **CREMEANS**…  
 “Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar” is about a bachelorette party in New Orleans.  
 Where the ladies… let’s just say… leaned *hard* into poor decision-making.

**( FLASH CUTS):  
** — Beads flying through thick humid air.  
 — Neon sign: _“BOURBON STREET.”  
_ — Screaming topless woman on a balcony, flinging plastic necklaces like confetti.

**CREMEANS** _(deadpan, quoting)  
_ “Passion’s got a hold of me.”  
 Right.  
 Moving on.

---

***CREMEANS*** *points to the next item on the list.*

**CREMEANS (CONT'D)  
** Number five: *“It Has a Wow Finish.”*

***JEFF****, looking marginally less like death, chimes in—thoughtful, even.*

**JEFF** _(quietly reflective)  
_ That one’s about my girlfriend’s interpretation of Rick and Ilsa from *Casablanca*.

---

**(OBSERVATION – THE BAND):**

**V.O. (Collective thought)  
***JEFF*** *has a girlfriend?*

---



**KATHY (V.O.)**    
** And she’s pulling her *deep emotional insights* from *Casablanca*?  
 Seriously?

*The band exchanges looks—part disbelief, part concern.*

**GILLEY** _(flat-out incredulous)  
_ Since when do *you* have a girlfriend?

**BILL** _(half-joking, half-confused)  
_ And *Casablanca*? That’s a weird-ass place to get romantic inspiration.

***JEFF*** *shrugs. Unbothered. Zen-like.*

**JEFF** _(evenly)  
_ She has… interesting… perspectives.

---

***CREMEANS*** *doesn’t have time for this narrative arc. He skips straight to the finale.*

**CREMEANS** _(snapping back to focus)  
_ Alright—last but not least: *“Snap and Sizzle.”*

*He raises a hand before anyone can open their mouth.*

**CREMEANS (CONT'D)  
** I think I can figure that one out just by reading the title.

---

**( VISUAL):  
**Close-up** — Setlist taped to an amp.  
 Bold black marker: *“SNAP AND SIZZLE.”*

---



**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** Didn’t need the backstory.  
 Some titles just *tell* you everything.  
 Some truths are best left… unexplored.

---

*He looks up from the clipboard. Direct. Commanding.*

**CREMEANS (CONT'D)  
** Look—I don’t care what these songs mean.  
 I care that you *nail* them.  
 And stay hydrated.

*He gestures at the dwindling stash of water bottles like a battlefield medic.*

---



**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** Hydration.  
 It was the secret weapon.  
 The difference between vomiting in the wings…  
 and bringing the house down.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
** The band surrounds the water like pilgrims at a sacred well.  
 They drink.  
 Not out of obligation—but out of belief.

*Backstage at Dyche Stadium.  
 Chicago, Illinois.  
 Just shy of 2 PM.*

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The backstage zone *hums* with raw, uncontrollable energy.

 His clipboard hangs useless at his side.  
 His face is frozen in stunned disbelief.

---

**(SOUND):  
** A wall of noise—  
 Crowd roaring.  
 Basslines pounding.

**( VISUAL):

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** I… I didn’t understand it.

---



**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** It was like… magic.  
 Uncut. Unfiltered.  
 First track: _“Not Taken Kindly.”

---

He rewinds the Moment in his head—**KATHY** commanding the stage like a hurricane in combat boots.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**

The concrete *shudders* beneath the stampede.

**V.O. (Collective Thought)

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** This wasn’t a show.

**Nick Stewart**, the A&R scout, stands beside **CREMEANS**, arms folded, posture rigid.

**CREMEANS** _(bright, booming)  
_ Want some water? Gotta stay hydrated!

**( VISUAL):

**NICK STEWART** _(calm, cool)  
_ No, thank you.

But **CREMEANS** isn't letting go.

**CREMEANS** _(intense, near-maniacal)

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
** Hydration wasn’t just health advice.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)** _(dry, to himself)

**CREMEANS**, now fully riding the wave of crowd energy, is lit up like Times Square.

**( VISUAL):

_Backstage at Dyche Stadium.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**

**( VISUAL – FLASHBACK):

They recreated the **gated reverb** sound.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
