for the last third of that song…  
we had a fantastic view of ***KATHY****’s assets*.

---

( VISUAL):  
Quick cuts:  
— **KATHY** mid-performance, spinning.  
— The producer winking, smug.

---

**CREMEANS** stares, mouth slightly open.

**CREMEANS** _(incredulous)  
_Are you… serious?

---

The producer breaks into laughter.

PRODUCER _(laughing)  
_Relax. I’m kidding!

*Beat.*

PRODUCER (CONT'D) _(now sincere)  
_Well… mostly kidding.  
She did accidentally moon the camera a few times at the end there.

---



**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
Oh, for the love of…

---

Nick Stewart turns toward **CREMEANS**, amused and now *fully dialed in*.

NICK STEWART _(genuinely curious)  
_So…  
the fraternity flag?  
That part of the act?

---

**CREMEANS** sighs, rubs his temples.

**CREMEANS** _(resigned)  
_It’s a long story.  
Involves an IUD, some ibuprofen,  
and a very bad decision at a fraternity party.

---

(FINAL SHOT):  
Camera locks on **CREMEANS**.  
His face: *exhaustion, disbelief, and dawning horror*.  
The crowd still roars behind him—  
but now it's blended with the *reality crash* of what just happened.

---

*Still backstage. Dyche Stadium.  
Chicago, Illinois.  
The* Moment *after the miracle.*

---

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The roar is fading.   The house lights start rising, casting a pale wash over the sea of confetti.   Stagehands are already unbolting, unplugging, hauling. **CREMEANS** stands still amid the motion—shell-shocked, exhilarated, *processing*.

---

(SOUND):   Echoes of the crowd dissolving.    Meal-on-metal clanging.   Scattered applause.   Low murmurs.   And… the footsteps of the band approaching from stage left.

---

( VISUAL):   Camera on **CREMEANS**’ face—drenched in sweat, blinking against the light.   Exhaustion. Disbelief.   And underneath it… *hope*.  Real hope.

Nick Stewart stands nearby—no clipboard, no sunglasses, no swagger.  Just a man who’s *seen something*.

NICK STEWART (V.O.)    
This business is full of phonies.  Guys with big words and no follow-through.  But this guy… **CREMEANS**… He was cut from something else.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**    
He’s Toledo steel.  Sharp. Honest.  Cuts through bullshit like it’s butter.

He turns to **CREMEANS**—expression open, engaged.

NICK STEWART _(decisive)  
I think I can do business with a man like you.

( VISUAL):  
Close-up on Nick’s face—*no smile, no pretense*. Just clarity.

**CREMEANS** blinks. Still processing. Still sweaty.

**CREMEANS** _(half-laugh, half-dazed)  
Business?

NICK STEWART (firm, certain)  
I want to meet the band.   When they come off.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
This was it.  This was *the* Moment.  Or… at least one of them.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
Still had to deal with the whole… mooning incident.

**CREMEANS** glances toward the stage entrance—gears kicking in again.

**CREMEANS** _(practical)  
_Sure. Just…Give me a second.

*Gestures at a nearby stack of empty water bottles.*

**CREMEANS** (CONT'D)  
They’re coming in hot, sweaty, and stupidly thirsty.

---

( VISUAL):  
Quick cut — Water bottles, dented and half-empty.  
Cut to — The stage entrance, where the band emerges like survivors from battle.

Nick Stewart grins—*amused, approving.*

NICK STEWART (chuckling)  
*Of* course.

The band stumbles in—_flushed, dripping, elated.

V.O. (Collective Thought)  
Water!

**KATHY** (V.O.)**    
I need a shower.  And a stiff drink.

(FINAL SHOT):  
Camera tracks the band as they cross the backstage floor.  **CREMEANS** stands waiting—arms full of water.  Nick Stewart beside him, already imagining contracts and studio dates. The band—tired, loud, half-laughing—heads toward the men who might change everything.

---

*Still backstage.  Still Dyche Stadium.  Chicago, Illinois.  The end of one performance. The start of something else entirely.*

---

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The **band staggers in**—sweaty, flushed, buzzing with adrenaline.  The final echoes of the crowd **ripple through the steel bones** of the stadium.

---

**(SOUND): ** 
Crowd still fading.  Gear being slammed into cases.  Heavy breathing.  Excited half-laughs. Footsteps. The *aftermath.*

---

**( VISUAL): ** 
**Camera captures them up close—** faces glowing, hair stuck to foreheads, clothes wrinkled and sweat-streaked.  They look wrecked. They look victorious.

---

Suddenly—**KATHY** freezes.  Eyes wide.  Mouth slightly open.

She’s staring at **GILLEY’s** guitar. **Hanging from one of the tuning pegs**—like a banner of divine comedy—are **her panties**.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
**Oh. My. God.**

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
**Of all the gin joints, in all the towns, in all the world… my panties had to end up *on his guitar.*

**( VISUAL):  
**Extreme close-up—**fabric fluttering from the tuning peg.  Then a smash cut to **KATHY**’s face—pure, unfiltered mortification.  With ninja-speed embarrassment reflexes, she **snatches them** and **shoves them away**—somewhere beneath the toga—face burning.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**    
Whoops. **Collateral damage.

---

As **KATHY** recovers, **JIM and BILL** suddenly **lock eyes on Nick Stewart**—and freeze.

**( VISUAL):  
**Quick punch-ins—**JIM**’s pupils dilate.   **BILL**’s mouth drops open.  **Cut to Nick**—stoic, collected, hands in pockets.

**JIM** (low, urgent)  
*Holy* shit…It’s Nick Stewart!

**BILL** (barely breathing)  
From *Island Records?*

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**Nick Stewart?  Island Records?  What were they even talking about?

**JEFF, JEREMY**, and **KATHY** blink in confusion.

**JEFF** _(deadpan)  
*Who*?

**JIM** and **BILL** exchange reverent, almost religious looks.

**JIM** (whispering)  
_He’s a *legend.* Signed half the British invasion.

**BILL** _(whispering harder)  
Jeff, he’s the guy who discovered… *U2.*

**( VISUAL):  
**Rapid cuts—**JIM** and **BILL** staring like disciples.  
Nick Stewart coolly watching them all.  Unbothered. Slightly amused.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
Island Records…  That rang a bell.  MTV. 3 AM. Fuzzy reception. Something with a lion.

**KATHY**, now composed—and internally recalibrating—eyes Nick Stewart with sudden intrigue.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
Okay.  *Now* things were getting interesting.

**(FINAL SHOT):**  
** Camera centers on the band**, their fatigue giving way to something else—*hope*, *urgency*, *holy shit, this might be real.*

**Nick Stewart** stands still. Watching. *An offer is coming. And everything’s about to change.*

*Still backstage*.  Still Dyche Stadium.  Chicago, Illinois.  *Moments* after the miracle.

---

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The band now stands in a *nervous semicircle*—like students before a surprise oral exam—staring at Nick Stewart, the A&R demigod who just emerged from myth and metaphor into their very real, very sweaty orbit.

**CREMEANS**, still clutching his sacramental armload of water bottles, stays off to the side, hovering somewhere between *proud dad* and *project manager with PTSD*.

---

(SOUND):  
The tail end of the crowd’s roar drifting up into the rafters.  Equipment clanks in the background like industrial punctuation.  The *soft panting* of people trying to play it cool.  A quiet but unmistakable hum of *tension thick enough to cut with a Ginsu*.

---

( VISUAL):  
Camera on Nick Stewart—tight, steady.  His face is calm.  His gaze? Not. He’s *reading* them.  Each one.  And they *know it.*

Nick breaks the silence.

NICK STEWART (even, measured)  
_Well…That was certainly… *something.*

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**    
I’ve seen every kind of band.  Over-rehearsed. Over-hyped.  Shiny but hollow.  These kids?  Raw. Messy. Electric.  Like a broken lamp still throwing off sparks.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**    
They’ve got raw energy.  Untamed. Unpolished.  And a manager who seems to juggle a clipboard, a hangover, and a nuclear-level panty crisis without dropping the ball.

Nick glances at **CREMEANS**, grins slightly—then returns to scanning the band like a field surgeon deciding which parts are worth saving.

**NICK STEWART**
Let’s talk about the performance.

*Pause.*

**NICK STEWART (CONT'D)**
You grabbed that crowd by the collar in under thirty seconds.  That’s not _luck.  _That’s instinct.  You made them believe they were watching *something great.*


( VISUAL):  
Flashbacks—snaps from the performance:  
**KATHY** spinning. **JEREMY**'s shimmer. **JIM**’s snare snap. The crowd’s faces turned to *rapture*.

NICK STEWART (CONT'D)  
That kind of *connection*—  You can’t teach that.  It either *lives in your bones*…  or it doesn’t.

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
He was talking about us.  *Us.*

**BILL** (V.O.)**    
This is it.   This is the speech that ends with a contract in someone’s hand and a plane ticket in someone’s shoe.

Nick’s eyes move methodically—locking onto each band member.  Measuring. Calculating.  He’s a lion in a button-down shirt.

**NICK STEWART (CONT'D)**  
You’re rough.  Frayed.  But that’s not a weakness.  It’s *texture*.  It’s _honest._Most of what I see is sterile, produced within an inch of its life.  But *you*?  You kill on stage.

( VISUAL):  
Close-ups—**KATHY**’s cautious smile.  **JEREMY** blinking hard, jaw clenched.  **JIM** holding back a grin.  **JEFF**… trying not to faint.

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
Rough around the edges?  Please.  We were *splinters held together with duct tape and tequila.*

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
They were a mess.  A symphonic, toe-tapping, ass-shaking mess.  And somehow… that *worked.*

Then, without preamble, Nick’s focus sharpens.  He turns to **CREMEANS**.

NICK STEWART _(clipped, direct)  
***Mr. CREMEANS***…  I’d like a word.  Privately.

( VISUAL):  
The camera shifts to **CREMEANS**—clipboard finally gone, face suddenly unreadable.  He nods once—*serious mode engaged.*

(FINAL SHOT):  
Camera slowly pulls back.  The band holds still—watching, hoping, barely breathing.  The air around them is charged—like lightning’s about to strike, or already has.

Nick and **CREMEANS** step aside.

And just like that…  
everything’s in motion.

*Still Dyche Stadium.  Still backstage.  Still glowing with the afterburn of something impossible.*

---

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The air is *radioactive* with tension.  Everyone holds their breath.  Even the sound of roadies packing up seems muted by the *gravity* of what’s about to happen.  **CREMEANS** stands completely still—his clipboard gone, his anxiety filed away like a tax return from another lifetime.

**(SOUND):  
**The tail-end hum of the crowd.  Metal gear ratcheting into place.**  Silence from the band.  Then, soft and surgical—the *hiss* of a Mountain Dew can being cracked open.

**( VISUAL):  
The camera cuts in *tight* on **CREMEANS’ face**.  Blank. Calm.  A man standing in the middle of chaos, with a can of cold sugar water and an unshakable belief in himself.  Without missing a beat, **CREMEANS** pulls a business card from his pocket—not flashy, not oversized, just *intentional.*  He hands it to **Nick Stewart**, whose eyebrow *lifts half a centimeter.*

**CREMEANS** (even, level)  
*I* only talk to principals.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
**It was a line I’d been saving.**  A silver bullet in a world of blanks.  And this? This was the monster I built it for.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**    
**Play hardball.**Even if your bat’s made of plastic.  Swing like it’s made of maple.

Without another syllable, **CREMEANS turns**—*a smooth, surgical 180*—and **walks out the nearest door**. No strut.  No smile.  Just presence.

**( VISUAL):  
**Slow-motion tracking shot of his **retreating silhouette**, the light from the corridor framing him like a saint walking into the unknown.

**The band stands frozen.**  Jaws slack.  Eyes wide.  Hearts pounding.

**V.O. – COLLECTIVELY**  
**What… the actual hell… just happened?**

**BILL (V.O.)**    
**Did he just…Did he just imply he only talks to Chris *fucking* Blackwell?

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**Is he insane?

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
***No.***  That was the most baller move I’ve ever witnessed.

**JIM (V.O.)**    
I think we just saw history rewritten.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
I need a goddamn drink.

There’s a long, loaded beat. Then—**Nick Stewart starts to laugh.** Not a polite chuckle. Not industry laughter.  *Real, cathartic, shaking-the-dust-off-his-soul kind of laughter.*

**( VISUAL):  
Close-up on **Nick’s face**, cracked open in unfiltered joy.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**    
I’ve seen agents fake it.  Labels push it.  Bands die trying to fake what that man just pulled off.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**    
He *checkmated* me.  With a can of soda and a goddamn laminated card.

(beat)  
**That’s when I knew.

(beat)  
**I had to work with this band.  
Because any band with *that guy* behind them…That’s not a gamble.  That’s destiny.

---

**(OBSERVATION – JEFF – YEARS LATER):**

**JEFF (V.O.)**    
**We didn’t know** what was happening.  But we knew one thing:  **CREMEANS** had just kicked open a door we didn’t even know existed.

**(OBSERVATION – BILL – YEARS LATER):**

**BILL (V.O.)**    
**I still think he was bluffing.**  But damn… what a bluff.

**(OBSERVATION – KATHY – YEARS LATER):**

**KATHY (V.O.)**    
He made it look like this was all part of the plan.  Even when the plan was made on the back of a napkin in a stolen dorm room microwave.

**(OBSERVATION – JIM – YEARS LATER):**

**JIM (V.O.)**    
**That was our manager.**  Our chaos conductor.  The only man alive who thought a *Mountain Dew* was a negotiation tool.

**(OBSERVATION – JEREMY – YEARS LATER):**

**JEREMY (V.O.)**    
**All I remember is thinking:**  We’re either going to be famous…  or arrested.

---

**Back in the** Moment**—  **Nick’s laughter fades.  He straightens his jacket.  Then addresses the band with the gravity of a State Department diplomat.

**NICK STEWART** (cool again, deadly serious)  
_Right.

(beat)
Well… I believe **Mr. CREMEANS** mentioned something about hydration?

He picks up a water bottle and holds it out—*not like a drink*, but like a *torch*.


**(FINAL SHOT):  
**The band stares at Nick.  Then the water bottle.  Then each other.

Their world has just shifted—by a line, a laugh, and the quiet exit of a man who’d just played the biggest hand of his life… and *won*.

Still backstage.  Still Dyche Stadium.  Still Chicago.  But nothing is the same.

---

## **COMMUTED: THE SCOUTING REPORT MONTAGE**

**(SOUND:** A driving, rhythmic instrumental track with a subtle electronic undercurrent begins. The music has a sense of purpose and Momentum, reflecting the methodical nature of Nick’s investigation. No lyrics, just music.)

**( VISUAL – but restrained, more like a Soderbergh film):** Clean, crisp visuals with a focus on detail and observation. The montage is fast-paced but not chaotic, emphasizing the collection of data.

**(1) W.O. WRIGHT’S, BEAVERCREEK, OH: INITIAL ASSESSMENT (NIGHT):** Nick Stewart arrives at W.O. Wright’s, a dimly lit bar in Beavercreek. He’s dressed casually but observantly, blending into the background. Commuted is setting up their equipment. The visuals emphasize:

- **Venue Assessment:** Wide shots of the bar, showing its size, layout, and general atmosphere. Nick notes the capacity on a small notepad. He times how long it takes the band to set up.
- **Crowd Observation:** Nick observes the early arrivals, noting their demographics (age, style of dress, etc.). He counts heads as people enter.
- **Pre-Show Buzz:** Nick eavesdrops on conversations, trying to gauge the level of anticipation for the band. He notes the number of people who mention knowing the band or having seen them before.
- **Sound Check Analysis:** Nick observes the band’s sound check, noting the quality of the sound system and the band’s adjustments. He uses a decibel meter app on his phone to measure the sound levels.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Beavercreek. Not exactly a hotbed of musical innovation. But you have to start somewhere.

**INT. W.O. WRIGHT’S BAR – BEAVERCREEK, OH – NIGHT**

*It’s packed. Pre-show energy buzzes through the air like static cling in a polyester dryer. W.O. Wright’s, a 350-capacity bar carved out of Midwestern drywall and dreams, is at its absolute max. Every inch is bodies, breath, and beer.*

**(SOUND):  
** A driving, rhythmic *analog instrumental* plays over the crowd—live drums, fat bassline, layered synth, all Momentum.  
 No lyrics. Just movement.

**NICK STEWART** slips in just before the final click of the fire marshal’s people-counting clicker.  He’s one of the last let in.  An hour early, but this place is *already humming*. He’s dressed like a man who doesn’t need to impress you:  Worn sport coat, soft leather boots, button-down open at the collar.  Just a pen and a little black notebook.  He scans the room with the trained eyes of someone used to discovering treasure under layers of noise.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
**No guest list. No VIP badge.  
Just me, the notebook, and a hunch.  Twelve minutes it took to sell out.  Three months ago.  That doesn’t happen by accident in a town like Beavercreek. A name like a river that is a working river.

---

**WIDE SHOT – THE BAR INTERIOR:**  
**Everything smells like anticipation and Miller Lite.**People are shoulder to shoulder.  Bar staff in constant motion.  Stage prepped, lit dimly in red and blue hues.

**AT THE SOUNDBOARD:  
**CREMEANS** is coordinating like a NASA tech—clipboard clutched like a lifeline.  **KATHY** does her own mic check.  **BILL** tweaks his synth levels.  **JEREMY** adjusts his pedalboard with the precision of a surgeon who grew up on Van Halen.

**( DETAIL):**  
Nick glances at his *analog wristwatch*.  
He jots:  **“7:04 p.m. – stage nearly live-ready.”**

No stopwatch, just instinct.  He watches the *crowd response* to even a mic test.

NICK MOVES THROUGH THE CROWD:  He catches snippets of conversation:

**BEER-SOAKED COLLEGE GUY ** 
Dude, if they play “Wow Finish” second again I swear I’ll lose it.

**GIRL IN TORN DENIM JACKET**  
**I heard they wrote a *new* one.** **GILLEY**’s gonna rip my gash in two tonight.

Nick jots again:  **“Repeat attendance. Anticipation: rabid. Word-of-mouth strong.”**

**NICK (V.O.)**    
**They weren’t just fans.**  They were believers.  Disciples in flannel and wet boots.  Commuted was their church.

**ON STAGE:**  
The band huddles briefly, laughing, nodding.  **CREMEANS** whispers something to **KATHY**.  **GILLEY** cracks his knuckles like he’s about to enter the octagon.

Nick notes:  **“Band chemistry: visible. Unforced.”**

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**Lights dim just a notch.  Crowd tightens.  The bar goes from *loud* to *rabid* in a blink.

Nick doesn’t lean back.  He leans *forward*.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
This wasn’t just a band.  It was a wildfire that found dry wood.

---

**(2) W.O. WRIGHT’S: PERFORMANCE DATA (NIGHT):** Commuted takes the stage. Nick focuses on collecting data during their performance. The visuals emphasize:

- **Setlist Tracking:** Close-ups of Nick’s notebook as he meticulously records the order of the songs, the length of each song (using his stopwatch), and the transitions between them.
- **Audience Reaction Measurement:** Nick observes the crowd’s reactions to each song, noting the level of applause, dancing, and general engagement. He counts how many people leave during the set.
- **Financial Data Collection:** Nick discreetly observes the bar staff, noting how many drinks are being ordered and how quickly the bartenders are working. He times how long it takes to get served at the bar. He also notes the price of the cover charge.
- **Post-Show Analysis:** After the performance, Nick observes the band’s interaction with the fans, noting how many people approach them and what they talk about. He times how long the band spends packing up their gear.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Data. It’s the lifeblood of this business. You can’t rely on gut feelings or hunches. You need numbers.

**INT. W.O. WRIGHT’S BAR – BEAVERCREEK, OH – NIGHT**

*The* Moment *Commuted hits the stage, something shifts. The tension in the air turns kinetic. This isn’t just a show—it’s a test.*

---

**(SOUND):  
**Commuted rips into their first number—tight, raw, electric.  
The crowd roars back, louder than their 350 bodies should be able to muster.

**(VISUAL):  
**Clean lines, sharp close-ups.  The chaos of rock filtered through a scientific lens.

**NICK STEWART** stands in the back, notebook open, stopwatch in hand—sleek and silver, old-school.  He is still.  Everything around him isn’t.

---

**CLOSE-UP – NICK’S NOTEBOOK:  
Setlist:**

1.     “Not Taken Kindly” – 4:18  
2.     “The Left Hand” – 3:46  
3.     “Payment in Kind” – 4:05  
4.     “Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar” – 4:41  
5.     “It Has a Wow Finish” – 3:33  
6.     “Come Inside Me” – 11:02

He notes transitions:   **“Clean segues. No dead air. Tight.”**

---

**WIDE SHOT – THE CROWD:  
Bodies moving. Heads bobbing.  One guy’s on a chair. A couple in the back starts dancing slowly to a mid-tempo number.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)**    
**This is where the story lives.**  Not on stage.  Out there.  Applause per square foot. Sweat per beer.  You measure heat by the temperature of the room, not the thermostat.

**NICK JOTS:  
“Dance floor: full by song two. Applause peaking at 2:03 during ‘Wow Finish.’”  “Zero exits before encore.”**

---

**AT THE BAR:  
**Nick angles closer.  
Counts glasses poured. Tracks the bartender's rhythm—snaps his watch when one order is placed and again when it's served.  
He eyes the chalkboard:  **“$3 cover. $1.50 PBRs. $2.50 house whiskey. Sold out of Miller by song three.”**

He scribbles:  **“Revenue potential: high. Engagement = consumption.”**

**NICK (V.O.)**    
Forget the label guys in the big glass offices.  This?  This is the market.  It’s loud. It’s sweaty. It drinks cheap beer and sings along like it’s gospel.

---

**POST-SHOW – THE HOUSE LIGHTS COME UP  
Fans swarm the stage like it’s a makeshift altar.  **KATHY**’s mobbed first.  Then **JEREMY**. Then **BILL**—he signs a *synth key*.  **GILLEY** gets cornered by three girls with lip gloss and banana bras.  
**CREMEANS** is the only one already loading out cables.

**NICK JOTS AGAIN:  
“Fan interactions: 37 total. Age range 18–34. High recall of lyrics. Gear pack-out: 27 mins.”**

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)**    
They weren’t just liked.  They were remembered.  And in this game, memory is everything.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
Nick watches as the bar begins to empty—buzz still in the air.  The band’s gear is packed. **KATHY** is sipping from a water bottle, grinning with someone’s phone number on her arm.

Nick closes his notebook.  Clicks his stopwatch.  And finally—*smiles*.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
Data never lies.  And the numbers tonight?  They sang.

---

**(3) BOGART’S, CINCINNATI, OH: SCALING UP (NIGHT):** Nick travels to Cincinnati to see Commuted perform at Bogart’s, a much larger and more established venue. The visuals emphasize:

- **Venue Comparison:** Wide shots of Bogart’s, contrasting it with W.O. Wright’s. Nick notes the difference in size, layout, and atmosphere. He notes the stated capacity of the venue.
- **Larger Crowd Observation:** Nick observes the significantly larger crowd, noting the change in demographics and overall energy. He uses a clicker to count heads entering the venue.
- **Professional Sound Assessment:** Nick pays close attention to the sound quality, noting the clarity of the vocals and instruments. He uses a more professional sound meter to measure the sound levels. He also notes the quality of the stage lighting.
- **Ticket Sale Data:** Nick talks to the box office staff, discreetly inquiring about ticket sales and attendance figures.

**NICK (V.O.)** 
Scaling up. That’s the challenge. Can they translate their success in smaller venues to larger crowds?

**INT. BOGART’S – CINCINNATI, OH – NIGHT**

*From the* Moment *Nick steps into Bogart’s, everything screams scale-up. Bigger sound. Bigger crowd. Bigger stakes.*

**(SOUND):  
**A deep, driving groove pulses under the ambient chatter—pre-show tension turned up to eleven.  
Bottles clink. Shoes shuffle. Anticipation thick enough to bottle and brand.

**(VISUAL):  
Wide, graceful pans across the room—*Bogart’s* in all its rock ‘n roll glory.  Multi-tiered balconies. Deep stage.  A lighting rig that *actually has a budget*.  Nick’s notepad opens with a snap.

**NICK’S NOTES:  
Venue Capacity: 1,500.  Architectural acoustics: favorable. Room geometry: slightly convex. Balcony bounce: minimal.

He walks the perimeter like a field agent inspecting terrain before an assault.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)**    
W.O. Wright’s was a pressure cooker.  Bogart’s is a proving ground.  Different physics.  More bodies, more variables, less margin for error.

---

**CROWD SCAN:**  
Nick’s thumb is busy with a mechanical *clicker counter*.  Every beep is another data point. **Click. Click. Click.**  He notes:  **Demographics: Expanded. More college kids, some late-30s hipsters. Leather jackets replacing flannel. More piercings. Fewer mullets.**

---

**TICKET WINDOW (EXT. BOGART’S):  

Nick leans in casually to the box office attendant, charm turned up just enough.

NICK (softly)  
How’s the house tonight?

The attendant shrugs, impressed.

**ATTENDANT**  
Sold out. Three days ago. Full prepay. Balcony too.

Nick smiles faintly.

---

**INSIDE – DURING SOUND CHECK: ** 
Nick crouches near the sound booth.  He’s swapped the clicker for a *pro-grade* analog decibel meter, dials turning like he’s tuning a submarine.  **Reading: 107 dB during warm-up. Clear highs. Thundering mids. Vocals cut clean.**

---

**STAGE LIGHTING – PERFORMANCE STARTS:  
**KATHY** steps into the spotlight—clean, white, direct.  Her silhouette commands the stage like a queen who *earned* the throne.  **GILLEY**’s guitar licks tear the air like it owes him money.  
**JEFF**’s bass is *felt* more than heard.  **BILL**’s synth is now *a wall*.  **JIM**’s snare echoes like an executive decision.

---

**NICK (V.O.)**    
No distortion.  No hiccups.  They were *clean*.  Too clean for a band from Clark County, Ohio.

---

**NICK’S NOTES:  
- “Adaptation = confirmed. Scale = absorbed, not feared.”  
- “Lighting: pro rig. Responsive. Dynamic.”  
- “Stage command: KATHY locked in by song two. JEREMY’s stage movement evolved. Band using full depth of platform.”

---

**AFTER THE SHOW – LOBBY AND MERCH TABLE: ** 
Fans linger.  Not just milling—they’re lined up.  Autographs, shirts, setlists torn from the stage.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
You can teach scales.  You can’t teach gravity.  And right now?  This band had *pull*.

**(FINAL SHOT):  
Nick leans against a steel column in the back, watching the last fans file out.  He flips the notebook closed.  No smile this time. Just a look that says: *This train might not stop at small towns much longer.*

**NICK (V.O.)**    
They didn’t just scale up.  They owned it.

---

**(4) BOGART’S: REVENUE ANALYSIS (NIGHT):** Commuted performs at Bogart’s. Nick continues his data collection, focusing on the financial aspects. The visuals emphasize:

- **Bar Revenue Tracking:** Nick observes the bar staff, noting the types of drinks being ordered and the flow of customers. He times how long the lines are at the bar.
- **Merchandise Sales:** Nick observes the merchandise table, noting how many items are being sold and what types of items are most popular. He discreetly counts the number of items sold.
- **Post-Show Revenue Analysis:** Nick talks to the club manager again, gathering more detailed information about the night’s revenue. He asks about the cost of renting the venue.
- **Comparing Data:** Nick compares the data from Bogart’s to the data from W.O. Wright’s, looking for trends and patterns. He calculates the revenue per capita.

**NICK (V.O.)** 
Ultimately, it’s about the money. Can they generate a profit? Can they justify the investment? These are the questions that the label will be asking.  
  
**INT. BOGART’S – CINCINNATI – NIGHT**

*The house is jammed. A sweat-slick sea of people throbs in time with the band. Bogart’s, capacity 1,500, is sold out—and acting like it.*

**(SOUND: Crowd noise at full throttle. Cash drawers slamming. The clink of bottles. The thrum of “It Has a Wow Finish” hammering from the stage.)**

**( VISUAL):  
Fast intercuts: Nick scans the crowd, eyes flicking like a lie detector.  
He times bar lines with a gold-plated stopwatch.  Counts heads at merch with a silent finger-point tally.  Marks tallies in a small black notebook, its pages dog-eared from obsession.

---

**BAR REVENUE TRACKING:  
**He drifts near the bar. It’s a full-on liquid economy.

**(CAMERA POV):**

- Four bartenders—sweating and moving like a pit crew.  
- Orders flying: Coors Light, gin and tonics, Jack on the rocks.   
- Nick clocks a 9-minute wait time during “Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar.”  
 
**NICK (V.O.)**    
You want to know if a band’s hot? Don’t look at the stage.  Look at the pour speed. That’s your stock ticker.

---

**MERCHANDISE SALES:  
**At the back, a long table swarmed with fans.

**(CAMERA POV):**
- Shirts: sold out of medium and large.  
- Cassettes: all gone.  
- Hand-numbered lyric zines: $2 a pop, line 18 deep.  

Nick scribbles: _"Merch Revenue Estimate: $4,100. Time: 9:32 PM."  

**NICK (V.O.)**    
_These kids weren’t just watching a band.  They were buying a brand.

---

**POST-SHOW REVENUE ANALYSIS:**  
Later, Nick huddles near the manager’s office door.

**MANAGER (low voice)**  
They blew past our average bar take by 40%. And that merch line? Jesus."

Nick nods once. Files it under: *Viable. Very.*

**NICK (V.O.)**    
*This* wasn’t just music. It was conversion.  Fans turned into cashflow.  Noise turned into margin.

He flips back to his notes from Beavercreek. His pen draws a quick checkmark. Then another.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
Scaling’s not a gamble. It’s the proof.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**Nick leans against a post, scanning his final numbers.  
Behind him, Commuted’s gear is being loaded out—fast, tight, practiced.  
The scent of money and sweat clings to the air.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***Now we’re in business.*

**(5) THE SMOKY DIVE: ATMOSPHERE AND AMBIENCE (NIGHT):** Nick sits at a sticky table in a dimly lit, smoky dive bar. The air is thick with the smell of stale beer and cigarettes. Commuted is playing to a small but enthusiastic crowd. The visuals focus on:

- The low light and smoky atmosphere: The camera struggles to focus, creating a hazy, almost dreamlike effect.
- Close-ups of Nick’s notebook, which now has smudges and beer stains on it.
- Nick’s notes include observations like: “Ambient noise levels: excessive. Visibility: poor. Probability of contracting lung cancer: high.”
- He is shown discreetly timing how long it takes for someone to spill a drink on the floor (3 minutes, 17 seconds). He notes this down.
- He observes how many people order food, and what they order, as a proxy for how long they intend to stay.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Atmosphere. It’s a crucial metric. Though difficult to quantify. Unless you’re measuring the number of airborne carcinogens.

**(5) THE SMOKY DIVE: ATMOSPHERE AND AMBIENCE – NIGHT**

**INT. UNKNOWN BAR – COLUMBUS, OH – NIGHT**

*If ambiance had a hangover, this is where it would wake up.*

The place is a rectangle of haze, neon, and unwashed wood. Cigarette smoke curls like lazy ghosts above the crowd. The jukebox hums between sets. Commuted is mid-performance, barely lit by a single red bulb over the "stage"—a riser with a frayed carpet and half-dead monitors.

**(SOUND: Gritty guitar fuzz, clinking pint glasses, low conversation, and the unmistakable sound of a pool cue breaking a rack.)**

---

**( VISUAL):  
**The camera struggles to autofocus. Smoke blooms like watercolor across the lens.  
The band blurs. Faces appear, vanish, reappear. The whole world seems pixelated by Marlboros and Busch Light.

---

**(NICK’S TABLE):  
**Nick sits at a sticky two-top, wedged between a jukebox and a glowing Budweiser sign.  
A yellow legal pad lies open—smudged, stained, one corner curled from what was either a spilled Jack & Coke or time.

His pen scratches deliberately.

**INSERT – LEGAL PAD NOTES:**

- _Ambient noise: absurd. Visibility: 4/10.  
     Floor spill time: 3:17. New record.  
     Customer sustenance index: 8 orders of fried pickles, 3 nacho platters, 1 mozzarella stick suicide.  
      
    _

- ---
    

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***Atmosphere. Everyone talks about it like it’s a vibe. A mood. A texture.  
But in reality, it’s particulate matter and late-stage capitalism.*

He pulls out a tiny notepad and counts how many food baskets pass from the kitchen.  
One, two, three…

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***Rule of thumb: if they’re ordering food, they’re not just here to get drunk. They came for the show.  
Or at least, they don’t want to leave during it.*

---

**(CAMERA POV):**

- A server spills a Coors Lite near table 7.  
      
    
- A patron lights a Marlboro with the stub of another.  
      
    
- A guy in a sleeveless Megadeth shirt shouts, “Play that one with the bridge!” and is ignored.  
      
    

Nick checks his watch. He jots: *“Crowd density: low. Enthusiasm: oddly sincere. Acoustic treatment: nonexistent.”*

He takes a sip from a sweating highball glass filled with what the menu claimed was bourbon. It's not.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***It wasn’t pretty. But pretty doesn’t sell records.  
Grit does. Smoke does. Real does.  
And these kids?  
They’re real.*

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**The camera pans from Nick’s scuffed legal pad…  
…to the band, backlit in greasy red light, playing like it’s Madison Square Garden…  
…to a dropped mozzarella stick congealing on the floor.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***They don’t even flinch at the grime.  
That’s how I know they belong.*

**(6) THE EMPTY BAR: MINIMAL VIABILITY (NIGHT):** Nick finds himself in an almost empty bar. Commuted is playing with admirable enthusiasm, despite the lack of an audience. The visuals emphasize:

- The emptiness of the bar: Wide shots of the empty room, with only a handful of patrons scattered around.
- Close-ups of Nick’s notes, which now include phrases like: “Occupancy rate: 8%. Revenue potential: negligible. Existential dread: palpable.”
- He is shown timing the length of the band's set, remarking to himself that they are playing a full set to almost no one.
- He takes notes on the band's professionalism, even under such poor circumstances.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Viability. That’s the key. Can they draw a crowd? Can they generate revenue? Can they avoid bankruptcy? These are the questions that keep me up at night.

**(6) THE EMPTY BAR: MINIMAL VIABILITY – NIGHT**

**INT. GENERIC MUSIC BAR – SPRINGFIELD, OH – NIGHT**

It’s a Tuesday. Or maybe a Monday pretending to be a Tuesday. The kind of night where even the roaches stay home.

**(SOUND: Echoes of guitar and snare bouncing off brick and glass. A soft buzz from fluorescent lights. The low clink of a lone beer bottle being set down. Once.)**

---

**( VISUAL):  
**Wide tracking shots across the venue’s wide emptiness.  
Eight patrons. Four look mildly interested. Two are asleep. One might be dead.  
The bartender wipes the same spot for a fifth time.  
The lighting is cold and clinical, as if to shame the void.

---

**(NICK’S TABLE):  
**Nick is seated near the back. Alone. Not unnoticed—just unapproached.  
His notebook looks tired now, the spine starting to split.

He clicks his stopwatch. Scribbles. Sips from a draft beer he didn’t order but accepted anyway.

---

**INSERT – NOTES:**

- *Occupancy: 8%.*
- *Revenue potential: theoretical.*
- *Existential dread: detectable from the parking lot.*
- _Playing a full set. Full commitment. No shortcuts. No complaints.  
      
    _

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***This is the test nobody talks about.  
Not the sold-out club. Not the college fest with free beer.  
This.  
The graveyard shift of rock and roll.*

He watches **BILL**, soaked in sweat, as if he were playing Red Rocks, not Red Flags.

---

**(CAMERA POV):  
****KATHY** belts out the chorus with unapologetic fury.  
**JEREMY’s** hair is everywhere. **GILLEY**’s solo howls like someone might be listening.  
They don’t flinch. They don’t check their watches.  
They just play.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***This is where you separate the weekend warriors from the lifers.  
The ones who’ll cancel if it rains… from the ones who play through a drought.*

He checks the setlist. They’re three songs over. No one's asked them to stop.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***Minimal viability doesn’t mean no hope.  
It means: do they keep showing up when no one else does?*

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**The band plays on, unwavering.  
A disinterested man at the bar flicks a peanut shell.  
Nick clicks his stopwatch.  
Smiles.

**NICK (V.O.)**    
***They passed.  
God help me, they passed.*

**(7) THE ROWDY CROWD: BEHAVIORAL ANALYSIS (NIGHT):** Nick observes Commuted playing to a rowdy, almost unruly crowd. The visuals shift to focus on:

- The crowd’s behavior: People are dancing, shouting, and even throwing things (mostly empty beer cups).
- Close-ups of Nick’s notes, which now include observations like: “Level of intoxication: high. Probability of property damage: significant. Potential for viral marketing: intriguing.”
- He times how long it takes for a fight to break out (11 minutes, 42 seconds). He notes this down.
- He observes how the band reacts to the rowdy crowd. Do they engage? Do they ignore it? Do they try to calm things down?

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Crowd dynamics. It’s a science. Or at least, it should be.

**(7) THE ROWDY CROWD: BEHAVIORAL ANALYSIS – NIGHT**

**INT. THE PIT – TOLEDO, OH – NIGHT**

There’s a line outside. There’s noise inside.  
And in between?  
A full moon and a crowd ready to burn something down—preferably the stage, if the music doesn’t blow it apart first.

**(SOUND: Thudding bass, sloshing drinks, primal whoops. The clatter of metal chairs becoming percussion instruments. A beer bottle misses its mark and explodes on tile.)**

**( VISUAL):

**INSERT – NICK’S NOTEBOOK (jagged handwriting):**

·        *Intoxication index: 9.3/10*

·        *Behavioral volatility: fluid*

·        *Fight clock: started*

·        _Potential for spontaneous human combustion: elevated  
  
_

·

---

**(STAGE LEFT):  
**The band keeps going. **KATHY**’s vocals spike into the mic, trying to match the energy.  
**JIM** hits the drums harder. Too hard. A cymbal pops.  
The crowd *loves* it.

**(NICK – V.O.):  
***Crowd dynamics.  
It’s like herding cats… if the cats were hammered, half-naked, and listening to New Order backwards.*

---

**(11 MINUTES, 42 SECONDS):  
**Two guys bump. A beer spills.  
Shouting escalates into shoving.  
Nick marks the time with a sigh—almost disappointed it took that long.

---

**(STAGE CENTER):  
****GILLEY** clocks the brewing brawl. Doesn’t flinch.

He leans into the mic between songs.

**GILLEY (deadpan, smiling):  
**“Let’s all take a deep breath and remember we’re here to *love* each other. Or at least keep it above the belt.”

Laughter. Applause. Some boos—good-natured.

He rips into the next song like he’s personally daring the crowd to throw another cup.

---

**(NICK – V.O.):  
***That’s leadership. Not the loud kind. The right kind.  
De-escalation by solo. Crowd control by riff.*

---

**( CAMERA SWEEP):  
**The fight fizzles. The room resets.  
The tempo takes over.  
Bodies sway again—not out of anger, but joy.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**Nick underlines one word in his notebook.

**INSERT – PAGE:  
Command.**

**NICK (V.O.):  
***You don’t just play the room.  
You run it.*

- The band’s ability to improvise and adapt to different musical styles.

**(9) THE DOUBLE SCOUT: COMPARING NOTES – NIGHT**

**INT. INDIE MUSIC CLUB – INDIANAPOLIS, IN – NIGHT**

A tight, low-ceilinged room with minimal lighting and maximum atmosphere.  
Brick walls, exposed ductwork, and a stage barely elevated from the dance floor.  
The kind of place where legends cut their teeth—and egos get bruised.

---

(SOUND: Muffled bass, ambient chatter, glasses clinking. A band mid-set. It’s Commuted—louder, looser, alive.)

( VISUAL):  
The camera tracks across the crowd—tight knots of twentysomethings, local musicians, curious college kids—and lands on two figures sitting apart from the buzz, watching with different kinds of intensity.

---

NICK STEWART — sleeves rolled, jacket draped over his chair, pen in hand, all calculation.  
SARAH MALCOM — fresh from NYU, stylish in an unassuming way, red pen dancing across a leather-bound notebook.

---

(OBSERVATION – NICK):  
NICK (V.O.): *Sarah’s sharp. Fashion-forward, culture-savvy. She sees what I miss. And I see what she doesn't know to look for. That’s why this works.*

(TARANTINO-ESQUE DIALOGUE WHISPERED BETWEEN THEM):

*"Possibly both."*

They jot simultaneously. Nick glances at his stopwatch.  
2:43 into the solo. Too long.

Glasses of cheap club wine. Low voices. Not quite whispering, but close.

(OBSERVATION – SARAH):  
SARAH (V.O.): *He’s old-school. Data-driven. I respect that. But sometimes, it’s the vibe. The story behind the sound. That’s what sticks.*

*"**KATHY**’s got it. I don’t know what it is, but she’s got it. Give her a stylist and a slightly better mic, and she’s the whole damn package."*

NICK (raising his glass):

(FINAL SHOT):  
Back to the stage. Commuted kicks off their second set, tighter, cleaner, still raw but focused.  
Nick and Sarah turn in unison, pens ready. Two sets of eyes, one band under the microscope.

**(10) THE DIFFERENT PERSPECTIVES: CONFLICTING DATA (NIGHT):** Nick and Sarah observe Commuted at a different venue, a slightly more upscale bar. Their observations begin to diverge. The visuals emphasize:

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):**

A beat. The tension isn’t hostile—but it crackles.

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):  
SARAH (V.O.):** *I don’t care how tight they play if no one remembers them. This is a business. And business is aesthetic.*

**(FINAL SHOT):

 Nick and Sarah stand a few paces apart, notebooks closed, each quietly convinced they’re right.

The music is electric. But the brand? Still foggy.

**(11) GILLEY’S “SUCCESS”: UNINTENDED CONSEQUENCES (NIGHT/MORNING):** This section is managed with dry humor and focuses on the unintended consequences of **GILLEY**’s charm. The visuals emphasize:

- A brief, almost erotic shot of **GILLEY** chatting with Sarah after the show, his charm clearly working with its magic.
- A quick cut to the next morning: **GILLEY** is shown leaving a hotel room, looking slightly disheveled but also pleased with himself. Sarah’s hand waves goodbye from under the covers.
- Nick is shown observing this from a distance, shaking his head slightly. He adds a note to his report: “Extracurricular activities: observed. Potential impact on band cohesion: unknown.” He times how long **GILLEY** is gone from the hotel.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Human factors. They’re always the hardest to predict. And the hardest to control.



**GILLEY (V.O.)** I was just being friendly.  
  
**(11) GILLEY’S “SUCCESS”: UNINTENDED CONSEQUENCES – NIGHT / MORNING**

**INT. CLUB – GREEN ROOM – NIGHT**

**GILLEY** leans against a faux-brick wall, beer in hand, wearing a grin that walks the line between cocky and clueless. Across from him, Sarah Malcom—poised, polished, professionally intrigued—tilts her head, clearly amused. Whatever he’s saying, it’s working.

---

**( VISUAL):  
**Extreme close-up: Sarah’s lips curling into a half-smile.

**CUT TO:**

**INT. HOTEL – HALLWAY – EARLY MORNING**

The lighting is unforgiving. **GILLEY** tiptoes down the hallway in a vintage t-shirt that probably doesn’t belong to him and socks that definitely don’t match.

He’s grinning like a man who thinks he got away with something.

---

**( VISUAL):  
**A single manicured hand lifts from beneath crisp hotel sheets, lazily waving goodbye from the half-open room.

---

**CUT TO: ACROSS THE HALL – NICK’S HOTEL ROOM DOOR – AJAR**

Nick Stewart, fully dressed, holding a cup of black coffee and a notepad, leans against the doorframe. He watches **GILLEY** pass with the expression of a man who just discovered the printer is jammed… again.

He scribbles something.

---

**INSERT – NICK’S NOTES:  
***“Extracurricular activities: observed.  
Time out: 7 hrs, 12 mins.  
Potential impact on internal dynamics: TBD.  
Backup guitarist = plan B?”*

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):  
NICK (V.O.):** *There’s no spreadsheet formula for what happens when libido meets logistics. But there should be.*

---

**(TARANTINO-ESQUE DIALOGUE – NICK, MUTTERING):  
***"Jesus, **GILLEY**. Day one of the tour."*

---

**(OBSERVATION – GILLEY):  
GILLEY (V.O.):** *Look, I was just being friendly. She asked about tunings. One thing led to another… and here we are.*

---

**( VISUAL):  
**A slow-motion shot of **GILLEY** doing finger guns at the vending machine as it dispenses a Mountain Dew. His smile says “mission accomplished.” His hair? Absolutely says "pillow fight survivor."

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**Back in Nick’s room. He taps the notepad once, closes it, and looks out the window toward the tour van.

**NICK (V.O.):** *This wasn’t in the scouting manual. But maybe it should’ve been.*

**(12) THE SYNTHESIS: COMBINING THE DATA (DAY):** Nick and Sarah meet at a neutral location (a coffee shop) to combine their data and finalize their report. The visuals emphasize:

- The process of combining the data: They compare their notes, discuss their observations, and create a comprehensive report.
- Close-ups of the report, which now includes both quantifiable data and subjective assessments.
- They are shown discussing the pros and cons of signing Commuted, weighing the potential risks and rewards. Nick notes how long the meeting takes to complete.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** The numbers don’t lie. But they don’t tell the whole story either. You need to consider the qualitative data as well. The intangibles. The… *je ne sais quoi*.

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):**

**SARAH (V.O.)** They’ve got potential. They just need the right guidance. And maybe a good publicist.

**(12) THE SYNTHESIS: COMBINING THE DATA – DAY**

**INT. INDEPENDENT COFFEE SHOP – DOWNTOWN COLUMBUS – LATE MORNING**

A mismatched pair of mid-level A&R operatives take up a corner booth littered with legal pads, spiral notebooks, and two aggressively caffeinated beverages. The vibe is part-strategy summit, part-postmortem therapy session.

Nick Stewart is all business—button-down, sleeves rolled up, surgical with a pen. Sarah Malcom is slouched like a cat in a sunbeam, her notepad dotted with doodles and underlined comments like *“**KATHY** = magnetic,”* and *“**JEREMY**’s hair = future liability?”*

---

**( VISUAL):  
**Wide shot of the coffee shop: exposed brick, indie folk music, a barista with an ironic mustache.  
Tight inserts of their papers overlapping—soundwave diagrams beside lipstick-smeared notes.  
Two brains, two styles. One conclusion approaching.

---

**(SOUND):** The clink of spoons, the hiss of espresso machines, the rhythmic scratch of pens meeting paper.

---

**NICK (V.O.):** *The numbers don’t lie. But they don’t tell the whole story either. You need the qualitative data. The intangibles. The… je ne sais quoi.*

---

Sarah flips through her notes, stopping on a page with a big circle around the phrase *“audience buy-in.”*

**SARAH (V.O.):** *They’ve got potential. They just need the right guidance. And maybe a publicist. Or five.*

---

**DIALOGUE – LIVE:**

**SARAH  
**(half-joking, sipping her drink)  
I still think “Come Inside Me” needs a new title.

**NICK  
**(straight-faced)  
It tested well in Cincy. Eighty percent of the crowd sang along by the third chorus.

**SARAH  
**(mocking)  
Yes, because human beings are incapable of resisting repetition and double entendre. That doesn’t mean it’s marketable.

**NICK  
**(deadpan)  
No. It means it’s memorable.

---

They lock eyes. Mutual respect. Shared exhaustion.

**NICK (CONT'D)  
**Look, I don’t need them to be polished. I need them to be undeniable.

**SARAH  
**(scribbling into a final draft)  
So what’s the pitch? "Crude but charismatic"?

**NICK  
**"Untapped energy. Regional resonance. Proof of concept delivered at scale."

**SARAH  
**That’s so boring I think I just blacked out.

**NICK  
**Welcome to A&R.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):  
NICK (V.O.):** *They’ve got what it takes. But more importantly—they’ve got what we can sell.*

---

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):  
SARAH (V.O.):** *Island’s roster could use a little chaos. These kids? They’re marketable chaos.*

---

**CUT TO:**

**INT. COFFEE SHOP – PRINTER (SLOW PUSH IN)  
**Nick hits “PRINT” on the final PDF. The report churns out, pages still warm. At the top:  
  

**TO: CHRIS BLACKWELL  
RE: POTENTIAL ACQUISITION – COMMUTED**

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**Nick and Sarah walk out, their folders full, their coffees empty. The world outside is bright and full of possibility—and at least one band's future just tilted toward stardom.

**(13) THE REPORT (QUANTIFIABLE RESULTS):** Nick and Sarah are shown separately, then together, meticulously compiling their data into detailed reports. The visuals emphasize:

- **Data Entry:** Close-ups of spreadsheets filled with numbers: venue capacities, ticket sales, bar revenue, set times, number of songs played, even the average length of applause after each song (measured in decibels and time). Nick is shown meticulously entering data, occasionally muttering about standard deviations and statistical significance. Sarah is seen inputting more qualitative data, like audience demographics, fashion trends observed at the shows, and social media mentions of the band.
- **Visualizations:** Charts and graphs begin to materialize on computer screens: line graphs showing audience growth over time, bar charts comparing revenue across different venues, pie charts illustrating audience demographics. Nick is shown scrutinizing these charts, looking for trends and patterns. Sarah creates mood boards containing visual representations of the band's image, potential album art, and target audience.
- **Conflicting Data Points:** A brief, almost comedic scene where Nick points to a particularly high spike in bar revenue at one show, while Sarah points to a photo from the same show showing a particularly rowdy (and potentially destructive) crowd. They debate the meaning of this conflicting data, Nick focusing on the immediate financial gain, Sarah considering the long-term image of the band. Nick calculates the average cost of a spilled beer at each venue.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Numbers. They’re cold, hard facts. They don’t lie. But they also don’t tell the whole story.

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):**

**SARAH (V.O.)** Image is everything. Especially in this business. You can have the best music in the world, but if you don’t have the right look, you’re not going anywhere.

**(13) THE REPORT (QUANTIFIABLE RESULTS) – NIGHT/DAY**

**INT. VARIOUS LOCATIONS – MONTAGE – DAY INTO NIGHT**

The screen splits and overlaps as we follow Nick and Sarah across their separate spaces—Nick in a beige-walled, paper-stacked apartment filled with dog-eared **BILL**board magazines and an AM radio softly crackling in the background; Sarah in a cozier, cluttered loft with Cure posters and three unfinished coffees at various degrees of temperature.

---

**( VISUAL):  
** Cut between detailed close-ups:

- Nick’s hand slamming a mechanical stopwatch to log set length.  
      
    
- A 1991 IBM computer rendering crude graphs pixel by pixel.  
      
    
- Sarah clipping images from *Spin* and *The Face*, pinning them beside Polaroids of the band.  
      
    
- A lightbulb flickering overhead as Nick taps his TI-85 calculator, muttering about “applause decay curves.”  
      
    

---

**(SOUND):  
**The low whir of dot matrix printers. Cassette deck clicks. The rattle of an old keyboard. Intermittent sighs of data-entry frustration.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):  
NICK (V.O.):** *Numbers. Cold, hard facts. They don’t lie. But they don’t tell the whole story either. Not unless you know what you’re looking for.*

---

**INT. NICK’S APARTMENT – NIGHT**

Nick’s monitor flickers as he scrolls through spreadsheet columns labeled “Applause Length (sec),” “Bar Revenue (gross),” “Repeat Attendees (% est.).” He sips flat Coke from a paper cup and murmurs…

**NICK  
**Standard deviation’s too tight for a fluke…

He inputs a formula and hits “Enter.” A line graph sharpens: *Bogart’s performance > 31% revenue increase over W.O. Wright’s*. He circles it in red ink. Twice.

---

**INT. SARAH’S LOFT – NIGHT**

Sarah is seated cross-legged on the floor. A mood board rests on an easel beside her—a collage of **KATHY** mid-lyric, **JEREMY’s** boots, and a ripped fraternity flag.

She scrawls on a Post-it: *“Nostalgia punk meets midwestern mystique”* and sticks it next to a lipstick-smeared quote: *“They’re like if The Replacements got fashion tips from Prince.”*

Her computer dings. She’s found early BBS mentions of the band.

**SARAH (V.O.):  
***Image is everything. Especially in this business. You can have the best music in the world, but if you don’t have the right look… you're invisible.*

---

**INT. OFFICE SPACE – DAY – SHARED MEETING TABLE**

Now together, they lay their materials on a long wooden table—old school style. No Wi-Fi. Just manila folders, coffee rings, and two very different lenses on the same band.

---

**(COMEDIC CUT):  
**Nick points to a bar graph showing record-breaking drink sales in Columbus.

**NICK  
**Thirty-seven percent spike in sales after the third song.

Sarah slides over a blurry Polaroid from that show: a shirtless guy crowd-surfing with a busted nose.

**SARAH  
**And this is *why*. You’re pitching fire to a fireworks factory.

**NICK  
**(beat)  
But profitable fire.

**SARAH  
**(beat)  
With a body count.

They smile. Truce by sarcasm.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):  
NICK (V.O.):** *We were speaking different languages. But by then, we’d both learned enough to translate.*

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):  
SARAH (V.O.):** *He had the math. I had the myth. Together… we might just have a movement.*

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**A primitive laser printer hums to life. One page emerges:  
  

**ISLAND RECORDS INTERNAL SCOUTING BRIEF  
SUBJECT: COMMUTED  
RECOMMENDATION: HIGH PRIORITY – DEVELOPMENT POTENTIAL**

Below it: Two signatures. Stewart. Malcom.

Cut to black.

**(14) THE REHEARSAL (REFINING THE PITCH):** Nick and Sarah meet again, this time in NYC, in a sterile, brightly lit conference room. They rehearse their presentation for the Island Records executives, focusing on presenting their findings in a clear and concise manner. The visuals emphasize:

- **Practice Presentation:** Nick stands at a whiteboard, using markers to illustrate key data points. Sarah sits at a table, reviewing her mood boards and making notes on her presentation slides. They practice their delivery, timing each other and offering constructive criticism.
- **Disagreement on Messaging:** A brief scene where Nick wants to focus solely on the quantifiable data, while Sarah insists on highlighting the band’s “unique brand identity” and “untapped potential.” They debate the best way to present the band to the executives. Nick times how long the rehearsal takes.
- **Compromise:** They reach a compromise, agreeing to present a balanced view that incorporates both the data and the more subjective aspects of the band.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** The pitch. It’s the most important part. You can have the best data in the world, but if you can’t present it effectively, it’s worthless.

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):**

**SARAH (V.O.)** You have to sell the dream. You have to make them believe.

---

**(14) THE REHEARSAL (REFINING THE PITCH) – DAY**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – NYC – DAY**

Fluorescent lights hum overhead in a glass-box room perched ten floors above Manhattan. A wall clock ticks loudly. There’s a pitcher of water no one touches and a whiteboard full of bullet points—half smudged from Nick’s palm. The tension crackles like static electricity.

---

**( VISUAL):  
**Clean lines, sterile palette. Wide, still frames. The room is antiseptic—until Sarah’s mood boards add pops of chaotic color like spilled paint on lab tile.

---

**(SOUND):  
**Markers squeaking. Slide projector clicking. The low ambient rumble of New York outside.

---

Nick stands beside the whiteboard, sleeves rolled, tie loosened like he’s about to fix a carburetor instead of selling a rock band.

**NICK  
**(gesturing to a crude hand-drawn graph)  
Venue scalability curve. Stronger-than-average retention rate across regionals. Liquor sales peaked 28 minutes into the set. That's a trigger point.

Sarah, seated at the conference table, flips through her acetate slides. On each is a snapshot: **KATHY**’s onstage snarl. **GILLEY** mid-leap. A crumpled fraternity flag doubling as iconography.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):  
NICK (V.O.):** *The pitch. It’s the most important part. You can have the best data in the world, but if you can’t present it effectively… it’s napkin math in a bar fight.*

---

Sarah stands, replacing one of Nick’s revenue charts with a photo of a sweaty crowd holding lighters.

**SARAH  
**They don’t just generate numbers. They generate heat. Raw. Emotional. Marketable.

Nick exhales sharply, wiping marker residue from his hand.

**NICK  
**I’m not pitching “heat.” I’m pitching investment-grade Momentum.

**SARAH  
**Yeah, and I’m pitching the part that *makes people care.* They’ve got a look. A vibe. They’re Gen X before Gen X knows what it is.

---

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):  
SARAH (V.O.):** *You have to sell the dream. The feeling. You have to make them believe. Otherwise, you’re just selling a spreadsheet.*

---

They circle each other in the room like chess opponents on a 4x6 rug. The projector hums. A silence hangs. Then:

**NICK  
**All right. We go in with both. Lead with growth. Close with fire.

**SARAH  
**Deal. But I got the closing line.

**NICK  
**Fair.

Nick scribbles on his yellow legal pad. Sarah clicks through her final slides. One shows the “LET IT GO” chant—fifteen thousand fists in the air. She slides a sticky note beside it: *“This is what a movement looks like.”*

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**The camera slowly pulls away as they run one more round of their pitch, Nick gesturing to revenue projections while Sarah cues a cassette with a live cut of “Come Inside Me.” They speak over the music. Sharpening. Syncing.

---

**(CUT TO BLACK)  
  
**

**TITLE CARD:** ***THE PITCH IS READY.***

**(15) THE MEETING (A POSITIVE ASSESSMENT):** Nick and Sarah are now in a sleek, modern boardroom at Island Records. They are presenting their findings to a group of high-powered executives. The visuals emphasize:

- **Professional Presentation:** Nick presents the quantifiable data using clear and concise charts and graphs. Sarah presents the more subjective aspects using compelling visuals and persuasive language.
- **Executive Reactions:** Close-ups of the executives’ faces reveal their reactions to the presentation. Some look impressed, others look skeptical. One executive is seen checking his watch. Nick times how long the meeting will take.
- **The Key** Moment**:** A specific Moment where Nick presents a particularly compelling piece of data, or Sarah makes a particularly persuasive point, which seems to sway the executives.
- **The Final Question:** An executive asks a tough question about the band’s long-term potential. Nick and Sarah exchange a quick glance, then deliver a confident and convincing answer.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** It wasn’t a slam dunk. But it was close.

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):**

**SARAH (V.O.)** We planted the seed. Now, we just have to wait and see if it grows.

**(15) THE MEETING (A POSITIVE ASSESSMENT) – DAY**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – EXECUTIVE BOARDROOM – NYC – DAY**

The boardroom is a fortress of glass and leather. A long lacquered table stretches like a runway under a sculptural light fixture. Floor-to-ceiling windows reveal Manhattan simmering under a noonday sun. The soundtrack is silence—until Nick clicks the first slide.

---

**( VISUAL):  
** Slick lighting. Chrome finishes. Wide shots that make the room feel colder than a banker’s handshake. Then tight zooms on eyes, watches, and subtle nods.

---

**(SOUND):  
** A low hum of air conditioning, the soft *click* of a remote, the quiet rustle of legal pads and expensive suit fabric.

---

Nick, sharply dressed but without a tie, stands confidently beside a mounted TV. His demeanor is laser-focused. Sarah, poised and luminous in a tailored blazer, stands beside a mounted mood board easel.

---

**NICK  
** (gesturing to a bar graph)  
 This is ticket growth, week over week, across five cities. Seventy-one percent net gain in foot traffic. Liquor sales mirror the spike, which—according to the venues—coincide exactly with “Come Inside Me”’s chorus. Every. Time.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):  
**NICK (V.O.):** *It wasn’t a slam dunk. But it was close. You could see it in their eyes. The money guys were starting to lean forward.*

---

A white-haired executive scribbles something and nods. A junior exec mouths “seventy-one percent?” in disbelief. Another, arms folded, glances at his Rolex.

---

Sarah steps forward, flips the easel page—revealing a collage of fan Polaroids, ticket stubs, hand-drawn flyers, and stage snapshots.

---

**SARAH  
** They’ve got *presence*. This isn’t just about the sound, it’s the vibe. It’s *generational identity* before the generation has even realized what it wants.

---

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):  
**SARAH (V.O.):** *We planted the seed. Now, we just have to wait and see if it grows. And hope nobody tramples it first.*

---

The room stills. A slide transitions to a pie chart: *Revenue per Audience Member (vs. Regional Median)*. The edges of a decision begin to blur into the room.

---

Then—*the question*.

**EXECUTIVE #1  
**(firm, skeptical)  
You’re pitching rough stock. No polish. No track record. What makes you think they’ll scale?

---

A pause. Nick and Sarah exchange a glance—not panic, not hesitation, but calibration.

Nick steps forward. Hands on the table.

**NICK  
**Because I’ve seen them bomb in a dive bar at 2 a.m. to six people… and still give a stadium-grade performance. That’s not polish. That’s DNA.

Sarah follows with a soft, persuasive tone.

**SARAH  
**They don’t need to be reengineered. Just amplified.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):  
**The camera pans slowly across the table: one executive pensively nodding, another removing his glasses, a third flipping to the last page of the pitch deck. The energy has shifted.

**CUT TO BLACK.  
TITLE CARD:** *Decision Pending…*

**(16) THE MEETING (A POSITIVE ASSESSMENT - THE CLIMAX):** Nick and Sarah are in a sleek, minimalist boardroom at Island Records. They stand before Chris Blackwell himself, along with several other high-ranking executives. The atmosphere is tense but professional. The visuals emphasize:

- **The Presentation:** Nick and Sarah deliver their presentation, seamlessly weaving together quantifiable data and subjective observations. Charts and graphs are projected onto a large screen, interspersed with photos and short video clips of the band performing.
- **Blackwell’s Reactions:** Close-ups of Chris Blackwell’s face reveal his reactions to the presentation. He listens intently, occasionally nodding or raising an eyebrow. He is shown taking notes on a yellow legal pad.
- **The Key Question:** Near the climax of the presentation, Chris Blackwell leans forward, his expression serious.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (His voice calm but direct) So… why haven’t we signed them already? It sounds like they’re worth an offer.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** This was the Moment of truth.

Nick takes a deep breath and explains the situation with **CREMEANS**.

**NICK** (His voice slightly hesitant) Their manager… he refused to even talk to me.

**(VISUAL):** Quick flashback to **CREMEANS** handing Nick his business card and saying, “I only talk to principals.”

**NICK (CONT'D)** He said… (quotes **CREMEANS** precisely) …“I only talk to principals.”

**(OBSERVATION – BLACKWELL):**

**CHRIS BLACKWELL (V.O.)** Interesting. Very interesting.

Blackwell leans back in his chair, stroking his chin thoughtfully.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (His voice curious) So… is this man a megalomaniac? Extraordinarily stupid? Or simply… insanely sure of his position?

**(VISUAL):** Close-ups of Nick and Sarah exchanging a quick glance.

**NICK** (His voice confident) Insanely sure, sir. Without a doubt.

**SARAH** (Her voice equally confident) Absolutely.

Blackwell turns his attention to Sarah.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (His voice direct) Sarah. Your opinion. Skip the part where you… “bonded” with the front man. Give me an honest assessment.

**(VISUAL):** A quick, almost subliminal flash of **GILLEY** and Sarah in the hotel room, then back to Sarah in the boardroom.

Sarah composes herself and delivers her assessment.

**SARAH** (Her voice professional and persuasive) Sir, with all due respect… I think we’d be foolish not to make a maximum effort to sign them. They have a raw energy, a unique sound, and a dedicated manager who clearly knows what he’s doing. They have the potential to be huge.

Blackwell then turns to Nick.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (His voice expectant) Nick. Your final word.

Nick doesn’t hesitate.

**NICK** (His voice firm and confident) Sir, I think this is the biggest opportunity this company has had in twelve years. Since you signed U2.

**(VISUAL):** Extreme close-up on Chris Blackwell’s face as he processes this information.

Blackwell lets out a low, long, admiring whistle.

**(SOUND:** A low, drawn-out whistle from Chris Blackwell. The music swells slightly, reaching a crescendo.)

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera pulls back to show the entire boardroom, the executives looking impressed and intrigued. The focus is on Chris Blackwell, his expression now one of keen interest and anticipation. The meeting has clearly gone well, and the future of Commuted is now hanging in the balance. The location is the Island Records boardroom. The time is the conclusion of the meeting. The montage ends with the distinct implication that Commuted is on the verge of something big. The scene ends with Blackwell's whistle.

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS BOARDROOM – CONTINUOUS**

The boardroom is quiet, the tension from the presentation now replaced by a sense of anticipation. Chris Blackwell sits at the head of the table, his expression thoughtful. Nick Stewart and Sarah stand nearby, watching him intently. The other executives remain seated, their expressions a mixture of curiosity and professional detachment.

**(SOUND:** The quiet hum of the air conditioning, the distant sounds of the city outside, and the faint sound of Chris Blackwell’s finger pressing a button on a speakerphone.)

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on Chris Blackwell’s hand as he presses the button on the speakerphone. The speakerphone is a sleek, modern design, a symbol of the power and influence of Island Records.

A disembodied voice answers from the speakerphone.

**DISBODIED VOICE (V.O.)** (Calm and professional) Yes, Mr. Blackwell?

**(OBSERVATION – BLACKWELL):**

**CHRIS BLACKWELL (V.O.)** Time to make a move.



**CHRIS BLACKWELL (V.O.)** Sometimes, you have to go to the source. You have to see it for yourself.

Blackwell speaks into the speakerphone, his voice calm and decisive.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (His voice clear and commanding) I need three first-class tickets to Dayton.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on Nick Stewart and Sarah, their expressions a mixture of surprise and excitement.

A brief Moment of silence hangs in the air as the disembodied voice processes the request.

**DISBODIED VOICE (V.O.)** (After a short pause) Confirming… three first-class tickets to Dayton… departing Friday morning.

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**

**NICK (V.O.)** Friday morning. That was… fast.

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):**

**SARAH (V.O.)** He’s serious. He’s really serious.

Blackwell looks up from the speakerphone, his eyes meeting Nick Stewart’s. A slight smile plays on his lips.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (His voice calm and confident) We’re going to see a show.

**(VISUAL):** The camera focuses on Chris Blackwell’s face, his expression now one of quiet anticipation. Then the camera slowly pulls back, encompassing the entire boardroom, the executives looking intrigued.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera continues to pull back, the boardroom receding into the distance. The focus shifts to a stylized shot of a map of the United States, with a highlighted route from New York City to Dayton, Ohio. The music swells slightly, then abruptly cuts out.

**(SOUND:** A dramatic, final chord, followed by complete silence.)

**(TEXT ON SCREEN):** FRIDAY.

**(CURTAIN DROP/FADE TO BLACK)**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS BOARDROOM - CONTINUOUS**

The air has a weight to it now. The buzz of fluorescent lights. The distant throb of Manhattan traffic. At the head of the polished boardroom table, CHRIS BLACKWELL leans back in his chair, fingers steepled, eyes locked in a thousand-yard stare that cuts through time and markets.

---

**(SOUND):** The low, electronic *beep* of a speakerphone being activated. The faint hum of a powerful machine waiting for instruction.

---

**(VISUAL):** Extreme close-up on Blackwell’s hand—weathered, decisive—as it presses the smooth black button of the speakerphone. Power as choreography.

---

**DISBODIED VOICE (V.O.)** Yes, Mr. Blackwell?

---

**(OBSERVATION – BLACKWELL):** BLACKWELL (V.O.): *In this business, hesitation is death. You move fast. Or you miss everything.*

---

 **BLACKWELL (into speakerphone)**  
 I need three first-class tickets to Dayton. Friday morning.

---

**(VISUAL):**  
Cut to Sarah. Her pen freezes mid-note. Nick blinks once. No sound. No movement. Just the shift of history underfoot.

---

**DISBODIED VOICE (V.O.):**  
Confirming… three first-class tickets to Dayton… departing Friday morning.

---

**(OBSERVATION – NICK):**  
NICK (V.O.): *Friday morning. That was fast. Then again—so’s lightning.*

**(OBSERVATION – SARAH):**  
SARAH (V.O.): *We just set something in motion. Something real. Something big.*

---

Blackwell leans forward, his elbows on the table. For the first time, he actually *smiles*.

**BLACKWELL**  
We’re going to see a show.

---

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on Blackwell’s face. The skin around his eyes creases. This is a man who *knows*. Knows when to strike. Knows what it looks like when lightning hits a garage band.

The camera pulls back. The table. The executives. Nick and Sarah. The skyline visible beyond the glass. They’re all tiny players now, dwarfed by the decision that just got made.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):** The frame pulls even farther back. The boardroom fades into a stylized map of the United States. A glowing red line traces a route from New York City to Dayton, Ohio. The words scrawl across the screen:

**FRIDAY.**

(SOUND):  
 One final, thunderous chord of music. Then dead silence.

**FADE TO BLACK.*
